when you say she's a programmer , she did do some , but the real thing is to have said the future is going to be much , much more than this .	當你說她是程式設計師時 , 她做了一些事 , 但真正的 , 是要說未來會比這個還要多 。
now , a hundred years later , this guy comes along , alan turing , and in 1936 , and invents the computer all over again .	一百年後 , 這個傢伙出現了亞特林 , 1936年 , 發明了電腦 。
now , of course , babbage's machine was entirely mechanical .	當然 , 巴比斯的機器是完全機械的 。
turing's machine was entirely theoretical .	turing的機器完全是理論性的 。
both of these guys were coming from a mathematical perspective , but turing told us something very important .	這些人都是從數學角度來的 , 但土耳其告訴我們一件非常重要的事 。
he laid down the mathematical foundations for computer science , and said , " it doesn't matter how you make a computer . "	他把數學基礎放在電腦科學上 , 說: 「 不論你如何製作電腦 。 」
it doesn't matter if your computer's mechanical , like babbage's was , or electronic , like computers are today , or perhaps in the future , cells , or , again , mechanical again , once we get into nanotechnology .	不管是電腦的機械裝置 , 像是babbage的 , 或是電子裝置 , 像現今的電腦 , 或也許在未來的細胞 , 或再一次 , 一旦我們進入了奈米科技 。
we could go back to babbage's machine and just make it tiny . all those things are computers .	我們可以回到babbage的機器 , 讓它變小 , 所有這些東西都是電腦 。
there is in a sense a computing essence .	有一個計算機的本質 。
this is called the church–turing thesis .	這是所謂的教堂演唱論 。
and so suddenly , you get this link where you say this thing babbage had built really was a computer .	突然間 , 你看到了這個連結 , 你說巴比斯建造了這個東西 , 真的是一台電腦 。
in fact , it was capable of doing everything we do today with computers , only really slowly .	事實上 , 它能夠做到我們今天用電腦做的每件事 , 只能慢慢地 。
to give you an idea of how slowly , it had about 1k of memory .	為了讓你們知道 , 記憶有多慢 , 它有1k的記憶力 。
it used punch cards , which were being fed in , and it ran about 10 , 000 times slower the first zx81 .	它會用穿孔卡 , 被吸進來 , 最早的zx81會慢一萬倍 。
it did have a ram pack .	它的確有一堆雨水 。
you could add on a lot of extra memory if you wanted to .	如果你想加入多餘的記憶體 。
so , where does that bring us today ?	那麼 , 這帶給我們什麼呢 ?
so there are plans .	所以 , 有一些計畫 。
over in swindon , the science museum archives , there are hundreds of plans and thousands of pages of notes written by charles babbage about this analytical engine .	在瑞典 , 科學博物館檔案 , 有數百個計劃和數以千計的筆記 , 由查爾斯•巴貝奇寫下這個分析引擎 。
one of those is a set of plans that we call plan 28 , and that is also the name of a charity that i started with doron swade , who was the curator of computing at the science museum , and also the person who drove the project to build a difference engine , and our plan is to build it .	其中一個是我們稱之為 「 計畫28 」 的計畫 , 也是我一開始的慈善機構的名字 , 他是科學博物館的競賽者 , 也是開車建造不同引擎的人 , 我們的計劃就是要建造它 。
here in south kensington , we will build the analytical engine .	在南肯辛頓 , 我們會建造分析引擎 。
the project has a number of parts to it .	這個計畫有許多零件可以用來做 。
one was the scanning of babbage's archive .	其中一個是巴比斯的檔案 。
that's been done . the second is now the study of all of those plans to determine what to build .	這已經完成了 。 第二個是研究所有計劃的研究 , 來決定要建造什麼 。
the third part is a computer simulation of that machine , and the last part is to physically build it at the science museum .	第三部分是電腦模擬這台機器的最後一部分就是在科學博物館建造它 。
when it's built , you'll finally be able to understand how a computer works , because rather than having a tiny chip in front of you , you've got to look at this humongous thing and say , " ah , i see the memory operating , i see the cpu operating , i hear it operating . i probably smell it operating . "	當它建成時 , 你終於可以理解電腦如何運作 , 因為不如在你面前有一個小小的晶片 , 你得看看這個龐大的東西 , 然後說: 「 啊 , 我看到記憶操作 , 我看到cpu操作 , 我聽見它在運作 。 我可能聞到它 。 」
but in between that we're going to do a simulation .	但在這兩者之間 , 我們要做模擬 。
babbage himself wrote , he said , as soon as the analytical engine exists , it will surely guide the future course of science .	巴比斯自己寫下 , 他說 , 一旦分析引擎存在 , 它將會引導未來科學的發展 。
of course , he never built it , because he was always fiddling with new plans , but when it did get built , of course , in the 1940s , everything changed .	當然 , 他從來沒有打造它 , 因為他總是和新計劃結合 , 但當他建造時 , 當然 , 在1940年代 , 一切都改變了 。
now , i'll just give you a little taste of what it looks like in motion with a video which shows just one part of the cpu mechanism working .	現在 , 我給大家一點一點點味道 , 用影片顯示cpu機制運作的其中一部分 。
so this is just three sets of cogs , and it's going to add . this is the adding mechanism in action , so you imagine this gigantic machine .	所以這只是三組齒輪 , 它會加上它 。 這是行動的加速機制 , 所以你想像這台巨大的機器 。
so , give me five years .	所以 , 給我五年 。
before the 2030s happen , we'll have it .	在2030年代之前 , 我們將會有它 。
thank you very much .	非常謝謝 。
in this imagefilled talk , yann arthusbertrand displays his three most recent projects on humanity and our habitat stunning aerial photographs in his series " the earth from above , " personal interviews from around the globe featured in his web project " 6 billion others , " and his soontobereleased movie , " home , " which documents human impact on the environment through breathtaking video .	在這張影像中 , 雅恩•亞伯特蘭德展示了他最近期人類和我們居住的居住地照片 , 在他的系列中 , 《地》中 , 來自世界各地的個人訪問 , 《六十億人的網路專案》 , 以及他的小說《六十億人》 , 透過呼吸的影片 , 記錄了人類對環境的影響 。
art , climate change , environment , film , future , humanity , media , photography	藝術、氣候變遷、環境、未來、人類、媒體、攝影 。
yann arthusbertrand captures fragile earth in wideangle	yan藝術hubertrand在寬角處捕捉脆弱的地球 。
i have a big impact on the planet to travel here by plane .	我對地球的影響很大 , 由飛機來到這裡 。
i emitted , in the atmosphere , nine tons of co2 ; that is the weight of two elephants .	我在大氣中排放九噸的二氧化碳 , 那是兩隻大象的重量 。
i came here to speak about ecology , and i emitted as much co2 as a frenchman in one year .	我來這裡談的是生態學 , 一年內我將二氧化碳排放成法國人 。
so what do i have to do ?	所以 , 我該怎麼做 ?
i have to kill a frenchman when i come back at home ?	當我回到家時 , 我得殺害一位法國人嗎 ?
i have to do my carbon offset in another way , like i do every time .	我必須用另一種方式來做我的碳排放 , 就像我每次都在做一樣 。
in fact my work is to show our impact on our planet .	事實上 , 我的作品是要展現我們對地球的影響 。
i'm going to show you some examples of the last pictures i've done in the last year .	我要給你們看一些例子 , 是我去年拍的最後一張照片 。
alberta sand oil , a lot of pollution .	亞伯達•沙石 , 很多污染 。
you know the problem ; we don't want to believe what we know .	你知道問題 , 我們不想相信我們所知道的 。
in alberta people work nonstop , 24 hours by seven to extract as much oil as they can .	在阿爾伯塔人工作非營運24小時 , 七小時 , 盡可能抽取石油 。
we know about the end of oil .	我們知道石油的終點 。
oil sand is not a longterm solution .	石油沙子不是長期的解決方案 。
but we use three times more oil than we find every year .	但我們每年使用三倍的石油 , 比我們所發現的石油還要多 。
we don't want to believe what we know .	我們不想相信我們所知道的 。
coral reef in new caledonia .	新加州的珊瑚礁 。
100 percent of the coral may be wiped out before 2050 because of global warming .	在2050年之前 , 百分之百的珊瑚可能會因為全球暖化而消失 。
and you know how coral are very sensitive to temperature , and are very important for the biodiversity of the sea .	你知道珊瑚對溫度非常敏感 , 對海洋的生物多樣性非常重要 。
north pole . i've done this picture last summer .	北極 , 我去年夏天拍了這張照片 。
it was impossible to do this picture 15 years ago .	15年前這張照片是不可能的 。
now there is a new way open between atlantic and pacific .	在大西洋和太平洋之間有一個新方法 。
the thickness of the arctic decreased more than 40 percent since 1960 .	從1960年以來 , 北極的濃度減少了超過40% 。
there is a new face of kilimanjaro without ice .	沒有冰的吉里馬尼歐有新的面孔 。
it lost 80 percent of its ice .	它失去了80%的冰 。
according to scientists , in 100 years all the mountain glacier will be gone .	根據科學家 , 在一百年內 , 所有山的冰河都會消失 。
glaciers are very important for the life on earth .	冰河對地球的生命是非常重要的 。
like al gore told you , two billion people live on the water from the glacier of himalaya .	就像高爾說過的 , 有20億人住在喜馬拉雅冰河的水上 。
return of fish men .	回歸魚類的人 。
one fifth of human kind depend on fish to live .	五分之一的人類依賴魚來生存 。
today now 70 percent of the fish stock are overexploited .	現今 , 70%的魚類被濫用了 。
according to fao , if we don't change our system of fishing the main sea resources will be gone in 2050 .	根據faceo , 如果我們不改變我們的捕魚系統 , 主要的海洋資源將會在2050年消失 。
we don't want to believe what we know .	我們不想相信我們所知道的 。

here in america , 90 percent of the corn cultivated is used to feed animals or to do oil .	在美國 , 百分之九十的玉米培養被用來餵食動物或做石油 。
palm tree plantation in borneo .	棕櫚樹種植在出生時 。

for generations , we've been raising our children , not unlike millions of other species living beside us .	數世代以來 , 我們一直在養育我們的孩子 , 而不是其他數百萬種生物 , 除了我們之外 。
for the past 30 years i've been closely watching the earth and its dwellers from high up in the sky .	過去三十年來 , 我非常靠近地球和它在天空中高空中高空的dweller 。
our life is tied to the wellbeing of our planet .	我們的生命與地球的幸福息息息息相關 。
we depend on water , forests , deserts , oceans .	我們依賴水、森林、沙漠、海洋 。
fishing , breeding , farming are still the world's foremost human occupations .	捕魚、繁殖 , 農場仍然是世界上最頂尖的人類職業 。
and what binds us together is far greater than what divides us .	把我們結合在一起的比我們分裂還要大很多 。
we all share the same need for the earth's gifts the same wish to rise above ourselves , and become better .	我們都分享地球的禮物 , 相同的願望 , 相同的願望 , 並且變得更好 。
and yet we carry on raising walls to keep us apart .	然而 , 我們還帶著提高牆壁 , 使我們不分離 。
today our greatest battle is to protect the natural offerings of our planet .	今天 , 我們最大的戰役是保護我們星球的天然生產力 。
in less than 50 years we've altered it more thoroughly than in the entire history of mankind .	在不到五十年的時間裡 , 我們將它徹底改變 , 遠比人類歷史上人類的歷史還要嚴重 。
half of the world's forests have vanished .	世界上一半的森林消失了 。
water resources are running low .	水資源在運作低 。
intensive farming is depleting soils .	強烈的農業正在耗盡土壤 。
our energy sources are not sustainable .	我們的能源來源並不永續 。
the climate is changing .	氣候正在改變 。
we are endangering ourselves .	我們正在危害我們自己 。
we're only trying to improve our lives .	我們只想改善我們的生活 。
but the wealth gaps are growing wider .	但財富差距越來越大 。
we haven't yet understood that we're going at a much faster pace than the planet can sustain .	我們還沒了解到 , 我們的速度比地球的永續發展還要快很多 。
we know that solutions are available today .	我們知道 , 解決方案是可行的 。
we all have the power to change this trend for the better .	我們都有改變這個趨勢的力量 。
so what are we waiting for ?	那麼 , 我們在等什麼呢 ?

in this accessible talk from tedxboston , richard resnick shows how cheap and fast genome sequencing is about to turn health care upside down .	在tedxboston的這場演說中 , 理查.雷尼克顯示出 , 健康照護將如何降低 。
dna , biotech , health care , science , technology	dna、生物科技、健康照護、科學、技術、技術 。
richard resnick: welcome to the genomic revolution	理查.雷斯尼克:歡迎來到基因體革命 。
ladies and gentlemen , i present to you the human genome .	各位先生女士 , 我向你們展示人類基因組 。
chromosome one , top left .	染色體是左上角 。
bottom right are the sex chromosomes .	右下角是性染色體 。
women have two copies of that big x chromosome ; men have the x and , of course , that small copy of the y .	女性有兩份大x染色體的複製品 ; 男性有x , 當然 , 小型y的複製品 。
sorry boys , but it's just a tiny little thing that makes you different .	很抱歉的男孩 , 但這只是一個小小的小東西 , 讓你有所不同 。
so if you zoom in on this genome , then what you see , of course , is this double helix structure the code of life spelled out with these four biochemical letters , or we call them bases , right: a , c , g and t .	所以 , 如果你放大這個基因組 , 你可以看到 , 這雙螺旋結構 , 生命的編碼是這四個生物化學字母的編碼 , 或者我們稱它們為基礎:a、c、g和t 。
how many are there in the human genome ? three billion .	人類基因組中有多少人 ? 30億人 。
is that a big number ?	這是個大數字嗎 ?
well , everybody can throw around big numbers .	嗯 , 每個人都可以在大數字中丟下 。
but in fact , if i were to place one base on each pixel of this 1280 by 800 resolution screen , we would need 3 , 000 screens to take a look at the genome .	但事實上 , 如果我把一個像素放在這個1280到800個解析度螢幕上 , 我們就需要3000個螢幕來觀察基因組 。
so it's really quite big .	這真的很大 。
and perhaps because of its size , a group of people all , by the way , with y chromosomes decided they would want to sequence it .	或許是因為它的大小 , 一群人 , 順便一提 , y染色體決定要定序 。
and so 15 years , actually , and about four billion dollars later , the genome was sequenced and published .	事實上 , 15年後 , 大約40億美金 , 基因組是序列和出版的 。
in 2003 , the final version was published , and they keep working on it .	在2003年 , 最後一個版本出版了 , 他們一直在做這件事 。
that was all done on a machine that looks like this .	這些都是在機器上完成的 , 看起來像這樣 。
it costs about a dollar for each base a very slow way of doing it .	它的成本是每一塊錢--一個非常緩慢的做法 。
well folks , i'm here to tell you that the world has completely changed and none of you know about it .	嗯 , 各位 , 我來這裡告訴你們 , 世界已經完全改變了 , 你們都不知道 。
so now what we do is we take a genome , we make maybe 50 copies of it , we cut all those copies up into little 50base reads , and then we sequence them , massively parallel .	我們現在做的是將基因組做五十個複製 , 我們把這些複製片切成五十個棒子 , 然後我們將它們定序 , 大量的平行 。
and then we bring that into software , and we reassemble it and we tell you what the story is .	然後我們把這個帶到軟體中 , 重新組合它 , 告訴各位故事是什麼 。
and so just to give you a picture of what this looks like , the human genome project: 3 gigabases , right .	所以 , 為了給你一張圖片 , 人類基因組計劃:3gabes , 沒錯 。
one run on one of these machines: 200 gigabases in a week .	一台運行在其中一台機器上:每週200個gbases 。
and that 200 is going to change to 600 this summer , and there's no sign of this pace slowing .	今年夏天將要改變600個 , 沒有這種速度慢下來的跡象 。
so the price of a base , to sequence a base , has fallen 100 million times .	所以 , 基礎的代價 , 將基礎序列列列定序 , 總共有一億次 。
that's the equivalent of you filling up your car with gas in 1998 , waiting until 2011 , and now you can drive to jupiter and back twice .	相當於你在1998年填滿車子 , 等到2011年 , 等到2011年 , 你就可以駕駛到木星和兩倍 。
world population , pc placements , the archive of all the medical literature , moore's law , the old way of sequencing , and here's all the new stuff .	世界人口、pc位置、醫學文獻的檔案、摩爾定律、古老的定序方式 , 等等都是新東西 。
guys , this is a log scale ; you don't typically see lines that go up like that .	各位 , 這是個邏輯尺度 ; 你通常不會看到像這樣的線條 。
so the worldwide capacity to sequence human genomes is something like 50 , 000 to 100 , 000 human genomes this year .	所以 , 世界各地的基因序列 , 今年大約有五萬到十萬個人類基因組 。
and we know this based on the machines that are being placed .	而我們知道這一點 , 基於已被放置的機器 。
this is expected to double , triple or maybe quadruple year over year for the foreseeable future .	這是預期兩倍、三倍或四倍的一年 , 預計未來是可預見的 。
in fact , there's one lab in particular that represents 20 percent of all that capacity .	事實上 , 有一個實驗室代表了百分之二十的能力 。
it's called the beijing genomics institute .	它叫做北京基因學研究所 。
the chinese are absolutely winning this race to the new moon , by the way .	順道一提 , 中國在新月球上贏得了這場比賽 。
what does this mean for medicine ?	這對醫學的意義是什麼 ?
so a woman is age 37 .	一個女人是37歲 。
she presents with stage 2 estrogen receptorpositive breast cancer .	她展示了階段2個雌激素接受性乳癌 。
she is treated with surgery , chemotherapy and radiation .	她接受手術治療 , 化療和放射性治療 。
two years later , she comes back with stage three c ovarian cancer .	兩年後 , 她帶著三階段的卵巢癌回來 。
unfortunately , treated again with surgery and chemotherapy .	不幸的是 , 再一次用手術和化療治療來治療 。
she comes back three years later at age 42 with more ovarian cancer , more chemotherapy .	三年後 , 她在42歲時回來 , 更有卵巢癌 , 更有化療 。
six months later , she comes back with acute myeloid leukemia .	六個月後 , 她回來時 , 帶著急性的白血病回來 。
she goes into respiratory failure and dies eight days later .	八天後 , 她走進呼吸道失敗 。
so first , the way in which this woman was treated , in as little as 10 years , will look like bloodletting .	首先 , 這位女士被治療的過程 , 大約十年後 , 會看起來像血管一樣 。
and it's because of people like my colleague , rick wilson , at the genome institute at washington university , who decided to take a look at this woman postmortem .	那是因為像我同事rickwilson這樣的人 , 在華盛頓大學的基因組研究所 , 她決定要看看這位女子後期 。
and he sequenced , he took skin cells , healthy skin , and cancerous bone marrow , and he sequenced the whole genomes of both of them in a couple of weeks , no big deal .	他將皮膚細胞、健康的皮膚和癌症的骨髓序列序列列列列 , 兩者的基因組數週內 , 沒有大的交易 。
and then he compared those two genomes in software , and what he found , among other things , was a deletion , a 2 , 000base deletion across three billion bases in a particular gene called tp53 .	然後他把這兩組基因組做比較 , 他發現 , 其中有一組廢棄物 , 一個2 , 000個鹼基在一個叫做tp53的基因中 , 一個叫做tp53的基因 。
if you have this deleterious mutation in this gene , you're 90 percent likely to get cancer in your life .	如果你的基因中有這種嚴重的突變 , 你有90%的可能罹患癌症 。
so unfortunately , this doesn't help this woman , but it does have severe , profound if you will , implications to her family .	不幸的是 , 這並不幫助這位女士 , 但如果你願意的話 , 它的確是嚴重的 , 深刻的影響她的家人 。
i mean , if they have the same mutation , and they get this genetic test , and they understand it , then they can go and get regular screens , and they can catch cancer early and potentially live a significantly longer life .	我的意思是 , 如果他們有同樣的突變 , 他們得到了這個基因測試 , 然後他們了解它 , 那麼他們就可以得到一般的篩檢 , 他們可以早期發現癌症 , 可能活得更長壽 。
let me introduce you now to the beery twins , diagnosed with cerebral palsy at the age of two .	讓我向各位介紹beerywins , 診斷出brebralpalsy的年齡 。
their mom is a very brave woman who didn't believe that the symptoms weren't matching up , and through some heroic efforts and a lot of internet searching , she was able to convince the medical community that , in fact , they had something else .	他們的母親是一位非常勇敢的女性 , 不相信症狀不適合 , 透過一些英雄的努力和網路搜尋 , 她能夠說服醫學社群 , 事實上 , 他們也有別的 。
what they had was doparesponsive dystonia .	他們所擁有的 , 是多麼的反應性失調症 。
and so they were given ldopa , and their symptoms did improve , but they weren't totally asymptomatic .	所以他們被賦予了 「 ldopa 」 , 他們的症狀確實改善了 , 但他們並非完全的症狀 。
turns out the gentleman in this picture is a guy named joe beery , who was lucky enough to be the cio of a company called life technologies .	這張照片的先生是一位叫joebery的傢伙 , 他很幸運能成為一家叫做生命科技的公司 。
they're one of the two companies that makes these massive whole genome sequencing tools .	它們是兩家公司之一 , 製造這些龐大的基因組定序工具 。
and so what he did was he got his kids sequenced .	所以他做的是 , 他拿到了他的孩子的序列 。
and what they found was a series of mutations in a gene called spr , which is responsible for producing serotonin , among other things .	他們發現一系列的突變 , 叫做 「 春天 」 , 負責製造血清素 , 及其它東西 。
so on top of ldopa , they gave these kids a serotonin precursor drug , and they're effectively normal now .	所以 , 在德opa的頂端 , 他們給了這些孩子一個血清素前的藥 , 他們現在是正常的 。
guys , this would never have happened without whole genome sequencing .	沒有完整的基因序列 , 這絕對不會發生 。
and at the time this was a few years ago it cost $100 , 000 .	當時是幾年前 , 它花了十萬美金 。
today it's $10 , 000 . next year it's $1 , 000 .	今天是一萬元 。 明年是一千元 。
the year after it's $100 , give or take a year .	一百元以後的一年 , 給予一年 。
that's how fast this is moving .	速度就是這麼快 。
so here's little nick likes batman and squirt guns .	這裡有小小的尼克 , 像是蝙蝠俠和松鼠槍 。
and it turns out nick shows up at the children's hospital with this distended belly like a famine victim .	結果發現 , 尼克出現在兒童醫院 , 這種異常的肚子 , 像是一個飢荒的受害者 。
and it's not that he's not eating , it's that when he eats , his intestine basically opens up and feces spill out into his gut .	不是說他不吃東西 , 而是當他吃東西時 , 他的腸道基本上就打開了 , 進到腸道裡 。
so a hundred surgeries later , he looks at his mom and says , " mom , please pray for me . i'm in so much pain . "	一百個手術後 , 他看著他的媽媽說: 「 媽 , 請為我禱告 。 我真的很痛 。 」
his pediatrician happens to have a background in clinical genetics and he has no idea what's going on , but he says , " let's get this kid's genome sequenced . "	他的小兒科醫生剛好有臨床遺傳學的背景 , 他不知道發生什麼事 , 但他說: 「 咱們來取得這個孩子的基因序列 。 」
and what they find is a singlepoint mutation in a gene responsible for controlling programmed cell death .	他們發現一個單一的基因突變 , 負責控制細胞死亡的基因 。
so the theory is that he's having some immunological reaction to what's going on to the food essentially , and that's a natural reaction , which causes some programmed cell death .	所以 , 理論是 , 他有一些免疫反應 , 基本上對食物的影響 , 這是天然的反應 , 導致一些細胞死亡 。
but the gene that regulates that down is broken .	但控制下的基因是壞掉的 。
and so this informs , among other things , of course , a treatment for bone marrow transplant , which he undertakes .	所以 , 這種資訊 , 當然 , 對於骨髓移植的治療 , 這種治療方式 , 是他所做的 。
and after nine months of grueling recovery , he's now eating steak with a1 sauce .	經過九個月的苦難復原後 , 他現在正在吃牛排 , 拿著一塊醬 。
the prospect of using the genome as a universal diagnostic is upon us today .	利用基因組作為普遍診斷的前景 , 就是今天我們 。
today , it's here .	今天 , 它就在這裡 。
and what it means for all of us is that everybody in this room could live an extra five , 10 , 20 years just because of this one thing .	對我們所有人來說 , 這意味著 , 在這間房間裡的每個人都可以過5、10、20年 , 只是因為這一件事而已 。
which is a fantastic story , unless you think about humanity's footprint on the planet and our ability to keep up food production .	這是個很棒的故事 , 除非你在地球上想出人類的足跡 , 以及我們能維持糧食生產的能力 。
so it turns out that the very same technology is also being used to grow new lines of corn , wheat , soybean and other crops that are highly tolerant of drought , of flood , of pests and pesticides .	結果發現 , 同樣的技術也被用來種植玉米、小麥、黃豆和其他農作物 , 高度包含乾旱、洪水、殺蟲劑和殺蟲劑 。
now look , as long as we continue to increase the population , we're going to have to continue to grow and eat genetically modified foods , and that's the only position that i'll take today .	仔細看 , 只要我們繼續增加人口 , 我們就得繼續生長和吃基因改造的食物 , 這是我今天唯一要吃的位置 。
unless there's anybody in the audience that would like to volunteer to stop eating ?	除非在觀眾席中有人想要自願不再吃東西 ?

this is a typewriter , a staple of every desktop for decades .	這是一台打字機 , 數十年來 , 每台桌面的釘子 。

daniel kraft demos his marrow miner a new device that quickly harvests lifesaving bone marrow with minimal pain to the donor . he emphasizes that the adult stem cells found in bone marrow can be used to treat many terminal conditions , from parkinson's to heart disease .	danielkraft展示他的骨髓 , 一個新的裝置 , 很快就收集了生命的骨髓 , 和捐贈者的最少疼痛 。 他強調 , 骨髓中的成年幹細胞可以用來治療許多臨界條件 , 從巴金森氏症到心臟病 。

so , a few years ago , i'm doing my transplant fellowship at stanford .	幾年前 , 我在史丹佛大學進行移植 。
i'm in the operating room . we have bob here , who is a volunteer donor .	我在手術室 , 這裡有bob , 他是志工捐贈者 。
we're sending his marrow across the country to save the life of a child with leukemia .	我們把他的骨髓送到全國 , 來拯救一個患有白血病的孩子 。
so actually how do we harvest this bone marrow ?	所以 , 我們該如何收集這些骨髓呢 ?
well we have a whole o . r . team , general anesthesia , nurses , and another doctor across from me .	我們有一整個o.r.r.團隊 , 普遍麻醉、護士 , 以及另一位醫生 。
bob's on the table , and we take this sort of small needle , you know , not too big .	巴布在桌上 , 我們拿著這個小針 , 你知道的 , 不太大 。
and the way we do this is we basically place this through the soft tissue , and kind of punch it into the hard bone , into the tuchus that's a technical term and aspirate about 10 mls of bone marrow out , each time , with a syringe .	我們的做法基本上就是透過軟組織把這個放進硬骨裡 , 把它放進圖中 , 一個技術術語 , 每次都會用針筒來刺激10磅的骨髓 。
and hand it off to the nurse . she squirts it into a tin .	把它交給護士 , 她將它安靜到一個小小的房間裡 。
hands it back to me . and we do that again and again .	把它交給我 , 我們再次這樣做 。
about 200 times usually .	通常是兩百次 。
and by the end of this my arm is sore , i've got a callus on my hand , let alone bob , whose rear end looks something more like this , like swiss cheese .	我的手臂的尾端是索爾 , 我手上有一通電話 , 更別說鮑勃 , 他的耳朵看起來像這樣 , 像是瑞士起士 。
so i'm thinking , you know , this procedure hasn't changed in about 40 years .	所以我在想 , 這種手術在40年內並沒有改變 。
and there is probably a better way to do this .	這樣做可能有更好的方法 。
so i thought of a minimally invasive approach , and a new device that we call the marrow miner .	所以我想到一個極度侵入式的方法 , 一個我們稱之為 「 骨髓礦工 」 的新裝置 。
and the marrow miner , the way it works is shown here .	標記礦工是這樣運作的 。
our standard seethrough patient .	我們的標準分裂患者 。
instead of entering the bone dozens of times , we enter just once , into the front of the hip or the back of the hip .	與其進入骨頭幾十次 , 我們進入了一次 , 進入髖部或臀部的前面 。
and we have a flexible , powered catheter with a special wire loop tip that stays inside the crunchy part of the marrow and follows the contours of the hip , as it moves around .	我們有一個彈性、強大的導管 , 帶著一個特殊的迴圈尖 , 留在 「 三月 」 中 , 追隨 「 髖部 」 的路徑 , 隨著它四處移動 。
so it enables you to very rapidly aspirate , or suck out , rich bone marrow very quickly through one hole .	所以它能讓你非常快速地吸引人或吸引人的骨髓 , 非常迅速地穿過一個洞 。
we can do multiple passes through that same entry .	我們可以通過同樣的入口 , 做多重 。
and , so , very quickly , bob can just get one puncture , local anesthesia , and do this harvest as an outpatient .	所以 , 很快的 , 鮑勃就能得到一個懲罰 , 當地的麻醉 , 並把這些收穫當作一個廣告 。
so i did a few prototypes . i got a small little grant at stanford .	所以我做了幾個原型 。 我在史丹佛大學拿了個小小的補丁 。
and played around with this a little bit .	玩一下這個 。
and our team members developed this technology .	我們的團隊成員開發了這項技術 。
and eventually we got two large animals , and pig studies .	最後我們有兩個大型動物和豬研究 。
and we found , to our surprise , that we not only got bone marrow out , but we got 10 times the stem cell activity in the marrow from the marrow miner , compared to the normal device .	我們發現 , 對於我們的驚喜 , 我們不僅得到骨髓 , 還得到10倍的幹細胞活動 , 相較於一般的裝置 。
this device was just fda approved in the last year .	這個裝置在去年才被核准 。
here is a live patient . you can see it following the flexible curves around .	這裡是活的病患 , 你可以看到它跟隨靈活的曲線 。
there will be two passes here , in the same patient , from the same hole .	同一個病人 , 同一個病人 , 會在同一個洞裡經過兩條路 。
this was done under local anesthesia , as an outpatient .	這是在當地的麻醉劑 , 作為一個廣告 。
and we got , again , about three to six times more stem cells than the standard approach done on the same patient .	同樣的 , 我們得到了三到六倍的幹細胞 , 比同一個病人做的標準方法還要多 。
so why should you care ? bone marrow is a very rich source of adult stem cells .	所以 , 你為什麼要在乎 ? 骨髓是成人幹細胞的豐富來源 。
you all know about embryonic stem cells .	你們都知道胚胎幹細胞 。
they've got great potential but haven't yet entered clinical trials .	他們有很大的潛力 , 但還沒有進入臨床試驗 。
adult stem cells are throughout our body , including the bloodforming stem cells in our bone marrow , which we've been using as a form of stemcell therapy for over 40 years .	成人幹細胞在我們的身體中 , 包括我們骨髓裡的血液幹細胞 , 我們一直使用這種幹細胞治療法 , 超過四十年來 。
in the last decade there's been an explosion of use of bone marrow stem cells to treat the patient's other diseases such as heart disease , vascular disease , orthopedics , tissue engineering , even in neurology to treat parkinson's and diabetes .	在過去的十年中 , 使用骨髓幹細胞來治療病人的其他疾病 , 例如心臟病、血管疾病、組織工程 , 甚至在神經邏輯上治療帕金森氏症和糖尿病 。
we've just come out , we're commercializing , this year , generation 2 . 0 of the marrow miner .	我們剛剛出櫃 , 今年商業化 , 兩代的遊行礦工 。
the hope is that this gets more stem cells out , which translates to better outcomes .	希望這能得到更多幹細胞 , 轉化成更好的結果 。
it may encourage more people to sign up to be potential livesaving bone marrow donors .	它可能會鼓勵更多人簽下潛在的骨髓捐贈者 。
it may even enable you to bank your own marrow stem cells , when you're younger and healthier , to use in the future should you need it .	它甚至可能讓你可以把你自己的骨髓幹細胞安排 , 當你比較年輕、更健康 , 在未來你就應該要用它 。
and ultimately and here's a picture of our bone marrow transplant survivors , who come together for a reunion each year at stanford .	最終 , 這是一張我們骨髓移植的倖存者照片 , 每年在史丹佛 , 聚集在一起 。
hopefully this technology will let us have more of these survivors in the future .	希望這項技術能讓我們在未來有更多這些倖存者 。
physicist and surfer garrett lisi presents a controversial new model of the universe that just maybe answers all the big questions . if nothing else , it's the most beautiful 8dimensional model of elementary particles and forces you've ever seen .	物理學家和衝浪莉西提出一個有爭議的宇宙模型 , 可能可以回答所有大問題 。 如果沒有 , 它是你所見過最美麗的基本粒子和力量 。
physics , science , technology	物理、科學、科技、科技、科技 。
garrett lisi on his theory of everything	garrettlisi理論上 , 所有事情的理論都在他的理論上 。
whoa , dude . check out those killer equations . sweet .	哇 , 老兄 , 看看那些殺手方程式 。 很甜 。
actually , for the next 18 minutes i'm going to do the best i can to describe the beauty of particle physics without equations .	事實上 , 接下來的十八分鐘 , 我會盡我所能 , 來描述粒子物理的美麗 。
it turns out there's a lot we can learn from coral .	事實證明 , 我們可以從珊瑚身上學到很多 。
coral is a very beautiful and unusual animal .	珊瑚是非常美麗且不尋常的動物 。
each coral head consists of thousand of individual polyps .	每個珊瑚頭部是由數千個個個體的聚合物所組成 。
these polyps are continually budding and branching into genetically identical neighbors .	這些聚合物不斷地擴散到基因相同的鄰居身上 。
if we imagine this to be a hyperintelligent coral , we can single out an individual and ask him a reasonable question .	如果我們想像這是一個超級聰明的珊瑚 , 我們可以單獨獨獨獨立 , 問他一個很合理的問題 。
we can ask how exactly he got to be in this particular location compared to his neighbors if it was just chance , or destiny , or what ?	我們可以問他在這個特定位置的位置 , 與他的鄰居相比 , 或命運 , 或如何 ?
now , after admonishing us for turning the temperature up too high , he would tell us that our question was completely stupid .	在把溫度升到太高之後 , 他會告訴我們 , 我們的問題完全是愚蠢的 。
these corals can be quite kind of mean , you see , and i have surfing scars to prove that .	這些珊瑚的意思是 , 你看 , 我有衝浪疤可以證明這一點 。
but this polyp would continue and tell us that his neighbors were quite clearly identical copies of him .	但這個聚會會會繼續告訴我們 , 他的鄰居非常明顯地對他有同感 。
that he was in all these other locations as well , but experiencing them as separate individuals .	他也處於其他地方 , 但也把他們和個體分開 。
for a coral , branching into different copies is the most natural thing in the world .	對珊瑚而言 , 分散到不同的複製品是世界上最自然的東西 。
unlike us , a hyperintelligent coral would be uniquely prepared to understand quantum mechanics .	與我們不同 , 超級智慧的珊瑚會特別準備好要了解量子力學 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics very accurately describes how our universe works .	量子力學的數學非常準確地描述我們的宇宙如何運作 。
and it tells us our reality is continually branching into different possibilities , just like a coral .	它告訴我們 , 我們的現實持續地擴散到不同的可能性 , 就像珊瑚一樣 。
it's a weird thing for us humans to wrap our minds around , since we only ever get to experience one possibility .	對我們人類來說 , 這是一件很奇怪的事 , 因為我們只能體驗一個可能性 。
this quantum weirdness was first described by erwin schrödinger and his cat .	這種量子奇怪的現象首先是艾爾文•薛丁格和他的貓的描述 。
the cat likes this version better .	貓喜歡這個版本 。
in this setup , schrödinger is in a box with a radioactive sample that , by the laws of quantum mechanics , branches into a state in which it is radiated and a state in which it is not .	在這個設定中 , 薛丁格在一個盒子裡 , 一個放射性樣本 , 由量子力學定律 , 分裂成一個狀態 , 它是放射性和一個狀態 , 它不是 。
in the branch in which the sample radiates , it sets off a trigger that releases poison and schrödinger is dead .	在樣本放射線中 , 它會產生一種觸發 , 釋放毒藥和薛丁格的觸發 。
but in the other branch of reality , he remains alive .	但在現實中 , 他仍然活著 。
these realities are experienced separately by each individual .	每個人的真實體驗都不同 。
as far as either can tell , the other one doesn't exist .	無論如何 , 另一個也不存在 。
this seems weird to us , because each of us only experiences an individual existence , and we don't get to see other branches .	這對我們來說是很奇怪的 , 因為我們每個人都經歷了個人的存在 , 而我們無法看見其他的分支 。
it's as if each of us , like schrödinger here , are a kind of coral branching into different possibilities .	就好像我們每一個人 , 像schordinger一樣 , 都是一種珊瑚在不同的可能性中分支 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics tells us this is how the world works at tiny scales .	量子力學的數學告訴我們 , 世界在小尺度上是如何運作的 。
it can be summed up in a single sentence: everything that can happen , does .	它可以在單一句子中總結起來:所有可能發生的事 , 都可以 。
but this does not mean everything happens .	但這並不意味著一切都發生了 。
the rest of physics is about describing what can happen and what can't .	物理的其他部分是要描述可能發生什麼事 , 以及什麼不能 。
what physics tells us is that everything comes down to geometry and the interactions of elementary particles .	物理學告訴我們 , 所有東西都來到幾何和基本粒子的互動 。
and things can happen only if these interactions are perfectly balanced .	事情才有可能發生 , 即使這些互動是完全平衡的 。
now i'll go ahead and describe how we know about these particles , what they are and how this balance works .	現在 , 我先來描述一下我們對這些粒子的認識 , 它們是什麼 , 以及這個平衡是如何運作的 。
in this machine , a beam of protons and antiprotons are accelerated to near the speed of light and brought together in a collision , producing a burst of pure energy .	在這台機器中 , 質子和反質子的光速加速到近光速的近端 , 融合在一起 , 產生出純粹能量的爆炸 。
this energy is immediately converted into a spray of subatomic particles , with detectors and computers used to figure out their properties .	這種能量會立刻轉換成海底粒子的噴霧 , 探測器和電腦以前用來找出它們的特性 。
this enormous machine the large hadron collider at cern in geneva has a circumference of 17 miles and , when it's operating , draws five times as much power as the city of monterey .	這台巨大的機器 , 位於日內瓦的大型強子對撞機 , 有17英哩的圓形 , 當它在運作時 , 引發了五倍的力量 , 就像蒙特里的城市一樣 。
we can't predict specifically what particles will be produced in any individual collision .	我們無法準確預測哪些粒子會在任何個體碰撞中產生什麼 。
quantum mechanics tells us all possibilities are realized .	量子力學告訴我們所有可能性都被發現 。
but physics does tell us what particles can be produced .	但物理學告訴我們 , 粒子能產生什麼 。
these particles must have just as much mass and energy as is carried in by the proton and antiproton .	這些粒子的質量和能量相同於質子和反質子所攜帶的能量 。
any particles more massive than this energy limit aren't produced , and remain invisible to us .	任何粒子都比這種能量限制更大 , 且對我們來說仍然是隱形的 。
this is why this new particle accelerator is so exciting .	這就是為什麼新粒子加速器如此令人興奮 。
it's going to push this energy limit seven times beyond what's ever been done before , so we're going to get to see some new particles very soon .	它將超越前所未有的能量限制七倍之外所以我們會很快地看到一些新的粒子
but before talking about what we might see , let me describe the particles we already know of .	但在談我們可能看到的之前 , 讓我先描述我們已經知道的粒子 。
there's a whole zoo of subatomic particles .	有一系列的亞原子粒子 。
most of us are familiar with electrons .	我們大部分人都很熟悉電子 。
a lot of people in this room make a good living pushing them around .	在這間房間裡的許多人 , 使得他們生活得更好 。
but the electron also has a neutral partner called the neutrino , with no electric charge and a very tiny mass .	但電子也有一個中立的夥伴 , 叫做中子 , 沒有電荷和一個非常小的質量 。
in contrast , the upanddown quarks have very large masses , and combine in threes to make the protons and neutrons inside atoms .	相較之下 , 上下的夸克有很大的質量 , 三分之三 , 將質子和中子結合在一起 , 使原子在原子裡 。
all of these matter particles come in left and righthanded varieties , and have antiparticle partners that carry opposite charges .	所有這些粒子都在左邊和右邊的品種 , 有反粒子的伴侶 , 帶著相反的載荷 。
these familiar particles also have less familiar second and third generations , which have the same charges as the first but have much higher masses .	這些熟悉的粒子也較不熟悉的第二代和第三代 , 相同的載荷是第一代 , 但質量較高 。
these matter particles all interact with the various force particles .	這些粒子都與各種力量相互作用 。
the electromagnetic force interacts with electrically charged matter via particles called photons .	電磁力會互相作用 , 通過所謂的光子粒子 , 產生電磁力 。
there is also a very weak force called , rather unimaginatively , the weak force , that interacts only with lefthanded matter .	還有一個非常弱的力量 , 非常不想像力 , 弱的力量 , 只有左撇子的物質相互作用 。
the strong force acts between quarks which carry a different kind of charge , called color charge , and come in three different varieties: red , green and blue .	夸克之間的強力作用有著不同的載荷 , 叫做顏色載荷 , 再來三種不同的品種:紅、綠和藍 。
you can blame murray gellmann for these names they're his fault .	你可以怪罪murraygellmann給這些名字 , 這是他的錯 。
finally , there's the force of gravity , which interacts with matter via its mass and spin .	最後 , 引力是引力 , 與物質交互作用 , 透過它的質量和旋轉 。
the most important thing to understand here is that there's a different kind of charge associated with each of these forces .	最重要的是 , 每一股力量都有不同的載荷 。
these four different forces interact with matter according to the corresponding charges that each particle has .	這四種不同的力量 , 根據每個粒子都有的相應載荷 。
a particle that hasn't been seen yet , but we're pretty sure exists , is the higgs particle , which gives masses to all these other particles .	一個還沒見過的粒子但我們很確定是希格斯粒子這使得其他粒子的質量
the main purpose of the large hadron collider is to see this higgs particle , and we're almost certain it will .	大型強子對撞機的主要目的就是看到希格斯粒子 , 我們幾乎可以確定它會發生 。
but the greatest mystery is what else we might see .	但最神秘的是我們可能看到的 。
and i'm going to show you one beautiful possibility towards the end of this talk .	我要給你們看一段美麗的可能性 , 來到這場演說的結束 。
now , if we count up all these different particles using their various spins and charges , there are 226 .	如果我們用不同的旋轉和載荷來計算這些不同的粒子 , 有226個粒子 。
that's a lot of particles to keep track of .	這是很多粒子用來追蹤的 。
and it seems strange that nature would have so many elementary particles .	看起來很奇怪 , 大自然會有這麼多元的粒子 。
but if we plot them out according to their charges , some beautiful patterns emerge .	但如果我們根據他們的指控 , 加上一些美麗的圖案 , 就會出現了 。
the most familiar charge is electric charge .	最熟悉的電荷是電荷 。
electrons have an electric charge , a negative one , and quarks have electric charges in thirds .	電子有電荷 , 負電荷 , 夸克有三分之一的電荷 。
so when two up quarks and a down quark are combined to make a proton , it has a total electric charge of plus one .	所以當兩個夸克和一個夸克結合成一個質子 , 它有完全的電荷 。
these particles also have antiparticles , which have opposite charges .	這些粒子也有反粒子 , 有相反的載荷 。
now , it turns out the electric charge is actually a combination of two other charges: hypercharge and weak charge .	結果發現 , 電荷其實是另外兩個載荷的組合:超電荷和弱荷 。
if we spread out the hypercharge and weak charge and plot the charges of particles in this twodimensional charge space , the electric charge is where these particles sit along the vertical direction .	如果我們把超電荷和弱電荷分散出來 , 將粒子的載荷放在這兩維電荷空間中 , 電荷是這些粒子在垂直方向附近的位置 。
the electromagnetic and weak forces interact with matter according to their hypercharge and weak charge , which make this pattern .	電磁力和弱力會根據高電荷和弱電荷相互作用 , 產生這種模式 。
this is called the unified electroweak model , and it was put together back in 1967 .	這叫做 「 統一的電擊模型 」 , 它在1967年被放回來 。
the reason most of us are only familiar with electric charge and not both of these is because of the higgs particle .	我們之所以很熟悉 , 是因為希格斯粒子 。
the higgs , over here on the left , has a large mass and breaks the symmetry of this electroweak pattern .	左邊的希格斯有很大的質量 , 打破了這個選舉模式的對稱性 。
it makes the weak force very weak by giving the weak particles a large mass .	它會讓弱力變弱 , 使弱粒子變弱 , 使得弱粒子變大 。
since this massive higgs sits along the horizontal direction in this diagram , the photons of electromagnetism remain massless and interact with electric charge along the vertical direction in this charge space .	自從這張圖中 , 大量的希格斯會沿著水平方向 , 電磁共振成像的光子仍然很大 , 在這個載荷空間中的垂直方向相互作用 。
so the electromagnetic and weak forces are described by this pattern of particle charges in twodimensional space .	所以電磁力和弱力被二維空間中的粒子載荷所描述的模式 。
we can include the strong force by spreading out its two charge directions and plotting the charges of the force particles in quarks along these directions .	我們可以把強力的力量分散出兩個載荷的方向並將引導電粒子的載荷放在這些方向上
the charges of all known particles can be plotted in a fourdimensional charge space , and projected down to two dimensions like this so we can see them .	所有已知粒子的載荷都可以在四度載荷空間中繪製 , 並投射到兩度空間 , 這樣我們就能看見它們 。
whenever particles interact , nature keeps things in a perfect balance along all four of these charge directions .	每當粒子互動時 , 大自然就會沿著四個載荷方向保持完美的平衡 。
if a particle and an antiparticle collide , it creates a burst of energy and a total charge of zero in all four charge directions .	如果粒子和反粒子碰撞 , 它會產生能量的破裂 , 總載四個電荷方向的零 。
at this point , anything can be created as long as it has the same energy and maintains a total charge of zero .	在這一刻 , 任何東西都可以被創造出來 , 只要它有相同的能量 , 維持一個完全零的載荷 。
for example , this weak force particle and its antiparticle can be created in a collision .	例如 , 這種弱力粒子和反粒子可以在碰撞中產生 。
in further interactions , the charges must always balance .	在更進一步的互動中 , 控訴一定要平衡 。
one of the weak particles could decay into an electron and an antineutrino , and these three still add to zero total charge .	其中一個弱的粒子可以腐化成電子和反中子 , 這三種粒子仍然加上零 ,
nature always keeps a perfect balance .	大自然總是保持完美的平衡 。
so these patterns of charges are not just pretty .	所以這些載荷的模式並不很漂亮 。
they tell us what interactions are allowed to happen .	他們告訴我們 , 什麼互動允許發生 。
and we can rotate this charge space in four dimensions to get a better look at the strong interaction , which has this nice hexagonal symmetry .	我們可以在四度空間中旋轉這個載荷空間 , 來更好地觀察這個強大的互動 , 它有這種美妙的六角形對稱性 。
in a strong interaction , a strong force particle , such as this one , interacts with a colored quark , such as this green one , to give a quark with a different color charge this red one .	在強烈的互動中 , 強力的粒子 , 例如這一個 , 和有色的夸克互動 , 例如這個綠色的夸克 , 用不同的色荷來充當這個紅色 。
and strong interactions are happening millions of times each second in every atom of our bodies , holding the atomic nuclei together .	而強烈的互動每秒發生在我們身體的每一個原子中 , 每秒鐘都在發生數百萬次 , 把原子核放在一起 。
but these four charges corresponding to three forces are not the end of the story .	但這四個載荷相對應到三種力 , 並不是故事的終點 。
we can also include two more charges corresponding to the gravitational force .	我們還可以將兩種載荷給引力 。
when we include these , each matter particle has two different spin charges , spinup and spindown .	當我們將這些物質結合在一起 , 每個粒子都有兩個不同的旋轉載荷、旋轉和旋轉 。
so they all split , and give a nice pattern in sixdimensional charge space .	所以他們都分開 , 在六度載荷空間中提供一個好的圖案 。
we can rotate this pattern in six dimensions , and see that it's quite pretty .	我們可以在六維空間中旋轉這個模式 , 看看它是很漂亮的 。
right now , this pattern matches our best current knowledge of how nature is built at the tiny scales of these elementary particles .	此時此刻 , 這種模式符合了我們目前對大自然的知識 , 以這些基本粒子的微小規模建造 。
this is what we know for certain .	這是我們確定的 。
some of these particles are at the very limit of what we've been able to reach with experiments .	有些粒子是極限的 , 我們能用實驗來接觸到的 。
from this pattern , we already know the particle physics of these tiny scales . the way the universe works with these tiny scales is very beautiful .	從這個模式中 , 我們已經知道這些微小的物理學 。 宇宙與這些微小的尺度是非常美麗的 。
but now i'm going to discuss some new and old ideas about things we don't know yet .	但現在我要討論一些我們還不知道的新想法 。
we want to expand this pattern using mathematics alone , and see if we can get our hands on the whole enchilada .	我們想單獨用數學來拓展這個模式 , 看看我們能不能把我們的手放在整個安達拉達州 。
we want to find all the particles and forces that make a complete picture of our universe .	我們想找到所有的粒子和力量 , 讓宇宙成為完整的圖片 。
and we want to use this picture to predict new particles that we'll see when experiments reach higher energies .	我們想用這張照片來預測我們將看到的新粒子 , 當實驗達到更高的能量時 。
so there's an old idea in particle physics that this known pattern of charges , which is not very symmetric , could emerge from a more perfect pattern that gets broken similar to how the higgs particle breaks the electroweak pattern to give electromagnetism .	所以 , 在粒子物理學中有個古老的想法 , 這種已知的電荷模式 , 不對稱 , 可以從更完美的模式中出現 , 希格斯粒子會突破電流模式 , 以提供電磁性 。
in order to do this , we need to introduce new forces with new charge directions .	為了做到這一點 , 我們需要引入新的載荷方向 。
when we introduce a new direction , we get to guess what charges the particles have along this direction , and then we can rotate it in with the others .	當我們介紹一個新的方向 , 我們就能猜測粒子在這個方向上載電荷 , 然後我們可以把粒子轉換成另一個方向 。
if we guess wisely , we can construct the standard charges in six charge dimensions as a broken symmetry of this more perfect pattern in seven charge dimensions .	如果我們很明智地猜測 , 我們就能建構標準載荷的六度空間 , 作為一個破碎的對稱性 , 在七度空間中 , 一個完美的圖案 。
this particular choice corresponds to a grand unified theory introduced by pati and salam in 1973 .	在1973年 , 這種特殊的選擇對應 , 由pati和salam所提出的理論 。
when we look at this new unified pattern , we can see a couple of gaps where particles seem to be missing .	當我們看到這個新統一的模式 , 我們可以看到一些缺陷 , 粒子似乎缺少了 。
this is the way theories of unification work .	這是統一理論的運作方式 。
a physicist looks for larger , more symmetric patterns that include the established pattern as a subset .	物理學家會尋找更大、更對稱的模式 , 包括建立模式的基礎 。
the larger pattern allows us to predict the existence of particles that have never been seen .	更大的模式讓我們能夠預測從未見過的粒子存在 。
this unification model predicts the existence of these two new force particles , which should act a lot like the weak force , only weaker .	這種統一模型預測了這兩種新力粒子的存在 , 它應該很像弱力 , 只有弱力 。
now we can rotate this set of charges in seven dimensions and consider an odd fact about the matter particles: the second and third generations of matter have exactly the same charges in sixdimensional charge space as the first generation .	現在我們可以把這組載荷轉換成七度 , 並考慮一下關於物質粒子的奇怪事實:在六度載荷空間中的第二代和第三代物質有完全相同的載荷空間 。
these particles are not uniquely identified by their six charges .	這些粒子並非獨一無二的辨識出它們的六個載荷 。
they sit on top of one another in the standard charge space .	他們坐在標準載荷空間的另一端 。
however , if we work in eightdimensional charge space , then we can assign unique new charges to each particle .	然而 , 如果我們在八度載荷空間中工作 , 那麼 , 我們就能針對每一個粒子發出獨特的新載荷 。
then we can spin these in eight dimensions , and see what the whole pattern looks like .	接著 , 我們可以在八度內旋轉 , 看看整個圖案看起來是什麼樣子 。
here we can see the second and third generations of matter now related to the first generation by a symmetry called " triality . "	這裡我們可以看到第二代和第三代物質與第一代的對稱性有關 , 叫做 「 試驗性 」 。
this particular pattern of charges in eight dimensions is actually part of the most beautiful geometric structure in mathematics .	在八度空間中這種特殊的載荷模式實際上是數學中最漂亮的幾何結構之一 。
it's a pattern of the largest exceptional lie group , e8 .	這是最大例外的謊言群體的模式e8 。
this lie group is a smooth , curved shape with 248 dimensions .	這個謊言團體是一個平滑的曲線形狀有248度的形狀
each point in this pattern corresponds to a symmetry of this very complex and beautiful shape .	在這個模式中 , 每一點都對應到一個非常複雜且美麗的形狀 。
one small part of this e8 shape can be used to describe the curved spacetime of einstein's general relativity , explaining gravity .	這種e8形狀的一小部分可以用來描述愛因斯坦的廣義相對論 , 解釋重力 。
together with quantum mechanics , the geometry of this shape could describe everything about how the universe works at the tiniest scales .	加上量子力學 , 這種形狀的幾何圖形可以描述宇宙在最小的尺度上如何運作 。
the pattern of this shape living in eightdimensional charge space is exquisitely beautiful , and it summarizes thousands of possible interactions between these elementary particles , each of which is just a facet of this complicated shape .	這種形狀的形狀在八度載荷空間中是非常美麗的 , 它在這些基本粒子之間總結成千上萬的交互作用 , 每一個都只是一個複雜的形狀的面向 。
as we spin it , we can see many of the other intricate patterns contained in this one .	正如我們所旋轉的 , 我們可以看到許多其他複雜的圖案 , 包含在這一個圖案中 。
and with a particular rotation , we can look down through this pattern in eight dimensions along a symmetry axis and see all the particles at once .	帶著特定的旋轉 , 我們可以在八度空間沿著對稱軸向下看 , 同時看到所有粒子 。
it's a very beautiful object , and as with any unification , we can see some holes where new particles are required by this pattern .	它是一個非常美麗的物體 , 和任何統一物一樣 , 我們可以看到一些洞 , 新的粒子被這個模式所需要 。
there are 20 gaps where new particles should be , two of which have been filled by the patisalam particles .	新粒子應該有20個差距 , 其中兩個被派粒子填滿 。
from their location in this pattern , we know that these new particles should be scalar fields like the higgs particle , but have color charge and interact with the strong force .	從它們的位置來看 , 我們知道這些新的粒子應該像希格斯粒子一樣可怕的粒子 , 但有色荷力和強力的作用 。
filling in these new particles completes this pattern , giving us the full e8 .	在這些新的粒子中填滿了這個圖案 , 給予我們完整的e8 。
this e8 pattern has very deep mathematical roots .	這個e8模式有很深的數學根源 。
it's considered by many to be the most beautiful structure in mathematics .	被認為是數學中最漂亮的結構 。
it's a fantastic prospect that this object of great mathematical beauty could describe the truth of particle interactions at the smallest scales imaginable .	這是個神奇的前景 , 一個偉大的數學美麗物體可以描述粒子在最小的尺度相互作用的真相 。
and this idea that nature is described by mathematics is not at all new .	這種想法 , 大自然是由數學所描述的 , 完全不是全新的 。
in 1623 , galileo wrote this: " nature's grand book , which stands continually open to our gaze , is written in the language of mathematics .	在1623年 , 伽利略寫了這個: 「 大自然的孫子書 , 不斷地打開我們的視覺 , 寫在數學的語言中 。
its characters are triangles , circles and other geometrical figures , without which it is humanly impossible to understand a single word of it ; without these , one is wandering around in a dark labyrinth . "	它的角色是三角形 , 圓圈和其他幾何圖形 , 沒有人能理解它的單一字 ; 沒有這些字 , 一個在黑暗的迷宮周圍 。 」
i believe this to be true , and i've tried to follow galileo's guidance in describing the mathematics of particle physics using only triangles , circles and other geometrical figures .	我相信這是真的 , 我試著跟隨著伽利略的指引 , 描述粒子物理的數學數學 , 只用三角形、圓圈和其他幾何數字 。
of course , when other physicists and i actually work on this stuff , the mathematics can resemble a dark labyrinth .	當然 , 當其他物理學家和我真的在研究這個東西時 , 數學可以重新組成一個黑暗的迷宮 。
but it's reassuring that at the heart of this mathematics is pure , beautiful geometry .	但 , 值得知道 , 在數學的核心是純淨的 , 美麗的幾何 。
joined with quantum mechanics , this mathematics describes our universe as a growing e8 coral , with particles interacting at every location in all possible ways according to a beautiful pattern .	加入量子力學 , 這種數學描述了我們的宇宙 , 隨著長大的e8珊瑚 , 粒子在每個地方互動 , 根據一個美麗的圖案 , 所有可能的粒子 。
and as more of the pattern comes into view using new machines like the large hadron collider , we may be able to see whether nature uses this e8 pattern or a different one .	隨著圖案的觀點越來越多 , 用像大型強子對撞機 , 我們可能可以看見大自然是否使用這種e8型式或不同的形式 。
this process of discovery is a wonderful adventure to be involved in .	這項發現的過程 , 是一項很棒的冒險 。
if the lhc finds particles that fit this e8 pattern , that will be very , very cool .	如果lhc找到符合這個e8模式的粒子 , 那會是非常非常非常酷的 。
if the lhc finds new particles , but they don't fit this pattern well , that will be very interesting , but bad for this e8 theory .	如果lhc找到新的粒子 , 但它們不符合這個模式 , 那會非常有趣 , 但對這個e8理論來說是不好的 。
and , of course , bad for me personally .	當然 , 對我來說 , 不好 。
now how bad would that be ?	那會有多糟 ?
well , pretty bad .	嗯 , 很不好 。
but predicting how nature works is a very risky game .	但 , 預測大自然如何運作是非常危險的遊戲 。
this theory and others like it are long shots .	這個理論和其他類似的理論是很長的 。
one does a lot of hard work knowing that most of these ideas probably won't end up being true about nature .	一個人做了很多努力 , 知道大部分這些想法可能不會是對大自然的真理 。
that's what doing theoretical physics is like: there are a lot of wipeouts .	這就是理論物理學的樣子:有大量的野生動物 。
in this regard , new physics theories are a lot like startup companies .	在這個方面 , 新的物理理論很像新創公司 。
as with any large investment , it can be emotionally difficult to abandon a line of research when it isn't working out .	如同任何大投資一樣 , 可能會對一系列的研究感到非常困難 。
but in science , if something isn't working , you have to toss it out and try something else .	但在科學上 , 如果沒有用的話 , 你就得去試試別的 。
now , the only way to maintain sanity and achieve happiness in the midst of this uncertainty is to keep balance and perspective in life .	現在 , 要維持清潔和達成幸福的唯一方法就是維持平衡和生活的觀點 。
i've tried the best i can to live a balanced life .	我盡了最好的生存平衡生活 。
i try to balance my life equally between physics , love and surfing my own three charge directions .	我試著在物理、愛、衝浪我自己的三條載荷方向之間平衡我的生活 。
this way , even if the physics i work on comes to nothing , i still know i've lived a good life .	這樣 , 即使我所研究的物理學都沒有 , 我仍然知道我過著好的生活 。
and i try to live in beautiful places .	我試著生活在美麗的地方 。
for most of the past ten years i've lived on the island of maui , a very beautiful place .	過去十年來 , 我住在大麻島 , 一個非常美麗的地方 。
now it's one of the greatest mysteries in the universe to my parents how i managed to survive all that time without engaging in anything resembling fulltime employment .	宇宙中最偉大的謎團之一 , 是我父母 , 我如何能在沒有完整的職業中生存下來的時刻 。
i'm going to let you in on that secret .	我要讓你們看這個秘密 。
this was a view from my home office on maui .	這是我家的辦公室的照片 。
and you may have noticed that these beautiful views are similar , but in slightly different places .	你可能已經注意到這些美麗的觀點是相似的 , 但在稍微不同的地方 。
that's because this used to be my home and office on maui .	那是因為這曾經是我在梅伊的家和辦公室 。
i've chosen a very unusual life .	我選擇了非常不尋常的生活 。
but not worrying about rent allowed me to spend my time doing what i love .	但 , 不擔心租金讓我花時間做我所愛的事 。
living a nomadic existence has been hard at times , but it's allowed me to live in beautiful places and keep a balance in my life that i've been happy with .	活著的遊牧存在很艱辛 , 但它讓我能活在美麗的地方 , 保持平衡 , 我一生都很快樂 。
it allows me to spend a lot of my time hanging out with hyperintelligent coral .	我可以花很多時間和超級聰明的珊瑚在一起 。
but i also greatly enjoy the company of hyperintelligent people .	但我也很享受超級智慧的人的公司 。
so i'm very happy to have been invited here to ted .	我很高興被邀請來ted 。
chris anderson: i probably understood two percent of that , but i still absolutely loved it . so i'm going to sound dumb .	克里斯•安德森:我大概了解了百分之二 , 但我仍然很愛它 。 所以我要聽起來很蠢 。
your theory of everything garrett lisi: i'm used to coral .	你的所有東西的理論:我習慣了珊瑚 。
ca: that's right . the reason it's got a few people at least excited is because , if you're right , it brings gravity and quantum theory together .	克里斯:沒錯 。 讓幾個人至少感到興奮是因為 , 如果你是對的 , 它會把重力和量子理論結合在一起 。
so are you saying that we should think of the universe , at its heart that the smallest things that there are , are somehow an e8 object of possibility ?	所以 , 你是說 , 我們應該去思考宇宙 , 最小的事物 , 無論何種可能的e8物體 ?
i mean , is there a scale to it , at the smallest scale , or . . . ?	我的意思是 , 在最小的尺度上 , 是否有規模 ?
gl: well , right now the pattern i showed you that corresponds to what we know about elementary particle physics that already corresponds to a very beautiful shape .	格林:嗯 , 現在我給你們看的圖案 , 是對我們所知的基本粒子物理學已經對應到一個非常漂亮的形狀 。
and that's the one that i said we knew for certain .	這就是我所說的 , 我們肯定知道 。
and that shape has remarkable similarities and the way it fits into this e8 pattern could be the rest of the picture .	這種形狀有很大的相似性和它融入這個e8的圖案中 , 可能是其餘的圖片 。
and these patterns of points that i've shown for you actually represent symmetries of this highdimensional object that would be warping and moving and dancing over the space time that we experience .	我向各位展示的這些圖案 , 其實代表著這種高維的物體的對稱性 , 會被扭曲、移動和跳舞在我們所經歷的時空中 。
and that would be what explains all these elementary particles that we see .	這就解釋了我們所看到的所有元素粒子 。
ca: but a string theorist , as i understand it , explains electrons in terms of much smaller strings vibrating i know you don't like string theory vibrating inside it .	克:但弦理論學家 , 如我所知 , 用較小的弦弦來解釋電子 , 我知道你不喜歡弦理論的震動 。
how should we think of an electron in relation to e8 ?	我們該如何看待電子與e8的關係呢 ?
gl: no , it would be one of the symmetries of this e8 shape .	格林:不 , 它是這個e8形狀的對稱之一 。
so what's happening is , as the shape is moving over spacetime , it's twisting . and the direction it's twisting as it moves is what particle we see . so it would be ca: the size of the e8 shape , how does that relate to the electron ?	所以 , 當形狀在空間中移動時 , 它是扭曲的 。 當它移動時 , 它的方向是粒子的 。 所以它會是克:e8形狀的大小 , 和電子是怎麼相連的 ?
i kind of feel like i need that for my picture .	我覺得我需要這張照片 。
is it bigger ? is it smaller ?	它更大嗎 ? 它更小嗎 ?
gl: well , as far as we know electrons are point particles , so this would be going down to the smallest possible scales .	格林:嗯 , 正如我們所知 , 電子是指定的粒子 , 所以它會降到最小的尺度 。
so the way these things are explained in quantum field theory is , all possibilities are expanding and developing at once .	所以 , 在量子場理論中 , 所有可能性都在擴張和發展中 。
and this is why i use the analogy to coral .	這就是為什麼我要用類比來做珊瑚 。
and in this way , the way that e8 comes in is it will be as a shape that's attached at each point in spacetime .	如此一來 , e8的出現方式是 , 每一刻都附著在空間的形狀 。
and , as i said , the way the shape twists the directional along which way the shape is twisting as it moves over this curved surface is what the elementary particles are , themselves .	正如我所說的 , 形狀扭曲了方向 , 形狀在轉動這曲線表面的形狀是基本粒子本身 。
so through quantum field theory , they manifest themselves as points and interact that way .	透過量子場理論 , 他們表現出自己是指點 , 以這種方式互動 。
i don't know if i'll be able to make this any clearer .	我不知道我能不能讓這個更清楚 。
ca: it doesn't really matter .	克里斯:這並不重要 。
it's evoking a kind of sense of wonder , and i certainly want to understand more of this .	它發揮了一種奇妙的感覺 , 我當然也想了解更多這一點 。
but thank you so much for coming . that was absolutely fascinating .	但 , 非常謝謝你來到這裡 , 這真是令人著迷的 。
the legendary chimpanzee researcher jane goodall talks about tacare and her other community projects , which help people in booming african towns live sidebyside with threatened animals .	傳奇的黑猩猩研究員珍•古巴爾談到計程車和其它社區計畫 , 協助在非洲大城的居住地 , 威脅動物 。
africa , animals , biodiversity , environment , global issues , pollution , primates , science	非洲、動物、生物多樣性、環境、全球議題、污染、靈長類、科學、科學 。
jane goodall helps humans and animals live together	珍•古柯鹼能協助人類和動物一起生活 。
good afternoon , good evening , whatever .	好的下午 , 晚安 , 等等 。
we can go , jambo , guten abend , bonsoir , but we can also ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh .	我們可以去 , 詹姆士 , 吉姆博 , 邦索爾 , 但我們也可以ooh , oh , oh , oh , oh , oh , oh , oh , oh , oh , oh 。
that is the call that chimpanzees make before they go to sleep in the evening .	這是黑猩猩在晚上睡覺之前所謂的 「 黑猩猩 」 。
you hear it going from one side of the valley to the other , from one group of nests to the next .	你聽到它從山谷的一邊到另一邊 , 從一群巢穴到下一個 。
and i want to pick up with my talk this evening from where zeray left off yesterday .	今天晚上我要拿起我的演說 , 今天晚上 , 零光是昨天離開的地方 。
he was talking about this amazing , threeyearold australopithecine child , selam .	他在談論這個驚人、三歲的澳洲兒童 , 塞拉姆 。
and we've also been hearing about the history , the family tree , of mankind through dna genetic profiling .	我們也聽說過歷史、家族樹 , 透過dna基因獲利 , 人類的基因樹 。
and it was a paleontologist , the late louis leakey , who actually set me on the path for studying chimpanzees .	這位是一位古生物學家 , 最近的路易斯路克西 , 他讓我走上研究黑猩猩的路徑 。
and it was pretty extraordinary , way back then .	當時是非常不凡的 。
it's kind of commonplace now , but his argument was because he'd been searching for the fossilized remains of early humans in africa .	現在有點常見 , 但他的論點是 , 因為他一直在尋找非洲早期人類的化石 。
and you can tell an awful lot about what those beings looked like from the fossils , from the shape of the muscle attachments , something about the way they lived from the various artifacts found with them .	你可以從化石中分辨出非常多人的樣子 , 從肌肉附著的形狀 , 和他們生活的方式有關 。
but what about how they behaved ? that's what he wanted to know .	但它們的行為呢 ? 這是他想要知道的 。
and of course , behavior doesn't fossilize .	當然 , 行為不會化石 。
he argued and it's now a fairly common theory that if we found behavior patterns similar or the same in our closest living relatives , the great apes , and humans today , then maybe those behaviors were present in the apelike , humanlike ancestor some seven million years ago .	他主張 , 現在是一個相當常見的理論 , 如果我們在我們最接近的活體親戚、大猩猩 , 和人類的行為 , 那麼也許這些行為在七百萬年前就出現了 , 人類的祖先 。
and therefore , perhaps we had brought those characteristics with us from that ancient , ancient past .	因此 , 或許我們把這些特徵從古老、古老的過去帶到我們身上 。
well , if you look in textbooks today that deal with human evolution , you very often find people speculating about how early humans may have behaved , based on the behavior of chimpanzees .	嗯 , 今天如果你看教科書處理人類演化 , 你通常會發現人們在猜測早期人類的行為 , 根據黑猩猩的行為來推測 。
they are more like us than any other living creature , and we've heard about that during this ted conference .	它們比任何生物更像我們 , 在ted研討會中我們也聽說過 。
so it remains for me to comment on the ways in which chimpanzees are so like us , in certain aspects of their behavior .	所以 , 我還是要在這些黑猩猩的行為中留下評論 , 在某些方面 , 黑猩猩的行為 。
every chimpanzee has his or her own personality .	每個黑猩猩都有自己的個性 。
of course , i gave them names . they can live to be 60 years or more , although we think most of them probably don't make it to 60 in the wild .	當然 , 我給他們名字 。 他們可以活到六十年 , 儘管我們認為大多數人可能不會在野外生存到六十歲 。
mr . wurzel . the female has her first baby when she's 11 or 12 .	華茲先生 , 女生在十一或十二歲時 , 她的第一個嬰兒 。
thereafter , she has one baby only every five or six years , a long period of childhood dependency when the child is nursing , sleeping with the mother at night , and riding on her back .	在那裡 , 她每五到六年就只有一個嬰兒 , 一個長期的童年依賴於童年 , 孩子在晚上和母親同床睡覺 , 背著她 。
and we believe that this long period of childhood is important for chimpanzees , just as it is for us , in relation to learning .	我們相信這段長期的童年對黑猩猩很重要 , 就如同我們一樣 , 和學習有關 。
as the brain becomes ever more complex during evolution in different forms of animals , so we find that learning plays an ever more important role in an individual's life history .	隨著大腦在不同的動物演化過程中變得更複雜 , 所以我們發現 , 學習在個人的生命歷史中扮演著更重要的角色 。
and young chimpanzees spend a lot of time watching what their elders do .	年輕的黑猩猩花了很多時間觀看他們的長輩所做的事 。
we know now that they're capable of imitating behaviors that they see .	我們現在知道他們有能力模仿他們所看到的行為 。
and we believe that it's in this way that the different toolusing behaviors that have now been seen in all the different chimpanzee populations studied in africa how these are passed from one generation to the next , through observation , imitation and practice , so that we can describe these toolusing behaviors as primitive culture .	我們相信 , 這種方式是不同的工具行為 , 現在已經在所有不同黑猩猩的族群中 , 研究這些族群是如何通過一個世代傳到下一個世代 , 透過觀察、模仿和練習 , 來形容這些工具的行為是原始的文化 。
chimpanzees don't have a spoken language . we've talked about that .	黑猩猩沒有口語的語言 。 我們已經談到這一點 。
they do have a very rich repertoire of postures and gestures , many of which are similar , or even identical , to ours and formed in the same context . greeting chimpanzees embracing .	牠們的確有非常豐富的姿勢和姿勢 , 很多都很相似 , 甚至是相同的 , 在同一個情境中形成 。 希臘的黑猩猩會擁抱 。
they also kiss , hold hands , pat one another on the back .	他們也親吻雙手 , 雙手 , 把另一張貼在背上 。
and they swagger and they throw rocks .	他們會變汗 , 他們會丟石頭 。
in chimpanzee society , we find many , many examples of compassion , precursors to love and true altruism .	在黑猩猩的社會中 , 我們發現許多關於同情心的例子 , 都是愛和真正的利他主義 。
unfortunately , they , like us , have a dark side to their nature .	不幸的是 , 他們和我們一樣 , 他們有著黑暗的一面 。
they're capable of extreme brutality , even a kind of primitive war .	它們有能力極度殘酷 , 甚至是一種原始的戰爭 。
and these really aggressive behaviors , for the most part , are directed against individuals of the neighboring social group .	而這些非常積極的行為 , 大部分的部分 , 都是對抗鄰近社會群體的個體 。
they are very territorially aggressive .	它們是非常積極的 。
chimpanzees , i believe , more than any other living creature , have helped us to understand that , after all , there is no sharp line between humans and the rest of the animal kingdom .	黑猩猩 , 我相信 , 比任何其他生物 , 都協助我們了解 , 畢竟 , 人類和其他動物王國之間沒有鯊魚界線 。
it's a very blurry line , and it's getting more blurry all the time as we make even more observations .	這是一條非常模糊的線 , 隨著我們觀察更加模糊 。
the study that i began in 1960 is still continuing to this day .	我從1960年開始的這項研究至今仍持續著 。
and these chimpanzees , living their complex social lives in the wild , have helped more than anything else to make us realize we are part of , and not separated from , the amazing animals with whom we share the planet .	而這些黑猩猩 , 生活在野外的複雜社交生活 , 幫助我們了解到我們是其中的一部分 , 而非分離 , 和我們共享這個星球的神奇動物 。
so it's pretty sad to find that chimpanzees , like so many other creatures around the world , are losing their habitats .	所以 , 很難找到黑猩猩 , 就像世界上許多其他生物一樣 , 失去了牠們的棲息地 。
this is just one photograph from the air , and it shows you the forested highlands of gombe .	這只是從空氣中拍攝的一張照片 , 它向你展示了戈姆貝的森林高地 。
and it was when i flew over the whole area , about 16 years ago , and realized that outside the park , this forest , which in 1960 had stretched almost unbroken along the eastern shore of lake tanganyika , which is where the tiny , 30squaremile gombe national park lies , that a question came to my mind .	那時我在整個地區飛越 , 大約16年前 , 了解到在公園之外 , 這個森林 , 在1960年間 , 幾乎沒有在湖泊的海岸上 , 那裡是小小的 , 三十平方公園 , 我心中有個問題 。
" how can we even try to save these famous chimpanzees , when the people living around the national park are struggling to survive ? "	「 我們要如何試著拯救這些有名的黑猩猩 , 當住在全國公園附近的人掙扎著生存 ? 」
more people are living there than the land could possibly support .	更多人住在那裡 , 超過土地可能支持 。
the numbers increased by refugees pouring in from burundi and over the lake from congo .	難民數目增加 , 來自於緬甸 , 以及來自剛果湖泊的湖泊 。
and very poor people they couldn't afford to buy food from elsewhere .	貧窮的人 , 他們負擔不起從其他地方買食物 。
this led to a program , which we call tacare .	這個計畫導致了我們稱之為 「 計程車 」 。
it's a very holistic way of improving the lives of the people living in the villages around the park .	這是一種非常全面的方式 , 來改善生活在公園周圍的村民的生活 。
it started small with 12 villages . it's now in 24 .	它從12個村落開始 , 現在是24個村落 。
there isn't time to go into it , but it's including things like tree nurseries , methods of farming most suitable to this now very degraded , almost desertlike land up in these mountains .	沒有時間可以進去 , 但它包含了一些東西 , 像是樹木護士 , 目前最適合農耕的方法 , 幾乎像沙漠一樣落在這些山中 。
ways of controlling , preventing soil erosion .	控制的方式 , 預防土壤的侵蝕 。
ways of reclaiming overused farmland , so that within two years they can again be productive .	重建過度使用的農地 , 這樣兩年後他們就能再次有生產力 。
working to help the villagers obtain fresh water from wells .	為了幫助村民從井中取得淡水 。
perhaps build some schoolrooms .	也許可以建立一些教室 。
most important of all , i believe , is working with small groups of women , providing them with opportunities for microcredit loans .	最重要的是 , 我相信 , 與一小群婦女合作 , 提供他們機會給微型貸款 。
and we've got , as is the case around the world , about 95 percent of all loans returned .	我們已經知道 , 世界上有95%的貸款回來了 。
empowering women , working with education , providing scholarships for girls so they can finish secondary school , in the clear understanding that , all around the world , as women's education improves , family size drops .	賦權女性 , 和教育合作 , 為女孩提供獎學金 , 這樣她們才能完成中學 , 清楚知道 , 全世界的女性教育改善 , 家庭大小的輟學 。
we provide information about family planning and about hiv/aids .	我們提供家庭規劃和愛滋病的資訊 。
and as a result of this program , something's happening for conservation .	由於這個計畫 , 關於保育 , 發生了什麼事 。
what's happening for conservation is that the farmers living in these 24 villages , instead of looking on us as a bunch of white people coming to study a whole bunch of monkeys and by the way , many of the staff are now tanzanian but when we began the tacare program , it was a tanzanian team going into the villages .	關於保育的狀況是 , 農夫住在這24個村落 , 而不是把我們當成一群白人來研究一群猴子 , 順道一提 , 許多員工現在是坦尚尼亞人 , 但當我們開始計劃時 , 坦尚尼亞團隊進入村落 。
it was a tanzanian team talking to the villagers , asking what they were interested in .	那是一個坦尚尼亞團隊和村民談話 , 問他們對什麼感興趣 。
were they interested in conservation ? absolutely not .	他們對保育感興趣嗎 ? 絕對不是 。
they were interested in health ; they were interested in education .	他們對健康有興趣 , 他們對教育有興趣 。
and as time went on , and as their situation began to improve , they began to understand ever more about the need for conservation .	隨著時間持續下去 , 當他們的情況開始改善 , 他們開始對保育的需求越來越了解 。
they began to understand that as the upper levels of the hills were denuded of trees , so you've got this terrible soil erosion and mudslides .	他們開始了解 , 隨著山丘上升的層次被摧毀 , 所以你有了這種糟糕的土壤侵蝕和泥土 。
today , we are developing what we call the greater gombe ecosystem .	今天 , 我們正在發展我們所謂的 「 大黃金生態系統 」 。
this is an area way outside the national park , stretching out into all these very degraded lands .	這是個地方 , 在全國公園之外 , 延伸到這些非常乾燥的土地上 。
and as these villages have a better standard of life , they are actually agreeing to put between 10 percent and 20 percent of their land in the highlands aside , so that once again , as the trees grow back , the chimpanzees will have leafy corridors through which they can travel to interact as they must for genetic viability with other remnant groups outside the national park .	當這些村莊有更好的生命標準 , 他們其實同意在高地上10%到20%的土地 , 所以 , 同樣的 , 隨著樹木長回來 , 黑猩猩就會有葉子 , 牠們可以在國家公園外的遺傳能力互動 。
so tacare is a success .	所以 , 泰卡爾是成功的 。
we're replicating it in other parts of africa , around other wilderness areas which are faced with extreme population pressure .	我們在非洲的其他地方複製它 , 其他的荒野地區 , 正面臨著極端人口的壓力 。
the problems in africa , however , as we've been discussing for the whole of these first couple of days of ted , are major problems .	然而 , 非洲的問題 , 正如我們前幾天所討論的 , 都是大問題 。
there is a great deal of poverty .	有很大的貧窮 。
and when you get large numbers of people living in land that is not that fertile , particularly when you cut down trees , and you leave the soil open to the wind for erosion , as desperate populations cut down more and more trees , so that they can try and grow food for themselves and their families , what's going to happen ? something's got to give .	當你有大量的人住在陸地上那不是肥沃 , 尤其是當你砍樹時 , 你把土壤留在空氣中 , 如同絕望的族群砍下更多樹木 , 所以他們可以試著為自己和家人種食物 , 會發生什麼事 ? 一定要給予 。
and the other problems in not only africa , but the rest of the developing world and , indeed , everywhere what are we doing to our planet ?	而其他的問題不僅是非洲 , 還有其他開發中國家 , 的確 , 到處都是我們對地球所做的事 ?
you know , the famous scientist , e . o . wilson said that if every person on this planet attains the standard of living of the average european or american , we need three new planets .	你知道 , 知名的科學家e.wilson說如果地球上每一個人都能維持平均歐洲或美國人的平均壽命的標準我們需要三個新星球
today , they are saying four . but we don't have them . we've got one .	今天 , 他們說了四個 。 但我們沒有 。 我們有一顆 。
and what's happened ? i mean , the question here is , here we are , arguably the most intelligent being that's ever walked planet earth , with this extraordinary brain , capable of the kind of technology that is so well illustrated by these ted conferences , and yet we're destroying the only home we have .	發生了什麼事 ? 我的意思是 , 問題是 , 我們是最聰明的生物 , 最聰明的生物 , 有著非凡的大腦 , 可以用這些ted會議來描述的技術 , 但我們卻在摧毀我們唯一的家 。
the indigenous people around the world , before they made a major decision , used to sit around and ask themselves , " how does this decision affect our people seven generations ahead ? "	世界各地的原住民 , 在他們做出重大決定之前 , 以前會坐下來問自己: 「 這種決定會如何影響我們的七代人 ? 」
today , major decisions and i'm not particularly talking about africa here , but the developed world major decisions involving millions of dollars , and millions of people , are often based on , " how will this affect the next shareholders' meeting ? "	今天 , 主要的決定 , 我並不是在談論非洲 , 而是已開發國家的主要決策 , 數百萬人 , 通常是基於 「 下一個股東會議如何影響下一個股東會議 ? 」
and these decisions affect africa .	這些決定會影響非洲 。
as i began traveling around africa talking about the problems faced by chimpanzees and their vanishing forests , i realized more and more how so many of africa's problems could be laid at the door of previous colonial exploitation .	當我開始在非洲四處旅行時 , 談到黑猩猩和牠們消失的森林 , 我越來越了解到 , 非洲有多少問題可以在以前殖民地剝削 。
so i began traveling outside africa , talking in europe , talking in the united states , going to asia .	所以我開始在非洲外旅行 , 在歐洲 , 說話 , 在美國 , 要去亞洲 。
and everywhere there were these terrible problems .	到處都有這些可怕的問題 。
and you know the kind i'm talking about . i'm talking about pollution .	各位知道我在說什麼 , 我在談污染 。
the air that we breathe that often poisons us .	我們呼吸的空氣通常會毒害我們 。
the earth is poisoning our foods .	地球正在毒害我們的食物 。
the water water is perhaps one of the most crucial issues that we're going to face in this century and everywhere water is being polluted by agricultural , industrial and household chemicals that still are being sprayed around the world , seemingly with the inability to profit from past experience .	水源可能是我們這個世紀所面臨的最關鍵問題之一 , 每個地方的水都被農業、工業和家庭化學物質污染 , 仍然在全世界流通 , 看似無能為力 , 從過去經驗中獲利 。
the mangroves are being cut down ; the effects of things like the tsunami get worse .	紅樹林被砍掉了 ; 海嘯的影響更糟 。
we've talked about the soil erosion .	我們已經談到土壤侵蝕 。
we have the reckless burning of fossil fuels along with other greenhouse gasses , so called , leading to climate change .	我們有不幸的燃燒化石燃料 , 和其他溫室氣體一起 , 叫做 「 氣候變遷 」 。
finally , all around the world , people have begun to believe that there is something going on very wrong with our climate .	最後 , 世界各地 , 人們開始相信 , 我們的氣候非常錯誤 。
all around the world climates are mixed up .	全世界的氣候都是混合在一起的 。
and it's the poor people who are affected worse .	窮人受到影響更糟糕 。
it's africa that already is affected .	非洲已經受到影響 。
in many parts of subsaharan africa , the droughts are so much worse .	在撒哈拉以南非洲許多地區 , 乾旱更糟糕 。
and when the rain does come , it so often leads to flooding and added distress , and the cycle of poverty and hunger and disease .	當雨來臨時 , 通常會導致洪水 , 加上痛苦 , 貧窮和疾病的循環 。
and the numbers of people living in an area that the land cannot support , who are too poor to buy food , who can't move away because the whole land is degraded .	居住在一個地區 , 土地無法支援 , 他們太貧窮 , 無法購買食物 , 因為整片土地被降低 。
and so you get desertification creeping , creeping , creeping as the last of the trees are cut down .	所以你得到了沙漠化的危機 , 火化 , 當樹的最後一棵被砍掉時 , 你就會被砍掉 。
and this kind of thing is not just in africa . it's all over the world .	這種東西不只在非洲 , 全世界都在 。
so it wasn't surprising to me that as i was traveling around the world i met so many young people who seemed to have lost hope .	所以 , 我並不意外 , 當我在世界各地旅行時 , 我遇到這麼多年輕人似乎失去了希望 。
we seem to have lost wisdom , the wisdom of the indigenous people .	我們似乎失去了智慧 , 原住民的智慧 。
i asked a question . " why ? "	我問了一個問題: 「 為什麼 ? 」
well , do you think there could be some kind of disconnect between this extraordinarily clever brain , the kind of brain that the ted technologies exemplify , and the human heart ? talking about it in the nonscientific term , in terms of love and compassion . is there some disconnect ?	嗯 , 你認為 , 在這種非凡的聰明大腦中 , 可能有某種區別的大腦 , 像是ted技術的爆炸 , 人類的心 ? 以非科學的角度 , 以愛和同理心來談論它 。 是否有一些隔閡 ?
and these young people , when i talk to them , basically they were either depressed or apathetic , or bitter and angry . and they said more or less the same thing , " we feel this way because we feel you've compromised our future and there's nothing we can do about it . "	這些年輕人 , 當我和他們談話時 , 基本上他們都很沮喪、很生氣 。 他們說了更多或比較不一樣的東西: 「 我們有這種感覺 , 因為我們覺得自己已經妥協了我們的未來 , 沒有我們能做的事 。 」
we have compromised their future .	我們已經承諾了他們的未來 。
i've got three little grandchildren , and every time i look at them and i think how we've harmed this beautiful planet since i was their age , i feel this desperation .	我有三個小孫子 , 每當我看著他們時 , 我就會想 , 我們如何傷害這個美麗的星球 , 自我年紀以來 , 我感覺到這種絕望 。
and that led to this program we call roots and shoots , which began right here in tanzania and has now spread to 97 countries around the world .	這個計畫導致了我們稱之為根和芽 , 剛開始在坦尚尼亞這裡 , 現在散播到世界上97個國家 。
it's symbolic . roots make a firm foundation .	它是象徵性的 。 樹根建立了一間公司基金會 。
shoots seem tiny ; to reach the sun they can break through a brick wall .	射擊似乎很小 , 要抵達太陽 , 才能穿過磚牆 。
see the brick wall as all these problems we've inflicted on the planet , environmental and social . it's a message of hope .	把磚牆視為是所有我們在地球上遇到的問題 , 環保和社會的問題 , 都是希望的訊息 。
hundreds and thousands of young people around the world can break through and can make this a better world for all living things .	世界各地有成千上萬的年輕人可以打破 , 讓這個世界變得更好 。
the most important message of roots and shoots: every single one of us makes a difference , every single day .	最重要的訊息是根和芽 , 我們每個人每一天都能有所不同 。
we have a choice . every one of us in this room , we have a choice as to what kind of difference we want to make .	我們有選擇 。 在座的每個人 , 我們都有選擇 , 來決定我們想要做什麼樣的差異 。
the very poor have no choice . it's up to us to change things so that the poor have choice as well .	窮人沒有選擇 , 我們要改變事物 , 讓窮人也有選擇 。
the roots and shoots groups all choose three projects .	樹根和芽團體都選擇了三個計畫 。
it depends on how old they are , and which country , whether they're in a city or rural , as to what kinds of projects .	這取決於他們有多古老 , 以及哪個國家 , 不論他們在城市或鄉村 , 都取決於什麼樣的計畫 。
but basically , we have programs now from preschool right through university , with more and more adults starting their own roots and shoots groups .	但 , 基本上 , 我們現在有來自學齡前學院的計畫 , 越來越多的成年人開始自己的根和芽團體 。
and every group chooses , between them , three different kinds of project to make this a better world , recognizing that all these different problems are interconnected and impinge on each other .	每一組選舉 , 在他們之間 , 三個不同的項目 , 來讓這個更美好的世界 , 認知到所有這些不同的問題都是互相連結的 , 並互相阻礙 。
so one of their projects will be to help their own human community .	其中一個計畫是幫助他們自己的人類社群 。
and then , if they're able , they may raise money to help communities in other parts of the world .	然後 , 如果他們能做到 , 他們可能會募到錢來協助世界上其他地方的社區 。
one of their projects will be to help animals not just wildlife , domestic animals as well .	其中一項計畫是協助動物 , 不只是野生動物 , 家畜動物 。
and one of their projects will be to help the environment that we all share .	其中一個計畫是幫助我們共享的環境 。
and woven throughout all of this is a message of learning to live in peace and harmony within ourselves , in our families , in our communities , between nations , between cultures , between religions and between us and the natural world .	在這整個過程中 , 要傳達自我和平和和諧的訊息 , 在我們的家庭、我們的社區、國家、文化、宗教之間 , 和我們之間的宗教之間 。
we need the natural world . we cannot go on destroying it at the rate we are .	我們需要自然的世界 。 我們不能以我們的速度來摧毀它 。
we not do have more than this one planet .	我們的確沒有超過這個星球 。
just picking one or two of the projects right here in africa that the roots and shoots groups are doing , one or two projects only in tanzania , in uganda , kenya , south africa , congobrazzaville , sierra leone , cameroon and other groups . and as i say , it's in 97 countries around the world .	這裡有一到兩項計畫 , 非洲的根和芽團體正在進行 , 只有在坦尚尼亞、烏干達、肯亞、南非、剛果、獅子山共和國、喀麥隆和其他團體 。 如我所說 , 它是在世界上97個國家 。
of course , they're planting trees . they're growing organic vegetables .	當然 , 他們正在種樹 , 種有機蔬菜 。
they're working in the refugee camps , with chickens and selling the eggs for a little amount of money , or just using them to feed their families , and feeling a sense of pride and empowerment , because they're no longer helpless and depending on others with their vegetables and their chickens .	他們在難民營工作 , 用雞和雞把蛋賣掉 , 或用它們來餵飽他們的家人 , 並感受到驕傲和賦權 , 因為它們不再是無助的 , 依靠它們的蔬菜和雞 。
it's being used in uganda to give some psychological help to exchild soldiers .	它被用在烏干達 , 給予一些心理協助 , 讓士兵延伸 。
doing projects like this is bringing them out of themselves .	這樣做 , 將他們自己帶出去 。
once again , they're useful members of society .	再一次 , 他們是有用的社會成員 。
we have this program in prisons as well .	我們在監獄裡也有這個計畫 。
so , there's no time for more roots and shoots now .	所以 , 目前沒有更多根和芽的時刻 。
but oh , they're also working on hiv/aids .	但 , 喔 , 他們也在研究愛滋病 。
that's a very important component of roots and shoots , with older kids talking to younger ones .	那是根和芽的重要成因 , 年長的孩子和年輕的孩子談話 。
and unwanted pregnancies and things like that , which young people listen to better from other youth , rather than adults .	那些沒有預期的懷孕和類似的事情 , 年輕人會傾聽其他年輕人 , 而不是成年人 。
hope . that's the question i get asked as i'm going around the world: " jane , you've seen so many terrible things , you've seen your chimpanzees decrease in number from about one million , at the turn of the century , to no more than 150 , 000 now , and the same with so many other animals .	希望 。 這也是我在世界各地所面臨的問題: 「 珍 , 你看過這麼多可怕的事情 , 你看過你的黑猩猩 , 從一百萬分之一 , 到現在 , 沒有超過150 , 000隻 , 和許多其他動物一樣 。
forests disappearing , deserts where once there was forest .	森林消失了 , 一旦有森林 , 沙漠就在那裡 。
do you really have hope ? " well , yes .	你真的有希望嗎 ? 」 是的 。
you can't come to a conference like ted and not have hope , can you ?	你不能來像ted這樣的研討會 , 沒有希望 , 你能嗎 ?
and of course , there's hope . one is this amazing human brain .	當然 , 有希望 。 一個是令人驚嘆的人類大腦 。
and i mean , think of the technologies .	我的意思是 , 想想科技 。
and i've just been so thrilled , finally , to come to people talking about compost latrines .	我一直很興奮 , 最後 , 來到人們談到作曲線 。
it's one of my hobbyhorses .	這是我的嗜好之一 。
we just flush all this water down the lavatory , it's terrible .	我們就把這些水沖到水道下 , 很糟糕 。
and then talking about renewable energy desperately important .	接著 , 談到可再生能源極度重要 。
do we care about the planet for our children ?	我們是否關心孩子的星球 ?
how many of us have children or grandchildren , nieces , nephews ?	我們有多少人有孩子或孫子、姪子、姪子 ?
do we care about their future ?	我們是否在乎他們的未來 ?
and if we care about their future , we , as the elite around the world , we can do something about it . we can make choices as to how we live each day .	如果我們關心他們的未來 , 我們身為世界各地的菁英 , 我們就能做點什麼 。 我們可以選擇每天的生活方式 。
what we buy . what we wear .	我們買了什麼、穿什麼、穿什麼 。
and choose to make these choices with the question , how will this affect the environment around me ?	選擇用這些問題來做選擇 , 這會如何影響我周遭的環境 ?
how will it affect the life of my child when he or she grows up ?	當他或她長大後 , 會如何影響我的孩子 ?
or my grandchild , or whatever it is .	或我的孫子 , 或任何東西 。
so the human brain , coupled with the human heart , and we join hands around the world .	所以 , 人類的大腦 , 與人類的心相結合 , 我們加入了世界各地 。
and that's what ted is helping so well with , and google who help us , and esri are helping us with mapping in gombe national park .	ted的幫助很大 , google也幫助我們 , esri也幫助我們 , esri也幫助我們在gombe國家公園的地圖 。
all of these technologies we can use .	所有我們能使用的科技 。
now let's link them , and it's beginning to happen , isn't it ?	現在讓我們把它們連結起來 , 開始發生 , 不是嗎 ?
you've heard about it this afternoon . it's beginning to happen .	你們已經聽過這個下午 , 開始發生了 。
this change , this change . to see change that we must have if we care about the future .	這種改變 , 這種改變 。 看看如果我們關心未來 , 我們一定有的改變 。
and the next reason for hope nature is amazingly resilient .	希望大自然的下一個理由是驚人的恢復力 。
you can take an area that's absolutely destroyed , with time and perhaps some help it can regenerate .	你可以拿一個完全摧毀的區域 , 隨著時間 , 或許還有一些幫助可以再生 。
and an example is the tacare program .	一個例子是計程車計畫 。
i told you , where a seemingly dead tree stump if you stop hacking them for firewood , which you don't need to because you have wood lots , then in five years you can have a 30foot tree .	我告訴各位 , 看似死掉的樹木 , 如果你停止為消防栓 , 你不需要因為你有木材 , 五年內 , 就可以有三十英尺長的樹木 。
and animals , almost on the brink of extinction , can be given a second chance . that's my next book .	而動物 , 幾乎在滅絕的邊緣 , 可以得到第二次機會 。 這是我的下一本書 。
it's inspiring . and it brings me to my last category of hope , and we've heard about this so much in the last two days: this indomitable human spirit . this determination of people , the resilience of the human spirit , so that people who you would think would be battered by poverty , or disease , or whatever , can pull themselves up out of it , sometimes with a helping hand , and take their part in society , and take their part in changing the world .	它很有啟發性 。 它帶我到最後一個希望類別 , 我們在過去的兩天中聽到了這麼多關於這種不可避免的人類精神 , 人類精神的韌性 , 所以你認為會被貧窮或疾病所侵害的人 , 或者 , 不論如何 , 都可以把自己趕出去 , 有時 , 透過協助手 , 和社會的一部分 , 改變他們的世界 。
and just to think of one or two people out of africa who are just really inspiring .	想想非洲有一到兩個人 , 他們真的很鼓舞人心 。
