if they want to mix up a cake , they're doing it by hand .	如果他們想把蛋混合起來 , 他們會用手做蛋糕 。
that burns calories just as much as going on the treadmill does .	這種燃燒卡路里和跑步機一樣大 。
when they do do intentional physical activity , it's the things they enjoy . they tend to walk , the only proven way to stave off cognitive decline , and they all tend to have a garden .	當他們做實體活動時 , 這是他們享受的事物 。 他們傾向走路 , 唯一證明如何減緩認知衰退 , 他們都傾向有花園 。
they know how to set up their life in the right way so they have the right outlook .	他們知道如何以正確的方式建立他們的人生 , 讓他們有正確的看法 。
each of these cultures take time to downshift .	每一種文化都需要時間下降 。
the sardinians pray . the seventhday adventists pray .	薩丁尼亞人祈禱 , 七天的廣告家祈禱 。
the okinawans have this ancestor veneration .	okinawans擁有這個祖先的神經 。
but when you're in a hurry or stressed out , that triggers something called the inflammatory response , which is associated with everything from alzheimer's disease to cardiovascular disease .	但當你受傷或壓力時 , 會觸發一種稱為發炎反應 , 這種反應和阿茲海默症有關 , 和心血管疾病有關 。
when you slow down for 15 minutes a day you turn that inflammatory state into a more antiinflammatory state .	當你一天慢下來15分鐘 , 把炎熱狀態轉化為更反炎狀態 。
they have vocabulary for sense of purpose , ikigai , like the okinawans .	他們有詞典的目的感 , 愛基加 , 例如 「 俄語 」 。
you know the two most dangerous years in your life are the year you're born , because of infant mortality , and the year you retire .	你知道你生命中最危險的兩年是你出生的一年 , 因為嬰兒死亡率 , 而你退休的那一年 。
these people know their sense of purpose , and they activate in their life , that's worth about seven years of extra life expectancy .	這些人知道自己的目的 , 他們活化了他們的生命 , 這值得花七年的預期壽命 。
there's no longevity diet .	沒有長壽的飲食 。
instead , these people drink a little bit every day , not a hard sell to the american population .	相反地 , 這些人每天都喝一點點錢 , 不是美國人 。
they tend to eat a plantbased diet .	他們通常會吃植物的飲食 。
doesn't mean they don't eat meat , but lots of beans and nuts .	並不是說他們不吃肉 , 而是很多豆子和堅果 。
and they have strategies to keep from overeating , little things that nudge them away from the table at the right time .	他們有策略來阻止過度過度的策略 , 讓他們在正確的時間內遠離桌子 。
and then the foundation of all this is how they connect .	這一切的基礎是他們如何連結 。
they put their families first , take care of their children and their aging parents .	他們先把家人送到家裡 , 照顧他們的孩子和老爸的父母 。
they all tend to belong to a faithbased community , which is worth between four and 14 extra years of life expectancy if you do it four times a month .	他們都傾向於以信仰為基礎的社區 , 值得四到十四年的預期壽命 , 每個月做四次 。
and the biggest thing here is they also belong to the right tribe .	這裡最大的原因是他們屬於對的部落 。
they were either born into or they proactively surrounded themselves with the right people .	他們要麼出生 , 要麼他們積極地圍繞著對人的身邊 。
we know from the framingham studies , that if your three best friends are obese there is a 50 percent better chance that you'll be overweight .	我們從弗林明罕的研究中得知 , 如果你的三個最好的朋友都肥胖了 , 你將會過度過重 。
so , if you hang out with unhealthy people , that's going to have a measurable impact over time .	所以 , 如果你和不健康的人在一起 , 隨著時間 , 會造成很大的影響 。
instead , if your friend's idea of recreation is physical activity , bowling , or playing hockey , biking or gardening , if your friends drink a little , but not too much , and they eat right , and they're engaged , and they're trusting and trustworthy , that is going to have the biggest impact over time .	相反地 , 如果你的朋友對重建的想法是實體的活動 , 弓 , 腳踏車或花園 , 如果你的朋友喝得一點點 , 但他們吃得太多 , 他們也很投入 , 他們相信和信任 , 隨著時間 , 會產生最大的影響 。
diets don't work . no diet in the history of the world has ever worked for more than two percent of the population .	飲食不行得通 , 世界上歷史上沒有飲食 , 超過百分之二的人口都行得通 。
exercise programs usually start in january ; they're usually done by october .	運動計畫通常是一月開始 , 通常是十月份做的 。
when it comes to longevity there is no short term fix in a pill or anything else .	談到長壽時 , 沒有藥丸或其他任何東西的短期解決方案 。
but when you think about it , your friends are longterm adventures , and therefore , perhaps the most significant thing you can do to add more years to your life , and life to your years . thank you very much .	但當你想一想 , 你的朋友是長期的冒險 , 因此 , 或許你能多多年的時間來增加你的生命 , 和你的日子 。 非常謝謝你們 。
ink that conducts electricity ; a window that turns from clear to opaque at the flip of a switch ; a jelly that makes music . all this stuff exists , and catarina mota says: it's time to play with it . mota leads us on a tour of surprising and cool new materials , and suggests that the way we'll figure out what they're good for is to experiment , tinker and have fun .	墨水會傳送電力 ; 一扇窗 , 轉向一個開關 , 一個可以創作音樂的水母 。 所有這些東西都存在 , 加大莫大說:該是玩 。 馬塔帶領我們進入一個驚喜和酷的新材料 , 並且建議我們如何去做實驗、粉紅色、有趣 。
creativity , design , technology	創造力、設計、科技、科技
catarina mota: play with smart materials	catarinamota:用智慧型材料來玩 。
i have a friend in portugal whose grandfather built a vehicle out of a bicycle and a washing machine so he could transport his family .	我有一個在葡萄牙的朋友 , 他的祖父建造了一台車 , 用腳踏車和洗衣機來運送他的家人 。
he did it because he couldn't afford a car , but also because he knew how to build one .	他這麼做是因為他買不起車 , 也因為他知道如何建造一台車 。
there was a time when we understood how things worked and how they were made , so we could build and repair them , or at the very least make informed decisions about what to buy .	有一段時間 , 我們了解到東西是如何運作的 , 以及它們是如何被製造出來的 , 這樣我們就能建立並修復它們 , 或在最少被知名的決策中 , 決定要買什麼 。
many of these doityourself practices were lost in the second half of the 20th century .	許多這些做法在二十世紀的第二半失去了 。
but now , the maker community and the opensource model are bringing this kind of knowledge about how things work and what they're made of back into our lives , and i believe we need to take them to the next level , to the components things are made of .	但現在 , 製造者和開放原始碼模型把知識帶回我們的生命中 , 它們是如何運作的 , 我相信我們需要把它們帶到下一個層面 , 到下一個層面 。
for the most part , we still know what traditional materials like paper and textiles are made of and how they are produced .	大部分的情況下 , 我們仍然知道像紙張和紡織品的傳統材料是什麼 , 製造出來的 。
but now we have these amazing , futuristic composites plastics that change shape , paints that conduct electricity , pigments that change color , fabrics that light up .	但現在我們有了這些驚人、具體的塑膠 , 會改變形狀 , 油漆會產生電力 , 顏料會改變顏色 , 會亮起來 。
let me show you some examples .	讓我給你們看一些例子 。
so conductive ink allows us to paint circuits instead of using the traditional printed circuit boards or wires .	所以 , 導電墨讓我們可以用傳統的印刷電路或電線來繪製電路 。
in the case of this little example i'm holding , we used it to create a touch sensor that reacts to my skin by turning on this little light .	以我所舉的這個小例子來說 , 我們用它來創造一個觸覺感應器 , 藉由啟動這個小小的光線來對我的皮膚做出反應 。
conductive ink has been used by artists , but recent developments indicate that we will soon be able to use it in laser printers and pens .	導電墨水被藝術家使用 , 但近期的發展指出 , 我們很快就能用雷射印表機和筆 。
and this is a sheet of acrylic infused with colorless lightdiffusing particles .	這是加密的加密表 , 充滿了無色光的粒子 。
what this means is that , while regular acrylic only diffuses light around the edges , this one illuminates across the entire surface when i turn on the lights around it .	這意謂著 , 一般的加密器只會在邊緣周圍散光 , 在這一顆光照亮整個表面 , 當我把光照在周圍的光線上時 。
two of the known applications for this material include interior design and multitouch systems .	其中兩個已知的應用程式包括內部設計和多觸覺系統 。
and thermochromic pigments change color at a given temperature .	熱染色體在特定溫度上改變顏色 。
so i'm going to place this on a hot plate that is set to a temperature only slightly higher than ambient and you can see what happens .	所以 , 我要把這個放在一個熱板上 , 設定在溫度上 , 比野生動物更高 , 你可以看到發生了什麼事 。
so one of the principle applications for this material is , amongst other things , in baby bottles , so it indicates when the contents are cool enough to drink .	所以 , 這種材料的原則之一是 , 在嬰兒瓶中 , 其它的原則是 , 當內容夠酷時 , 它會指出 , 內容是很酷的飲料 。
so these are just a few of what are commonly known as smart materials .	這些只是一些常被稱為智慧型材料的東西 。
in a few years , they will be in many of the objects and technologies we use on a daily basis .	幾年後 , 它們將成為我們日常使用的物品和技術 。
we may not yet have the flying cars science fiction promised us , but we can have walls that change color depending on temperature , keyboards that roll up , and windows that become opaque at the flick of a switch .	我們可能還沒有飛行汽車 , 科幻小說讓我們承諾 , 但是我們可以有牆壁 , 以溫度來改變顏色 , 按鍵板滾動 , 轉動的窗戶 , 轉換成開關的光線 。
so i'm a social scientist by training , so why am i here today talking about smart materials ?	所以 , 我是一位社會科學家 , 為何我今天要談的是智慧型材料 ?
well first of all , because i am a maker .	首先 , 因為我是個製造家 。
i'm curious about how things work and how they are made , but also because i believe we should have a deeper understanding of the components that make up our world , and right now , we don't know enough about these hightech composites our future will be made of .	我很好奇事物是如何運作的 , 以及它們是如何製作的 , 也因為我相信我們應該更深入了解組成我們的世界的元件 , 而現在 , 我們對這些高科技的組合並不足夠 。
smart materials are hard to obtain in small quantities .	智慧型材料很難在很小的數量中取得 。
there's barely any information available on how to use them , and very little is said about how they are produced .	幾乎沒有任何資訊可以用在如何使用它們 , 很少是說它們是如何產生的 。
so for now , they exist mostly in this realm of trade secrets and patents only universities and corporations have access to .	所以現在 , 它們主要存在於交易秘密和專利領域 , 只有大學和企業才能取得 。
so a little over three years ago , kirsty boyle and i started a project we called open materials .	三年前 , 我和kirsty男孩開始了一個計畫 , 我們稱之為 「 開放材料 」 。
it's a website where we , and anyone else who wants to join us , share experiments , publish information , encourage others to contribute whenever they can , and aggregate resources such as research papers and tutorials by other makers like ourselves .	這是個網站 , 我們和任何想要加入我們的人 , 共同實驗 , 發表訊息 , 鼓勵其他人可以發揮貢獻 , 包括研究論文和教學 , 像是我們自己 。
we would like it to become a large , collectively generated database of doityourself information on smart materials .	我們希望它能成為一個龐大、集體的多元資料庫 , 以智慧型材料來建立資料庫 。
but why should we care how smart materials work and what they are made of ?	但為何我們要在乎聰明的材料如何運作和它們的成果 ?
first of all , because we can't shape what we don't understand , and what we don't understand and use ends up shaping us .	首先 , 因為我們無法塑造我們不了解的事物 , 以及我們不了解的 , 最後用的是塑造我們 。
the objects we use , the clothes we wear , the houses we live in , all have a profound impact on our behavior , health and quality of life .	我們所使用的物品 , 衣服 , 我們所居住的房子 , 都對我們的行為、健康和生活品質有很大的影響 。
so if we are to live in a world made of smart materials , we should know and understand them .	如果我們要生活在一個智慧型材料的世界 , 我們應該要知道並了解它們 。
secondly , and just as important , innovation has always been fueled by tinkerers .	第二 , 同樣重要的是 , 創新總是被粉紅色的人所燃燒 。
so many times , amateurs , not experts , have been the inventors and improvers of things ranging from mountain bikes to semiconductors , personal computers , airplanes .	許多時候 , 業餘者 , 不是專家 , 曾經是來自山區的發明家和改進者 , 從自行車到半導體、個人電腦、飛機 。
the biggest challenge is that material science is complex and requires expensive equipment .	最大的挑戰是 , 物質科學是複雜且需要昂貴的設備 。
but that's not always the case .	但事實並非如此 。
two scientists at university of illinois understood this when they published a paper on a simpler method for making conductive ink .	伊利諾大學的兩個科學家了解這一點 , 當時他們在一個簡單的方法上發表了一張紙 , 用來做導電墨 。
jordan bunker , who had had no experience with chemistry until then , read this paper and reproduced the experiment at his maker space using only offtheshelf substances and tools .	約旦bunker , 他完全沒有化學經驗 , 直到那時 , 閱讀這篇論文 , 並在他的製造者空間中複製這個實驗 , 只用自身的物質和工具 。
he used a toaster oven , and he even made his own vortex mixer , based on a tutorial by another scientist/maker .	他用了烤箱 , 甚至製作了他自己的vortex混合器 , 根據另一個科學家/maker的直覺 。
jordan then published his results online , including all the things he had tried and didn't work , so others could study and reproduce it .	約旦後來在網路上發表了他的結果 , 包括所有他曾經嘗試過的東西 , 沒有工作 , 其他人可以研究並繁殖它 。
so jordan's main form of innovation was to take an experiment created in a wellequipped lab at the university and recreate it in a garage in chicago using only cheap materials and tools he made himself .	所以 , 約旦的主要創新是要在大學創造一個很好的實驗 , 並在芝加哥的車庫用便宜的材料和工具來重建這個實驗 。
and now that he published this work , others can pick up where he left and devise even simpler processes and improvements .	現在他發表了這項工作 , 其他人可以在他左邊的位置 , 設想更簡單的過程和改善 。
another example i'd like to mention her project's goal is to highlight the expressive qualities of materials while focusing on the creativity and skills of the builder .	另外一個例子 , 我想提到她的專案目的 , 是要強調材料的特質 , 同時專注於創造力和技能 。
electronics kits are very powerful in that they teach us how things work , but the constraints inherent in their design influence the way we learn .	電子設備在他們教導我們事物如何運作 , 但他們設計的限制會影響我們學習的方式 。
so hannah's approach , on the other hand , is to formulate a series of techniques for creating unusual objects that free us from predesigned constraints by teaching us about the materials themselves .	另一方面 , 漢娜的做法是建立一系列的技術 , 來創造出不尋常的物品 , 來免費我們的限制 , 來教導我們這些材料本身 。
so amongst hannah's many impressive experiments , this is one of my favorites .	在漢娜許多令人印象深刻的實驗中 , 這是我最喜歡的一個實驗之一 。
[ " paper speakers " ] what we're seeing here is just a piece of paper with some copper tape on it connected to an mp3 player and a magnet .	[紙喇叭]我們現在看到的只是一張紙 , 上面有一些銅帶 , 連接到mp3播放器和磁鐵 。
so based on the research by marcelo coelho from mit , hannah created a series of paper speakers out of a wide range of materials from simple copper tape to conductive fabric and ink .	所以 , 根據麻省理工學院的marcelocoho的研究 , 漢娜創造了一系列的紙喇叭 , 從簡單的銅線到導電布和墨水 。
just like jordan and so many other makers , hannah published her recipes and allows anyone to copy and reproduce them .	就像jordan和許多其他製造商 , 漢娜出版了她的食譜 , 讓任何人可以複製和繁殖它們 。
but paper electronics is one of the most promising branches of material science in that it allows us to create cheaper and flexible electronics .	但紙質電子學是最有前景的材料科學分支 , 它讓我們能夠創造更便宜且彈性的電子學 。
so hannah's artisanal work , and the fact that she shared her findings , opens the doors to a series of new possibilities that are both aesthetically appealing and innovative .	所以漢娜的工藝工作 , 她分享她的發現 , 把門打開給一連串的新可能性 , 都是合理的、有創新的 。
so the interesting thing about makers is that we create out of passion and curiosity , and we are not afraid to fail .	所以 , 製造者有趣的是 , 我們用熱情和好奇心創造出來 , 而我們並不害怕失敗 。
we often tackle problems from unconventional angles , and , in the process , end up discovering alternatives or even better ways to do things .	我們經常從未有的角度解決問題 , 在過程中 , 最後發現了其他的替代方案 , 甚至更好的方式來做事 。
so the more people experiment with materials , the more researchers are willing to share their research , and manufacturers their knowledge , the better chances we have to create technologies that truly serve us all .	所以越多人用材料做實驗 , 越多研究人員願意分享他們的研究 , 製造出他們的知識 , 我們就越有機會創造出真正為我們服務的科技 。
so i feel a bit as ted nelson must have when , in the early 1970s , he wrote , " you must understand computers now . "	所以 , 我覺得tednelson一定有時 , 在1970年代早期 , 他寫道: 「 你現在必須要了解電腦了 。 」
back then , computers were these large mainframes only scientists cared about , and no one dreamed of even having one at home .	當時 , 電腦是這些大型的主流 , 只有科學家在乎 , 沒有人在家裡想過 , 甚至在家裡也沒有人夢想過 。
so it's a little strange that i'm standing here and saying , " you must understand smart materials now . "	所以這有點奇怪 , 我站在這裡 , 說: 「 你現在必須要了解智慧型材料 。 」
just keep in mind that acquiring preemptive knowledge about emerging technologies is the best way to ensure that we have a say in the making of our future .	請記住 , 要獲得新興科技的先進知識是確保我們未來的說法最好的 。
when we drive , we get into a glass bubble , lock the doors and press the accelerator , relying on our eyes to guide us even though we can only see the few cars ahead of and behind us . but what if cars could share data with each other about their position and velocity , and use predictive models to calculate the safest routes for everyone on the road ? jennifer healey imagines a world without accidents .	當我們開車時 , 我們會進入玻璃泡 , 把門鎖住 , 壓住加速器 , 仰賴我們的眼睛來引導我們 , 雖然我們只能看到我們身後的少數車子 。 但如果車子可以和彼此分享他們的位置和速度 , 用預測模型來計算每個人在路上最安全的路線嗎 ? 珍妮佛•艾利 , 想像一個沒有意外的世界 。
jennifer healey: if cars could talk , accidents might be avoidable	珍妮佛.療法:如果車子能說話 , 意外就會避免發生 。
let's face it: driving is dangerous .	讓我們面對現實:開車是危險的 。
it's one of the things that we don't like to think about , but the fact that religious icons and good luck charms show up on dashboards around the world betrays the fact that we know this to be true .	這是我們不喜歡思考的一件事 , 但事實上 , 宗教的圖標和好運的圖表顯示在世界各地的儀表板上 , 背叛我們所知的事實 。
car accidents are the leading cause of death in people ages 16 to 19 in the united states leading cause of death and 75 percent of these accidents have nothing to do with drugs or alcohol .	車禍是16到19歲的人死因的主要原因 , 在美國 , 導致死亡 , 75%的意外事件與毒品或酒精無關 。
no one can say for sure , but i remember my first accident .	沒有人能肯定地說話 , 但我記得我的第一個意外 。
i was a young driver out on the highway , and the car in front of me , i saw the brake lights go on .	我是一位年輕的司機在高速公路上 , 車子在我面前 , 我看到了煞車燈亮了 。
i'm like , " okay , all right , this guy is slowing down , i'll slow down too . "	我說: 「 好吧 , 好吧 , 這個傢伙正在慢下來 , 我也會慢下來 。 」
i step on the brake .	我站在煞車上 。
but no , this guy isn't slowing down .	但 , 不 , 這個傢伙並沒有慢下來 。
this guy is stopping , dead stop , dead stop on the highway .	這個傢伙停下來 , 停下來 , 停在高速公路上 。
it was just going 65 to zero ?	只需要65到0 ?
i slammed on the brakes .	我衝在煞車上 。
i felt the abs kick in , and the car is still going , and it's not going to stop , and i know it's not going to stop , and the air bag deploys , the car is totaled , and fortunately , no one was hurt .	我感覺到abskick進來 , 車仍然在走 , 不會停下來 , 我知道它不會停下來 , 空氣袋部署 , 幸運的是 , 沒有人會受傷 。
but i had no idea that car was stopping , and i think we can do a lot better than that .	但我不知道車子已經停下來了 , 我認為我們能做得更好 。
i think we can transform the driving experience by letting our cars talk to each other .	我認為我們可以改變駕駛經驗 , 讓車子彼此交流 。
i just want you to think a little bit about what the experience of driving is like now .	我只是想讓你們思考一下現在駕駛的經驗是什麼 。
get into your car . close the door . you're in a glass bubble .	走進你的車 , 關門 。 你在一個玻璃泡泡 。
you can't really directly sense the world around you .	你無法直接感知你周遭的世界 。
you're in this extended body .	你身在這個延伸的身體中 。
you're tasked with navigating it down partiallyseen roadways , in and amongst other metal giants , at superhuman speeds .	你的任務是用一部分的路徑來導航它 , 在另一塊金屬巨人中 , 在超級人類的速度中 。
okay ? and all you have to guide you are your two eyes .	好嗎 ? 你只需要指引你是你的雙眼 。
okay , so that's all you have , eyes that weren't really designed for this task , but then people ask you to do things like , you want to make a lane change , what's the first thing they ask you do ?	好吧 , 那你只有眼睛 , 不是為了這個任務而設計的 , 但是人們要求你做這樣的事 , 你想做出一個改變 , 他們要你做的第一件事是什麼 ?
take your eyes off the road . that's right .	把你的眼睛從路邊脫下來 , 沒錯 。
stop looking where you're going , turn , check your blind spot , and drive down the road without looking where you're going .	別再看你要去哪裡 , 轉身 , 看看你的盲點 , 不用看你要去哪裡 。
you and everyone else . this is the safe way to drive .	你和其他人 , 這是開車的安全路徑 。
why do we do this ? because we have to , we have to make a choice , do i look here or do i look here ?	為什麼我們要這樣做 ? 因為我們必須做出選擇 , 我要在這裡看或是看這裡 ?
and usually we do a fantastic job picking and choosing what we attend to on the road .	通常我們會做一份很棒的工作 , 選擇我們要在路上做的事 。
but occasionally we miss something .	但偶爾 , 我們錯過了某樣東西 。
occasionally we sense something wrong or too late .	偶爾 , 我們會感覺錯了或太遲 。
in countless accidents , the driver says , " i didn't see it coming . "	無數的意外 , 司機說: 「 我看不到它來了 。 」
and i believe that . i believe that .	我相信 , 我相信 。
we can only watch so much .	我們只能看得太多 。
but the technology exists now that can help us improve that .	但現在的科技可以幫助我們改善這一點 。
in the future , with cars exchanging data with each other , we will be able to see not just three cars ahead and three cars behind , to the right and left , all at the same time , bird's eye view , we will actually be able to see into those cars .	在未來 , 車子互相交換資料 , 我們不只能看到三輛車 , 三輛車 , 到右邊和左邊 , 同時 , 鳥的眼睛 , 我們就能看見這些車子 。
we will be able to see the velocity of the car in front of us , to see how fast that guy's going or stopping .	我們將能夠看到在我們面前的車子的速度 , 看到那個人走得多快 , 或停下來 。
if that guy's going down to zero , i'll know .	如果那個人下降到零 , 我就會知道 。
and with computation and algorithms and predictive models , we will be able to see the future .	有了計算和演算法和預測模型 , 我們就能看見未來 。
you may think that's impossible .	你可能覺得這不可能 。
how can you predict the future ? that's really hard .	你要如何預測未來 ? 這真的很難 。
actually , no . with cars , it's not impossible .	實際上 , 沒有車子 , 不是不可能 。
cars are threedimensional objects that have a fixed position and velocity .	汽車是三維的物體 , 有固定的位置和速度 。
they travel down roads .	他們在路上行走 。
often they travel on prepublished routes .	通常他們會在公開的路線上旅行 。
it's really not that hard to make reasonable predictions about where a car's going to be in the near future .	要做出合理的預測 , 並不難 , 無法預測未來車會在哪裡 。
even if , when you're in your car and some motorcyclist comes bshoom ! 85 miles an hour down , lanesplitting i know you've had this experience that guy didn't " just come out of nowhere . "	即便你在車子裡 , 有些摩托車的人來了 , 每小時85英哩 ! 拉內斯普洛斯--我知道你有過這個經驗--那傢伙沒有 「 不出門 」 的經驗 。
that guy's been on the road probably for the last half hour .	那個人在路上大概是過去的半小時 。
right ? i mean , somebody's seen him .	對嗎 ? 我的意思是 , 有人看過他 。
ten , 20 , 30 miles back , someone's seen that guy , and as soon as one car sees that guy and puts him on the map , he's on the map position , velocity , good estimate he'll continue going 85 miles an hour .	十、二十、三十英哩後 , 有人看過這個傢伙 , 一旦一輛車看到那個人 , 把他放在地圖上 , 他就在地圖上位置、速度、估計他會每小時要走85英哩 。
you'll know , because your car will know , because that other car will have whispered something in his ear , like , " by the way , five minutes , motorcyclist , watch out . "	你會知道 , 因為你的車會知道 , 因為另一輛車會在他的耳朵上揮之不去 , 比如: 「 順便一提 , 五分鐘 , 摩托車騎士 , 看 。 」
you can make reasonable predictions about how cars behave .	你可以做出合理的預測 , 預測車子的行為 。
i mean , they're newtonian objects .	我的意思是 , 它們是牛頓的物體 。
that's very nice about them .	這對他們是非常好的 。
so how do we get there ?	那我們該怎麼辦到呢 ?
we can start with something as simple as sharing our position data between cars , just sharing gps .	我們可以從簡單的開始 , 如共享汽車之間的位置資料 , 分享gps 。
if i have a gps and a camera in my car , i have a pretty precise idea of where i am and how fast i'm going .	如果我有一台gps和一台攝影機 , 我對於我在哪裡 , 以及我要走多快 。
with computer vision , i can estimate where the cars around me are , sort of , and where they're going .	有了電腦視覺 , 我可以估計我周圍的車子的位置 , 有點像 , 他們會去哪裡 。
and same with the other cars .	和其他車子一樣 。
they can have a precise idea of where they are , and sort of a vague idea of where the other cars are .	他們可以有一個精確的點子 , 一個模糊的點子 , 可以解釋其他車子在哪裡 。
what happens if two cars share that data , if they talk to each other ?	如果兩輛車共用這些資料 , 如果他們彼此交談 , 會發生什麼事 ?
i can tell you exactly what happens .	我可以告訴你發生了什麼事 。
professor bob wang and his team have done computer simulations of what happens when fuzzy estimates combine , even in light traffic , when cars just share gps data , and we've moved this research out of the computer simulation and into robot test beds that have the actual sensors that are in cars now on these robots: stereo cameras , gps , and the twodimensional laser range finders that are common in backup systems .	波布教授和他的團隊做了電腦模擬 , 來模擬當燃料結合時 , 甚至在光線交通中 , 我們把這個研究從電腦模擬和機器人測試床上 , 讓機器人的感測器現在在這些機器人上 , 史里奧攝影機、gps , 以及二維的雷射範圍 , 發現這些系統中常見的系統 。
we also attach a discrete shortrange communication radio , and the robots talk to each other .	我們也將一個短距離通訊無線電附著 , 機器人彼此交流 。
when these robots come at each other , they track each other's position precisely , and they can avoid each other .	當這些機器人互相接觸時 , 它們會精確地追蹤彼此的位置 , 它們就能避免彼此 。
we're now adding more and more robots into the mix , and we encountered some problems .	我們現在越來越多的機器人在混合中加入 , 我們遇到了一些問題 。
one of the problems , when you get too much chatter , it's hard to process all the packets , so you have to prioritize , and that's where the predictive model helps you .	其中一個問題是 , 當你有太多的聊天 , 要處理所有包裝 , 要優先順序 , 那就是預測模型可以幫助你 。
if your robot cars are all tracking the predicted trajectories , you don't pay as much attention to those packets .	如果你的機器人汽車都在追蹤預測軌跡 , 你不會注意到那些包裝 。
you prioritize the one guy who seems to be going a little off course .	你優先把一個看起來有點偏離軌道的那個人 。
that guy could be a problem .	那個人可能會是個問題 。
and you can predict the new trajectory .	你可以預測新的軌跡 。
so you don't only know that he's going off course , you know how .	所以你不只知道他要走下去 , 你知道他怎麼走 。
and you know which drivers you need to alert to get out of the way .	而且你知道你需要哪個駕駛 , 才能走出路 。
and we wanted to do how can we best alert everyone ?	我們想做的事是如何讓每個人更能警告嗎 ?
how can these cars whisper , " you need to get out of the way ? "	這些車是怎麼可能的 ? " 你需要走出路 ? "
well , it depends on two things: one , the ability of the car , and second the ability of the driver .	嗯 , 這取決於兩件事:第一 , 車的能力 , 第二 , 駕駛的能力 。
if one guy has a really great car , but they're on their phone or , you know , doing something , they're not probably in the best position to react in an emergency .	如果一個人有一台很棒的車 , 但他們在手機上 , 或在做某件事 , 他們可能不是最好的職位 , 要在緊急情況下做出反應 。
so we started a separate line of research doing driver state modeling .	所以 , 我們開始了一系列的研究 , 做為駕駛狀態模型 。
and now , using a series of three cameras , we can detect if a driver is looking forward , looking away , looking down , on the phone , or having a cup of coffee .	現在 , 使用一系列三台攝影機 , 我們可以偵測駕駛向前 , 向下看 , 看著手機 , 或喝杯咖啡 。
we can predict the accident and we can predict who , which cars , are in the best position to move out of the way to calculate the safest route for everyone .	我們可以預測意外 , 我們可以預測誰 , 哪個車子 , 最好的位置是要讓每個人計算最安全的路線 。
fundamentally , these technologies exist today .	基本上 , 這些科技是現今存在的 。
i think the biggest problem that we face is our own willingness to share our data .	我認為我們所面臨的最大的問題就是我們自願分享我們的資料 。
i think it's a very disconcerting notion , this idea that our cars will be watching us , talking about us to other cars , that we'll be going down the road in a sea of gossip .	我覺得這是個非常令人困惑的概念 , 我們的車會看著我們 , 和其他車子談起 , 我們會在大西洋向下走 。
but i believe it can be done in a way that protects our privacy , just like right now , when i look at your car from the outside , i don't really know about you .	但我相信 , 可以用一種保護我們的隱私的方式來保護我們的隱私 , 就像現在 , 當我從外面看你的車 , 我不知道你在做什麼 。
if i look at your license plate number , i don't really know who you are .	如果我看你的牌號碼 , 我不知道你是誰 。
i believe our cars can talk about us behind our backs .	我相信我們的車子可以在我們的背後談論我們 。
and i think it's going to be a great thing .	我認為這將會是件好事 。
i want you to consider for a moment if you really don't want the distracted teenager behind you to know that you're braking , that you're coming to a dead stop .	請各位考慮一下 , 如果你不希望你背後的青少年分散的青少年 , 知道你在煞車 , 你正要停下來 。
by sharing our data willingly , we can do what's best for everyone .	透過分享我們的數據 , 我們就能為每個人做最好的做法 。
so let your car gossip about you .	所以 , 讓你的車子對你說話 。
it's going to make the roads a lot safer .	它會讓道路變得更安全 。
x prize founder peter diamandis talks about how he helped stephen hawking fulfill his dream of going to space by flying together into the upper atmosphere and experiencing weightlessness at zero g .	xprize創辦人彼得•迪安德斯談到他如何幫助史蒂芬•霍金的夢想 , 透過把他一起飛到大氣中 , 並在零g中體驗無重力的夢想 。
business , flight , science , short talk , space , technology , universe	商業、飛行、科學、短暫的演講、科技、宇宙、宇宙 。
peter diamandis on stephen hawking in zero g	彼得•迪安德斯在零格的斯蒂芬霍金州斯蒂芬.戴維斯上了peter.
those of you who know me know how passionate i am about opening the space frontier .	那些認識我的人 , 都知道我有多熱情 , 打開太空前進 。
so when i had the chance to give the world's expert in gravity the experience of zero gravity , it was incredible .	所以當我有機會給予世界重力的專家 , 不可思議地心引力的體驗 , 這實在是不可思議 。
and i want to tell you that story .	我想要告訴你們這個故事 。
i first met him through the archon x prize for genomics .	我第一次見到他 , 透過archonxprize來基因組學獎 。
it's a competition we're holding , the second x prize , for the first team to sequence 100 human genomes in 10 days .	這是我們的競爭 , 第二個xprize , 第一個團隊在10天內完成100個人類基因組定序 。
we have something called the genome 100 100 individuals we're sequencing as part of that .	我們有一種叫做基因組100個人的基因組 , 我們被定序為其中一部分 。
craig venter chairs that event .	克雷格•凡特的椅子 。
and i met professor hawking , and he said his dream was to travel into space .	我遇見了霍金教授 , 他說他的夢想是進入太空 。
and i said , " i can't take you there , but i can take you into weightlessness into zerog .	我說: 「 我不能帶你到那裡 , 但我可以帶你到無重力之中 。
and he said , on the spot , " absolutely , yes . "	他說: 「 沒錯 , 是的 。 」
well , the only way to experience zerog on earth is actually with parabolic flight , weightless flight .	嗯 , 世界上唯一能體驗零的途徑 , 其實是飛行傘 , 無重力飛行 。
you take an airplane , you fly over the top , you're weightless for 25 seconds .	你拿一個飛機 , 你飛越頂端 , 你有25秒的重量 。
come back down , you weigh twice as much .	再回來 , 再重兩倍 。
you do it again and again .	你再做一次 。
you can get eight , 10 minutes of weightlessness how nasa's trained their astronauts for so long .	你可以得到8 , 10分鐘的無重力訓練nasa的太空人多久才被訓練出來 。
we set out to do this .	我們開始這樣做 。
it took us 11 years to become operational .	我們花了11年才開始營運 。
and we announced that we were going to fly stephen hawking .	我們宣佈我們要飛史蒂芬•霍金 。
we had one government agency and one company aircraft operator say , you're crazy , don't do that , you're going kill the guy .	我們有一間政府機構 , 一間公司的飛機操作員說 , 你瘋了 , 別這樣做 , 你要殺了這個傢伙 。
and he wanted to go .	他想要去 。
we worked hard to get all the permissions .	我們努力取得所有允許 。
and six months later , we sat down at kennedy space center .	六個月後 , 我們坐在甘迺迪太空中心 。
we had a press conference , we announced our intent to do one zerog parabola , give him 25 seconds of zerog .	我們有一場媒體研討會 , 我們宣佈了我們的意圖 , 給他25秒的零 。
and if it went really well , we might do three parabolas .	如果它運行得非常好 , 我們可能會做三架拋物線 。
well , we asked him why he wanted to go up and do this .	嗯 , 我們問他為什麼要去做這件事 。
and what he said , for me , was very moving .	他對我說 , 對我來說 , 非常感動 。
he said , " life on earth is at an everincreasing risk of being wiped out by disaster . . .	他說: 「 地球上的生命 , 被災難摧毀的風險越來越高 。
i think the human race doesn't have a future if it doesn't go into space .	我想 , 人類在太空中不會有未來 。
i therefore want to encourage public interest in space . "	所以我想鼓勵大眾對太空的興趣 。 」
we took him out to the kennedy space center , up inside the nasa vehicle , into the back of the zerog airplane .	我們把他帶到甘迺迪太空中心 , 在美國太空總署的飛機後面 , 帶到零飛機的後面 。
we had about 20 people who made donations we raised $150 , 000 in donations for children's charities who flew with us .	我們有大約20個捐贈者 , 他們捐贈了一萬五萬美金給兒童慈善機構的捐贈者 。
a few tedsters here .	這裡有幾個tedster 。
we set up a whole er .	我們設立了整個急診室 。
we had four emergency room doctors and two nurses on board the airplane .	我們有四個急診室醫生和兩位護士在飛機上 。
we were monitoring his po2 of his blood , his heart rate , his blood pressure .	我們在監測他的血液中 , 他的心跳率 , 他的血壓 。
we had everything all set in case of an emergency ; god knows , you don't want to hurt this worldrenowned expert .	上帝知道 , 你不想傷害這個世界的專家 。
we took off from the shuttle landing facility , where the shuttle takes off and lands .	我們從太空梭降落設施中脫落 , 太空梭起飛和降落 。
and my partner byron lichtenberg and i carefully suspended him into zerog .	我和我的伴侶lichtenberg , 小心地把他綁在零 。
once he was there , [we] let him go to experience what weightlessness was truly like .	一旦他在那裡 , 我們讓他去體驗無重力的感覺 。
and after that first parabola , you know , the doc said everything is great . he was smiling , and we said go .	在第一個拋物架之後 , 你知道嗎 , 醫生說一切都很棒 。 他微笑了 , 我們說: 「 去吧 ! 」
so we did a second parabola .	所以我們做了第二個拋物線 。
we actually floated an apple in homage to sir isaac newton because professor hawking holds the same chair at cambridge that isaac newton did .	實際上 , 我們把一顆蘋果搬到比薩•牛頓 , 因為霍金教授在劍橋有同樣的椅子 , 艾薩克•牛頓的確 。
and we did a fourth , and a fifth and a sixth .	我們做了第四次 , 第五次和第六次 。
and a seventh and an eighth .	第七和第八個 。
and this man does not look like a 65yearold wheelchairbound man .	這個人看起來不像一個65歲的輪椅人 。
he was so happy .	他很高興 。
we are living on a precious jewel , and it's during our lifetime that we're moving off this planet .	我們正生活在一個珍貴的珠寶上 , 而在我們的一生中 , 我們正在離開這個星球 。
please join us in this epic adventure .	請加入我們這個史詩般的冒險 。
medical animator david bolinsky presents 3 minutes of stunning animation that show the bustling life inside a cell .	醫學動畫家大衛•鮑林斯基在細胞內展現了三分鐘的驚人動畫 。
design , entertainment , film , health , medicine , science , technology , visualizations	設計、娛樂、電影、健康、醫學、科學、技術、視覺化 。
david bolinsky animates a cell	davidbolinsky是一個細胞的動畫
i'm a medical illustrator , and i come from a slightly different point of view .	我是個醫學插圖師 , 我來自一個稍微不同的觀點 。
i've been watching , since i grew up , the expressions of truth and beauty in the arts and truth and beauty in the sciences .	我一直在觀察 , 自從我長大後 , 藝術和美麗的表達方式 , 都是科學的美 。
and while these are both wonderful things in their own right they both have very wonderful things going for them truth and beauty as ideals that can be looked at by the sciences and by math are almost like the ideal conjoined twins that a scientist would want to date .	雖然這些都是他們自己的權利 , 他們都有非常美好的事物 , 會讓他們成為理想和美麗的理想 , 可以透過數學 , 就像一個科學家想約會的理想結合的雙胞胎 。
these are expressions of truth as awefull things , by meaning they are things you can worship .	這些是真理的表達 , 意思是 , 它們是你可以崇拜的事物 。
they are ideals that are powerful . they are irreducible .	它們是很強大的理想 。 它們是不可思議的 。
they are unique . they are useful sometimes , often a long time after the fact .	他們是獨一無二的 , 有時是有用的 , 通常是事實之後很長一段時間 。
and you can actually roll some of the pictures now , because i don't want to look at me on the screen .	你現在可以滾一些照片 , 因為我不想在螢幕上看著我 。
truth and beauty are things that are often opaque to people who are not in the sciences .	真相和美 , 通常是對不在科學領域的人來說 , 相反的 。
they are things that describe beauty in a way that is often only accessible if you understand the language and the syntax of the person who studies the subject in which truth and beauty is expressed .	它們是用來形容美的事物 , 通常只能用你了解語言和研究主題的人的語調來形容美 。
if you look at the math , e=mc squared , if you look at the cosmological constant , where there's an anthropic ideal , where you see that life had to evolve from the numbers that describe the universe these are things that are really difficult to understand .	如果你看數學 , e=mc的平方 , 如果你看宇宙的常數 , 那裡有一個人類的理想 , 你可以看到生命必須從數字演化出來 , 來描述宇宙這些東西是非常難理解的 。
and what i've tried to do since i had my training as a medical illustrator since i was taught animation by my father , who was a sculptor and my visual mentor i wanted to figure out a way to help people understand truth and beauty in the biological sciences by using animation , by using pictures , by telling stories so that the things that are not necessarily evident to people can be brought forth , and can be taught , and can be understood .	自從我教導我身為醫學插畫家之後 , 我就試著去做 , 我父親是雕塑家和我的視覺導師 , 我想要想辦法幫助人們了解生物科學的真與美 , 透過使用動畫 , 透過用圖片 , 來告訴故事 , 告訴大家 , 那些不見得會被帶到的事物 , 可以被教導 , 並且可以被理解 。
students today are often immersed in an environment where what they learn is subjects that have truth and beauty embedded in them , but the way they're taught is compartmentalized and it's drawn down to the point where the truth and beauty are not always evident .	今天的學生們常常在一個環境中沉浸在他們學習的主題中 , 擁有真實和美麗的主題 , 但他們被教導的方式是相互矛盾的 , 並且被吸引到真相和美並不是總是明顯的 。
it's almost like that old recipe for chicken soup where you boil the chicken until the flavor is just gone .	差不多是雞湯的古老食譜 , 你把雞炸掉 , 直到味道消失了 。
we don't want to do that to our students .	我們不想這樣對我們的學生做 。
so we have an opportunity to really open up education .	所以我們有機會真正開放教育 。
and i had a telephone call from robert lue at harvard , in the molecular and cellular biology department , a couple of years ago . he asked me if my team and i would be interested and willing to really change how medical and scientific education is done at harvard .	幾年前 , 我和哈佛的robertlue打電話給我 , 在哈佛的分子和細胞生物學系裡 , 他問我 , 我的團隊是否會對我感興趣 , 並願意真正改變哈佛醫學和科學教育的做法 。
so we embarked on a project that would explore the cell that would explore the truth and beauty inherent in molecular and cellular biology so that students could understand a larger picture that they could hang all of these facts on .	所以我們開始著手進行一個計畫 , 探索細胞的真與美 , 探索分子和細胞生物學中的真與美 , 讓學生可以更大的理解這些事實 。
they could have a mental image of the cell as a large , bustling , hugely complicated city that's occupied by micromachines .	他們可以把細胞的心智圖像做為一個大型、忙碌的、非常複雜的城市 , 由微機械組成 。
and these micromachines really are at the heart of life .	而這些微機械是生命的核心 。
these micromachines , which are the envy of nanotechnologists the world over , are selfdirected , powerful , precise , accurate devices that are made out of strings of amino acids .	這些微機械 , 來自世界各地的奈米技術專家 , 都是自我導向、強大、精準、精準的裝置 , 由胺基酸的弦組成 。
and these micromachines power how a cell moves .	而這些微機械能是細胞如何移動的 。
they power how a cell replicates . they power our hearts .	它們會影響細胞如何複製 , 它們會影響我們的心臟 。
they power our minds .	它們會影響我們的心智 。
and so what we wanted to do was to figure out how we could make this story into an animation that would be the centerpiece of biovisions at harvard , which is a website that harvard has for its molecular and cellular biology students that will in addition to all the textual information , in addition to all the didactic stuff put everything together visually , so that these students would have an internalized view of what a cell really is in all of its truth and beauty , and be able to study with this view in mind , so that their imaginations would be sparked , so that their passions would be sparked and so that they would be able to go on and use these visions in their head to make new discoveries and to be able to find out , really , how life works .	所以我們想做的是想辦法把這個故事做成一個動畫 , 讓哈佛生物的中心在哈佛大學 , 一個網站是哈佛的分子和細胞生物學學生 , 加上所有文字的資訊 , 加上所有做法 , 加上所有做法 , 加上所有做法 , 加上所有做法 , 讓這些學生可以把一切放在一起 , 以內化的視覺和美麗來研究這個觀點 , 以致於他們的想法 , 以此類推測 , 以致於他們的生命 , 以此類推論 , 以至於他們會如何運用這些觀點 。
so we set out by looking at how these molecules are put together .	所以我們開始研究這些分子如何組合在一起 。
we worked with a theme , which is , you've got macrophages that are streaming down a capillary , and they're touching the surface of the capillary wall , and they're picking up information from cells that are on the capillary wall , and they are given this information that there's an inflammation somewhere outside , where they can't see and sense .	我們和一個主題合作 , 也就是 , 你有巨噬菌體 , 正在流著微小的管道 , 它們會觸碰微血管牆的表面 , 它們會從細菌牆上取得資訊 , 它們會得到在外面某處發炎的資訊 , 在那裡 , 它們無法看見和感知 。
but they get the information that causes them to stop , causes them to internalize that they need to make all of the various parts that will cause them to change their shape , and try to get out of this capillary and find out what's going on .	但他們得到的資訊會使他們停下來 , 使他們內化 , 他們需要做出各式各樣的零件 , 讓他們改變他們的形狀 , 試著脫離這個微鏡 , 找出發生了什麼事 。
so these molecular motors we had to work with the harvard scientists and databank models of the atomically accurate molecules and figure out how they moved , and figure out what they did .	所以這些分子馬達我們必須和哈佛科學家和資料庫模型一起合作 , 準確地準確的分子 , 並找出它們是如何移動 , 找出它們是如何做到的 。
and figure out how to do this in a way that was truthful in that it imparted what was going on , but not so truthful that the compact crowding in a cell would prevent the vista from happening .	想出如何用這種方式來實現這個狀況 , 卻沒有真正的事實 , 細胞內的群眾會阻止這個狀況 。
and so what i'm going to show you is a threeminute reader's digest version of the first aspect of this film that we produced . it's an ongoing project that's going to go another four or five years .	接下來我要給你們看的是一部三分鐘的讀者我們製作的這部電影的第一個面向 。 這是個不斷的計劃 , 接下來要花四到五年 。
and i want you to look at this and see the paths that the cell manufactures these little walking machines , they're called kinesins that take these huge loads that would challenge an ant in relative size .	我希望你們看看這個 , 看看細胞製造這些小步行機器的路徑 , 他們叫kinesins , 採用相對大小的載荷來挑戰一隻螞蟻 。
run the movie , please .	播放這部電影 , 拜託 。
but these machines that power the inside of the cells are really quite amazing , and they really are the basis of all life because all of these machines interact with each other .	但這些機器在細胞內的力量是非常驚人的 , 它們真的是所有生命的基礎 , 因為所有這些機器彼此之間的互動 。
they pass information to each other .	它們互相傳遞訊息 。
they cause different things to happen inside the cell .	它們會造成細胞內部發生不同的事 。
and the cell will actually manufacture the parts that it needs on the fly , from information that's brought from the nucleus by molecules that read the genes .	細胞會製造出果蠅需要的部分 , 來自原子核的資訊 , 這些分子會讀取基因的基因 。
no life , from the smallest life to everybody here , would be possible without these little micromachines .	沒有生命 , 從最小的生命到這裡的每一個人 , 若沒有這些小小的微機械 。
in fact , it would really , in the absence of these machines , have made the attendance here , chris , really quite sparse .	事實上 , 在這些機器的缺席之中 , 真的會讓這台機關變得很快 , 克里斯 , 真的很恐怖 。
this is the fedex delivery guy of the cell .	這是fedex的傳送人員 。
this little guy is called the kinesin , and he pulls a sack that's full of brand new manufactured proteins to wherever it's needed in the cell whether it's to a membrane , whether it's to an organelle , whether it's to build something or repair something .	這個小傢伙叫做松果 , 他拿了一袋袋子 , 滿是全新的製造蛋白質 , 到任何細胞需要的位置 , 不管是蛋白質 , 不管是蛋白質 , 不管是蛋白質 , 不管是製造或修補某樣東西 。
and each of us has about 100 , 000 of these things running around , right now , inside each one of your 100 trillion cells .	我們每個人都有大約十萬個這些東西正在四處奔跑 , 現在 , 在你每一百兆個細胞中 。
so no matter how lazy you feel , you're not really intrinsically doing nothing .	所以 , 不論你覺得多懶惰 , 你本質上沒有做任何事 。
so what i want you to do when you go home is think about this , and think about how powerful our cells are .	所以當你回家想想 , 我希望你能做什麼 , 想想我們的細胞有多強大 。
and think about some of the things that we're learning about cellular mechanics .	想想看 , 我們學到了一些關於細胞機械的知識 。
once we figure out all that's going on and believe me , we know almost a percent of what's going on once we figure out what's going on , we're really going to be able to have a lot of control over what we do with our health , with what we do with future generations , and how long we're going to live .	一旦我們了解了這一切 , 相信我 , 我們就知道發生了什麼事 , 一旦我們了解了發生了什麼事 , 我們將會有很大的控制權 , 掌控我們對未來世代的影響 , 以及我們將會活多久 。
and hopefully we'll be able to use this to discover more truth , and more beauty .	希望我們能用它來發現更多真相 , 更美麗 。
but it's really quite amazing that these cells , these micromachines , are aware enough of what the cell needs that they do their bidding .	但這些細胞 , 這些微機械 , 非常了不起 , 足以了解細胞的需求 , 足以維持它們的支撐 。
they work together . they make the cell do what it needs to do .	它們一起工作 , 讓細胞做它需要做什麼 。
and their working together helps our bodies huge entities that they will never see function properly .	他們一起工作 , 協助我們的身體 , 讓它們永遠看不到正常的功能 。
enjoy the rest of the show . thank you .	享受剩下的節目 。 謝謝 。
becky blanton planned to live in her van for a year and see the country , but when depression set in and her freelance job ended , her camping trip turned into homelessness . in this intimate talk , she describes her experience of becoming one of america's working homeless .	貝克•布蘭頓計畫要在她的車上住一年 , 見到這個國家 , 但當憂鬱和她的自由工作結束時 , 她的營地變成了無家可歸 。 在這個親密的演講中 , 她描述了她成為美國無家可歸的經歷 。
adventure , happiness , life , personal growth , poverty , social change , society , storytelling	冒險、幸福、生活、個人成長、貧窮、社會改變、社會、說故事 , 講故事 。
becky blanton: the year i was homeless	貝琪•布蘭頓:那年 , 我是無家可歸的 。
i'm a writer and a journalist , and i'm also an insanely curious person , so in 22 years as a journalist , i've learned how to do a lot of new things .	我是作家和記者 , 我也是個好奇的人 , 在22年內 , 身為記者 , 我學了如何做很多新事 。
and three years ago , one of the things i learned how to do was to become invisible .	三年前 , 我學到的一件事情 , 就是變成隱形的 。
i became one of the working homeless .	我成為了無家可歸之家之一 。
i quit my job as a newspaper editor after my father died in february of that same year , and decided to travel .	我辭掉了我父親死於同一年二月的報紙編輯的工作 , 決定去旅行 。
his death hit me pretty hard .	他的死亡擊中了我 。
and there were a lot of things that i wanted to feel and deal with while i was doing that .	當我在做這件事時 , 我會想和處理很多事情 。
i've camped my whole life . and i decided that living in a van for a year to do this would be like one long camping trip .	我一生都在營運 , 我決定住在旅行車裡一年 , 要做這樣的事 , 就好像一個長期的營地 。
so i packed my cat , my rottweiler and my camping gear into a 1975 chevy van , and drove off into the sunset , having fully failed to realize three critical things .	所以我把我的貓、我的旋轉器和營地裝滿了1975年的清潔車 , 開車到日落 , 完全沒有意識到三件重要的事 。
one: that society equates living in a permanent structure , even a shack , with having value as a person .	第一:社會等同於一個永久的結構 , 甚至是一團糟 , 身為一個人的價值 。
two: i failed to realize how quickly the negative perceptions of other people can impact our reality , if we let it .	第二:我沒有意識到別人的負面認知 , 會如何影響我們的現實 , 如果我們放下它 。
three: i failed to realize that homelessness is an attitude , not a lifestyle .	三:我沒有意識到無家可歸是一種態度 , 而不是生活方式 。
at first , living in the van was great .	一開始 , 住在車上很棒 。
i showered in campgrounds . i ate out regularly .	我在營地表演 , 我常常吃飯 。
and i had time to relax and to grieve .	我有時間放鬆和悲慟 。
but then the anger and the depression about my father's death set in .	但接著憤怒和憂鬱 , 我父親的死亡就出現了 。
my freelance job ended . and i had to get a fulltime job to pay the bills .	我的自由工作結束了 , 我得付一份全職工作來支付帳單 。
what had been a really mild spring turned into a miserably hot summer .	一個非常溫和的春天 , 後來變成一個非常熱的夏天 。
and it became impossible to park anywhere without being very obvious that i had a cat and a dog with me , and it was really hot .	沒有任何地方的公園 , 很明顯我有一隻貓和一隻狗 , 真的很熱 。
the cat came and went through an open window in the van .	貓來了 , 穿過車子裡的窗戶 。
the doggy went into doggy day care .	小玩意兒進入了小玩意兒的日常生活 。
whenever i could , i used employee showers in office buildings and truck stops .	每當我可以 , 我都會用在辦公大樓裡的員工 , 卡車停下來 。
or i washed up in public rest rooms .	或是我在公共場所洗衣服 。
nighttime temperatures in the van rarely dropped below 80 degrees fahrenheit , making it difficult or impossible to sleep .	夜晚的溫度極少於華氏80度以下的華氏度 , 使得睡眠很難 。
food rotted in the heat .	食物在熱氣中轉動 。
ice in my ice chest melted within hours , and it was pretty miserable .	在我的冰塊中 , 幾小時內融化了 , 且它是非常悲慘的 。
i couldn't afford to find an apartment , or couldn't afford an apartment that would allow me to have the rottweiler and the cat .	我負擔不起找個公寓 , 或買不起公寓 , 讓我可以有旋轉者和貓 。
and i refused to give them up , so i stayed in the van .	我拒絕放棄他們 , 所以我待在車子裡 。
and when the heat made me too sick to walk the 50 feet to the public restroom outside my van at night , i used a bucket and a trash bag as a toilet .	當熱氣使我生病 , 走到五十英尺外的公共廁所 , 晚上我用桶和垃圾袋當廁所 。
when winter weather set in , the temperatures dropped below freezing . and they stayed there .	當冬天氣象進來時 , 溫度下降 , 停留在冰凍之下 。
and i faced a whole new set of challenges .	我面對了一系列的挑戰 。
i parked a different place every night so i would avoid being noticed and hassled by the police .	我每晚都停在一個不同的地方 , 讓我避免被警察察察覺並被警察察察察覺 。
i didn't always succeed .	我並不總是成功 。
but i felt out of control of my life .	但我感到無法掌控我的人生 。
and i don't know when or how it happened , but the speed at which i went from being a talented writer and journalist to being a homeless woman , living in a van , took my breath away .	我不知道發生了什麼事 , 但是我從一個有才華的作家和記者 , 變成一個無家可歸的女人 , 住在車子裡 , 把我的呼吸帶走 。
i hadn't changed . my i . q . hadn't dropped .	我沒有改變 。 我的智商 , 還沒有放棄 。
my talent , my integrity , my values , everything about me remained the same .	我的才華 , 我的正直、我的價值觀、我的價值觀 , 所有關於我的事都一樣 。
but i had changed somehow .	但我已經改變了 。
i spiraled deeper and deeper into a depression .	我轉向更深層、更深層的憂鬱 。
and eventually someone referred me to a homeless health clinic .	最後 , 有人幫我介紹一個無家可歸的健康診所 。
and i went . i hadn't bathed in three days .	我去了 。 我三天沒洗澡 。
i was as smelly and as depressed as anyone in line .	我和排隊中的任何人一樣緊張和沮喪 。
i just wasn't drunk or high .	我只是沒喝醉或很高 。
and when several of the homeless men realized that , including a former university professor , they said , " you aren't homeless . why are you really here ? "	當許多無家可歸的人意識到 , 包括前大學教授 , 他們說: 「 你不是無家可歸 。 你為什麼會在這裡 ? 」
other homeless people didn't see me as homeless , but i did .	其他無家可歸的人不認為我是無家可歸的 , 但我確實做到了 。
then the professor listened to my story and he said , " you have a job . you have hope .	接著 , 教授傾聽我的故事 , 他說: 「 你有工作 , 你有希望 。
the real homeless don't have hope . "	真正的無家可歸沒有希望 。 」
a reaction to the medication the clinic gave me for my depression left me suicidal . and i remember thinking , " if i killed myself , no one would notice . "	治療診所給了我憂鬱症的反應 。 我記得心想: 「 如果我殺了自己 , 沒有人會注意到 。 」
a friend told me , shortly after that , that she had heard that tim russert , a nationally renowned journalist , had been talking about me on national t . v .	不久之後 , 一位朋友告訴我 , 她聽說timrusert , 一個全國知名的記者 , 一直在說我在國家t.v 。
an essay i'd written about my father , the year before he died , was in tim's new book .	我寫了一篇關於我父親的論文 , 在他死前的那一年 , 他在提姆的新書中 。
and he was doing the talk show circuit . and he was talking about my writing .	他在做這場演說的電路 。 他在談論我的寫作 。
and when i realized that tim russert , former moderator of " meet the press , " was talking about my writing , while i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , i started laughing .	當我意識到 , timrussert , 《會議》的前任者 , 正在談我的寫作 , 當我住在華爾瑪的停車場 , 我開始笑 。
i started laughing because it got to the point where , was i a writer , or was i a homeless woman ?	我開始笑 , 因為它到了那個地方 , 我是一位作家 , 還是一個無家可歸的女人 ?
so i went in the bookstore . and i found tim's book .	所以我去了書店 , 我找到了tim的書 。
and i stood there . and i reread my essay .	我站在那裡 , 重返我的論文 。
because i was a writer .	因為我是個作家 。
i was a writer .	我是個作家 。
shortly after that i moved back to tennessee .	在那之後不久 , 我搬回田納西 。
i alternated between living in a van and couch surfing with friends .	我改變了生活在車廂和沙發衝浪的朋友之間 。
and i started writing again .	我又開始寫作 。
by the summer of the following year i was a working journalist .	接下來的一年夏天 , 我是一位職業記者 。
i was winning awards . i was living in my own apartment .	我贏得獎項 。 我住在我自己的公寓裡 。
i was no longer homeless .	我不再無家可歸 。
and i was no longer invisible .	我不再是隱形的 。
thousands of people work full and parttime jobs , and live in their cars .	數以千計的人全職工作 , 住在他們的車子裡 。
but society continues to stigmatize and criminalize living in your vehicle or on the streets .	但社會持續將生活在你的車上或在街道上被汙名化和犯罪化 。
so the homeless , the working homeless , primarily remain invisible .	所以無家可歸 , 工作無家可歸 , 主要還是隱形的 。
but if you ever meet one , engage them , encourage them , and offer them hope .	但如果你遇到一個人 , 加入他們 , 鼓勵他們 , 並提供他們希望 。
the human spirit can overcome anything if it has hope .	如果有希望的話 , 人類的精神可以克服任何事 。
and i'm not here to be the poster girl for the homeless .	我不是來這裡是無家可歸的海報 。
i'm not here to encourage you to give money to the next panhandler you meet .	我不是要鼓勵你們捐錢給下一個乞討者 。
but i am here to tell you that , based on my experience , people are not where they live , where they sleep , or what their life situation is at any given time .	但我來這裡要告訴各位 , 根據我的經驗 , 人們不是他們住的地方 , 他們睡在哪裡 , 或他們的人生狀況在任何時刻 。
three years ago i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , and today i'm speaking at ted .	三年前 , 我住在一個沃爾瑪停車場 , 今天我在ted演講 。
hope always , always finds a way . thank you .	希望總是找到一個方法 。 謝謝 。
at tedxchange , thailand's " mr . condom , " mechai viravaidya , walks us through the country's bold plan to raise its standard of living , starting in the 1970s . first step: population control . and that means a lot of frank , funny and very effective talk about condoms .	在tedxchange , 泰國的《保險套》 , mechaiviravaida , 走過我們國家的大膽計劃 , 從1970年代開始 , 第一步:人口控制 。 這意味著很多法蘭克、有趣的和非常有效的討論保險套 。
culture , global issues , health , population , science	文化、全球議題、健康、人口、科學、科學 。
mechai viravaidya: how mr . condom made thailand a better place	mechaiviraida:保險套如何讓泰國成為更好的地方 。
now , when i was a young man 40 years ago , the country was very , very poor with lots and lots and lots of people living in poverty .	四十年前 , 當我還是個年輕人時 , 這個國家非常貧窮 , 有許多人生活在貧困中 。
we decided to do something about it , but we didn't begin with a welfare program or a poverty reduction program .	我們決定要做點什麼 , 但我們不是從福利計畫開始 , 或是一個貧窮的減少計畫開始 。
but we began with a familyplanning program , following a very successful maternal child health activity , sets of activities .	但我們從一個家庭禁止計畫開始 , 遵循一個非常成功的孕產兒健康活動 , 一系列活動 。
so basically , no one would accept family planning if their children didn't survive .	基本上 , 沒有人會接受家庭規劃 , 如果他們的孩子沒有存活下來 。
so the first step: get to the children , get to the mothers , and then follow up with family planning .	所以 , 第一步:去看孩子 , 去看媽媽 , 然後跟著家庭計畫 。
not just child mortality alone , you need also family planning .	不只是兒童死亡率 , 你也需要家庭規劃 。
now let me take you back as to why we needed to do it .	現在 , 讓我帶各位回到為什麼我們需要這樣做 。
in my country , that was the case in 1974 .	在我的國家 , 那是1974年 。
seven children per family tremendous growth at 3 . 3 percent .	每個家庭的七個孩子成長率是3.3% 。
there was just no future .	沒有任何未來 。
we needed to reduce the population growth rate .	我們需要減少人口成長率 。
so we said , " let's do it . "	我們說: 「 我們來做吧 。 」
the women said , " we agree . we'll use pills , but we need a doctor to prescribe the pills , " and we had very , very few doctors .	女人說: 「 我們同意 , 我們會用藥丸 , 但我們需要醫生來開藥丸 。 」 我們有非常少的醫生 。
we didn't take no as an answer ; we took no as a question .	我們沒有把答案當成一個答案 , 我們把不當作一個問題 。
we went to the nurses and the midwives , who were also women , and did a fantastic job at explaining how to use the pill .	我們去了護士和助產士 , 同時也是女性 , 在解釋如何使用藥丸時 , 做了一個很棒的工作 。
that was wonderful , but it covered only 20 percent of the country .	那真是太棒了 , 但它只佔全國百分之二十 。
what do we do for the other 80 percent leave them alone and say , " well , they're not medical personnel . "	我們為其他80%的人做些什麼 ? 說: 「 嗯 , 他們不是醫療人員 。 」
no , we decided to do a bit more .	不 , 我們決定再多做一點 。
so we went to the ordinary people that you saw .	所以 , 我們去了你所看到的一般人 。
actually , below that yellow sign i wish they hadn't wiped that , because there was " cocacola " there .	事實上 , 在那黃色的標誌之下 , 我希望他們還沒聽過 , 因為那裡有 「 可口可樂 」 。
we were so much bigger than cocacola in those days .	當時我們比可口可樂更大 。
and no difference , the people they chose were the people we chose .	沒有差別 , 他們選的人就是我們選的人 。
they were wellknown in the community , they knew that customers were always right , and they were terrific , and they practiced their family planning themselves .	他們在社區中很知名 , 他們知道客戶一直是對的 , 他們很厲害 , 他們練習他們的家庭規劃他們自己 。
so they could supply pills and condoms throughout the country , in every village of the country .	所以他們可以在全國各地提供藥丸和保險套 。
so there we are . we went to the people who were seen as the cause of the problem to be the solution .	所以 , 我們就在那裡 。 我們去找那些被視為問題的成因 , 來解決方案 。
wherever there were people and you can see boats with the women , selling things here's the floating market selling bananas and crabs and also contraceptives wherever you find people , you'll find contraceptives in thailand .	不論在哪裡有人 , 你都能看見那些婦女 , 賣東西 , 這是漂浮的市場賣香蕉和螃蟹 , 還有避孕裝置 , 只要你在泰國找到人 , 你會在泰國找到避孕裝置 。
and then we decided , why not get to religion because in the philippines , the catholic church was pretty strong , and thai people were buddhist .	然後我們決定 , 為何不去宗教 , 因為在菲律賓 , 天主教堂很強壯 , 泰國人是佛教徒 。
we went to them and they said , " look , could you help us ? "	我們去找他們 , 他們說: 「 看 , 你能幫我們嗎 ? 」
i'm there the one in blue , not the yellow holding a bowl of holy water for the monk to sprinkle holy water on pills and condoms for the sanctity of the family .	我在藍色的那邊 , 不是黃色的拿著一碗聖水給僧人 , 用藥丸和保險套來吐水 。
and this picture was sent throughout the country .	這張照片是在全國各地寄來的 。
so some of the monks in the villages were doing the same thing themselves .	有些村莊的僧侶也在做同樣的事 。
and the women were saying , " no wonder we have no sideeffects .	女人說: 「 難怪我們沒有副作用 。
it's been blessed . "	它被祝福了 。 」
that was their perception .	那是他們的感知 。
and then we went to teachers .	然後我們去了老師 。
you need everybody to be involved in trying to provide whatever it is that make humanity a better place .	你需要每個人去試著提供任何讓人類成為一個更好的地方 。
so we went to the teachers .	所以我們去了老師們 。
over a quarter of a million were taught about family planning with a new alphabet a , b for birth , c for condom , i for iud , v for vasectomy .	超過四分之一的家庭計劃被教導要用新的字母a、b , 為了生育 , 保險套 , 我為iud , 維護陰道學 。
and then we had a snakes and ladders game , where you throw dice .	然後我們有了蛇和梯子遊戲 , 你扔掉的方向 。
if you land on anything profamily planning , you move ahead .	如果你在任何可行的規劃上登陸 , 你就向前移動 。
like , " mother takes the pill every night .	例如: 「 媽媽每天晚上都會吃藥 。
very good , mother . move ahead .	非常好 , 媽媽 , 繼續前進 。
uncle buys a condom . very good , uncle . move ahead .	叔叔買保險套 , 非常好 , 叔叔 , 前往 。
uncle gets drunk , doesn't use condom . come back , start again . "	叔叔喝酒 , 不用保險套 , 再回來吧 。 」
again , education , class entertainment .	再一次 , 教育 , 課堂娛樂 。
and the kids were doing it in school too .	孩子也在學校做這件事 。
we had relay races with condoms , we had children's condomblowing championship .	我們和保險套有相對的競爭 , 我們有孩子的保險套競賽 。
and before long , the condom was know as the girl's best friend .	不久之前 , 保險套被稱為女孩最好的朋友 。
in thailand , for poor people , diamonds don't make it so the condom is the girl's best friend .	在泰國 , 對貧窮的人來說 , 鑽石不會這樣做 , 保險套就是女孩最好的朋友 。
we introduced our first microcredit program in 1975 , and the women who organized it said , " we only want to lend to women who practice family planning .	我們在1975年推出了我們的第一個微型信息計畫 , 那些組織的女性說: 「 我們只想借給做家庭規劃的婦女 。
if you're pregnant , take care of your pregnancy .	如果你懷孕了 , 照顧你的懷孕 。
if you're not pregnant , you can take a loan out from us . "	如果你不懷孕 , 你可以從我們身上拿出一支貸款 。 」
and that was run by them .	這是他們所經營的 。
and after 35/36 years , it's still going on .	在35/36年之後 , 它仍然持續著 。
it's a part of the village development bank ; it's not a real bank , but it's a fund microcredit .	它是村落發展銀行的一部分 ; 它不是真正的銀行 , 但它是資金小額貸款 。
and we didn't need a big organization to run it it was run by the villagers themselves .	我們不需要一個大型組織來經營它 , 由村民自己運作 。
and you probably hardly see a thai man there , it's always women , women , women , women .	你可能看不見一個泰國男子 , 總是女人、女人、女人、女人 。
and then we thought we'd help america , because america's been helping everyone , whether they want help or not .	然後我們認為我們會幫助美國 , 因為美國一直在幫助每個人 , 不管他們是否想要幫忙 。
and this is on the fourth of july .	這是7月4日 。
we decided to provide vasectomy to all men , but in particular , american men to the front of the queue , right up to the ambassador's residence during his [unclear] .	我們決定為所有男人提供隱形體 , 但尤其是 , 美國男性站在隊伍的前面 , 位於阿巴斯德的住所 。
and the hotel gave us the ballroom for it very appropriate room .	旅館給了我們這間球場 , 非常適當的房間 。
and since it was near lunch time , they said , " all right , we'll give you some lunch .	自從很接近午餐時間 , 他們說: 「 好 , 我們會給你一些午餐 。
of course , it must be american cola .	當然 , 這一定是美國的可樂 。
you get two brands , coke and pepsi .	你有兩個品牌 , 可口可樂和百事可樂 。
and then the food is either hamburger or hotdog . "	然後食物是漢堡或熱狗 。 」
and i thought a hotdog will be more symbolic .	我覺得熱狗會更符合象徵性 。

i said , " don't worry . come over and i'll do the whole lot of you . "	我說: 「 別擔心 , 過來 , 我會做你們很多人 。 」
in all this thing , from seven children to 1 . 5 children , population growth rate of 3 . 3 to 0 . 5 .	在這一切中 , 從七個孩子到1.5個孩子 , 人口成長率是3.3.5 。

but it's everybody's job who can change attitude and behavior .	但每個人都能改變態度和行為 。
then aids came along and hit thailand , and we had to stop doing a lot of good things to fight aids .	接著愛滋病出現 , 撞到泰國 , 我們得要停止做很多好事來對抗愛滋病 。

so i went to the military and asked to borrow 300 radio stations .	所以我去了軍方 , 要求借300個電台 。

he became the chairman of the national aids committee and increased the budget fiftyfold .	他成為了國家愛滋病委員會的主席 , 增加了五十倍 。

and these girls who go around teaching about safe sex and hiv were known as mother theresa .	而這些女孩們圍繞著教導安全性愛和愛滋病感染的女孩 , 被稱為 「 媽媽 」 。
and then we went down one more step .	然後我們再走下一步 。
these are primary school kids third , fourth grade going to every household in the village , every household in the whole of thailand , giving aids information and a condom to every household , given by these young kids .	這些是小學三、四年級的孩子 , 在村子裡的每個家庭 , 每個家庭都有愛滋病資訊和保險套 , 由這些孩子提供 。

and they loved him . you need a symbol of something .	他們很愛他 , 你需要一個東西的象徵

because poor people are business people who lack business skills and access to credit .	因為窮人是商人 , 他們缺乏商業技能和取得信用 。

so , that was done .	所以 , 完成了 。
the money goes from the company into the village via treeplanting .	貨幣從公司到村落的村莊 , 再來是樹木 ,
it's not a free gift .	這不是免費的禮物 。
they plant the trees , and the money goes into their microcredit fund , which we call the village development bank .	他們種植樹木 , 金錢進到他們的微型基金 , 我們稱之為村落發展銀行 。
everybody joins in , and they feel they own the bank , because they have brought the money in .	每個人都加入 , 他們覺得自己擁有銀行 , 因為他們把錢帶進來 。
and before you can borrow the money , you need to be trained .	在你借錢之前 , 你得要被訓練 。
and we believe if you want to help the poor , those who are living in poverty , access to credit must be a human right .	我們相信如果你想要幫助窮人 , 那些生活在貧困中的人 , 取得信用信用必須是人權 。

otherwise they'll never get out of poverty .	否則他們永遠不會脫離貧窮 。

so anyone sitting in and watching tv , get in touch with me .	所以 , 任何人坐著看電視 , 跟我接觸 。

and then now , finally in education , we want to change the school as being underutilized into a place where it's a lifelong learning center for everyone .	現在 , 終於在教育中 , 我們想要改變學校 , 把學校當作被剝削到一個地方 , 讓每個人成為終身學習中心 。

your smartphone may feel like a friend but a true friend would give you a smile once in a while . at ted2013 , keller rinaudo demos romo , the smartphonepowered mini robot who can motor along with you on a walk , slide you a cup of coffee across the table , and react to you with programmable expressions .	你的智慧手機可能像朋友一樣 , 但真正的朋友會給你一陣微笑 。 在ted2013年 , 凱勒•里納多•狄摩斯 , 智慧型手機機器人可以跟你一起走路 , 把你一杯咖啡放在桌上 , 並且對你做出可程式的表情 。
keller rinaudo: a mini robot powered by your phone	kellerrinaudo:一台小型機器人 , 由你的手機發電 。
so just by a show of hands , how many of you all have a robot at home ?	請舉手 , 你們當中有多少人在家裡有機器人 ?
not very many of you .	不是你們很多人 。
okay . and actually of those hands , if you don't include roomba how many of you have a robot at home ?	好的 。 實際上 , 那些手 , 如果你不介紹室巴 , 你們當中有多少人在家裡有機器人 ?
that's the problem that we're trying to solve at romotive that i and the other 20 nerds at romotive are obsessed with solving .	這是我們在romotive解決的問題 , 我和其他20位romotive的怪胎 , 都對解決這個問題很著迷 。
so we really want to build a robot that anyone can use , whether you're eight or 80 .	所以 , 我們真的想要建立一個機器人 , 任何人都可以使用 , 不論你是八到八十歲 。
and as it turns out , that's a really hard problem , because you have to build a small , portable robot that's not only really affordable , but it has to be something that people actually want to take home and have around their kids .	結果發現 , 這真的是個很困難的問題 , 因為你必須建造一個小型、可攜式的機器人 , 不但能負擔得起 , 但它必須是人們真的想要回家 , 讓孩子身邊 。
this robot can't be creepy or uncanny .	這種機器人無法輕視或忽視 。
he should be friendly and cute .	他應該是友善且可愛的 。
romo's a robot that uses a device you already know and love your iphone as his brain .	romo是一個你已經知道且愛你的iphone的機器人 。
and by leveraging the power of the iphone's processor , we can create a robot that is wifi enabled and computer visioncapable for 150 bucks , which is about one percent of what these kinds of robots have cost in the past .	透過iphone處理器的力量 , 我們就能創造一個機器人 , 它能讓wi-fi和電腦視覺可用150美元 , 也就是過去這類機器人的成本 。
when romo wakes up , he's in creature mode .	當romo醒來時 , 他正處於生物模式 。
so he's actually using the video camera on the device to follow my face .	所以他實際上是用攝影機在裝置上來追蹤我的臉 。
if i duck down , he'll follow me .	如果我死了 , 他會跟著我 。
he's wary , so he'll keep his eyes on me .	他很害怕 , 所以他會把眼睛留在我身上 。
if i come over here , he'll turn to follow me .	如果我來這裡 , 他就會跟著我 。
if i come over here he's smart .	如果我來這裡 , 他很聰明 。
and if i get too close to him , he gets scared just like any other creature .	如果我太靠近他 , 他就會害怕任何其他生物 。
so in a lot of ways , romo is like a pet that has a mind of his own .	所以 , 在很多方面 , romo就像一隻寵物 , 他有自己的思想 。
thanks , little guy .	謝謝 , 小傢伙 。
and if i want to explore the world uhoh , romo's tired if i want to explore the world with romo , i can actually connect him from any other ios device .	如果我想要探索這個世界 , romo已經累壞了 , 如果我想要和romo一起探索這個世界 , 我真的可以將他與任何ios設備連結起來 。
so here's the ipad .	這是ipad 。
and romo will actually stream video to this device .	而romo實際上會把視頻傳給這個裝置 。

if i get in front of romo here .	如果我站在這裡 。
and if i want to control him , i can just drive .	如果我想要控制他 , 我可以開車 。
so i can drive him around , and i can take pictures of you .	所以 , 我可以隨身開車 , 我可以拍攝你們的照片 。

and in the same way that you scroll through content on an ipad , i can actually adjust the angle of the camera on the device .	就如同你在ipad上穿過的內容一樣 , 我可以在裝置上調整相機的角度 。
