but the most important thing about romo is that we wanted to create something that was literally completely intuitive .	但最重要的是 , 我們想要創造一個完全直覺的東西 。
you do not have to teach someone how to drive romo .	你不需要教別人如何駕駛romo 。
in fact , who would like to drive a robot ?	事實上 , 誰想驅動機器人 ?
thank you , scott .	謝謝你 , 史考特 。
and even cooler , you actually don't have to be in the same geographic location as the robot to control him .	更酷的是 , 你不需要在同一個地理位置上 , 來控制他 。
so he actually streams twoway audio and video between any two smart devices .	所以他實際上在兩台智慧型裝置之間偷走了雙向和影片 。
so you can log in through the browser , and it's kind of like skype on wheels .	你可以在瀏覽器上登入 , 有點像是輪子的skype 。
so we were talking before about telepresence , and this is a really cool example .	所以 , 我們先來談談電信 , 這是個很酷的例子 。
you can imagine an eightyearold girl , for example , who has an iphone , and her mom buys her a robot .	你可以想像一個八歲的女孩 , 舉例來說 , 她有iphone , 她媽媽買了一台機器人 。
that girl can take her iphone , put it on the robot , send an email to grandma , who lives on the other side of the country .	那個女孩可以拿她的iphone , 把它放在機器人上 , 把電子郵件寄給祖母 , 送到全國的另一端 。
grandma can log into that robot and play hideandgoseek with her granddaughter for fifteen minutes every single night , when otherwise she might only be able to get to see her granddaughter once or twice a year .	奶奶可以登入那個機器人 , 和她的孫女一起玩躲藏 , 每晚十五分鐘 , 否則她只能看見她的孫女 , 或一年兩倍 。
so those are a couple of the really cool things that romo can do today .	所以這些是romo今天能做到的一些很酷的事 。
but i just want to finish by talking about something that we're working on in the future .	但我只想談談我們未來正在努力的事物 。
this is actually something that one of our engineers , dom , built in a weekend .	這其實是我們其中一個工程師在週末建造的 。
it's built on top of a google open framework called blockly .	它是用google的開放框架建立在一個叫做 「 街區 」 的google框架上 。
this allows you to drag and drop these blocks of semantic code and create any behavior for this robot you want .	這樣就可以讓你拖著 , 把這些複雜的密碼堆積起來 , 為你所想要的機器人創造出任何行為 。
you do not have to know how to code to create a behavior for romo .	你不需要知道如何編寫程式來為romo創造一個行為 。
and you can actually simulate that behavior in the browser , which is what you see romo doing on the left .	你實際上可以模擬瀏覽器中的行為 , 左邊是romo在做的事 。
and then if you have something you like , you can download it onto your robot and execute it in real life , run the program in real life .	如果你有你喜歡的東西 , 你可以把它下載到你的機器人上 , 在真實生活中執行 , 執行這個程式 。
and then if you have something you're proud of , you can share it with every other person who owns a robot in the world .	如果你有你感到驕傲的 , 你可以和世界上所有擁有機器人的人分享 。
so all of these wifi–enabled robots actually learn from each other .	所有這些wi-fi的機器人 , 其實是從彼此身上學到的 。
the reason we're so focused on building robots that everyone can train is that we think the most compelling use cases in personal robotics are personal .	我們之所以專注在建立能訓練的機器人上 , 是因為我們認為 , 個人機械人最有說服力的案例是個人的 。
they change from person to person .	他們改變了人和人 。
so we think that if you're going to have a robot in your home , that robot ought to be a manifestation of your own imagination .	所以 , 我們認為如果你要在你的家中有一個機器人 , 機器人應該要成為你自己的想像力的展現 。
so i wish that i could tell you what the future of personal robotics looks like .	我希望我能告訴你個人機器人的未來是什麼樣子 。
to be honest , i have no idea .	老實說 , 我不知道 。
but what we do know is that it isn't 10 years or 10 billion dollars or a large humanoid robot away .	但我們確實知道 , 不是十年或一百億美金 , 或一大型人形機器人 。
the future of personal robotics is happening today , and it's going to depend on small , agile robots like romo and the creativity of people like yourselves .	個人機器人的未來正在發生 , 它將取決於小型、敏捷的機器人 , 例如romo , 以及像你這樣的人的創造力 。
so we can't wait to get you all robots , and we can't wait to see what you build .	所以 , 我們不能等待你全部的機器人 , 我們等不及要看你所建造的 。
author and activist isabel allende discusses women , creativity , the definition of feminism and , of course , passion in this talk .	作者和活躍主義者是阿拉伯女性 , 創造力 , 女性主義的定義 , 當然 , 在這場演說中 , 熱情是如此 。
entertainment , global issues , love , parenting , storytelling , women , world cultures	娛樂、全球議題、愛、養育、說故事、女性、世界文化、文化、世界文化、文化 。
isabel allende tells tales of passion	伊莎貝爾•艾倫說過熱情的故事 。
thank you so much . it's really scary to be here among the smartest of the smart .	非常謝謝你 。 非常可怕 , 非常可怕 , 非常聰明 。
i'm here to tell you a few tales of passion .	我來這裡是要告訴各位一些熱情的故事 。
there's a jewish saying that i love .	有一個猶太人說我喜歡 。
what is truer than truth ? answer: the story .	什麼是真相 ? 答案是:故事 。
i'm a storyteller . i want to convey something that is truer than truth about our common humanity .	我是個說故事的人 。 我想傳達出比我們共同的人道真相更真實的東西 。
all stories interest me , and some haunt me until i end up writing them .	所有故事都對我感興趣 , 直到我終於寫下它們 。
certain themes keep coming up: justice , loyalty , violence , death , political and social issues , freedom .	有些主題不斷出現:正義、忠誠、暴力、死亡、政治和社會議題、自由 。
i'm aware of the mystery around us , so i write about coincidences , premonitions , emotions , dreams , the power of nature , magic .	我知道我們周圍的謎團 , 所以我寫下巧合、預演、情緒、夢想、大自然的力量、魔法 。
in the last 20 years i have published a few books , but i have lived in anonymity until february of 2006 , when i carried the olympic flag in the winter olympics in italy .	在過去的20年裡 , 我出版了幾本書 , 但我住在2006年2月 , 直到我在義大利的奧林匹克國旗 。
that made me a celebrity . now people recognize me in macy's , and my grandchildren think that i'm cool .	這讓我成為了名人 。 現在人們認得我是macy的 , 而我的孫子認為我很酷 。
allow me to tell you about my four minutes of fame .	容我告訴你我四分鐘的名氣 。
one of the organizers of the olympic ceremony , of the opening ceremony , called me and said that i had been selected to be one of the flagbearers .	奧林匹克儀式的組織者 , 打開儀式 , 打電話給我 , 說我被選為旗幟的一員 。
i replied that surely this was a case of mistaken identity because i'm as far as you can get from being an athlete .	我回答說 , 這肯定是錯誤的身分認同的案例 , 因為我可以從運動員身上得到的 。
actually , i wasn't even sure that i could go around the stadium without a walker .	事實上 , 我甚至不確定我可以在沒有步行者的體育場四周 。
i was told that this was no laughing matter .	我被告知 , 這不是笑話 。
this would be the first time that only women would carry the olympic flag .	這是第一次 , 只有婦女會攜帶奧林匹克國旗 。
five women , representing five continents , and three olympic gold medal winners .	五個女人 , 代表五個大陸 , 三位奧運金牌贏家 。
my first question was , naturally , what was i going to wear ?	我的第一個問題是 , 很自然的 , 我將要穿什麼 ?
a uniform , she said , and asked for my measurements .	一個制服 , 她說 , 問了我的測量 。
i had a vision of myself in a fluffy anorak , looking like the michelin man .	我有一個想像 , 在一個流暢的亂流中 , 看起來像是米開林人 。
by the middle of february , i found myself in turin , where enthusiastic crowds cheered when any of the 80 olympic teams was in the street .	在二月中期 , 我發現自己在土耳其 , 那裡有熱情的群眾歡呼 , 在街上有80個奧運隊在街上 。
those athletes had sacrificed everything to compete in the games .	那些運動員犧牲了所有東西來競爭遊戲 。
they all deserved to win , but there's the element of luck .	他們都應得勝利 , 但運氣的元素 。
a speck of snow , an inch of ice , the force of the wind , can determine the result of a race or a game .	一英吋的雪 , 一英吋的冰 , 風的力量 , 可以決定種族或遊戲的結果 。
however , what matters most more than training or luck is the heart .	然而 , 最重要的是訓練或運氣是心臟 。
only a fearless and determined heart will get the gold medal .	只有一種無畏和堅決的心才會得到金牌 。
it is all about passion .	這一切都是關於熱情 。
the streets of turin were covered with red posters announcing the slogan of the olympics .	土耳其的街道被紅海報覆蓋 , 宣佈奧運的口號 。
passion lives here . isn't it always true ?	熱情生活在這裡 , 不是嗎 ?
heart is what drives us and determines our fate .	心是驅使我們和決定我們的命運 。
that is what i need for my characters in my books: a passionate heart .	這就是我在我的書中所需要的:熱情的心 。
i need mavericks , dissidents , adventurers , outsiders and rebels , who ask questions , bend the rules and take risks .	我需要mavericks、異議者、異議者、外人、反叛者 , 他們問問題、彎曲規則、冒險 。
people like all of you in this room .	像在座所有人一樣 。
nice people with common sense do not make interesting characters .	一個常識的人 , 沒有創造有趣的角色 。
they only make good former spouses .	它們只會製造出好的前配偶 。
in the green room of the stadium , i met the other flag bearers: three athletes , and the actresses susan sarandon and sophia loren .	在體育場的綠色房間裡 , 我遇見了其他的旗幟熊:三位運動員 , 也是索菲亞•羅倫 。
also , two women with passionate hearts: wangari maathai , the nobel prizewinner from kenya who has planted 30 million trees . and by doing so , she has changed the soil , the weather , in some places in africa , and of course the economic conditions in many villages .	此外 , 有兩個充滿熱情的婦女 , 一個來自肯亞的諾貝爾獎得主 , 她種植了三千萬棵樹 。 藉此 , 她改變了土壤 , 天氣 , 在非洲的某些地方 , 當然還有許多村莊的經濟狀況 。
and somaly mam , a cambodian activist who fights passionately against child prostitution .	媽媽媽 , 柬埔寨的活動家 , 熱情地對抗兒童賣淫 。
when she was 14 years old , her grandfather sold her to a brothel .	當她十四歲時 , 她的祖父把她賣給兄弟 。
she told us of little girls raped by men who believe that having sex with a very young virgin will cure them from aids .	她告訴我們小女孩被男人強暴 , 她們相信在愛滋病中有性行為 , 會治癒她們 。
and of brothels where children are forced to receive five , 15 clients per day , and if they rebel , they are tortured with electricity .	在那裡 , 孩子們被迫每天收到五、十五個客戶 , 如果他們反抗 , 他們就會受到電力折磨 。
in the green room i received my uniform .	在綠色的房間裡 , 我收到了制服 。
it was not the kind of outfit that i normally wear , but it was far from the michelin man suit that i had anticipated . not bad , really .	這不是我一般穿的衣服 , 而是來自密西林人的服裝 , 我預期的不是很糟 , 真的很糟 。
i looked like a refrigerator .	我看起來像是冰箱 。
but so did most of the flagbearers , except sophia loren , the universal symbol of beauty and passion .	但 , 大部分的旗幟家 , 除了蘇菲亞洛倫 , 美和熱情的普遍象徵 。
sophia is over 70 and she looks great .	蘇菲亞超過70歲 , 她看起來很棒 。
she's sexy , slim and tall , with a deep tan .	她很性感、很瘦、很高、很高、很高 。
now , how can you have a deep tan and have no wrinkles ?	那麼 , 你如何能擁有一個深刻的坦克斯 , 沒有皺紋 ?
when asked in a tv interview , " how could she look so good ? "	在電視訪談中被問到: 「 她怎麼看起來這麼好 ? 」
she replied , " posture . my back is always straight , and i don't make old people's noises . "	她回答: 「 姿勢 , 我的背總是直直的 , 我不會讓老人的噪音 。 」
so , there you have some free advice from one of the most beautiful women on earth .	所以 , 這裡有一些免費的建議 , 來自地球上最美麗的女性 。
no grunting , no coughing , no wheezing , no talking to yourselves , no farting .	沒有誇張 , 沒有咳嗽 , 沒有吹口哨 , 沒有跟自己說話 , 沒有遙控 。
well , she didn't say that exactly .	嗯 , 她並沒有說這句話 。
at some point around midnight , we were summoned to the wings of the stadium , and the loudspeakers announced the olympic flag , and the music started by the way , the same music that starts here , the aida march .	在午夜的某個時點 , 我們被召喚到體育場的翅膀 , 大聲調員宣佈奧運國旗 , 音樂從這裡開始 , 相同的音樂從這裡開始 , 艾達•馬赫 。
sophia loren was right in front of me she's a foot taller than i am , not counting the poofy hair .	蘇菲亞•羅倫在我面前 , 她比我高一英尺 , 不是在計算小毛髮 。
she walked elegantly , like a giraffe on the african savannah , holding the flag on her shoulder . i jogged behind on my tiptoes holding the flag on my extended arm , so that my head was actually under the damn flag .	她走得很優雅 , 像非洲大草原上的長頸鹿 , 把旗子放在肩膀上 , 我在我的尖邊伸出旗子 , 所以我的頭其實是在丹旗下 。
all the cameras were , of course , on sophia .	當然 , 所有的相機都在蘇菲亞 。
that was fortunate for me , because in most press photos i appear too , although often between sophia's legs .	這對我來說很幸運 , 因為在大部分的媒體照片中 , 我也出現在蘇菲亞的雙腿之間 。
a place where most men would love to be .	大部分男人都喜歡成為一個地方 。
the best four minutes of my entire life were those in the olympic stadium .	我人生中最棒的四分鐘是奧林匹克體育館裡的那些人 。
my husband is offended when i say this although i have explained to him that what we do in private usually takes less than four minutes so he shouldn't take it personally .	當我說這句話時 , 我的丈夫被冒犯了 , 雖然我向他解釋 , 我們在私下的做法通常只花不到四分鐘 , 所以他不應該私下採取它 。
i have all the press clippings of those four magnificent minutes , because i don't want to forget them when old age destroys my brain cells .	我有四分鐘的媒體按鈕 , 因為我不想忘記 , 古老的腦細胞破壞我的大腦細胞 。
i want to carry in my heart forever the key word of the olympics passion .	我想永遠帶著奧林匹克熱情的關鍵字 。
so here's a tale of passion .	這是個充滿熱情的故事 。
the year is 1998 , the place is a prison camp for tutsi refugees in congo .	今年是1998年 , 剛果的特魯西難民營是個監獄營 。
by the way , 80 percent of all refugees and displaced people in the world are women and girls .	順道一提 , 世界上80%的難民和歧視者是女性和女孩 。
we can call this place in congo a death camp , because those who are not killed will die of disease or starvation .	我們可以稱之為 「 剛果死亡營地 」 , 因為那些未被殺死的人 , 會死於疾病或飢餓 。
the protagonists of this story are a young woman , rose mapendo , and her children .	這個故事的主角是一位年輕女子 , 羅塞•地圖 , 和她的孩子 。
she's pregnant and a widow .	她懷孕和寡婦 。
soldiers have forced her to watch as her husband was tortured and killed .	士兵強迫她去看她的丈夫被虐待和殺害 。
somehow she manages to keep her seven children alive , and a few months later , she gives birth to premature twins .	不知怎麼的 , 她能讓她七個孩子活下來 , 幾個月後 , 她生下了雙胞胎 。
two tiny little boys .	兩個小男孩 。
she cuts the umbilical cord with a stick , and ties it with her own hair .	她用棍子來切斷腫瘤 , 用自己的頭髮做結合 。
she names the twins after the camp's commanders to gain their favor , and feeds them with black tea because her milk cannot sustain them .	她把雙胞胎命名為營隊的指揮者 , 以獲得他們的利益 , 餵飽黑人茶 , 因為她的牛奶無法維持它們 。
when the soldiers burst in her cell to rape her oldest daughter , she grabs hold of her and refuses to let go , even when they hold a gun to her head .	當軍人在她的牢房中強暴她最老的女兒時 , 她抓住她的女兒 , 拒絕放手 , 即使她們拿著槍頭 。
somehow , the family survives for 16 months , and then , by extraordinary luck , and the passionate heart of a young american man , sasha chanoff , who manages to put her in a u . s . rescue plane , rose mapendo and her nine children end up in phoenix , arizona , where they're now living and thriving .	不知怎麼的 , 家庭存活了16個月 , 接著 , 由亞利桑那州 , 一位年輕人的熱情之心 , 薩薩哈•查諾夫 , 把她送進美國救援飛機 , 羅斯•貝多和她的九個孩子最後到了鳳凰 , 亞利桑納 , 在那裡 , 他們活著和茁壯 。
mapendo , in swahili , means great love .	在斯瓦希里 , 地圖是很棒的愛 。
the protagonists of my books are strong and passionate women like rose mapendo .	我的書中的主角是堅強且熱情的女性 , 例如羅斯地圖 。
i don't make them up . there's no need for that .	我不會把它們弄出來 , 沒有必要的 。
i look around and i see them everywhere .	我環顧四周 , 無所不在 。
i have worked with women and for women all my life .	我一生都在與女性和女性一起工作 。
i know them well .	我知道他們很清楚 。
i was born in ancient times , at the end of the world , in a patriarchal catholic and conservative family .	我出生於古代 , 在世界末日 , 在父權天主教和保守家庭中 。
no wonder that by age five i was a raging feminist although the term had not reached chile yet , so nobody knew what the heck was wrong with me .	難怪在我五歲時 , 我是個憤怒的女權主義者雖然這個詞尚未接觸到智利 , 所以沒有人知道我是怎麼回事的 。
i would soon find out that there was a high price to pay for my freedom , and for questioning the patriarchy .	我很快就會發現 , 為我的自由付出很高的代價 , 並且質疑父權主義 。
but i was happy to pay it , because for every blow that i received , i was able to deliver two .	但我很高興能付出這筆錢 , 因為每一股我都能付出兩台錢 。
once , when my daughter paula was in her twenties , she said to me that feminism was dated , that i should move on .	有一次 , 我女兒保拉在她二十歲時 , 她對我說女權主義是約會的 , 我應該繼續下去 。
we had a memorable fight . feminism is dated ?	我們有了不可思議的鬥爭 , 女權主義是約會的 ?
yes , for privileged women like my daughter and all of us here today , but not for most of our sisters in the rest of the world who are still forced into premature marriage , prostitution , forced labor they have children that they don't want or they cannot feed .	是的 , 對於像我女兒和所有人這樣的特權女性來說 , 現今在世界上大部分的姊妹仍然被強迫做早婚、妓女、迫使勞工 , 她們有孩子 , 她們不想要或不能餵飽 。
they have no control over their bodies or their lives .	他們無法控制自己的身體或自己的生命 。
they have no education and no freedom .	他們沒有教育 , 也沒有自由 。
they are raped , beaten up and sometimes killed with impunity .	他們被強暴、被毆打、有時被無罪殺 。
for most western young women of today , being called a feminist is an insult .	至今大部分的西方女性 , 被稱為女性主義者是一種侮辱 。
feminism has never been sexy , but let me assure you that it never stopped me from flirting , and i have seldom suffered from lack of men .	女權主義從來沒有性感 , 但讓我向你保證 , 它從來沒有阻止我發情 , 而我也因為缺乏男性而遭受過嚴重的痛苦 。
feminism is not dead , by no means .	女權主義沒有死 , 沒有意義 。
it has evolved . if you don't like the term , change it , for goddess' sake .	它演化了 。 如果你不喜歡這個詞 , 改變它 , 改變它 , 給女神的選擇 。
call it aphrodite , or venus , or bimbo , or whatever you want ; the name doesn't matter , as long as we understand what it is about , and we support it .	稱之為 「 異性 」 , 金星 , 或任何你想要的 , 名字並不重要 , 只要我們了解它是什麼 , 我們就支持它 。
so here's another tale of passion , and this is a sad one .	這是另外一個熱情的故事 , 這是個悲傷的例子 。
the place is a small women's clinic in a village in bangladesh .	這個地方是一個小婦女診所 , 位於孟加拉的村莊 。
the year is 2005 .	今年是2005年 。
jenny is a young american dental hygienist who has gone to the clinic as a volunteer during her threeweek vacation .	珍妮是一位年輕的美國牙醫衛生學家 , 她在三週的假期中擔任志工 。
she's prepared to clean teeth , but when she gets there , she finds out that there are no doctors , no dentists , and the clinic is just a hut full of flies .	她準備要清潔牙齒 , 但當她到達那裡時 , 她發現沒有醫生 , 沒有牙醫 , 診所只是充滿蒼蠅的小屋 。
outside , there is a line of women who have waited several hours to be treated .	外面有一群女人 , 等了幾個小時才能被治療 。
the first patient is in excruciating pain because she has several rotten molars .	第一位病人在痛苦中 , 是因為她有幾種腐爛的腫瘤 。
jenny realizes that the only solution is to pull out the bad teeth .	珍妮知道 , 唯一的解決方案就是拿出壞牙齒 。
she's not licensed for that ; she has never done it .	她不為此授權 ; 她從來沒有做過 。
she risks a lot and she's terrified .	她冒了很多險 , 且她很害怕 。
she doesn't even have the proper instruments , but fortunately she has brought some novocaine .	她甚至沒有適當的樂器 , 但幸運的是她帶了一些新鮮事 。
jenny has a brave and passionate heart .	珍妮有勇敢和熱情的心 。
she murmurs a prayer and she goes ahead with the operation .	她是一位禱告師 , 她向前走 。
at the end , the relieved patient kisses her hands .	最後 , 幻想的病人親吻她的手 。
that day the hygienist pulls out many more teeth .	那天 , 衛生學家拉出更多牙齒 。
the next morning , when she comes again to the socalled clinic , her first patient is waiting for her with her husband .	隔天早上 , 她再次來到所謂的診所 , 她的第一位病人正在和丈夫等著她 。
the woman's face looks like a watermelon .	女人的臉看起來就像是水手 。
it is so swollen that you can't even see the eyes .	你甚至看不到眼睛的腫脹 。
the husband , furious , threatens to kill the american .	丈夫 , 非常憤怒 , 威脅要殺死美國人 。
jenny is horrified at what she has done , but then the translator explains that the patient's condition has nothing to do with the operation .	珍妮對她所做的事感到害怕 , 但翻譯解釋病人的狀況和手術無關 。
the day before , her husband beat her up because she was not home in time to prepare dinner for him .	前一天 , 她的丈夫打敗她 , 因為她當時不在家 , 為他準備晚餐 。
millions of women live like this today .	現今有數百萬名女性生活在這裡 。
they are the poorest of the poor .	他們是窮人中最窮的人 。
although women do twothirds of the world's labor , they own less than one percent of the world's assets .	雖然女性有三分之二的勞動力 , 但她們擁有世界上少於1%的資產 。
they are paid less than men for the same work if they're paid at all , and they remain vulnerable because they have no economic independence , and they are constantly threatened by exploitation , violence and abuse .	他們的薪水低於同事 , 如果他們薪水很低 , 他們仍然很脆弱 , 因為他們沒有經濟獨立 , 且他們經常受到剝削、暴力和虐待 。
it is a fact that giving women education , work , the ability to control their own income , inherit and own property , benefits the society .	事實上 , 給予婦女教育、工作能力、控制自己的收入、繼承和自身財產 , 讓社會受益 。
if a woman is empowered , her children and her family will be better off .	如果一個女人被賦予權力 , 她的孩子和家人會更好 。
if families prosper , the village prospers , and eventually so does the whole country .	如果家庭繁榮 , 村子繁榮 , 最終 , 整個國家也是如此 。
wangari maathai goes to a village in kenya .	wangarimaathai到肯亞的一個村子 。
she talks with the women and explains that the land is barren because they have cut and sold the trees .	她跟女人說話 , 解釋土地是barren , 因為他們已經砍樹 , 賣樹木 。
she gets the women to plant new trees and water them , drop by drop .	她讓婦女去種新的樹和水 , 一滴一滴下去 。
in a matter of five or six years , they have a forest , the soil is enriched , and the village is saved .	在5或6年之內 , 他們有一片森林 , 土壤充滿豐富 , 村子就拯救了 。
the poorest and most backward societies are always those that put women down .	最貧窮和最後退的社會總是把女人放下 。
yet this obvious truth is ignored by governments and also by philanthropy .	然而 , 這種顯而易見的事實卻被政府和慈善事業忽略了 。
for every dollar given to a women's program , 20 dollars are given to men's programs .	每一塊錢給婦女計畫 , 每一塊20塊美金給男人的計畫 。
women are 51 percent of humankind .	女性是51%的人 。
empowering them will change everything more than technology and design and entertainment .	給予他們力量 , 將改變一切 , 遠超過科技和設計和娛樂 。
i can promise you that women working together linked , informed and educated can bring peace and prosperity to this forsaken planet .	我可以向各位保證 , 女性一起工作、聯繫、資訊、受過教育 , 能讓和平和繁榮帶給這個史無前例的星球 。
in any war today , most of the casualties are civilians , mainly women and children . they are collateral damage .	在任何戰爭中 , 大部分的傷亡都是平民 , 主要是女人和小孩 。 他們是相對的傷害 。
men run the world , and look at the mess we have .	男人跑遍世界 , 看看我們有哪一團糟 。
what kind of world do we want ?	我們想要什麼樣的世界 ?
this is a fundamental question that most of us are asking .	這是我們大多數人在問的一個根本問題 。
does it make sense to participate in the existing world order ?	要參與現有的世界秩序是有道理的嗎 ?
we want a world where life is preserved and the quality of life is enriched for everybody , not only for the privileged .	我們想要一個世界 , 生活的品質和生活的品質 , 不僅是對所有人的特權而已 。
in january i saw an exhibit of fernando botero's paintings at the uc berkeley library .	在一月 , 我看到了fernandobotero的畫作 , 在加州柏克萊圖書館 。
no museum or gallery in the united states , except for the new york gallery that carries botero's work , has dared to show the paintings because the theme is the abu ghraib prison .	沒有美國的博物館或藝廊 , 除了紐約的畫廊 , 那些帶著波特羅的作品 , 都很高興能展現這幅畫 , 因為主題是阿布格拉伯監獄 。
they are huge paintings of torture and abuse of power , in the voluminous botero style .	它們是巨大的虐待和濫用權力的大畫作 , 在大型的玻璃風格中 。
i have not been able to get those images out of my mind or my heart .	我無法把這些影像從我的心中得到 , 或我的心中 。
what i fear most is power with impunity .	我最擔心的是 「 不幸 」 的力量 。
i fear abuse of power , and the power to abuse .	我害怕濫用權力和濫用權力 。
in our species , the alpha males define reality , and force the rest of the pack to accept that reality and follow the rules .	在我們的物種中 , 雄性領袖定義了現實 , 迫使其餘的包裝接受現實 , 並遵循規則 。
the rules change all the time , but they always benefit them , and in this case , the trickledown effect , which does not work in economics , works perfectly .	規則不斷地改變 , 但他們總是有益 , 在這個案例中 , 被欺騙的效果 , 在經濟上行不通 , 完美地運作 。
abuse trickles down from the top of the ladder to the bottom .	從梯子的頂端 , 虐待技巧從梯子的頂端到底部 。
women and children , especially the poor , are at the bottom .	女性和孩子 , 尤其是窮人 , 在底部 。
even the most destitute of men have someone they can abuse a woman or a child .	即使是男人中最多的學徒 , 他們也能虐待一個女人或一個小孩 。
i'm fed up with the power that a few exert over the many through gender , income , race , and class .	我得到的力量是少於性別、收入、種族、階級的權力 。
i think that the time is ripe to make fundamental changes in our civilization .	我認為 , 時間是為了在我們的文明中做出根本的改變 。
but for real change , we need feminine energy in the management of the world .	但對真正的改變 , 我們需要女性化的精力在世界上的管理上 。
we need a critical number of women in positions of power , and we need to nurture the feminine energy in men .	我們需要很多女性在權力的位置上 , 我們需要培養男性的女性能量 。
i'm talking about men with young minds , of course .	當然 , 我在談的是年輕人的心智 。
old guys are hopeless ; we have to wait for them to die off .	老年人是無希望的 ; 我們必須等待他們死去 。
yes , i would love to have sophia loren's long legs and legendary breasts .	是的 , 我很想有索菲亞•洛倫的長腿和傳奇的胸部 。
but given a choice , i would rather have the warrior hearts of wangari maathai , somaly mam , jenny and rose mapendo .	但 , 為了一個選擇 , 我寧願有天使的熱心 , 瑪麗 , 媽媽 , 珍妮和玫瑰地圖 。
i want to make this world good .	我想要讓這個世界好 。
not better , but to make it good .	不是更好 , 而是要讓它更好 。
why not ? it is possible . look around in this room all this knowledge , energy , talent and technology .	為何不 ? 它是可能的 。 看看這間房間裡的知識、能量、才華和科技 。
let's get off our fannies , roll up our sleeves and get to work , passionately , in creating an almost perfect world .	咱們走下去 , 捲起袖子 , 熱情地工作 , 創造一個幾乎完美的世界 。
every day , in a city the size of london , 30 million meals are served . but where does all the food come from ? architect carolyn steel discusses the daily miracle of feeding a city , and shows how ancient food routes shaped the modern world .	每一天 , 倫敦的大小 , 三千萬份餐都被服務 。 但所有食物都來自哪裡 ? 建築師卡林•史蒂爾討論城市的日常奇蹟 , 並展現古老的糧食路線如何塑造現代的世界 。
cities , culture , food , global issues	城市、文化、食物、全球議題、全球議題 。
carolyn steel: how food shapes our cities	嘉賓史蒂爾:食物如何塑造我們的城市 。
how do you feed a city ?	你要如何餵飽城市 ?
it's one of the great questions of our time .	這是我們時代最棒的問題之一 。
yet it's one that's rarely asked .	但很少被問到 。
we take it for granted that if we go into a shop or restaurant , or indeed into this theater's foyer in about an hour's time , there is going to be food there waiting for us , having magically come from somewhere .	我們把它視為理所當然 , 如果我們走進商店或餐廳 , 或是在一小時內進入這個劇院的foyer , 那裡將會有食物等著我們 , 神奇地來自某處 。
but when you think that every day for a city the size of london , enough food has to be produced , transported , bought and sold , cooked , eaten , disposed of , and that something similar has to happen every day for every city on earth , it's remarkable that cities get fed at all .	但當你想到 , 倫敦的城市的大小 , 食物必須被生產、運送、購買、吃、丟棄、丟棄 , 類似的事情 , 都必須在地球上每一天發生 , 城市都能被餵食 。
we live in places like this as if they're the most natural things in the world , forgetting that because we're animals and that we need to eat , we're actually as dependent on the natural world as our ancient ancestors were .	我們生活在這樣的地方 , 彷彿他們是世界上最自然的事物 , 忘了 , 因為我們是動物 , 我們需要吃 , 我們其實是依賴自然界的祖先 。
and as more of us move into cities , more of that natural world is being transformed into extraordinary landscapes like the one behind me it's soybean fields in mato grosso in brazil in order to feed us .	隨著我們進入城市 , 越來越多的自然世界被轉化成非凡的景觀 , 像我身後的這個景觀 , 它在巴西的馬托格羅索 , 為了餵飽我們 。
these are extraordinary landscapes , but few of us ever get to see them .	這些是非凡的景觀 , 但少數人見到它們 。
and increasingly these landscapes are not just feeding us either .	而這些地景越來越多 , 不單只是給我們餵食 。
as more of us move into cities , more of us are eating meat , so that a third of the annual grain crop globally now gets fed to animals rather than to us human animals .	隨著我們進入城市 , 越來越多人吃肉 , 所以每年全球有三分之一的農作物被餵食給動物 , 而非我們人類的動物 。
and given that it takes three times as much grain actually ten times as much grain to feed a human if it's passed through an animal first , that's not a very efficient way of feeding us .	既然它需要三倍的穀物才能餵飽人類 , 如果它通過動物的第一條路 , 那就不是非常有效率的餵養我們 。
and it's an escalating problem too .	這也是一個惡化的問題 。
by 2050 , it's estimated that twice the number of us are going to be living in cities .	到了2050年 , 估計我們在城市中有兩倍的人口 。
and it's also estimated that there is going to be twice as much meat and dairy consumed .	據估計 , 肉類和乳類消耗量會增加兩倍 。
so meat and urbanism are rising hand in hand .	肉類和都市主義正在舉手 。
and that's going to pose an enormous problem .	這會帶來巨大的問題 。
six billion hungry carnivores to feed , by 2050 .	到2050年 , 60億隻飢餓的食肉食品 。
that's a big problem . and actually if we carry on as we are , it's a problem we're very unlikely to be able to solve .	這是個很大的問題 。 實際上 , 如果我們繼續這樣下去 , 這是個我們無法解決的問題 。
nineteen million hectares of rainforest are lost every year to create new arable land .	每年有九百萬公頃的雨林失去 , 創造出新的可耕地 。
although at the same time we're losing an equivalent amount of existing arables to salinization and erosion .	雖然同時 , 我們也失去了相當多現有的可耕種 , 來達成鹽化和侵蝕 。
we're very hungry for fossil fuels too .	我們對化石燃料也很渴望 。
it takes about 10 calories to produce every calorie of food that we consume in the west .	要花大約10卡路里才能產生我們在西方所消耗的每一卡路里 。
and even though there is food that we are producing at great cost , we don't actually value it .	儘管我們有很大的成本生產食物 , 我們其實不重視它 。
half the food produced in the usa is currently thrown away .	美國目前有一半的食物會被丟棄 。
and to end all of this , at the end of this long process , we're not even managing to feed the planet properly .	為了結束這一切 , 在長程結束後 , 我們甚至無法妥善管理地球的糧食 。
a billion of us are obese , while a further billion starve .	我們當中有十億人肥胖 , 同時又是十億人挨餓 。
none of it makes very much sense .	沒有什麼意義 。
and when you think that 80 percent of global trade in food now is controlled by just five multinational corporations , it's a grim picture .	當你認為80%的全球貿易現在被五大企業控制時 , 全球交易是很嚴格的 。
as we're moving into cities , the world is also embracing a western diet .	隨著我們進入城市 , 世界也在擁抱西方的飲食 。
and if we look to the future , it's an unsustainable diet .	如果我們看看未來 , 它是種無法永續的飲食 。
so how did we get here ?	我們是怎麼走到這一步的 ?
and more importantly , what are we going to do about it ?	更重要的是 , 我們要怎麼做 ?
well , to answer the slightly easier question first , about 10 , 000 years ago , i would say , is the beginning of this process in the ancient near east , known as the fertile crescent .	首先 , 來回答這個問題 , 大約一萬年前 , 我會說 , 這個過程的開端是古老的東岸 , 所謂的肥沃口腔 。
because , as you can see , it was crescent shaped .	因為 , 正如你所見 , 最近的形狀 。
and it was also fertile .	同時也是肥沃 。
and it was here , about 10 , 000 years ago , that two extraordinary inventions , agriculture and urbanism , happened roughly in the same place and at the same time .	大約一萬年前 , 這裡有兩個非凡的發明 , 農業和城市主義 , 發生在同一個地方 , 同時發生了 。
this is no accident , because agriculture and cities are bound together . they need each other .	這不是意外 , 因為農業和城市是互相連結的 。 他們需要彼此 。
because it was discovery of grain by our ancient ancestors for the first time that produced a food source that was large enough and stable enough to support permanent settlements .	因為它是從我們古老的祖先所發現的穀物 , 第一次產生出足夠的食物來源 , 足以維持永久的居住地 。
and if we look at what those settlements were like , we see they were compact .	如果我們看看這些定居處的樣子 , 我們會發現它們是完整的 。
they were surrounded by productive farm land and dominated by large temple complexes like this one at ur , that were , in fact , effectively , spiritualized , central food distribution centers .	他們被農地包圍 , 被大型寺廟複雜的神廟包圍 , 如同烏地 , 實際上 , 由中央食物分佈中心來主導 。
because it was the temples that organized the harvest , gathered in the grain , offered it to the gods , and then offered the grain that the gods didn't eat back to the people .	因為那是把收穫的神殿 , 聚集在穀物中 , 提供給神的神 , 接著 , 神才不會再吃掉人 。
so , if you like , the whole spiritual and physical life of these cities was dominated by the grain and the harvest that sustained them .	所以 , 如果你喜歡 , 這些城市的整個精神和生理生活 , 都是由穀物所主宰的 , 以及維持它們的收穫 。
and in fact , that's true of every ancient city .	事實上 , 每個古老城市都是如此 。
but of course not all of them were that small .	但當然不是全部都那麼小 。
famously , rome had about a million citizens by the first century a . d .	最著名的是 , 羅馬在第一世紀就有一百萬個市民 。
so how did a city like this feed itself ?	那麼 , 像這樣的城市如何自給自足 ?
the answer is what i call " ancient food miles . "	答案是 , 我稱之為 「 古老的食物旅程 」 。
basically , rome had access to the sea , which made it possible for it to import food from a very long way away .	基本上 , 羅馬能接觸到海洋 , 讓它可以從很長的路外進入港口食物 。
this is the only way it was possible to do this in the ancient world , because it was very difficult to transport food over roads , which were rough .	這是在古代世界中唯一能做到的辦法 , 因為很難把食物運送到道路上 , 這樣很艱辛 。
and the food obviously went off very quickly .	很顯然 , 食物很快就消失了 。
so rome effectively waged war on places like carthage and egypt just to get its paws on their grain reserves .	所以 , 羅馬有效地打擊了像卡瑟和埃及那樣的地區 , 只為了讓它在它們的穀物保留下來 。
and , in fact , you could say that the expansion of the empire was really sort of one long , drawn out militarized shopping spree , really .	事實上 , 你可以說 , 帝國的擴張是相當長的 , 把軍事化的購物速度拿出來 , 真的 。
in fact i love the fact , i just have to mention this: rome in fact used to import oysters from london , at one stage . i think that's extraordinary .	事實上 , 我很喜歡這個事實 , 我只需要提到這個:羅馬以前從倫敦到奧特斯特 , 在某個階段 , 我覺得這很不尋常 。
so rome shaped its hinterland through its appetite .	羅馬透過胃口塑造了它的蜂群 。
but the interesting thing is that the other thing also happened in the preindustrial world .	但有趣的是 , 另一件事情也發生在工業時代 。
if we look at a map of london in the 17th century , we can see that its grain , which is coming in from the thames , along the bottom of this map .	如果我們看看十七世紀的倫敦地圖 , 我們可以看到它的穀物 , 它的穀物是從這張地圖的底部來的 。
so the grain markets were to the south of the city .	所以 , 穀物市場到城市的南方 。
and the roads leading up from them to cheapside , which was the main market , were also grain markets .	道路從他們走到廉價的市場 , 也是主要的市場 。
and if you look at the name of one of those streets , bread street , you can tell what was going on there 300 years ago .	如果你看看其中一條街道的名字 , 麵包街 , 你可以知道300年前發生了什麼事 。
and the same of course was true for fish .	當然 , 對魚來說也是如此 。
fish was , of course , coming in by river as well . same thing .	當然 , 魚也是靠河流進來的 。 同樣的事 。
and of course billingsgate , famously , was london's fish market , operating onsite here until the mid1980s .	當然 , 很有名的 , 是倫敦的魚市場 , 直到1980年代中期一直在營運 。
which is extraordinary , really , when you think about it .	真的 , 真的 , 想想這點 , 真是太棒了 。
everybody else was wandering around with mobile phones that looked like bricks and sort of smelly fish happening down on the port .	其他所有人都在帶著行動電話 , 看起來像是磚塊 , 有點像在港口上流下的魚 。
this is another thing about food in cities: once its roots into the city are established , they very rarely move .	城市裡的食物是另一回事:一旦城市的根源被建立起來 , 它們很少會移動 。
meat is a very different story because , of course , animals could walk into the city .	肉類是個非常不一樣的故事 , 因為 , 動物可以走進城市 。
so much of london's meat was coming from the northwest , from scotland and wales .	倫敦的肉類來自西北部 , 蘇格蘭和威爾斯 。
so it was coming in , and arriving at the city at the northwest , which is why smithfield , london's very famous meat market , was located up there .	所以它來了 , 抵達西北部的城市 , 這就是為什麼史密斯菲爾德 , 倫敦著名的肉市場 , 位在那兒 。
poultry was coming in from east anglia and so on , to the northeast .	污染來自東部 , 諸如此類 , 到東北部 。
i feel a bit like a weather woman doing this . anyway , and so the birds were coming in with their feet protected with little canvas shoes .	我覺得有點像氣象女人在做這件事 。 不管怎樣 , 鳥兒就在腳上保護著小畫布鞋 。
and then when they hit the eastern end of cheapside , that's where they were sold , which is why it's called poultry .	然後當他們到了便宜的東部時 , 他們就在那兒賣 , 這就是為什麼它叫做 " 污染 " 。
and , in fact , if you look at the map of any city built before the industrial age , you can trace food coming in to it .	事實上 , 如果你看看任何城市在工業時代建立的地圖 , 你可以追蹤食物來到它之前的食物 。
you can actually see how it was physically shaped by food , both by reading the names of the streets , which give you a lot of clues .	你可以看到它是如何形塑的 , 透過閱讀街頭的名字 , 讓你知道很多線索 。
friday street , in a previous life , is where you went to buy your fish on a friday .	星期五街 , 在一個星期五的生活中 , 你在星期五去買你的魚 。
but also you have to imagine it full of food .	但你也得想像它充滿了食物 。
because the streets and the public spaces were the only places where food was bought and sold .	因為街道和公共空間是唯一能買到食物的地方 。
and if we look at an image of smithfield in 1830 you can see that it would have been very difficult to live in a city like this and be unaware of where your food came from .	如果我們看看1830年的史密斯菲爾德的影像 , 你可以看到 , 在這樣的城市中 , 很難想像你的食物來自哪裡 。
in fact , if you were having sunday lunch , the chances were it was mooing or bleating outside your window about three days earlier .	事實上 , 如果你有星期日午餐 , 你的機會就在三天前就在你的窗外 。
so this was obviously an organic city , part of an organic cycle .	顯然這是一個有機的城市 , 一個有機循環的一部分 。
and then 10 years later everything changed .	十年後一切都改變了 。
this is an image of the great western in 1840 .	這是1840年的偉大西方的照片 。
and as you can see , some of the earliest train passengers were pigs and sheep .	如你所見 , 一些最早的火車乘客是豬和羊 。
so all of a sudden , these animals are no longer walking into market .	突然間 , 這些動物不再進入市場 。
they're being slaughtered out of sight and mind , somewhere in the countryside .	他們從視覺和心中被屠宰 , 在鄉村的某處 。
and they're coming into the city by rail .	他們被鐵軌進入城市 。
and this changes everything .	這改變了一切 。
to start off with , it makes it possible for the first time to grow cities , really any size and shape , in any place .	首先 , 要從這裡開始 , 首次可以種植城市 , 任何大小和形狀 , 任何地方都有可能 。
cities used to be constrained by geography ; they used to have to get their food through very difficult physical means .	過去 , 城市被地理限制了 ; 他們以前得要用非常困難的實體方式來取得食物 。
all of a sudden they are effectively emancipated from geography .	突然間 , 他們從地理位置解放出來 。
and as you can see from these maps of london , in the 90 years after the trains came , it goes from being a little blob that was quite easy to feed by animals coming in on foot , and so on , to a large splurge , that would be very , very difficult to feed with anybody on foot , either animals or people .	正如你從倫敦的地圖看到的 , 在火車經過的90年後 , 它從一個小小的氣球 , 很容易被動物從腳上進來 , 到一個大的水泥 , 非常難和任何人在腳上、腳上、或人類一起餵食 。
and of course that was just the beginning . after the trains came cars , and really this marks the end of this process .	當然 , 這只是開端 。 火車經過車輛 , 真的是這個過程的終點 。
it's the final emancipation of the city from any apparent relationship with nature at all .	它是城市的最後一種解放 , 完全與大自然的關係 。
and this is the kind of city that's devoid of smell , devoid of mess , certainly devoid of people , because nobody would have dreamed of walking in such a landscape .	這種城市是缺乏氣味、缺乏混亂的城市 , 肯定是缺乏人的 , 因為沒有人會夢想在這樣的地景中走路 。
in fact , what they did to get food was they got in their cars , drove to a box somewhere on the outskirts , came back with a week's worth of shopping , and wondered what on earth to do with it .	事實上 , 他們所做的是拿到食物 , 開車到戶外的某個地方 , 再回來一週的購物中心 , 想知道地球上該怎麼做 。
and this really is the moment when our relationship , both with food and cities , changes completely .	此時此刻 , 與食物和城市的關係 , 完全改變了 。
here we have food that used to be the center , the social core of the city at the periphery .	這裡的食物是市中心 , 市區的社會核心 。
it used to be a social event , buying and selling food .	以前是社會活動 , 買東西和賣食物 。
we used to cook ; now we just add water , or a little bit of an egg if you're making a cake or something .	我們以前烹飪過來 , 只要加一點水 , 或少一點卵 , 只要你做蛋糕或其他東西 。
we don't smell food to see if it's okay to eat .	我們不會聞到食物 , 看看是否可以吃 。
we just read the back of a label on a packet .	我們剛在包裝上讀到標籤的後面 。
and we don't value food . we don't trust it .	我們不重視食物 , 我們不信任它 。
so instead of trusting it , we fear it .	所以 , 我們不相信它 , 而是害怕它 。
and instead of valuing it , we throw it away .	而不是評估它 , 而是把它丟掉 。
one of the great ironies of modern food systems is that they've made the very thing they promised to make easier much harder .	現代的糧食系統之一 , 其中一個很諷刺 , 是他們承諾要讓食物更容易 。
by making it possible to build cities anywhere and any place , they've actually distanced us from our most important relationship , which is that of us and nature .	藉由讓任何地方都可以建立城市 , 實際上 , 它們與我們最重要的關係有關係 , 也就是我們和大自然之間的距離 。
and also they've made us dependent on systems that only they can deliver , that , as we've seen , are unsustainable .	同時 , 它們也讓我們依賴了系統 , 只有它們才能實現 , 如我們所見 , 無法永續發展 。
so what are we going to do about that ?	那我們要怎麼做呢 ?
it's not a new question .	這不是一個新問題 。
500 years ago it's what thomas more was asking himself .	500年前 , 湯瑪斯自問得更多 。
this is the frontispiece of his book " utopia . "	這是他的書《烏托邦》的首席成果 。
and it was a series of semiindependent citystates , if that sounds remotely familiar , a day's walk from one another where everyone was basically farmingmad , and grew vegetables in their back gardens , and ate communal meals together , and so on .	這是一系列半獨立的城市 , 如果聽起來很遙遠 , 有一天 , 每個人基本上都是養殖 , 在他們的後花園裡種植蔬菜 , 然後一起吃餐 , 等等 。
and i think you could argue that food is a fundamental ordering principle of utopia , even though more never framed it that way .	我想你們可以主張 , 食物是烏托邦的基本秩序原則 , 儘管它從來沒有這麼想過 。
and here is another very famous " utopian " vision , that of ebenezer howard , " the garden city . "	這是另一個非常有名的 「 烏托邦 」 遠景 , 伊本霍華的 「 花園城市 」 。
same idea: series of semiindependent citystates , little blobs of metropolitan stuff with arable land around , joined to one another by railway .	同樣的點子:一系列半獨立的城市 , 都市的小塊大地 , 附近有可耕地 , 加入了鐵路 。
and again , food could be said to be the ordering principle of his vision .	同樣地 , 食物可以被說是他視覺的順序原則 。
it even got built , but nothing to do with this vision that howard had .	它甚至被建造出來 , 但和霍華的視覺無關 。
and that is the problem with these utopian ideas , that they are utopian .	而這些烏托邦的想法 , 就是他們是烏托邦人 。
utopia was actually a word that thomas moore used deliberately .	烏托邦其實是湯瑪斯•摩爾故意使用的詞 。
it was a kind of joke , because it's got a double derivation from the greek .	這是個笑話 , 因為希臘的雙重指揮 。
it can either mean a good place , or no place .	它可能意味著一個好的地方 , 或沒有地方 。
because it's an ideal . it's an imaginary thing . we can't have it .	因為這是一個理想的 , 一個想像性的事物 。 我們無法擁有它 。
and i think , as a conceptual tool for thinking about the very deep problem of human dwelling , that makes it not much use .	我認為 , 作為一個概念化的工具 , 來思考人類最深層的問題 , 讓它無法使用 。
so i've come up with an alternative , which is sitopia , from the ancient greek , " sitos " for food , and " topos " for place .	所以我想出了一個替代方案 , 來自古希臘的 「 聖地 」 、 「 食物 」 、 「 接地 」 。
i believe we already live in sitopia .	我相信我們已經住在西托邦 。
we live in a world shaped by food , and if we realize that , we can use food as a really powerful tool a conceptual tool , design tool , to shape the world differently .	我們生活在一個由食物塑造的世界 , 如果我們意識到 , 我們能用食物作為一個非常強大的工具 , 一個概念的工具 , 設計工具 , 以不同的方式形塑世界 。
so if we were to do that , what might sitopia look like ?	所以如果我們這樣做 , 會是什麼樣子 ?
well i think it looks a bit like this .	我想它看起來有點像這樣 。
i have to use this slide . it's just the look on the face of the dog .	我得用這張投影片 , 只是狗的臉 。
but anyway , this is it's food at the center of life , at the center of family life , being celebrated , being enjoyed , people taking time for it .	總之 , 這是生活中央的食物 , 在家庭生活的中心 , 被慶祝、被享受 , 人們花時間去做 。
this is where food should be in our society .	在我們的社會中 , 食物應該是這樣 。
but you can't have scenes like this unless you have people like this .	但 , 除非你有這樣的人 , 你就不可能有這樣的場景 。
by the way , these can be men as well .	順便一提 , 這些人也可以是男性 。
it's people who think about food , who think ahead , who plan , who can stare at a pile of raw vegetables and actually recognize them .	人們會想到食物 , 先思考 , 他們計畫 , 可以盯著一堆原始蔬菜 , 並且認得它們 。
we need these people . we're part of a network .	我們需要這些人 , 我們是網路的一部分 。
because without these kinds of people we can't have places like this .	因為如果沒有這些人 , 我們就不可能有這樣的地方 。
here , i deliberately chose this because it is a man buying a vegetable .	在這裡 , 我刻意選擇這一點 , 因為這是男人買蔬菜的男人 。
but networks , markets where food is being grown locally .	但網絡 , 食物在當地種植的市場 。
it's common . it's fresh .	很常見 , 很新鮮 。
it's part of the social life of the city .	它是城市的社會生活的一部分 。
because without that , you can't have this kind of place , food that is grown locally and also is part of the landscape , and is not just a zerosum commodity off in some unseen hellhole .	因為沒有這些 , 你不可能有這種地方 , 當地種植的食物 , 同時也是地景的一部分 , 不僅僅是一些失敗的地獄裡的零商品 。
cows with a view .	牛有一種觀點 。
steaming piles of humus .	一堆 「 嗡 」 的串流 。
this is basically bringing the whole thing together .	這基本上就是把整個東西結合在一起 。
and this is a community project i visited recently in toronto .	這是我最近在多倫多拜訪的社區計畫 。
it's a greenhouse , where kids get told all about food and growing their own food .	這是一個溫室 , 在那裡 , 孩子們會告訴所有關於食物和種植他們自己的食物 。
here is a plant called kevin , or maybe it's a plant belonging to a kid called kevin . i don't know .	這裡有個叫kevin的植物 , 或許它是屬於一個叫kevin的孩子 。 我不知道 。
but anyway , these kinds of projects that are trying to reconnect us with nature is extremely important .	總之 , 這些與大自然重新連結的項目是非常重要的 。
so sitopia , for me , is really a way of seeing .	所以 , 西托邦 , 對我來說 , 真的是種看法 。
it's basically recognizing that sitopia already exists in little pockets everywhere .	基本上就是認知到 , 西托邦已經存在在小口袋裡 。
the trick is to join them up , to use food as a way of seeing .	訣竅是加入它們 , 用食物作為一種看待方式 。
and if we do that , we're going to stop seeing cities as big , metropolitan , unproductive blobs , like this .	如果我們這樣做 , 我們將不再把城市視為是大、大都市、不生產力的爆炸 。
we're going to see them more like this , as part of the productive , organic framework of which they are inevitably a part , symbiotically connected .	我們會把它們看得更像這樣 , 作為生產力、有機架構的一部分 , 不可避免地是一部分 , 相互連結 。
but of course , that's not a great image either , because we need not to be producing food like this anymore .	但當然 , 這不是一個很棒的影像 , 因為我們不需要再生產像這樣的食物 。
we need to be thinking more about permaculture , which is why i think this image just sums up for me the kind of thinking we need to be doing .	我們需要更深入思考 , 這也是為什麼我認為這張影像總結了我認為我們需要做的事 。
it's a reconceptualization of the way food shapes our lives .	它是一種重新思考食物如何塑造我們的生活方式 。
the best image i know of this is from 650 years ago .	我所知道的最好的圖片是650年前 。
it's ambrogio lorenzetti's " allegory of good government . "	它是阿布羅吉歐•洛倫澤蒂的 「 良好政府的寓言 」 。
it's about the relationship between the city and the countryside .	重點是城市和鄉村之間的關係 。
and i think the message of this is very clear .	我覺得這訊息很清楚 。
if the city looks after the country , the country will look after the city .	如果城市照顧這個國家 , 國家會照顧這個城市 。
and i want us to ask now , what would ambrogio lorenzetti paint if he painted this image today ?	現在我要我們問 , 阿布羅吉歐•洛倫澤蒂如果他今天畫了這張圖片 , 阿布羅吉歐•洛倫澤蒂會怎麼樣 ?
what would an allegory of good government look like today ?	今天好的政府會是什麼樣子 ?
because i think it's an urgent question .	因為我認為這是一個迫切的問題 。
it's one we have to ask , and we have to start answering .	我們得要問 , 我們得要開始回答 。
we know we are what we eat .	我們知道我們吃的是什麼 。
we need to realize that the world is also what we eat .	我們需要了解 , 世界也是我們吃的 。
but if we take that idea , we can use food as a really powerful tool to shape the world better .	但如果我們採取這個想法 , 我們可以用食物作為一個非常強大的工具來塑造世界更好的工具 。
weeks from the charter for compassion launch , karen armstrong looks at religion's role in the 21st century: will its dogmas divide us ? or will it unite us for common good ? she reviews the catalysts that can drive the world's faiths to rediscover the golden rule .	幾週後 , 卡倫•阿姆斯壯在21世紀的宗教角色:它的教條會不會分裂我們嗎 ? 或者它會讓我們團結在一起 ? 她會評視世界上的信仰 , 來重新審視黃金法則 。
god , ted prize , global issues , politics , religion , tedglobal2009 , violence	上帝、ted , 全球議題、政治、宗教、tedglobal2009、暴力、暴力 。
karen armstrong: let's revive the golden rule	卡倫•阿姆斯壯:讓我們重建黃金法則 。
for years i've been feeling frustrated , because as a religious historian , i've become acutely aware of the centrality of compassion in all the major world faiths .	多年來 , 我感到很挫折 , 因為身為一個宗教歷史學家 , 我已經意識到所有主要的信仰中央的同情心 。
every single one of them has evolved their own version of what's been called the golden rule .	每一個人都演化出他們自己的版本 , 來稱之為黃金法則 。
sometimes it comes in a positive version " always treat all others as you'd like to be treated yourself . "	有時 , 它出現在一個正面的版本中 , 「 總是對待所有人 , 如同你對待自己 。 」
and equally important is the negative version " don't do to others what you would not like them to do to you . "	同樣重要的是負面版本: 「 別對別人做你不想做的事 。 」
look into your own heart , discover what it is that gives you pain and then refuse , under any circumstance whatsoever , to inflict that pain on anybody else .	看看你自己的心 , 發現它會給你痛苦 , 然後拒絕任何情況 , 在任何人的情況下 , 去衝突任何人的痛苦 。
and people have emphasized the importance of compassion , not just because it sounds good , but because it works .	人們強調了同情心的重要性 , 不只是因為它聽起來很好 , 也因為它有效 。
people have found that when they have implemented the golden rule as confucius said , " all day and every day , " not just a question of doing your good deed for the day and then returning to a life of greed and egotism , but to do it all day and every day , you dethrone yourself from the center of your world , put another there , and you transcend yourself .	人們發現 , 當他們執行黃金法則時 , 說: 「 整天 , 不單是做好事的一天 , 再回到貪婪和自我主義的生命 , 每天都在做 , 把自己從世界的中心 , 放到另一邊 , 超越你自己 。
and it brings you into the presence of what's been called god , nirvana , rama , tao .	它帶你進入了所謂的神、nirvana、rama、tao 。
something that goes beyond what we know in our egobound existence .	超越我們所知的 , 超越了我們的自我存在 。
but you know you'd never know it a lot of the time , that this was so central to the religious life .	但你知道你從來沒有認識過這段時間 , 對宗教生活是如此中心的 。
because with a few wonderful exceptions , very often when religious people come together , religious leaders come together , they're arguing about abstruse doctrines or uttering a council of hatred or inveighing against homosexuality or something of that sort .	因為有幾個奇妙的例外 , 通常當宗教人士聚在一起時 , 宗教領袖聚在一起 , 他們爭論abstrustrines , 或說是仇恨或侵略同性戀或某種類型的 。
often people don't really want to be compassionate .	人們通常不想同情心 。
i sometimes see when i'm speaking to a congregation of religious people a sort of mutinous expression crossing their faces because people often want to be right instead .	我有時會看到我在和宗教人士談話時 , 會看到一種完全的表情 , 因為人們通常會想對 。
and that of course defeats the object of the exercise .	這當然會打敗運動的物體 。
now why was i so grateful to ted ?	為什麼我這麼感激ted ?
because they took me very gently from my booklined study and brought me into the 21st century , enabling me to speak to a much , much wider audience than i could have ever conceived .	因為他們讓我非常溫柔地從我的書籍研究帶領我進入21世紀 , 讓我能和更多的觀眾說話 , 比我想像中更廣 。
because i feel an urgency about this .	因為我對此感到急迫 。
if we don't manage to implement the golden rule globally , so that we treat all peoples , wherever and whoever they may be , as though they were as important as ourselves , i doubt that we'll have a viable world to hand on to the next generation .	如果我們無法在全球實施黃金法則 , 這樣我們才能對待所有人 , 無論他們身為何人 , 儘管他們和我們自己一樣重要 , 我懷疑我們將會有一個可行的世界 , 來傳遞下一代 。
the task of our time , one of the great tasks of our time , is to build a global society , as i said , where people can live together in peace .	我們這個時代的任務之一 , 是建立一個全球社會 , 如我所說 , 在那裡人們可以一起生活在和平之中 。
and the religions that should be making a major contribution are instead seen as part of the problem .	要做出重大貢獻的宗教 , 反而被視為問題的一部分 。
and of course it's not just religious people who believe in the golden rule .	當然 , 這不只是宗教人士相信黃金法則 。
this is the source of all morality , this imaginative act of empathy , putting yourself in the place of another .	這是所有道德的來源 , 這種同理心的想像力 , 把你自己放在另一個地方 。
and so we have a choice , it seems to me .	所以 , 我們有一個選擇 , 似乎對我來說 。
we can either go on bringing out or emphasizing the dogmatic and intolerant aspects of our faith , or we can go back to the rabbis . rabbi hillel , the older contemporary of jesus , who , when asked by a pagan to sum up the whole of jewish teaching while he stood on one leg , said , " that which is hateful to you , do not do to your neighbor .	要麼我們要麼把我們信仰的信仰帶到外面 , 再來談談猶太教 , 老年猶太教 , 老年的猶太教徒 , 當他把整個猶太教給一腿時 , 說: 「 對你來說 , 這對你是有害的 , 不要對你的鄰居 。
that is the torah and everything else is only commentary . "	那就是托拉 , 所有其他的都只是留言 。 」
and the rabbis and the early fathers of the church who said that any interpretation of scripture that bred hatred and disdain was illegitimate .	瑞比斯和早期教會的父親說 , 任何關於經文的詮釋都被培養成仇恨和殘疾 , 都是違法的 。
and we need to revive that spirit .	我們需要重建這精神 。
and it's not just going to happen because a spirit of love wafts us down .	這不只會發生 , 因為愛情的靈魂讓我們失望 。
we have to make this happen , and we can do it with the modern communications that ted has introduced .	我們必須讓這一切發生 , 並且我們可以利用ted所介紹的現代溝通 。
already i've been tremendously heartened at the response of all our partners .	我已經對我們所有伴侶的反應很大 。
in singapore , we have a group going to use the charter to heal divisions recently that have sprung up in singaporean society , and some members of the parliament want to implement it politically .	在新加坡 , 我們有一群人 , 會用charter來治癒分裂 , 最近才在新加坡社會中興起 , 有些國會的成員想要在政治上實施它 。
in malaysia , there is going to be an art exhibition in which leading artists are going to be taking people , young people , and showing them that compassion also lies at the root of all art .	在馬來西亞 , 將會有一個展覽 , 主導藝術家將要帶領人、年輕人 , 並告訴他們 , 同情也是所有藝術的根源 。
throughout europe , the muslim communities are holding events and discussions , are discussing the centrality of compassion in islam and in all faiths .	在整個歐洲 , 穆斯林社區正在舉辦活動和討論 , 討論伊斯蘭的核心 , 以及所有信仰 。
but it can't stop there . it can't stop with the launch .	但它不能停在那裡 , 它不能停下來 。
religious teaching , this is where we've gone so wrong , concentrating solely on believing abstruse doctrines .	宗教教導 , 這是我們錯了的地方 , 唯一集中在相信abststrustrines 。
religious teaching must always lead to action .	宗教教學一定會導致行動 。
and i intend to work on this till my dying day .	我本來是想在這個臨終的日子裡工作 。
and i want to continue with our partners to do two things educate and stimulate compassionate thinking .	我想繼續跟伴侶一起做兩件事 , 教育和刺激同情思考 。
education because we've so dropped out of compassion .	教育是因為我們從同情心中退縮 。
people often think it simply means feeling sorry for somebody .	人們常認為這只是對某人感到抱歉的意思 。
but of course you don't understand compassion if you're just going to think about it .	但 , 當然 , 如果你想的話 , 你不會了解同情心 。
you also have to do it .	你也必須這麼做 。
i want them to get the media involved because the media are crucial in helping to dissolve some of the stereotypical views we have of other people , which are dividing us from one another .	我希望他們能得到媒體參與 , 因為媒體是很重要的 , 協助解決我們對其他人有的刻板印象 , 把我們從彼此身上分離出來 。
the same applies to educators .	同一個教育家也適用於教育家 。
i'd like youth to get a sense of the dynamism , the dynamic and challenge of a compassionate lifestyle .	我希望青年能感受到動態的感覺 , 動態和挑戰同情的生活方式 。
and also see that it demands acute intelligence , not just a gooey feeling .	此外 , 它也要求有敏銳的智能 , 不單只是個美好的感覺 。
i'd like to call upon scholars to explore the compassionate theme in their own and in other people's traditions .	我想打電話給學者 , 去探索他們自己的同情心 , 以及在其他人的傳統中 。
and perhaps above all , to encourage a sensitivity about uncompassionate speaking , so that because people have this charter , whatever their beliefs or lack of them , they feel empowered to challenge uncompassionate speech , disdainful remarks from their religious leaders , their political leaders , from the captains of industry .	最重要的是 , 鼓勵一個對不停的說話的敏感性 , 如此一來 , 因為人們有這個主意 , 或缺乏他們的信仰 , 他們覺得有能力去挑戰不舒服的言論 , 不論他們的宗教領袖 , 政治領袖 , 他們的政治領袖 , 來自產業的總部 。
because we can change the world , we have the ability .	因為我們可以改變世界 , 我們有能力 。
i would never have thought of putting the charter online .	我從來沒有想過要把charter放在網路上 。
i was still stuck in the old world of a whole bunch of boffins sitting together in a room and issuing yet another arcane statement .	我仍然困在舊世界裡 , 一群人坐在一間房間裡 , 還在說另一個阿卡內語 。
and ted introduced me to a whole new way of thinking and presenting ideas .	ted向我介紹一個全新的思維和展示想法 。
because that is what is so wonderful about ted .	因為這是ted的美妙之處 。

and of course the problems sometimes seem insuperable .	當然 , 問題有時似乎是很不可思議的 。
but i'd just like to quote , finish at the end with a reference to a british author , an oxford author whom i don't quote very often , c . s . lewis .	但最後 , 我想引用一句話 , 用英國作者來結束 , 牛津作家 , 我不常引用我說的 , c.路易斯 。
but he wrote one thing that stuck in my mind ever since i read it when i was a schoolgirl .	但他寫了一句話 , 自從我還是個學童時 , 我就讀了這句話 。
it's in his book " the four loves . "	在他的書《四個愛》中 。
he said that he distinguished between erotic love , when two people gaze , spellbound , into each other's eyes .	他說 , 他在愛情之間分辨出 , 當兩個人凝視、拼字、對方的眼睛 。
and then he compared that to friendship , when two people stand side by side , as it were , shoulder to shoulder , with their eyes fixed on a common goal .	然後他比較友誼 , 當兩個人站在一旁 , 肩膀肩膀肩膀肩膀 , 雙眼固定在共同的目標上 。
we don't have to fall in love with each other , but we can become friends .	我們不需要互相愛 , 但我們能成為朋友 。
and i am convinced .	我深信 。
i felt it very strongly during our little deliberations at vevey , that when people of all different persuasions come together , working side by side for a common goal , differences melt away .	我覺得在我們在vevey的小小決心時 , 非常強烈的感覺 , 當各種不同的說服的人聚在一起 , 一起工作 , 一邊是共同的目標 , 差異融化了 。
and we learn amity .	我們學到了 「 雄性 」 。
and we learn to live together and to get to know one another .	我們學會一起生活 , 認識彼此 。
thank you very much .	非常謝謝 。

they bail out as soon as they get to the top of saint ivo , that little spiral structure you see there .	一旦他們到了聖艾佛的頂端 , 你可以看到那個小小的螺旋結構 。

notices a lot of activity at the tre scalini restaurant , is reminded that it is lunchtime and she's hungry .	注意到在trestrepalini餐廳裡有很多活動 , 被提醒它是午餐時間 , 她很餓 。
they keep on motoring towards the campo de' fiori , which they soon reach . ajax the dog is put in a basket and lowered with a list of food into the marketplace , which flourishes there until about one in the afternoon , and then is completely removed and doesn't appear again until six or seven the following morning .	牠們不斷地移動到柬埔寨的功效 , 牠們很快就會接觸到 。 阿傑克斯把狗放進一個籃子裡 , 把食物放進市場中 , 直到下午大約一個人 , 然後完全被移除 , 直到凌晨六點 , 直到第七點 。
anyway , the pooch gets back to the dirigible with the stuff .	總之 , 口味會回歸到這些東西的寬度 。
unfortunately , when she goes to unwrap the prosciutto , ajax makes a lunge for it .	不幸的是 , 當她去解開這個原則時 , ajax會為它做個午餐 。
she's managed to save the prosciutto , but in the process she loses the tablecloth , which you can see flying away in the upper lefthand corner .	她成功拯救了原住民 , 但在她失去桌布的過程中 , 你可以看到在左上角飛走 。
they continue without their tablecloth , looking for a place to land this thing so that they can actually have lunch .	他們沒有桌布 , 尋找一個地方降落這個東西 , 讓他們可以吃午餐 。
they eventually discover a huge wall that's filled with small holes , ideal for docking a dirigible because you've got a place to tie up .	他們終於發現了一道巨大的牆 , 充滿了小洞 , 理想地點 , 因為你有一個地方可以綁在一起 。
turns out to be the exterior wall that part of it that remains of the coliseum , so they park themselves there and have a terrific lunch and have a spectacular view .	結果發現 , 這裡的外部牆 , 留在哥倫比亞的那一部分 , 所以他們停在那裡 , 吃了一頓很棒的午餐 , 也有很壯觀的景象 。
at the end of lunch , they untie the anchor , they set off through the baths of caracalla and over the walls of the city and then an abandoned gatehouse and decide to take one more look at the pyramid of cestius , which has this lightning rod on top .	午餐結束時 , 他們解開了教堂 , 他們在城市的牆壁上擺脫了卡拉拉 , 然後是廢棄的門廊 , 決定再看一看cestius的金字塔 , 上面有這條粗糙的屋頂 。
unfortunately , that's a problem: they get a little too close , and when you're in a dirigible you have to be very careful about spikes .	不幸的是 , 這是個問題:它們太靠近了 , 而當你身處一個可憐的靈感時 , 你必須非常小心 。
so that sort of brings her little story to a conclusion .	所以 , 這種故事帶給她一個結論 。
marcello , on the other hand , is sort of a lazy guy , but he's not due at work until about noon .	另一方面 , 瑪賽羅是個懶惰的傢伙 , 但他不是在工作直到上午才開始 。
so , the alarm goes off and it's five to 12 or so .	所以 , 警報開始了 , 五到十二 。
he gets up , leaps onto his scooter , races through the city past the church of santa maria della pace , down the alleys , through the streets that tourists may be wandering through , disturbing the quiet backstreet life of rome at every turn .	他走上去 , 躍進了他的樂團 , 穿越城市的種族 , 穿越了聖塔瑪麗亞•德拉斯的教堂 , 穿越了遊客的街道 , 可能每一輪都穿越羅馬的安靜背景 。
that speed with which he is moving , i hope i have suggested in this little image , which , again , can be turned around and read from both sides because there's text on the bottom and text on the top , one of which is upside down in this image .	他在移動的速度 , 我希望我建議這張小圖片 , 同樣地 , 可以從兩側轉過來 , 因為在底部和文字上有文字 , 其中一個是顛倒在這張圖片上 。
so , he keeps on moving , approaching an unsuspecting waiter who is trying to deliver two plates of linguine in a delicate white wine clam sauce to diners who are sitting at a table just outside of a restaurant in the street .	所以 , 他繼續移動 , 接近一間不懷疑的服務生 , 試圖在一片精緻的白色酒杯中發出兩塊口語 , 來吃飯 , 讓他們坐在餐廳外面的餐廳 。
waiter catches on , but it's too late .	等候會繼續下去 , 但太遲了 。
and marcello keeps moving in his scooter .	馬賽羅在他的樂團中繼續移動 。
everything he sees from this point on is slightly affected by the linguine , but keeps on moving because this guy's got a job to do .	他所看到的一切都稍微受到語言影響 , 但繼續移動 , 因為這傢伙有工作要做 。
removes some scaffolding . one of the reasons rome remains the extraordinary place it is that because of scaffolding and the determination to maintain the fabric , it is a city that continues to grow and adapt to the needs of the particular time in which it finds itself , or we find it .	除去一些支架 。 羅馬仍然是非凡的地方之一 , 就是因為支架和決心要維持布料 , 城市持續成長和適應特定時間的需求 , 或我們找到它 。
right through the piazza della rotonda , in front of the pantheon again wreaking havoc and finally getting to work .	透過pazadellrotonda , 在萬神殿前 , 再次震撼的哈佛 , 終於成功了 。
marcello , as it turns out , is the driver of the number 64 bus , and if you've been on the number 64 bus , you know that it's driven with the same kind of exuberance as marcello demonstrated on his scooter .	結果發現 , 64輛巴士的司機是64輛巴士的司機 , 如果你曾經在64輛巴士上 , 你知道它的驅動力是馬爾洛在他的摩托車上展示的 。
and finally carletto . you see his apartment in the upper lefthand corner .	最後 , 卡莉托 , 你可以看到他在左上角的公寓 。
he's looking at his table ; he's planning to propose this evening to his girlfriend of 40 years , and he wants it to be perfect .	他在看他的桌子 , 他計劃要向他的女友提出這個晚上 , 四十年來 , 他希望他能做到完美 。
he's got candles out , he's got flowers in the middle and he's trying to figure out where to put the plates and the glasses .	他拿著蠟燭 , 中間有花 , 他想辦法把板子和玻璃放在哪裡 。
but he's not happy ; something's wrong .	但他並不快樂 ; 有些問題 。
the phone rings anyway , he's called to the palazzo .	總之 , 電話響了 , 他被叫到palazo 。
he saunters he saunters at a good clip , but as compared to all the traveling we've just seen , he's sauntering .	他在好的短片中航行 , 但和我們剛才看到的所有旅行相比 , 他在飛行 。
everybody knows carletto , because he's in entertainment , actually ; he's in television .	大家都知道carleto , 因為他在娛樂中 , 事實上 , 他在電視中 。
he's actually in television repair , which is why people know him .	他其實是在電視修復中 , 這就是為什麼人們知道他 。
so they all have his number .	所以他們都有他的數字 。
he arrives at the palazzo , arrives at the big front door .	他抵達palazo , 抵達大門 。
enters the courtyard and talks to the custodian , who tells him that there's been a disaster in the palazzo ; nobody's tvs are working and there's a big soccer game coming up , and the crowd is getting a little restless and a little nervous .	進入法庭 , 和顧客交談 , 他告訴他 , 在巴拉索有場災難 ; 沒有人的電視在工作 , 那裡有一場大足球比賽 , 群眾變得有點無休 , 有點緊張 。
he goes down to the basement and starts to check the wiring , and then gradually works his way up to the top of the building , apartment by apartment , checking every television , checking every connection , hoping to find out what this problem is .	他走到地下室 , 開始檢查航線 , 然後逐漸地在建築的頂端工作 , 公寓的公寓 , 檢查每個電視節目、檢查每個連結 , 希望找出問題是什麼 。
he works his way up , finally , the grand staircase and then a smaller staircase until he reaches the attic .	他在路上工作 , 終於 , 大樓 , 接著樓梯變小 , 直到他抵達政治 。
he opens the window of the attic , of course , and there's a tablecloth wrapped around the building's television antenna .	他打開了閣樓的窗戶 , 當然 , 還有一張桌布圍繞著建築的電視天線 。
he removes it , the problems are solved , everybody in the palazzo is happy .	他移除它 , 問題解決了 , 在palazo的每個人都很高興 。
and of course , he also solves his own problem .	當然 , 他也解決他自己的問題 。
all he has to do now , with a perfect table , is wait for her to arrive .	他現在要做的 , 用一個完美的桌子 , 等著她到來 。
that was the first attempt , but it didn't seem substantial enough to convey whatever it was i wanted to convey about rome .	那是第一個嘗試 , 但看來不太重要 , 足以傳達我對羅馬的意見 。
so i thought , well , i'll just do piazzas , and i'll get inside and underneath and i'll show these things growing and show why they're shaped the way they are and so on .	所以我想 , 嗯 , 嗯 , 我會在裡面 , 在下面 , 我會展示這些東西的成長 , 展示它們的形狀 , 等等 。
and then i thought , that's too complicated . no , i'll just take my favorite bits and pieces and i'll put them inside the pantheon but keep the scale , so you can see the top of sant'ivo and the pyramid of cestius and the tempietto of bramante all side by side in this amazing space .	然後我想 , 這太複雜了 。 不 , 我會把我最愛的部分和碎片放進萬神殿裡 , 保持尺度 , 這樣你就可以看見聖誕節的最高層 , 及布拉曼特的金字塔 , 全側側側側的布拉曼人 。
now that's one drawing , so i thought maybe it's time for piranesi to meet escher .	這是一幅畫 , 所以我認為 , 也許是時候piranesi去見escher的時候了 。
you see that i'm beginning to really lose control here and also hope .	你可以看到 , 我開始失去控制權 , 也開始失去希望 。
there's a very thin blue line of exhaust that sort of runs through this thing that would be kind of the trail that holds it all together .	有一條非常細微的藍色線 , 可以穿越這條路 , 將它包住在一起的軌道 。
then i thought , " wait a minute , what am i doing ? "	然後我想: 「 等等 , 我在做什麼 ? 」
a book is not only a neat way of collecting and storing information , it's a series of layers .	一本書不只是收集和儲存資訊的好方法 , 它是一系列的層次 。
i mean , you always peel one layer off another ; we think of them as pages , doing it a certain way .	我的意思是 , 你總是把一層拿下來 , 我們把他們當成一頁 , 做某一頁 。
but think of them as layers . i mean , rome is a place of layers horizontal layers , vertical layers and i thought , well just peeling off a page would allow me to if i got you thinking about it the right way would allow me to sort of show you the depth of layers .	但 , 把它們想成是層層 。 我的意思是 , 羅馬是層層層層層 , 垂直層層次 , 我想 , 剛剛脫下一頁會允許我去思考 , 如果我用正確的方式來表達層層次的深度 。
the stucco on the walls of most of the buildings in rome covers the scars ; the scars of centuries of change as these structures have been adapted rather than being torn down .	羅馬大部分建築物的牆壁都遮住了傷疤 , 數世紀以來的傷疤 , 隨著這些結構的適應 , 而不是被摧毀 。
if i do a foldout page on the lefthand side and let you just unfold it , you see behind it what i mean by scar tissue .	如果我在左手邊做一個摺疊頁 , 讓你們看看它背後的我所謂的疤組織 。
you can see that in 1635 , it became essential to make smaller windows because the bad guys were coming or whatever .	你可以看到 , 在1635年 , 製造較小的窗戶是必要的 , 因為壞人要來了 。
adaptations all get buried under the stucco .	所有的改造都被埋在黏土之下 。
i could peel out a page of this palazzo to show you what's going on inside of it .	我可以把這一頁拼湊出來 , 讓大家看看裡面發生什麼事 。
but more importantly , i could also show you what it looks like at the corner of one of those magnificent buildings with all the massive stone blocks , or the fake stone blocks done with brick and stucco , which is more often the case .	但更重要的是 , 我也能向你們展示在那些巨大的建築物的角落中 , 其中一個巨大的石塊 , 或者是假的石塊 , 用磚塊和石塊做成 , 比較常發生 。
so it becomes slightly threedimensional .	所以它變得有點像三度空間 。
i could take you down one of those narrow little streets into one of those surprising piazzas by using a double gate fold double foldout page which , if you were like me reading a popup book as a child , you hopefully stick your head into .	我可以把你們其中一條狹窄的小街 , 帶到一個令人驚訝的小區塊裡 , 用兩層的摺疊頁 , 如果你跟我一樣 , 你希望你會把你的頭伸進去 。
you wrap the pages around your head and are in that piazza for that brief period of time .	你把你的腦袋包裹在那段短暫的短暫時間內 。
and i've really not done anything much more complicated than make foldout pages .	我真的沒有做任何更複雜的事情 , 比做摺疊頁更複雜 。
but then i thought , maybe i could be simpler here .	但接著我就想 , 也許我可以更簡單一點 。
let's look at the pantheon and the piazza della rotonda in front of it .	咱們來看看萬神殿和前面的pazadellrotonda
here's a book completely wide open .	這本書完全是開放的 。
ok , if i don't open the book the whole way , if i just open it 90 degrees , we're looking down the front of the pantheon , and we're looking sort of at the top , more or less down on the square .	好 , 如果我完全不打開這本書 , 如果我打開這本書 , 我們就從萬神廟的前面看下面 , 我們看到的正方形上方 , 或更少的下方 。
and if i turn the book the other way , we're looking across the square at the front of the pantheon .	如果我換了另一本書 , 我們就會在萬神廟的前面 。
no foldouts , no tricks just a book that isn't open the whole way .	沒有摺疊 , 沒有任何詭計 , 只是一本書 , 完全沒有打開整個過程 。
that seemed promising . i thought , maybe i'll do it inside and i can even combine the foldouts with the only partially opened book .	這看來很有前景 。 我想 , 也許我會在裡面做 , 我甚至可以把摺疊品和唯一一部分開放的書結合在一起 。
so we get inside the pantheon and it grows and so on and so forth .	於是我們進入了萬神廟 , 開始成長等等 。
and i thought , maybe i'm on the right track , but it sort of lost its human quality .	我想 , 也許我在正確的軌道上 , 但它有點像失去了它的人類特質 。
so i went back to the notion of story , which is always a good thing to have if you're trying to get people to pay attention to a book and pick up information along the way .	所以 , 我回到故事的概念 , 如果你想要讓人們注意到一本書 , 並在路上取得資訊 。
" pigeon's progress " struck me as a catchy title .	「 鴿子的進步 」 讓我陷入困境 。
if it was a homing pigeon , it would be called " homer's odyssey . "	如果它是一顆熱鴿子 , 它會被稱為 「 作家的奧迪斯西 」 。
but it was the journey of the . . .	但那是這趟旅程 。
i mean , if a title works , use it . but it would be a journey that went through rome and showed all the things that i like about rome .	我的意思是 , 如果一個標題可以用 , 但這將會是一趟旅程 , 穿越羅馬的旅程 , 展現我喜歡羅馬的一切 。
it's a pigeon sitting on top of a church .	這是一個鴿子坐在教堂的頂端 。
goes off during the day and does normal pigeon stuff . comes back , the whole place is covered with scaffolding and green netting and there's no way this pigeon can get home .	白天就離開 , 做正常的鴿子 。 回來 , 整個地方都被支架和綠色網絡覆蓋 , 這樣鴿子無法回家 。
so it's a homeless pigeon now and it's going to have to find another place to live , and that allows me to go through my catalog of favorite things , and we start with the tall ones and so on .	所以 , 現在是無家可歸的鴿子 , 要找到另一個地方來居住 , 這讓我能穿越我最愛的東西的目錄 , 我們從最高的那一開始 。
maybe it has to go back and live with family members ; that's not always a good thing , but it does sort of bring pigeons together again .	也許它必須回到家族成員的生活 , 這不一定是件好事 , 但它確實會把鴿子帶回來 。
and i thought , that's sort of interesting , but maybe there's a person who should be involved in this in some way .	我心想 , 這有點有趣 , 但也許有一個人應該用某種方式參與其中 。
so i kind of came up with this old guy who spends his life looking after sick pigeons .	所以我想出了一個老傢伙 , 他一生都在照顧生病的鴿子 。
he'll go anywhere to get them dangerous places and whatnot and they become really friends with this guy , and learn to do tricks for him and entertain him at lunchtime and stuff like that .	他會去任何地方 , 讓他們變得危險 , 什麼也不 , 他們會成為這個傢伙的朋友 , 學會為他招戲 , 在午餐時間和其他東西娛樂 。
there's a real bond that develops between this old man and these pigeons .	在這個老人和這些鴿子之間 , 有一個真正的連結 。
but unfortunately he gets sick . he gets really sick at the end of the story .	但 , 不幸的是 , 他生病了 。 他在故事的結尾就生病了 。
he's taught them to spell his name , which is aldo .	他被教導要他們拼字 , 也就是aldo 。
they show up one day after three or four days of not seeing him he lives in this little garret and they spell his name and fly around .	他們在三、四天後出席 , 沒有見到他住在這個小小的garret , 他們會說出他的名字 , 四處飛來飛去 。
and he finally gets enough strength together to climb up the ladder onto the roof , and all the pigeons , a la red balloon , are there waiting for him and they carry him off over the walls of the city .	他終於得到足夠的力量 , 爬上梯子的屋頂 , 所有的鴿子 , 紅色的氣球 , 在那裡等著他 , 他們把他帶到城市的牆壁上 。
and i forgot to mention this: whenever he lost a pigeon , he would take that pigeon out beyond the walls of the city .	我忘了提到這一點:只要他失去了鴿子 , 他就會把鴿子帶到城市的牆壁之外 。
in the old roman custom , the dead were never buried within the walls .	在古老的羅馬習俗中 , 死者從未埋在牆壁中 。
and i thought that's a really cheery story .	我覺得這是一個非常便宜的故事 。
. that's really going to go a long way .	真的很長一段時間 。
so anyway , i went through . . . and again , if packaging doesn't work and if the stories aren't going anywhere , i just come up with titles and hope that a title will sort of kick me off in the right direction .	總之 , 我經歷了...再一次 , 如果包裝不行 , 如果故事不在任何地方 , 我就想出一個標題 , 希望一個標題可以把我踢在正確的方向上 。
and sometimes it does focus me enough and i'll even do a title page .	有時 , 它會專注在我身上 , 我甚至會做一個標題 。
so , these are all title pages that eventually led me to the solution i settled on , which is the story of a young woman who sends a message on a homing pigeon she lives outside the walls of the city of rome to someone in the city .	所以 , 這些都是標題的頁面 , 最終引領我進入我安定的解決方案 , 故事是一位年輕女子 , 她在羅馬城外傳遞一個訊息 , 她住在羅馬城的牆壁 , 到城市的某人 。
and the pigeon is flying down above the appian way here .	而鴿子正從這邊飛下來 , 飛到這邊 。
you can see the tombs and pines and so on and so forth along the way .	你可以看到墳墓、松鼠等等 。
if you see the red line , you are seeing the trail of the pigeon ; if you don't see the red line , you are the pigeon .	如果你看到紅線 , 你就會看到鴿子的軌跡 ; 如果你看不到紅線 , 你就是鴿子 。
and it becomes necessary and possible , at this point , to try to convey what that sense would be like of flying over the city without actually moving .	在這個時點 , 它變得很必要且有可能 , 試著說服它的感覺 , 它會在沒有移動的城市中會是什麼感覺 。
past the pyramid of cestius these will seem very familiar to you , even if you haven't been to rome recently past the gatehouse .	在凱薩蒂斯的金字塔中 , 這些對你來說是很熟悉的 , 即使你最近沒去過羅馬的大道 。
this is something that's a little bit unusual .	這是有點不尋常的事 。
this pigeon does something that most homing pigeons do not do: it takes the scenic route , which was a device that i felt was necessary to actually extend this book beyond about four pages .	這隻鴿子做了一件最適合的鴿子不做的事:它需要一趟風景的路線 , 這是我覺得很必要的裝置 , 要把這本書延長到四頁以外 。
so , we circle around the coliseum , past the church of santa maria in cosmedin and the temple of hercules towards the river .	所以 , 我們圍繞著哥倫坡 , 過去的聖母瑪麗亞的教堂 , 以及海克力士的神殿 。
we almost collide with the cornice of the palazzo farnese designed by michelangelo , built of stone taken from the coliseum narrow escape .	我們幾乎和palazofrangelo的玉米相撞 , 由米開朗基羅所設計的石頭 , 由哥倫坡逃離 。
we swoop down over the campo de' fiori .	我們在campodefiori上掉下去 。
this is one of those things i show to my students because it's a complete bastardization a denial of any rules of perspective .	這是我向我的學生展示的其中一件事 , 因為這是一個完全的基準 , 完全否認任何的觀點 。
the only rule of perspective that i think matters is if it looks believable , you've succeeded .	我認為唯一重要的觀點是 , 如果它看起來是可信的 , 你就成功了 。
but you try and figure out where the vanishing points meet here ; a couple are on mars and a couple of others in cremona .	但你會試著找出消失點在哪裡 ; 一對夫婦在火星上 , 以及在克里蒙亞的幾個人 。
but into the piazza in front of santa maria della pace , where invariably a soccer game is going on , and we're hit by a soccer ball .	但在聖塔馬尼亞•德拉的前面 , 無可避免的足球賽正在進行 , 我們被足球打擊 。
now this is a terrible illustration of being hit by a soccer ball .	這是一個非常糟糕的圖像 , 由足球打擊 。
i have all the pieces: there's santa maria della pace , there's a soccer ball , there's a little bit of a bird's wing nothing's happening , so i had to rethink it .	我有各式各樣的:聖塔馬里亞•德拉•帕斯 , 有一顆足球 , 有一點點鳥在發生 , 所以我得重新思考一下 。
and if you do want to see santa maria della pace , these books are really flexible , incredibly interactive just turn it around and look at it the other way .	如果你真的想要看到聖誕老人的速度 , 這些書非常靈活 , 非常互動 , 只是轉過來 , 看看它的另一面 。
through the alley , we can see the impact is captured in the red line .	透過巷子 , 我們可以看到這影響是紅線捕捉到的 。
and then bird manages to pull itself together past this medieval tower one of the few remaining medieval towers towards the church of sant'agnese and around the dome looking down into piazza navona which we've already mentioned and seen and flown over a couple of times ; there's the bernini statue of the four rivers and then past the wonderful borromini sant'ivo , stopping just long enough on the 26foot diameter oculus of the pantheon to catch our breath .	之後 , 鳥會自行拉近這座中世紀的高樓 , 少數幾個中世紀的高樓 , 位於聖母峰的教堂 , 周圍的圓頂 , 向下看 , 我們已經提到 , 看到和流過幾次 ; 那裡有柏尼•斯雕像 , 雕像有四個河流 , 然後超越了美麗的布洛明尼西聖母島 , 距離太遠 , 距離我們26公尺長的天堂 。
and then we can swoop inside and around ; and because we're flying , we don't really have to worry about gravity at this particular moment in time , so this drawing can be oriented in any way on the page .	然後我們就可以在裡面掉下來 , 因為我們正在飛翔 , 在這一刻我們不用擔心重力 , 所以這張圖可以以任何方式在頁面上 。
we get a little exuberant as we pass gesu ; it's not surprising to sort of mimic the architecture in this way .	當我們經過gesu時 , 我們會得到一些驚喜 , 這並不令人驚訝 , 以這種方式模仿建築 。
past the wonderful wall filled with the juxtaposition that i was talking about ; beautiful carvings set into the walls above the neon " ristorante " sign , and so on .	經過我剛提到的美麗牆 , 充滿了我所說的混合物 ; 美麗的雕刻設在牆上 , 上面是 「 中風 」 標誌 , 等等 。
and eventually , we arrive at the courtyard of the palazzo , which is our destination .	最終 , 我們到了palazo的庭院 , 是我們的目的 。
straight up through the courtyard into a little window into the attic , where somebody is working at the drawing board .	直接穿過庭院 , 進入一個小窗戶 , 有人在畫板上工作 。
he removes the message from the leg of the bird ; this is what it says .	他把訊息從鳥的腿上移除 , 這是牠說的 。
as we look at the drawing board , we see what he's working on is , in fact , a map of the journey that the pigeon has just taken , and the red line extends through all the sights .	當我們看畫板時 , 我們會看到他正在努力的 , 事實上 , 鴿子的地圖已經拍攝了 , 紅線會延伸到所有視覺 。
and if you want the information , so that we complete this cycle of understanding , all you have to do is read these paragraphs .	如果你想要這些資訊 , 我們就完成了這個理解的循環 , 你只需要閱讀這些範例 。
thank you very much .	非常謝謝 。
mit researcher skylar tibbits works on selfassembly the idea that instead of building something , we can create materials that build themselves , much the way a strand of dna zips itself together . it's a big concept at early stages ; tibbits shows us three inthelab projects that hint at what a selfassembling future might look like .	麻省理工學院研究者skylarbbit在自組裝上工作 , 而不是建立某樣東西 , 我們可以創造出一系列dna自己的方式 。 這是個很大的概念 ; tibbit讓我們看到三項 「 自我組裝 」 的項目 , 可以隱藏在自我組裝未來的樣貌 。
skylar tibbits: can we make things that make themselves ?	skylartibbit:我們能否做出製造自己的東西 ?
today i'd like to show you the future of the way we make things .	今天 , 我想向各位展示我們製造東西的方式 。
i believe that soon our buildings and machines will be selfassembling , replicating and repairing themselves .	我相信很快地 , 我們的建築和機器會自我組裝、複製、修復自己 。
so i'm going to show you what i believe is the current state of manufacturing , and then compare that to some natural systems .	所以 , 我要給你們看我相信目前的製造狀態 , 然後將它和一些自然系統做比較 。
so in the current state of manufacturing , we have skyscrapers two and a half years [of assembly time] , 500 , 000 to a million parts , fairly complex , new , exciting technologies in steel , concrete , glass .	所以 , 在目前的製造狀態 , 我們有摩天大樓 , 兩年半的時間 , 五十萬到一百萬個零件 , 相當複雜、新、令人興奮的新技術 , 鋼鐵、混凝土、玻璃 。
we have exciting machines that can take us into space five years [of assembly time] , 2 . 5 million parts .	我們有令人興奮的機器可以帶領我們進入太空五年的時空 , 兩百五十萬個零件 。
but on the other side , if you look at the natural systems , we have proteins that have two million types , can fold in 10 , 000 nanoseconds , or dna with three billion base pairs we can replicate in roughly an hour .	但另一方面 , 如果你看自然系統 , 我們有兩百萬種類型的蛋白質 , 可以在一萬個奈米秒中摺疊 , 或者有三十億個鹼基對 , 我們可以在大約一小時內複製 。
so there's all of this complexity in our natural systems , but they're extremely efficient , far more efficient than anything we can build , far more complex than anything we can build .	在我們的自然系統中 , 所有這些複雜性 , 但它們的效率非常高 , 比任何我們能建造的東西都還要高 , 比任何我們能建造的東西都還要複雜 。
they're far more efficient in terms of energy .	它們比能源更有效率 。
they hardly ever make mistakes .	他們幾乎不會犯錯 。
and they can repair themselves for longevity .	他們可以為自己修復壽命 。
so there's something super interesting about natural systems .	所以 , 關於自然系統有個超級有趣的現象 。
and if we can translate that into our built environment , then there's some exciting potential for the way that we build things .	如果我們可以把它轉化成我們的建築環境 , 那麼 , 我們建造東西的方式有一些令人興奮的潛力 。
and i think the key to that is selfassembly .	我認為這關鍵在於自我組裝 。
so if we want to utilize selfassembly in our physical environment , i think there's four key factors .	所以如果我們想要在我們的實體環境中自行組裝 , 我認為有四個關鍵因素 。
the first is that we need to decode all of the complexity of what we want to build so our buildings and machines .	首先 , 我們需要解碼所有我們想要建造的複雜性 , 以便我們的建築物和機器 。
and we need to decode that into simple sequences basically the dna of how our buildings work .	我們需要把這個編碼成簡單的序列基本上就是我們建築物如何運作的dna
then we need programmable parts that can take that sequence and use that to fold up , or reconfigure .	接著 , 我們需要可編寫的零件 , 可以用那段序列來摺疊 , 或重組 。
we need some energy that's going to allow that to activate , allow our parts to be able to fold up from the program .	我們需要一些能量來啟動 , 使我們的部件能夠從計畫中折疊起來 。
and we need some type of error correction redundancy to guarantee that we have successfully built what we want .	我們需要某種類型的錯誤 , 來確保我們成功地建立了我們想要的 。
so i'm going to show you a number of projects that my colleagues and i at mit are working on to achieve this selfassembling future .	所以 , 我要給你們看一些計畫 , 我的同事和我在麻省理工學院工作 , 來達成這個自我組裝的未來 。
the first two are the macrobot and decibot .	首先是麥克風和決定性機器人 。
so these projects are largescale reconfigurable robots 8 ft . , 12 ft . long proteins .	這些計畫是大規模的可重組的機器人8英尺 , 12英尺長的蛋白質 。
they're embedded with mechanical electrical devices , sensors .	他們嵌入了機械電裝置、感應器 。
you decode what you want to fold up into , into a sequence of angles so negative 120 , negative 120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , negative 120 something like that ; so a sequence of angles , or turns , and you send that sequence through the string .	你將你想要的東西摺疊成一連串的角度 , 以負120、0、0、120、負120、負120 , 類似這樣的東西 。 所以一連串的角度 , 或轉動 , 通過弦 , 將這個序列寄出去 。
each unit takes its message so negative 120 it rotates to that , checks if it got there and then passes it to its neighbor .	每個單位都把訊息傳遞給負面的120 , 只要它到達那裡 , 然後傳遞給鄰居 。
so these are the brilliant scientists , engineers , designers that worked on this project .	這些是傑出的科學家、工程師、設計師 , 研究這個計畫 。
and i think it really brings to light: is this really scalable ?	我認為它真的能帶來光明:這真的是可擴展的嗎 ?
i mean , thousands of dollars , lots of man hours made to make this eightfoot robot .	我的意思是 , 數千美金 , 很多人花時間製作這八英尺的機器人 。
can we really scale this up ? can we really embed robotics into every part ?	我們真的能把這個規模擴大嗎 ? 我們真的能把機器人嵌入每一部分嗎 ?
the next one questions that and looks at passive nature , or passively trying to have reconfiguration programmability .	下一個問題 , 觀察被動的自然 , 或被動地嘗試重新設計程式 。
but it goes a step further , and it tries to have actual computation .	但它又更進一步 , 它嘗試有實際的計算能力 。
it basically embeds the most fundamental building block of computing , the digital logic gate , directly into your parts .	基本上 , 它嵌入了最基本的運算基礎 , 數位邏輯門 , 直接植入你的零件中 。
so this is a nand gate .	這是nandgates 。
you have one tetrahedron which is the gate that's going to do your computing , and you have two input tetrahedrons .	你有一台超載體 , 即將完成你的運算 , 你有兩個輸入電子 。
one of them is the input from the user , as you're building your bricks .	其中一個是使用者的輸入 , 當你在打破你的磚塊時 。
the other one is from the previous brick that was placed .	另外一個是從前所未有的磚塊裡出來的 。
and then it gives you an output in 3d space .	然後它會給你一個3d空間中的輸出 。
so what this means is that the user can start plugging in what they want the bricks to do .	意思是 , 使用者可以開始在他們想要的磚塊上做些什麼 。
it computes on what it was doing before and what you said you wanted it to do .	它計算了它之前的作用以及你所說的你想做的 。
and now it starts moving in threedimensional space so up or down .	現在它開始在三維空間中移動 , 以至於上或下 。
