so on the lefthand side , [1 , 1] input equals 0 output , which goes down .	左邊的是1 , 1.1 , 輸入等同等於0的輸出 , 下降了 。
on the righthand side , [0 , 0] input is a 1 output , which goes up .	在右手邊 , 0 , 0的輸入是1的輸出 , 結果會上升 。
and so what that really means is that our structures now contain the blueprints of what we want to build .	這意味著我們的結構現在包含了我們想要建造的藍圖 。
so they have all of the information embedded in them of what was constructed .	所以他們有所有的資訊 , 都嵌入在他們所建立的結構中 。
so that means that we can have some form of selfreplication .	這意味著我們能有某種形式的自我複製 。
in this case i call it selfguided replication , because your structure contains the exact blueprints .	在這個例子中 , 我稱它為自我複製 , 因為你的結構包含了特定的藍圖 。
if you have errors , you can replace a part .	如果你有錯誤 , 你可以取代一個部分 。
all the local information is embedded to tell you how to fix it .	所有當地的資訊都被嵌入去告訴你如何修復它 。
so you could have something that climbs along and reads it and can output at one to one .	所以你可以有一些東西可以爬上去 , 讀它 , 並且可以在一個地方輸出去 。
it's directly embedded ; there's no external instructions .	它是直接嵌入的 ; 沒有外部指示 。
so the last project i'll show is called biased chains , and it's probably the most exciting example that we have right now of passive selfassembly systems .	最後一個專案叫做偏見鏈 , 它可能是我們目前最令人興奮的例子 , 被動自組裝系統 。
so it takes the reconfigurability and programmability and makes it a completely passive system .	所以它需要重組性和程式性 , 讓它成為一個完全被動的系統 。
so basically you have a chain of elements .	基本上你有一連串的元素 。
each element is completely identical , and they're biased .	每個元素都是完全相同的 , 它們是偏見的 。
so each chain , or each element , wants to turn right or left .	所以每一鏈 , 或每一元素都想要轉右轉或左轉 。
so as you assemble the chain , you're basically programming it .	當你組裝鏈時 , 你基本上就是在編寫它 。
you're telling each unit if it should turn right or left .	你告訴每個單位是否該轉右轉或左轉 。
so when you shake the chain , it then folds up into any configuration that you've programmed in so in this case , a spiral , or in this case , two cubes next to each other .	所以 , 當你搖鏈時 , 它就會折疊到任何你編寫的構造中 , 在這個例子中 , 一個螺旋 , 或這個例子中 , 兩個立方體彼此相鄰 。
so you can basically program any threedimensional shape or onedimensional , twodimensional up into this chain completely passively .	基本上 , 你可以將任何三維形狀或立體的形狀編寫成這個鏈 , 完全被動地被動化 。
so what does this tell us about the future ?	所以 , 這告訴我們未來的意義是什麼 ?
i think that it's telling us that there's new possibilities for selfassembly , replication , repair in our physical structures , our buildings , machines .	我認為這告訴我們 , 自我組裝的新可能性 , 複製、修復我們的身體結構、建築物、機器 。
there's new programmability in these parts .	在這些部分有新的可程式性 。
and from that you have new possibilities for computing .	從那之後 , 你就有了新的運算能力 。
we'll have spatial computing .	我們會有空間運算 。
imagine if our buildings , our bridges , machines , all of our bricks could actually compute .	想像一下 , 如果我們的建築物、橋樑、機器 , 我們所有的磚頭都可以計算 。
that's amazing parallel and distributed computing power , new design possibilities .	這是很棒的平行和分散式運算能力 , 新的設計可能性 。
so it's exciting potential for this .	所以這對這個來說是很令人興奮的潛力 。
so i think these projects i've showed here are just a tiny step towards this future , if we implement these new technologies for a new selfassembling world .	所以我認為 , 我剛剛展示的這些項目 , 只是一個小小的步驟 , 如果我們能實現這些新的自我組裝世界的新技術 。
we've been to the moon , we've mapped the continents , we've even been to the deepest point in the ocean twice . what's left for the next generation to explore ? biologist and explorer nathan wolfe suggests this answer: almost everything . and we can start , he says , with the world of the unseeably small .	我們去過月球 , 繪製了大陸 , 我們甚至去過海底深處的深處 。 下一代要探險 ? 生物學家和探險家nathanwolfe提出這個答案:幾乎所有事情 。 我們都可以開始 , 他說 , 帶著不可預期的小世界 。
biodiversity , exploration , microbiology , science	生物多樣性、探索、微生物學、科學、科學 。
nathan wolfe: what's left to explore ?	內森•沃爾夫:要探究什麼 ?
recently i visited beloit , wisconsin .	最近我造訪了威斯康辛 。
and i was there to honor a great 20th century explorer , roy chapman andrews .	我在那裡榮耀一個偉大的20世紀探險家roychapmanandrews 。
during his time at the american museum of natural history , andrews led a range of expeditions to uncharted regions , like here in the gobi desert .	在他在美國自然歷史博物館的期間 , 安德魯斯領導了一系列的探險 , 來到聯合國沙漠 。
he was quite a figure .	他是個人物 。
he was later , it's said , the basis of the indiana jones character .	後來 , 他說 , 印第安娜瓊斯角色的基礎 。
and when i was in beloit , wisconsin , i gave a public lecture to a group of middle school students .	當我在貝洛特 , 威斯康辛時 , 我給了一群中學學生公開演講 。
and i'm here to tell you , if there's anything more intimidating than talking here at ted , it'll be trying to hold the attention of a group of a thousand 12yearolds for a 45minute lecture .	我來這裡是要告訴各位 , 如果ted演講比ted更恐怖的話還要多 , 它會試著把一千二歲的孩子的注意力放在45分鐘的講座上 。
at the end of the lecture they asked a number of questions , but there was one that's really stuck with me since then .	在演講結束後 , 他們問了幾個問題 , 但從那時起 , 有一個問題讓我困住了 。
there was a young girl who stood up , and she asked the question: " where should we explore ? "	有一個年輕女孩站起來 , 她問了一個問題: 「 我們該去哪裡探索 ? 」
i think there's a sense that many of us have that the great age of exploration on earth is over , that for the next generation they're going to have to go to outer space or the deepest oceans in order to find something significant to explore .	我認為 , 我們當中許多人認為 , 地球上偉大的探索時代已經結束了 , 下一代他們必須去外太空或最深的海洋 , 才能找到一個重要的探索 。
but is that really the case ?	但這真的是這樣嗎 ?
is there really nowhere significant for us to explore left here on earth ?	對我們來說 , 有沒有什麼意義可以讓我們在地球上探索 ?
it sort of made me think back to one of my favorite explorers in the history of biology .	它讓我回想起我最喜歡的生物學探索家之一 。
this is an explorer of the unseen world , martinus beijerinck .	這是未知世界的探險家 , 馬丁•貝爾辛克 。
so beijerinck set out to discover the cause of tobacco mosaic disease .	所以 , beijerinck開始發現菸草性疾病的原因 。
what he did is he took the infected juice from tobacco plants and he would filter it through smaller and smaller filters .	他把感染的果汁從煙草中除去 , 他會透過更小的過濾器過濾出來 。
and he reached the point where he felt that there must be something out there that was smaller than the smallest forms of life that were ever known bacteria , at the time .	他到達了他感覺到一定有比當時所知的細菌還小的生命形式還小 。
he came up with a name for his mystery agent .	他想出了一個名字給他的神秘代理 。
he called it the virus latin for " poison . "	他稱之為 " 毒藥 " 的病毒 。
and in uncovering viruses , beijerinck really opened this entirely new world for us .	在揭開病毒時 , 北jerinck為我們打開了這個全新的世界 。
we now know that viruses make up the majority of the genetic information on our planet , more than the genetic information of all other forms of life combined .	我們現在知道 , 病毒佔據了地球上大部分的基因信息 , 比其他生命形式的基因信息還要多 。
and obviously there's been tremendous practical applications associated with this world things like the eradication of smallpox , the advent of a vaccine against cervical cancer , which we now know is mostly caused by human papillomavirus .	很明顯地 , 對於這個世界的實際應用 , 像是天花消滅疫苗 , 這種疫苗對抗子宮頸癌 , 我們現在知道主要是由人類乳癌所造成的 。
and beijerinck's discovery , this was not something that occurred 500 years ago .	beijerinck的發現並不是500年前發生的事 。
it was a little over 100 years ago that beijerinck discovered viruses .	一百多年前 , 北京發現了病毒 。
so basically we had automobiles , but we were unaware of the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	基本上 , 我們有汽車 , 但我們不知道生命形式的形式 , 製造了地球上大部分的基因信息 。
we now have these amazing tools to allow us to explore the unseen world things like deep sequencing , which allow us to do much more than just skim the surface and look at individual genomes from a particular species , but to look at entire metagenomes , the communities of teeming microorganisms in , on and around us and to document all of the genetic information in these species .	我們現在有了這些驚人的工具 , 讓我們可以探索不敏感的世界 , 例如深度測序 , 使我們能做到更多 , 不僅僅是滑雪地表面 , 觀察不同物種的個別基因組 , 而是觀察整個新陳代謝的社群 , 包括我們周圍的微生物 , 以及我們周圍的基因信息 , 記錄這些物種中的所有基因信息 。
we can apply these techniques to things from soil to skin and everything in between .	我們可以把這些技術應用到土壤、皮膚和其他東西之間 。
in my organization we now do this on a regular basis to identify the causes of outbreaks that are unclear exactly what causes them .	在我的組織中 , 我們現在經常這樣做 , 來辨識出爆發的成因 , 正是他們造成的原因 。
and just to give you a sense of how this works , imagine that we took a nasal swab from every single one of you .	為了讓你們了解這如何運作 , 想像一下我們從你們每一個人身上拿了一根鼻子 。
and this is something we commonly do to look for respiratory viruses like influenza .	我們常常會尋找呼吸性病毒 , 例如流感 。
the first thing we would see is a tremendous amount of genetic information .	我們首先會看到的是非常大量的基因信息 。
and if we started looking into that genetic information , we'd see a number of usual suspects out there of course , a lot of human genetic information , but also bacterial and viral information , mostly from things that are completely harmless within your nose .	如果我們開始研究基因信息 , 我們會看到很多常見的疑問 , 當然 , 很多人類遺傳信息 , 還有細菌和病毒信息 , 大部分來自鼻子中完全無害的事物 。
but we'd also see something very , very surprising .	但我們也會看到非常令人驚訝的事物 。
as we started to look at this information , we would see that about 20 percent of the genetic information in your nose doesn't match anything that we've ever seen before no plant , animal , fungus , virus or bacteria .	當我們開始檢視這些資訊時 , 我們會發現 , 你的鼻子中有20%的基因信息 , 和我們從未見過的任何東西 , 沒有植物、動物、真菌、病毒或細菌 。
basically we have no clue what this is .	基本上 , 我們根本不知道這是什麼 。
and for the small group of us who actually study this kind of data , a few of us have actually begun to call this information biological dark matter .	對於我們研究這種數據的小組 , 我們當中有一些人已經開始稱之為 「 生物暗物質 」 。
we know it's not anything that we've seen before ; it's sort of the equivalent of an uncharted continent right within our own genetic information .	我們知道這不是我們以前看過的任何東西 ; 它和我們遺傳信息中未知的大陸一樣 。
and there's a lot of it .	還有很多 。
if you think 20 percent of genetic information in your nose is a lot of biological dark matter , if we looked at your gut , up to 40 or 50 percent of that information is biological dark matter .	如果你認為你的鼻子裡有百分之二十的基因信息是許多生物暗物質 , 如果我們觀察你的腸子 , 高達百分之四十或五十的信息是生物暗物質 。
and even in the relatively sterile blood , around one to two percent of this information is dark matter can't be classified , can't be typed or matched with anything we've seen before .	即使在相對穩定的血液中 , 大約百分之一到兩分之一是暗物質無法被分類 , 也不能被我們以前見過的任何東西分類 。
at first we thought that perhaps this was artifact .	一開始我們認為這可能是人造的 。
these deep sequencing tools are relatively new .	這些深度測序工具相對是新的 。
but as they become more and more accurate , we've determined that this information is a form of life , or at least some of it is a form of life .	但隨著它們變得越來越精確 , 我們決定了這些資訊是一種生命形式 , 至少有些是生命形式的生命 。
and while the hypotheses for explaining the existence of biological dark matter are really only in their infancy , there's a very , very exciting possibility that exists: that buried in this life , in this genetic information , are signatures of as of yet unidentified life .	雖然解釋生物暗物質存在的假設只是在他們的嬰兒體內 , 存在著非常令人興奮的可能性:生命中的遺傳信息 , 存在於未被辨識出來的生命中 , 被遺傳信息所包含的特徵 。
that as we explore these strings of a's , t's , c's and g's , we may uncover a completely new class of life that , like beijerinck , will fundamentally change the way that we think about the nature of biology .	當我們在探索a、t、c、g的弦時 , 我們可能會發現一個全新的生命類型 , 像是beijerinck , 會徹底改變我們對生物學的看法 。
that perhaps will allow us to identify the cause of a cancer that afflicts us or identify the source of an outbreak that we aren't familiar with or perhaps create a new tool in molecular biology .	這或許可以讓我們辨識出一個癌症的成因 , 或辨識出我們不熟悉的疫情來源 , 或可能在分子生物學中創造一個新的工具 。
i'm pleased to announce that , along with colleagues at stanford and caltech and ucsf , we're currently starting an initiative to explore biological dark matter for the existence of new forms of life .	我很高興地宣布 , 和史丹佛和加州理工學院和加州理工學院的同事們 , 我們正開始探索生物暗物質 , 以新形式的生命存在 。
a little over a hundred years ago , people were unaware of viruses , the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	一百多年前 , 人們不知道病毒 , 生命的形式 , 構成我們地球上大部分的基因信息 。
a hundred years from now , people may marvel that we were perhaps completely unaware of a new class of life that literally was right under our noses .	一百年後 , 人們可能會驚嘆我們可能完全沒有意識到新的生命階級 , 真的就在我們的鼻子之下 。
it's true , we may have charted all the continents on the planet and we may have discovered all the mammals that are out there , but that doesn't mean that there's nothing left to explore on earth .	這是真的 , 我們可能已經掌控了地球上的所有大陸 , 我們可能已經發現了所有的哺乳動物 , 但這並不代表地球上沒有任何東西可以探索 。
beijerinck and his kind provide an important lesson for the next generation of explorers people like that young girl from beloit , wisconsin .	beijerinck和他的仁慈為下一代探險家提供了一個重要的教訓 , 例如來自貝洛斯、威斯康辛的年輕女孩 。
and i think if we phrase that lesson , it's something like this: don't assume that what we currently think is out there is the full story .	我認為 , 如果我們說出這一課 , 有點像這樣:不要假設我們目前認為的完整故事 。
go after the dark matter in whatever field you choose to explore .	在你選擇去探索的領域後 , 再來看看黑暗物質 。
there are unknowns all around us and they're just waiting to be discovered .	我們身邊沒有人知道 , 他們正等著被發現 。
legendary scientist david deutsch puts theoretical physics on the back burner to discuss a more urgent matter: the survival of our species . the first step toward solving global warming , he says , is to admit that we have a problem .	傳奇的科學家大衛•德西斯把理論物理放在後面 , 討論一個更急迫的物質:我們人類的生存 。 解決全球暖化的第一步 , 他說 , 就是承認我們有問題 。
climate change , cosmos , culture , environment , global issues , physics , science , technology , universe	氣候變遷、宇宙、文化、環境、全球議題、物理、物理、科學、科技、宇宙、宇宙 。
david deutsch on our place in the cosmos	大衛deutsch在我們的宇宙中 , 位於宇宙中 。
we've been told to go out on a limb and say something surprising .	我們被告知要走上肢體 , 說些令人驚訝的事 。
so i'll try and do that , but i want to start with two things that everyone already knows .	我會試著這樣做 , 但我想從兩個大家都知道的事情開始 。
and the first one , in fact , is something that has been known for most of recorded history .	首先 , 事實上 , 是歷史上大部分記錄下來的一件事 。
and that is that the planet earth , or the solar system , or our environment or whatever , is uniquely suited to sustain our evolution or creation , as it used to be thought and our present existence , and most important , our future survival .	那就是地球 , 或太陽系 , 或環境等等 , 獨特地適合維持我們的演化或創造力 , 如同以前的思想和存在 , 以及最重要的 , 我們未來的生存 。
nowadays this idea has a dramatic name: spaceship earth .	現今這個想法有個很戲劇性的名字:太空船地球 。
and the idea there is that outside the spaceship , the universe is implacably hostile , and inside is all we have , all we depend on .	而這個想法是 , 在太空船之外 , 宇宙是不可思議的 , 而我們所擁有的只是我們所仰賴的 。
and we only get the one chance: if we mess up our spaceship , we've got nowhere else to go .	我們只有一個機會:如果我們搞砸了我們的太空船 , 我們還有其他地方要去 。
now , the second thing that everyone already knows is that contrary to what was believed for most of human history , human beings are not , in fact , the hub of existence .	第二件大家已經知道的事是 , 與大部分人類歷史的信念相反 , 人類不是存在的中心 。
as stephen hawking famously said , we're just a chemical scum on the surface of a typical planet that's in orbit around a typical star , which is on the outskirts of a typical galaxy , and so on .	正如史蒂芬•霍金所說的 , 我們只是一個典型的星球表面 , 一個典型的恆星環繞著一個典型的星系 , 位於典型的星系之外 , 等等 。
now the first of those two things that everyone knows is kind of saying that we're at a very untypical place , uniquely suited and so on , and the second one is saying that we're at a typical place .	首先 , 大家都知道這兩件事情是說我們在一個非常不典型的地方 , 獨一無二的安排等等 , 第二個是說我們在一個典型的地方 。
and especially if you regard these two as deep truths to live by and to inform your life decisions , then they seem a little bit to conflict with each other .	尤其是如果你把這兩者看成是深刻的真理 , 來傳達你的生命決策 , 那麼他們似乎和彼此有一點點衝突 。
but that doesn't prevent them from both being completely false .	但這並不會阻止他們完全錯誤 。
and they are . so let me start with the second one: typical . well is this a typical place ? well , let's look around , you know , and look in a random direction , and we see a wall , and chemical scum and that's not typical of the universe at all .	它們就這樣 。 讓我從第二個開始 , 典型的 。 嗯 , 這是個典型的地方嗎 ? 咱們來看看四周 , 看看隨機的方向 , 我們看到一面牆 , 化學的腫瘤 , 完全不是典型的宇宙 。
all you've got to do is go a few hundred miles in that same direction and look back , and you won't see any walls or chemical scum at all all you see is a blue planet . and if you go further than that , you'll see the sun , the solar system , and the stars and so on .	你所要做的就是走上幾百英哩的路 , 回頭看 , 你不會看到任何牆壁或化學氣質 , 你只能看到一個藍色的星球 。 如果你走得遠一點 , 你會看到太陽、太陽系、恆星等等 。
but that's still not typical of the universe , because stars come in galaxies .	但這仍然不是宇宙的典型 , 因為恆星在星系中存在 。
and most places in the universe , a typical place in the universe , is nowhere near any galaxies .	宇宙中的大部分地方 , 一個典型的地方 , 在宇宙中 , 幾乎沒有任何星系 。
so let's go out further , till we're outside the galaxy , and look back , and yeah , there's the huge galaxy with spiral arms laid out in front of us .	讓我們更進一步 , 直到我們在銀河之外 , 再回頭看 , 是的 , 在我們面前 , 有著螺旋手臂的巨大銀河 。
and at this point we've come 100 , 000 light years from here .	此時此刻 , 我們已經從這裡得到了十萬光年 。
but we're still nowhere near a typical place in the universe .	但我們仍處於一個典型的宇宙中 。
to get to a typical place , you've got to go 1 , 000 times as far as that into intergalactic space .	要到一個典型的地方 , 你要走一千倍 , 才能進入國際空間 。
and so what does that look like ? typical .	那看起來是什麼樣子 ? 典型的 。
what does a typical place in the universe look like ?	宇宙中一個典型的地方是什麼樣子 ?
well , at enormous expense , ted has arranged a highresolution immersion virtual reality rendering of intergalactic space the view from intergalactic space .	嗯 , 在巨大的費用上 , ted已經排列了高解析度的虛擬實境 , 由星系空間的觀點組成 。
so can we have the lights off , please , so we can see it ?	所以 , 我們能否把燈關掉 , 請看 , 我們能看到嗎 ?
well , not quite , not quite perfect you see , in intergalactic space intergalactic space is completely dark , pitch dark .	嗯 , 不太完美 , 在星際間的空間中 , 完全是黑暗、黑暗的 。
it's so dark that if you were to be looking at the nearest star to you , and that star were to explode as a supernova , and you were to be staring directly at it at the moment when its light reached you , you still wouldn't be able to see even a glimmer .	黑暗之處是如此的黑暗 , 如果你看著最近的恆星 , 那顆恆星是一顆超新星 , 而你正直接盯著它盯著你 , 當光線到達你時 , 你仍無法看見一個光明 。
that's how big and how dark the universe is .	宇宙是如此的巨大和黑暗 。
and that's despite the fact that a supernova is so bright , so brilliant an event , that it would kill you stone dead at a range of several light years .	儘管超新星太亮了 , 所以很聰明 , 很棒的一件事 , 它會在幾光年之內殺了你死的石頭 。
and yet from intergalactic space , it's so far away you wouldn't even see it .	然而 , 從星系的空間 , 到目前為止 , 你甚至看不到 。
it's also very cold out there less than three degrees above absolute zero .	在絕對零度以上 , 它也是非常冷的 。
and it's very empty . the vacuum there is one million times less dense than the highest vacuum that our best technology on earth can currently create . so that's how different a typical place is from this place .	它很空 , 真空 , 真空的密度比地球上最高的真空溫度低了一百萬倍 , 目前我們在地球上最好的科技所創造出來的更大 。 這就是典型的地方有多大 。
and that is how untypical this place is .	這就是這個地方的不典型 。
so can we have the lights back on please ? thank you .	所以 , 我們能把燈光放回去嗎 ? 謝謝 。
now how do we know about an environment that's so far away , and so different , and so alien , from anything we're used to ?	現在 , 我們如何知道一個遙遠的環境 , 如此不同的環境 , 從我們所習慣的任何東西到外星人 ?
well , the earth our environment , in the form of us is creating knowledge .	嗯 , 我們的環境 , 創造知識 。
well , what does that mean ? well , look out even further than we've just been i mean from here , with a telescope and you'll see things that look like stars .	嗯 , 這意味著什麼呢 ? 嗯 , 遠遠超過我們剛剛從這裡開始的意思 , 用望遠鏡 , 你會看到一些類似恆星的東西 。
they're called " quasars . " quasars originally meant quasistellar object .	他們稱之為 「 quars 」 。 quars原本是指量子星的物體 。
which means things that look a bit like stars . but they're not stars .	這意味著看起來有點像星星 , 但它們不是星星 。
and we know what they are . billions of years ago , and billions of light years away , the material at the center of a galaxy collapsed towards a supermassive black hole .	數十億年前 , 我們知道它們是什麼 。 數十億光年之外 , 銀河系中間的物質崩塌到一個超大質量的黑洞 。
and then intense magnetic fields directed some of the energy of that gravitational collapse . and some of the matter , back out in the form of tremendous jets which illuminated lobes with the brilliance of i think it's a trillion suns .	接著 , 強烈的磁場會引導引引力崩塌的能量 。 有些物質 , 以巨大的噴射機形式 , 以我認為它是一兆個太陽 。
now , the physics of the human brain could hardly be more unlike the physics of such a jet .	人類大腦的物理學幾乎不像這種噴射機的物理學 。
we couldn't survive for an instant in it . language breaks down when trying to describe what it would be like in one of those jets .	我們無法立即存活下來 。 語言破壞了 , 試圖描述在其中一個噴射機中會是什麼樣子 。
it would be a bit like experiencing a supernova explosion , but at pointblank range and for millions of years at a time .	這有點像經驗超級新星爆炸 , 但在指尖範圍和數百萬年的時間 。
and yet , that jet happened in precisely such a way that billions of years later , on the other side of the universe , some bit of chemical scum could accurately describe , and model , and predict , and explain , above all there's your reference what was happening there , in reality .	然而 , 這個噴射機發生在幾十億年後 , 在宇宙的另一面 , 有些化學氣質可以精確地描述 , 並且預測 , 最重要的是你在現實中所發生的狀況 。
the one physical system , the brain , contains an accurate working model of the other the quasar .	一個物理系統 , 大腦 , 包含一個精確的工作模式 , 其它的正方形 。
not just a superficial image of it , though it contains that as well , but an explanatory model , embodying the same mathematical relationships and the same causal structure .	不單只是一個超級基本的圖像 , 它也包含了它 , 一個解釋模型 , 包含了相同的數學關係 , 以及相同的因果結構 。
now that is knowledge . and if that weren't amazing enough , the faithfulness with which the one structure resembles the other is increasing with time . that is the growth of knowledge .	這是知識 。 如果這還不夠驚人 , 信心與其它結構的相似性會隨著時間增長 。 這就是知識的增長 。
so , the laws of physics have this special property .	所以 , 物理定律有這種特性 。
that physical objects , as unlike each other as they could possibly be , can nevertheless embody the same mathematical and causal structure and to do it more and more so over time .	那個實體物體 , 不像彼此一樣 , 可能是 , 永遠無法體現相同的數學和因果結構 , 並且不斷地做 。
so we are a chemical scum that is different . this chemical scum has universality .	所以 , 我們是一個不同的化學腫瘤 , 這種化學腫瘤具有普遍性 。
its structure contains , with everincreasing precision , the structure of everything . this place , and not other places in the universe , is a hub which contains within itself the structural and causal essence of the whole of the rest of physical reality . and so , far from being insignificant , the fact that the laws of physics allow this , or even mandate that this can happen , is one of the most important things about the physical world .	它的結構包含著有史無前例的精確度、結構的結構 。 這個地方 , 而不是宇宙中的其他地方 , 是一個謙遜的中心 , 包含了整個物理現實的本質 。 到目前為止 , 物理定律 , 允許它發生 , 甚至允許它實現 , 也是最重要的事之一 。
now how does the solar system and our environment , in the form of us acquire this special relationship with the rest of the universe ?	那麼 , 太陽系和我們的環境是如何在我們和宇宙的其他地方取得這種特別的關係 ?
well , one thing that's true about stephen hawking's remark i mean , it is true , but it's the wrong emphasis . one thing that's true about it is that it doesn't do it with any special physics . there's no special dispensation , no miracles involved . it does it simply with three things that we have here in abundance .	嗯 , 史蒂芬•霍金的評論是真的 , 但這是錯的 。 一件事是真的 。 一件事是不對的 。 沒有任何特殊的物理 。 沒有特殊的干擾 , 沒有奇蹟 。 它只是我們在這裡所存在的三件東西 。
one of them is matter , because the growth of knowledge is a form of information processing . information processing is computation , computation requires a computer there's no known way of making a computer without matter .	其中一個是重要的 , 因為知識的增長是一種資訊處理的形式 。 資訊處理是計算 , 計算需要一台電腦 , 不知不覺地製造電腦 。
we also need energy to make the computer , and most important , to make the media in effect onto which we record the knowledge that we discover .	我們也需要精力來製造電腦 , 最重要的是要讓媒體有效地記錄我們發現的知識 。
and then thirdly , less tangible , but just as essential for the openended creation of knowledge , of explanations , is evidence .	第三 , 比較不具體 , 但對於開放知識、解釋的開放原則 , 也是證據 。
now , our environment is inundated with evidence .	現在 , 我們的環境受到證據影響 。
we happen to get round to testing , let's say , newton's law of gravity about 300 years ago .	例如 , 牛頓定律大約300年前的重力定律 。
but the evidence that we used to do that was falling down on every square meter of the earth for billions of years before that , and will continue to fall on for billions of years afterwards . and the same is true for all the other sciences .	但是我們以前做的證據是 , 數十億年前地球的平方公尺落下了地球的每一平方公尺 , 數十億年後也會持續下降 。 所有其他的科學都一樣 。
as far as we know , evidence to discover the most fundamental truths of all the sciences is here just for the taking on our planet .	至於我們所知 , 證據發現所有科學中最基本的真理 , 只是為了在地球上採取行動 。
our location is saturated with evidence , and also with matter and energy .	我們的位置充滿了證據 , 也充滿了物質和能量 。
out in intergalactic space , those three prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge are at their lowest possible supply .	在星際空間中 , 這三種預先設定的知識是它們最低的可供應能力 。
as i said , it's empty ; it's cold ; and it's dark out there . or is it ?	如我所說 , 它是空的 , 它很冷 , 那裡是黑暗的 。 還是嗎 ?
now actually , that's just another parochial misconception .	實際上 , 這只是另外一個理論誤解 。
because imagine a cube out there in intergalactic space , the same size as our home , the solar system . now that cube is very empty by human standards , but that still means that it contains over a million tons of matter .	因為想像一個立方體存在於星際空間 , 和我們的家一樣大 , 太陽系 。 以人類標準來說 , 立方體是空的 , 但這仍然意味著它含有超過一百萬噸的物質 。
and a million tons is enough to make , say , a selfcontained space station , on which there's a colony of scientists that are devoted to creating an openended stream of knowledge , and so on .	一百萬噸足以製造出自動控制的太空站 , 那裡有一群科學家 , 致力於創造一個開放式知識流 , 諸如此類 。
now , it's way beyond present technology to even gather the hydrogen from intergalactic space and form it into other elements and so on .	現在 , 超越現在的科技 , 甚至從星系空間中收集氫氣 , 形成其它元素等等 。
but the thing is , in a comprehensible universe , if something isn't forbidden by the laws of physics , then what could possibly prevent us from doing it , other than knowing how ?	但 , 重點是 , 在一個不可思議的宇宙中 , 如果有某樣東西不被物理定律禁止 , 那麼 , 什麼能阻止我們去做 , 除了知道如何 ?
in other words , it's a matter of knowledge , not resources .	換句話說 , 它是知識 , 而不是資源 。
and the same well , if we could do that we'd automatically have an energy supply , because the transmutation would be a fusion reactor and evidence ?	同樣地 , 如果我們能自動進行能源供應 , 因為轉變會是核融合反應爐和證據 ?
well , again , it's dark out there to human senses . but all you've got to do is take a telescope , even one of presentday design , look out and you'll see the same galaxies as we do from here .	再說一次 , 它對人類的感官很暗 。 但你只需要用一台望遠鏡 , 甚至是現今的設計 , 看看你會從這裡看到相同的銀河系 。
and with a more powerful telescope , you'll be able to see stars , and planets .	有了更強大的望遠鏡 , 你會看到星星 , 和行星 。
in those galaxies , you'll be able to do astrophysics , and learn the laws of physics .	在那些星系中 , 你將能夠做天體物理學 , 並且學習物理定律 。
and locally there you could build particle accelerators , and learn elementary particle physics , and chemistry , and so on .	在那裡 , 你可以建造粒子加速器 , 學習基本粒子物理、化學等等 。
probably the hardest science to do would be biology field trips because it would take several hundred million years to get to the nearest lifebearing planet and back .	最難做到的科學是生物實地試驗 , 因為要花上幾億年才能到達最近的生死星 。
but i have to tell you and sorry , richard but i never did like biology field trips much , and i think we can just about make do with one every few hundred million years .	但我必須告訴各位 , 很抱歉 , 理察 , 但我從來沒有像生物實地旅行 , 我想我們能每幾億年就做一次 。
so in fact , intergalactic space does contain all the prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge . any such cube , anywhere in the universe , could become the same kind of hub that we are , if the knowledge of how to do so were present there .	所以 , 事實上 , 星系空間包含了所有開放式的知識 。 任何宇宙中任何地方的任何一個立方體 , 都可以成為我們所擁有的那種樞紐 , 如果我們知道如何做到這一點 。
so we're not in a uniquely hospitable place .	所以 , 我們並不處於一個獨特的敵意之中 。
if intergalactic space is capable of creating an openended stream of explanations , then so is almost every other environment . so is the earth . so is a polluted earth .	如果星系空間能夠創造出一個開放式的解釋 , 那麼幾乎所有其他的環境 。 這就是地球 。 這是污染的地球 。
and the limiting factor , there and here , is not resources , because they're plentiful , but knowledge , which is scarce .	而有限的因素 , 在這裡 , 不是資源 , 因為它們是豐富的 , 但知識 , 是很稀少的 。
now this cosmic knowledgebased view may and i think ought to make us feel very special . but it should also make us feel vulnerable , because it means that without the specific knowledge that's needed to survive the ongoing challenges of the universe , we won't survive them .	以宇宙為基礎的觀點 , 我覺得應該讓我們覺得很特別 。 但這也應該讓我們感到脆弱 , 因為這意味著 , 若沒有需要真正的知識來生存宇宙的挑戰 , 我們就不會生存它們 。
all it takes is for a supernova to go off a few light years away , and we'll all be dead !	只需要幾光年之外的超新星 , 我們都死了 !
martin rees has recently written a book about our vulnerability to all sorts of things , from astrophysics , to scientific experiments gone wrong , and most importantly to terrorism with weapons of mass destruction .	馬丁rees最近寫了一本關於我們對各種事物的脆弱性 , 從天體物理學、到科學實驗都錯了 , 最重要的是對大規模毀滅性武器的恐怖主義 。
and he thinks that civilization has only a 50 percent chance of surviving this century .	他認為文明只有50%的機會能在這個世紀生存 。
i think he's going to talk about that later in the conference .	我想他會在研討會上談到這一點 。
now i don't think that probability is the right category to discuss this issue in .	我不認為機率是正確的類別 , 來討論這個議題 。
but i do agree with him about this . we can survive , and we can fail to survive .	但我同意他 , 我們能生存下來 , 我們無法生存下來 。
but it depends not on chance , but on whether we create the relevant knowledge in time .	但它取決於偶然而不是偶然的 , 而是我們是否在時間內創造相關的知識 。
the danger is not at all unprecedented . species go extinct all the time .	危險不是史無前例的 。 物種總是滅絕 。
civilizations end . the overwhelming majority of all species and all civilizations that have ever existed are now history .	文明終結 , 絕大多數的物種和所有已存在的文明都已經有歷史了 。
and if we want to be the exception to that , then logically our only hope is to make use of the one feature that distinguishes our species , and our civilization , from all the others namely , our special relationship with the laws of physics , our ability to create new explanations , new knowledge to be a hub of existence .	若我們想成為那樣的例外 , 我們唯一的希望是用一種特徵來區別我們物種的特徵 , 以及我們的文明 , 和我們的特殊關係 , 和物理定律的特殊關係 , 我們創造新的解釋 , 新的知識 , 成為存在的擁抱 。
so let me now apply this to a current controversy , not because i want to advocate any particular solution , but just to illustrate the kind of thing i mean .	所以 , 讓我現在把它應用到目前的爭議 , 不是因為我想要提倡任何特定的解決方案 , 只是為了說明我是說的 。
and the controversy is global warming .	爭議是全球暖化 。
now , i'm a physicist , but i'm not the right kind of physicist . in regard to global warming , i'm just a layman . and the rational thing for a layman to do is to take seriously the prevailing scientific theory . and according to that theory , it's already too late to avoid a disaster .	我是物理學家 , 但我不是物理學家 。 在全球暖化的情況下 , 我只是一名女士 。 而對一位女士來說 , 要認真看待現有的科學理論 。 根據這個理論 , 已經太遲了 , 避免災難 。
because if it's true that our best option at the moment is to prevent co2 emissions with something like the kyoto protocol , with its constraints on economic activity and its enormous cost of hundreds of billions of dollars or whatever it is , then that is already a disaster by any reasonable measure .	因為如果說真的 , 我們現在最好的選項就是預防二氧化碳排放 , 例如京都議定書 , 其經濟活動的限制和巨大的成本 , 只要花上數百億美元或任何錢 , 那就已經被任何合理的衡量所造成了災難 。
and the actions that are advocated are not even purported to solve the problem , merely to postpone it by a little . so it's already too late to avoid it , and it probably has been too late to avoid it ever since before anyone realized the danger .	倡導者的行動甚至還沒被資格解決這個問題 , 只需要用一點點來重建它 。 所以它已經太遲可以避免它了 , 可能在任何人意識到危險之前就已經太遲了 。
it was probably already too late in the 1970s , when the best available scientific theory was telling us that industrial emissions were about to precipitate a new ice age in which billions would die .	可能在1970年代已經太晚了 , 最好的科學理論告訴我們 , 工業排放即將預防數十億人死亡的新冰河時代 。
now the lesson of that seems clear to me , and i don't know why it isn't informing public debate .	這一課對我來說是很明顯的 , 我不知道為何它沒有傳達公眾辯論 。
it is that we can't always know . when we know of an impending disaster , and how to solve it at a cost less than the cost of the disaster itself , then there's not going to be much argument , really .	就是我們無法永遠知道 。 當我們知道一個即興的災難時 , 如何用比災難本身的成本低於成本 , 真的沒有太多的爭論 。
but no precautions , and no precautionary principle , can avoid problems that we do not yet foresee .	但沒有預防措施 , 也沒有預防原則 , 可以避免我們尚未預防的問題 。
hence , we need a stance of problemfixing , not just problemavoidance .	因此 , 我們需要一個解決問題的平衡 , 不只是問題 。
and it's true that an ounce of prevention equals a pound of cure , but that's only if we know what to prevent .	事實是 , 一堆預防等同於一磅的療法 , 但這只是我們知道預防什麼 。
if you've been punched on the nose , then the science of medicine does not consist of teaching you how to avoid punches .	如果你在鼻子上被打了 , 那麼醫學的科學並不包含教導你如何避免懲罰 。
if medical science stopped seeking cures and concentrated on prevention only , then it would achieve very little of either .	如果醫學界不再尋求治療 , 只專注於預防 , 就會達成非常少的成就 。
the world is buzzing at the moment with plans to force reductions in gas emissions at all costs .	目前世界正在進行計畫 , 來強迫氣體排放量的減少 。
it ought to be buzzing with plans to reduce the temperature , and with plans to live at the higher temperature and not at all costs , but efficiently and cheaply . and some such plans exist , things like swarms of mirrors in space to deflect the sunlight away , and encouraging aquatic organisms to eat more carbon dioxide .	它應該要用計劃來減少溫度 , 用計劃來維持更高的溫度 , 而不是所有成本 , 而是有效率和便宜 。 有些計畫存在 , 例如太空中大量的鏡子 , 來反射太陽光 , 並鼓勵水分生物進食更多的二氧化碳 。
at the moment , these things are fringe research .	此時此刻 , 這些東西正在進行研究 。
they're not central to the human effort to face this problem , or problems in general .	它們不是人類的核心 , 或一般的問題 。
and with problems that we are not aware of yet , the ability to put right not the sheer good luck of avoiding indefinitely is our only hope , not just of solving problems , but of survival .	有了我們還不知道的問題 , 要把對的能力 , 不是避免的好運──絕對是我們唯一的希望 , 不只是解決問題 , 而是生存 。
so take two stone tablets , and carve on them .	拿兩個石頭表 , 把它們關在上面 。
on one of them , carve: " problems are soluble . "	其中一個是 , 卡夫: 「 問題是很困難的 。 」
and on the other one carve: " problems are inevitable . "	另一張車上: 「 問題是不可避免的 。 」
how can a struggling country break out of poverty if it's trapped in a system of bad rules ? economist paul romer unveils a bold idea: " charter cities , " cityscale administrative zones governed by a coalition of nations .	一個掙扎的國家 , 如果它被困在一個不好的規則中呢 ? 經濟學家保羅•羅默揭露了一個大膽的想法: 「 查理城市 」 , 市政區的行政區被國家聯盟統治 。
business , culture , economics , global issues , politics	商業、文化、經濟、全球議題、政治議題、政治 。
paul romer's radical idea: charter cities	保羅羅•羅默的極端點子:查爾•都市 。
take a look at this picture .	看看這張照片 。
it poses a very fascinating puzzle for us .	它對我們來說是非常著迷的謎題 。
these african students are doing their homework under streetlights at the airport in the capital city because they don't have any electricity at home .	這些非洲學生在首都機場的街燈下做功課 , 因為他們家裡沒有任何電力 。
now , i haven't met these particular students , but i've met students like them .	我還沒見過這些特別的學生 , 但我遇到了像他們這樣的學生 。
let's just pick one for example , the one in the green shirt .	舉個例子 , 綠色襯衫中的一個 。
let's give him a name , too: nelson .	讓我們給他一個名字:nelson 。
i'll bet nelson has a cellphone .	我打賭nelson有手機 。
so here is the puzzle .	這是個謎題 。
why is it that nelson has access to a cuttingedge technology , like the cellphone , but doesn't have access to a 100yearold technology for generating electric light in the home ?	為什麼nelson能取得先進技術 , 例如手機 , 但沒有一個100歲的科技能在家裡產生電燈 ?
now , in a word , the answer is " rules . "	以一個詞來說 , 答案是 「 規則 」 。
bad rules can prevent the kind of winwin solution that's available when people can bring new technologies in and make them available to someone like nelson .	不好的規則可以防止贏得的解決方案 , 讓人們可以把新的科技帶進來 , 讓像nelson這樣的人能取得 。
what kinds of rules ?	什麼規則 ?
the electric company in this nation operates under a rule , which says that it has to sell electricity at a very low , subsidized price in fact , a price that is so low it loses money on every unit that it sells .	這個國家的電力公司在一個規則下執行 , 說它必須在非常低、補助的價格上銷售 , 事實上 , 價格太低 , 每單位賣出的每一單位都損失金錢 。
so it has neither the resources , nor the incentives , to hook up many other users .	所以它沒有資源 , 沒有激勵力 , 沒有其他使用者 。
the president wanted to change this rule .	總統想要改變這個規則 。
he's seen that it's possible to have a different set of rules , rules where businesses earn a small profit , so they have an incentive to sign up more customers .	他看到 , 可能有不同的規則 , 企業賺到小利潤的規則 , 所以他們有獎勵來簽更多客戶 。
that's the kind of rules that the cellphone company that nelson purchases his telephony from operates under .	那是一種規則 , nelson購買了他的電話 。
the president has seen how those rules worked well .	總統看過這些規則是如何運作的 。
so he tried to change the rules for pricing on electricity , but ran into a firestorm of protest from businesses and consumers who wanted to preserve the existing subsidized rates .	所以他試著改變使用電力的規則 , 但他進入了企業和消費者的激烈抗議活動 , 他們想要保存現有的補助率 。
so he was stuck with rules that prevented him from letting the winwin solution help his country .	他被困住了規則 , 阻止他讓贏家解決方案幫助他的國家 。
and nelson is stuck studying under the streetlights .	尼爾森在街燈下學習 。
the real challenge then , is to try to figure out how we can change rules .	真正的挑戰是要試著弄清楚我們能如何改變規則 。
are there some rules we can develop for changing rules ?	是否有一些規則可以用來改造規則 ?
i want to argue that there is a general abstract insight that we can make practical , which is that , if we can give more choices to people , and more choices to leaders who , in many countries , are also people .	我想主張 , 有一個普遍抽象的洞見 , 我們可以做出實際的體驗 , 那就是 , 如果我們能給人們更多選擇 , 並且對許多國家的領導者有更多選擇 , 也是人 。
but , it's useful to present the opposition between these two .	但 , 這兩者之間的反對是有用的 。
because the kind of choice you might want to give to a leader , a choice like giving the president the choice to raise prices on electricity , takes away a choice that people in the economy want .	因為你可能想給領袖一個選擇 , 像是給總統一個選擇 , 來提高電力的價格 , 取代經濟中人民的選擇 。
they want the choice to be able to continue consuming subsidized electric power .	他們希望選擇能夠繼續消耗補助電力 。
so if you give just to one side or the other , you'll have tension or friction .	所以如果你給一邊或另一邊 , 你會有張力或摩擦力 。
but if we can find ways to give more choices to both , that will give us a set of rules for changing rules that get us out of traps .	但如果我們能找到方法 , 給予兩者更多的選擇 , 那就給了我們一套規則 , 來改變我們走出陷阱的規則 。
now , nelson also has access to the internet .	nelson也能取得網路 。
and he says that if you want to see the damaging effects of rules , the ways that rules can keep people in the dark , look at the pictures from nasa of the earth at night .	他說 , 如果你想要看到規則的破壞效應 , 規則能讓人們在黑暗中保持在黑暗中 , 看一下地球的照片 。
in particular check out asia .	特別是亞洲人 。
if you zoom in here , you can see north korea , in outline here , which is like a black hole compared to its neighbors .	如果你放大這裡 , 你可以看到北韓 , 在線上 , 這就像是黑洞和鄰居相比 。
now , you won't be surprised to learn that the rules in north korea keep people there in the dark .	現在 , 你不會很驚訝地發現北韓的規則會讓人們在黑暗中保持在黑暗中 。
but it is important to recognize that north korea and south korea started out with identical sets of rules in both the sense of laws and regulations , but also in the deeper senses of understandings , norms , culture , values and beliefs .	但很重要的是 , 要知道北韓和南韓的規則 , 在法律和規範方面 , 兩者都一模一樣的規則 , 但在更深層的理解、規範、文化、價值觀和信念上 。
when they separated , they made choices that led to very divergent paths for their sets of rules .	當他們分開時 , 他們做了一些選擇 , 導致他們有非常多樣化的規則 。
so we can change we as humans can change the rules that we use to interact with each other , for better , or for worse .	所以 , 我們可以改變人類的規則 , 改變我們互相互動的規則 , 更好 , 或更糟糕 。
now let's look at another region , the caribbean .	現在讓我們來看另一個區域 , 加勒比海 。
zoom in on haiti , in outline here .	放大海地 , 在外線這裡 。
haiti is also dark , compared to its neighbor here , the dominican republic , which has about the same number of residents .	海地也是黑暗的 , 相較於它的鄰居 , 多明尼加共和國 , 相較於相同的居民數量 。
both of these countries are dark compared to puerto rico , which has half as many residents as either haiti or the dominican republic .	這些國家兩者都很暗 , 與波多黎各相比 , 其中有一半的居民是海地或多明尼加共和國 。
what haiti warns us is that rules can be bad because governments are weak .	海地警告我們 , 規則可能很糟 , 因為政府很弱 。
it's not just that the rules are bad because the government is too strong and oppressive , as in north korea .	不單只是規則不好 , 因為政府太強、太壓迫 , 就像北韓一樣 。
so that if we want to create environments with good rules , we can't just tear down .	所以如果我們想創造一個有好規則的環境 , 我們就不能只靠撕裂 。
we've got to find ways to build up , as well .	我們也得找出方法來建構 。
now , china dramatically demonstrates both the potential and the challenges of working with rules .	現在 , 中國戲劇性地展示了與規則合作的潛力和挑戰 。
back in the beginning of the data presented in this chart , china was the world's hightechnology leader .	在這個圖表的開端 , 中國是世界高科技領袖 。
chinese had pioneered technologies like steel , printing , gunpowder .	中國有先驅的技術 , 像是鋼、列印、槍枝 。
but the chinese never adopted , at least in that period , effective rules for encouraging the spread of those ideas a profit motive that could have encouraged the spread .	但中國從來沒有採用過 , 至少在那個時期 , 有效的規則來鼓勵那些想法的傳播 , 一個可以鼓勵傳播的利潤動機 。
and they soon adopted rules which slowed down innovation and cut china off from the rest of the world .	他們很快就採用了規則 , 減慢了創新 , 並將中國從世界其它地方移除 。
so as other countries in the world innovated , in the sense both of developing newer technologies , but also developing newer rules , the chinese were cut off from those advances .	所以 , 如同世界上其他國家的創新 , 兩者都發展新技術 , 但同時發展新的規則 , 中國人從這些進步中被砍掉 。
income there stayed stagnant , as it zoomed ahead in the rest of the world .	收入保持穩定 , 隨著它在世界其他地方放大 。
this next chart looks at more recent data .	下一個圖表比較近期的數據 。
it plots income , average income in china as a percentage of average income in the united states .	中國的平均收入佔美國平均收入的比例 。
in the '50s and '60s you can see that it was hovering at about three percent .	在50到60年代 , 你可以看到 , 大約佔百分之三 。
but then in the late '70s something changed .	但到了70年代末期 , 有些改變了 。
growth took off in china . the chinese started catching up very quickly with the united states .	成長在中國起飛 , 中國開始趕上美國 。
if you go back to the map at night , you can get a clue to the process that lead to the dramatic change in rules in china .	如果你回到夜晚的地圖 , 你就能得到一個線索 , 讓中國的規則有很大的改變 。
the brightest spot in china , which you can see on the edge of the outline here , is hong kong .	中國最亮的地點 , 你可以看到在外線的邊緣 , 就是香港 。
hong kong was a small bit of china that , for most of the 20th century , operated under a very different set of rules than the rest of mainland china rules that were copied from working market economies of the time , and administered by the british .	香港是一小部分的中國 , 大部分20世紀以來 , 採用非常不同的規則 , 遠超過當時的主要中國規則 , 已經從工業市場經濟中複製出來 , 由英國人主導 。
in the 1950s , hong kong was a place where millions of people could go , from the mainland , to start in jobs like sewing shirts , making toys .	在1950年代 , 香港是數百萬人可以去的地方 , 從大陸開始 , 像是縫製襯衫 , 製作玩具 。
but , to get on a process of increasing income , increasing skills led to very rapid growth there .	但 , 為了增加收入的過程 , 增加技能 , 導致非常快速的成長 。
hong kong was also the model which leaders like deng xiaoping could copy , when they decided to move all of the mainland towards the market model .	香港也是個典範 , 像是英國xiaoping可以複製 , 當他們決定把所有大陸都移到市場模式時 。
but deng xiaoping instinctively understood the importance of offering choices to his people .	但 , 英雄要直覺地了解 , 給予他人選擇的重要性 。
so instead of forcing everyone in china to shift immediately to the market model , they proceeded by creating some special zones that could do , in a sense , what britain did: make the opportunity to go work with the market rules available to the people who wanted to opt in there .	所以 , 與其迫使中國人立即轉變為市場模式 , 他們創造了一些特殊的區塊 , 在某種意義上 , 英國所做的是:讓機會和市場規則合作 , 和想要選的人一起合作 。
so they created four special economic zones around hong kong: zones where chinese could come and work , and cities grew up very rapidly there ; also zones where foreign firms could come in and make things .	所以他們在香港附近創造了四個特殊的經濟區 , 中國人可以來工作 , 城市很快就在那裡長大 , 外國企業可以進來製造東西 。
one of the zones next to hong kong has a city called shenzhen .	香港旁邊有一座城市叫做 「 希恩文 」 。
in that city there is a taiwanese firm that made the iphone that many of you have , and they made it with labor from chinese who moved there to shenzhen .	在這個城市中 , 有一間台台灣公司 , 在座很多人都有iphone , 他們用中國的勞工搬到sanzhen 。
so after the four special zones , there were 14 coastal cites that were open in the same sense , and eventually demonstrated successes in these places that people could opt in to , that they flocked to because of the advantages they offered .	所以在四個特殊區域之後 , 有14個海岸線 , 以相同的方式開放 , 最終 , 在這些地方 , 人們可以選擇的成功 , 他們被鎖定在他們提供的優勢上 。
demonstrated successes there led to a consensus for a move toward the market model for the entire economy .	那裡的成功導致了共識 , 讓整個經濟體的市場模式向前邁進 。
now the chinese example shows us several points .	中國的例子顯示了好幾個點 。
one is: preserve choices for people .	第一 , 保存人們的選擇 。
two: operate on the right scale .	第二:在正確的規模操作 。
if you try to change the rules in a village , you could do that , but a village would be too small to get the kinds of benefits you can get if you have millions of people all working under good rules .	如果你試著改變一個村莊的規則 , 你可以做到 , 但一個村莊太小了 , 要是你有數百萬人在良好的規則下工作 , 就能得到好處 。
on the other hand , the nation is too big .	另一方面 , 國家太大了 。
if you try to change the rules in the nation , you can't give some people a chance to hold back , see how things turn out , and let others zoom ahead and try the new rules .	如果你試著改變國家的規則 , 你就不能給一些人一個機會 , 看看事情如何發生 , 讓其他人放大 , 嘗試新的規則 。
but cities give you this opportunity to create new places , with new rules that people can opt in to .	但城市給你一個機會 , 創造出新的地方 , 新的規則 , 讓人們可以選擇 。
and they're large enough to get all of the benefits that we can have when millions of us work together under good rules .	而他們大到足以取得所有我們在好規則下工作的好處 。
so the proposal is that we conceive of something called a charter city .	所以 , 提議是我們構想一個叫做 「 查理城市 」 的東西 。
we start with a charter that specifies all the rules required to attract the people who we'll need to build the city .	我們從一個章節開始 , 針對所有規則 , 來吸引我們所需要的人 , 來建造這個城市 。
we'll need to attract the investors who will build out the infrastructure the power system , the roads , the port , the airport , the buildings .	我們需要吸引投資者 , 建立基礎建設電力系統、道路、港口、機場、建築物 。
you'll need to attract firms , who will come hire the people who move there first .	你需要吸引公司 , 誰會先僱用先搬到那裡的人 。
and you'll need to attract families , the residents who will come and live there permanently , raise their children , get an education for their children , and get their first job .	你需要吸引家庭、居民來到那裡 , 永久生活 , 養育他們的孩子 , 為他們的孩子取得教育 , 取得他們的第一份工作 。
with that charter , people will move there .	有了那張圖表 , 人們會搬到那裡 。
the city can be built .	城市可以被建造出來 。
and we can scale this model .	我們可以把這個模型規模化 。
we can go do it over and over again .	我們可以一遍又一遍地進行 。
to make it work , we need good rules . we've already discussed that .	為了讓它運作 , 我們需要良好的規則 。 我們已經討論過 。
those are captured in the charter .	這些都是在charter上捕捉到的 。
we also need the choices for people .	我們也需要人們的選擇 。
that's really built into the model if we allow for the possibility of building cities on uninhabited land .	這真的是建立在模型中 , 如果我們能在未居住的土地上建立城市的可能性 。
you start from uninhabited territory .	你從未居住的領域開始 。
people can come live under the new charter , but no one is forced to live under it .	人們可以住在新chrter之下 , 但沒有人被迫住在它之下 。
the final thing we need are choices for leaders .	最後一件我們需要的是領導者的選擇 。
and , to achieve the kind of choices we want for leaders we need to allow for the potential for partnerships between nations: cases where nations work together , in effect , de facto , the way china and britain worked together to build , first a little enclave of the market model , and then scale it throughout china .	為了達成我們想要領導者的選擇 , 我們需要讓國家之間的合作關係 , 讓國家團結在一起 , 實際上 , 中國和英國合作 , 建立一個市場模型 , 然後擴大整個中國 。
in a sense , britain , inadvertently , through its actions in hong kong , did more to reduce world poverty than all the aid programs that we've undertaken in the last century .	在某種意義上 , 英國 , 不經意地 , 透過香港的行動 , 來減少世界貧窮 , 比我們在上個世紀所遭受的所有援助計畫還要多 。
so if we allow for these kind of partnerships to replicate this again , we can get those kinds of benefits scaled throughout the world .	所以 , 如果我們能讓這種合作關係再次複製 , 我們就能讓世界上各地的利益擴大 。
in some cases this will involve a delegation of responsibility , a delegation of control from one country to another to take over certain kinds of administrative responsibilities .	在某些情況下 , 這會涉及一種責任 , 一種控制權 , 從一個國家到另一個國家 , 來克服某些政府的責任 。
now , when i say that , some of you are starting to think , " well , is this just bringing back colonialism ? "	現在 , 當我這麼說時 , 有些人開始想: 「 嗯 , 這會帶回殖民主義嗎 ? 」
it's not . but it's important to recognize that the kind of emotions that come up when we start to think about these things , can get in the way , can make us pull back , can shut down our ability , and our interest in trying to explore new ideas .	並非如此 。 但重要的是要意識到當我們開始思考這些事情時會出現的那種情緒 , 可以讓我們回到過去 , 可以阻止我們的能力 , 並且我們對探索新想法的興趣 。
why is this not like colonialism ?	為什麼這不像殖民主義 ?
the thing that was bad about colonialism , and the thing which is residually bad in some of our aid programs , is that it involved elements of coercion and condescension .	關於殖民主義的壞事 , 在我們的一些援助計畫中 , 居住的壞事是它涉及了衝突和自閉症的元素 。
this model is all about choices , both for leaders and for the people who will live in these new places .	這個模式是關於選擇 , 無論是領導者 , 以及未來會居住在這些新地方的人 。
and , choice is the antidote to coercion and condescension .	選擇是對強迫和自閉症的解藥 。
so let's talk about how this could play out in practice .	所以 , 咱們來談談這如何在實踐中演奏 。
let's take a particular leader , raul castro , who is the leader of cuba .	讓我們拿一個特定的領導人拉爾•卡斯楚 , 他是古巴的領導者 。
it must have occurred to castro that he has the chance to do for cuba what deng xiaoping did for china , but he doesn't have a hong kong there on the island in cuba .	肯定是為了卡斯楚 , 他有機會為古巴做古巴的xiaoping做事 , 但他沒有在古巴島的香港 。
he does , though , have a little bit of light down in the south that has a very special status .	不過 , 他的確在南方有一點點光 , 那裡有很特別的地位 。
there is a zone there , around guantanamo bay , where a treaty gives the united states administrative responsibility for a piece of land that's about twice the size of manhattan .	這裡有一個區塊 , 位於保納莫灣 , 在那裡 , 一個條約給美國政府負責一塊土地 , 大約是曼哈頓兩倍大 。
castro goes to the prime minister of canada and says , " look , the yankees have a terrible pr problem .	克斯斯楚去了加拿大總理 , 說: 「 看 , 沒錯 , 沒問題 。
they want to get out .	他們想出去 。
why don't you , canada , take over ?	為何你不 , 加拿大 , 克服呢 ?
build run a special administrative zone .	建造一個特殊的行政區 。
allow a new city to be built up there .	允許一個新的城市在那裡建造 。
allow many people to come in .	讓許多人進來 。
let us have a hong kong nearby .	讓我們在附近有一個香港 。
some of my citizens will move into that city as well .	我的一些公民也會搬進這個城市 。
others will hold back . but this will be the gateway that will connect the modern economy and the modern world to my country . "	其他人會回來 , 但這將會是將現代經濟和現代世界連結到我的國家 。 」
now , where else might this model be tried ?	現在 , 這個模型還能被試驗到哪裡呢 ?
well , africa . i've talked with leaders in africa .	非洲 , 我和非洲的領導人談過 。
many of them totally get the notion of a special zone that people can opt into as a rule .	許多人完全得到一個特殊區域的概念 , 讓人們可以選擇一個規則 。
it's a rule for changing rules .	這是一個改變規則的規則 。
it's a way to create new rules , and let people optin without coercion , and the opposition that coercion can force .	它是一種創造新規則的方法 , 讓人們不需要合作 , 和合作的反面 。
they also totally get the idea that in some instances they can make more credible promises to longterm investors the kind of investors who will come build the port , build the roads , in a new city they can make more credible promises if they do it along with a partner nation .	他們也完全了解 , 在某些情況下 , 他們能做出更可信的承諾 , 來長期投資者 , 像是建造港口、建造道路、新城市 , 如果他們和一個夥伴合作 , 他們就能做出更可信的承諾 。
perhaps even in some arrangement that's a little bit like an escrow account , where you put land in the escrow account and the partner nation takes responsibility for it .	甚至在一些安排中 , 有點像是一個逃生帳戶 , 在那裡 , 你把土地放進逃生帳戶中 , 國民對此負起責任 。
there is also lots of land in africa where new cities could be built .	非洲也有許多土地可以建造新的城市 。
this is a picture i took when i was flying along the coast .	這是我在海岸飛行時拍的照片 。
there are immense stretches of land like this land where hundreds of millions of people could live .	這裡有巨大的土地 , 像這樣的土地 , 那裡有數億人可以住在那裡 。
now , if we generalize this and think about not just one or two charter cites , but dozens cities that will help create places for the many hundreds of millions , perhaps billions of people who will move to cities in the coming century is there enough land for them ?	現在 , 若我們將這點放進去 , 想一想 , 不只一、二個慈愛團體 , 而是數十億的城市 , 甚至數十億的人口 , 都能為他們創造一個地方 ?
well , throughout the world , if we look at the lights at night , the one thing that's misleading is that , visually , it looks like most of the world is already built out .	嗯 , 在世界各地 , 如果我們看夜間的燈光 , 一個錯誤的事情 , 就是 , 視覺上來說 , 世界上大部分的燈光已經被建造出來了 。
so let me show you why that's wrong .	所以 , 讓我給你們看為什麼會這樣 。
take this representation of all of the land .	以這代表所有土地 。
turn it into a square that stands for all the arable land on earth .	把它轉變成平方形 , 代表地球上所有可耕地 。
and let these dots represent the land that's already taken up by the cities that three billion people now live in .	讓這些點代表現在有三十億人口居住的城市 。
if you move the dots down to the bottom of the rectangle you can see that the cities for the existing three billion urban residents take up only three percent of the arable land on earth .	如果你把點移到長方形的底部 , 你可以看到現有的三十億個城市居民 , 只佔地球上可耕地的百分之三 。
so if we wanted to build cities for another billion people , they would be dots like this .	所以如果我們想要為數十億人建造城市 , 他們就會像這樣的點 。
we'd go from three percent of the arable land , to four percent .	我們從3%的可耕地 , 到4% 。
we'd dramatically reduce the human footprint on earth by building more cities that people can move to .	我們會大幅降低地球上的人類足跡 , 建造更多的城市 , 讓人們可以移動 。
and if these are cities governed by good rules , they can be cities where people are safe from crime , safe from disease and bad sanitation , where people have a chance to get a job .	如果這些城市被良好的規則所管理 , 他們可以成為城市 , 人們安全地從犯罪、疾病和不良衛生 , 在那裡 , 人們有機會找到工作 。
they can get basic utilities like electricity .	它們可以得到基本的電力 , 像是電力 。
their kids can get an education .	他們的孩子可以得到教育 。
so what will it take to get started building the first charter cities , scaling this so we build many more ?	所以 , 要開始建立第一座慈善城市 , 我們要怎麼做才能建造更多的土地 ?
it would help to have a manual .	它會幫助手冊 。
what university professors could do is write some details that might go into this manual .	大學教授可以做的是寫一些細節 , 可以進入這個手冊 。
you wouldn't want to let us run the cities , go out and design them .	你不會想讓我們跑城市 , 去設計它們 。
you wouldn't let academics out in the wild .	你不會讓學者走出野外 。
but , you could set us to work thinking about questions like , suppose it isn't just canada that does the deal with raul castro .	但 , 你可以讓我們思考一些問題 , 例如 , 假設 , 加拿大不僅僅是加拿大對抗種族災難 。
perhaps brazil comes in as a participant , and spain as well . and perhaps cuba wants to be one of the partners in a fourway joint venture .	或許巴西是參與者 , 西班牙也想成為四個關節的夥伴之一 。
how would we write the treaty to do that ?	我們要怎麼寫治療法呢 ?
there is less precedent for that , but that could easily be worked out .	這樣做比較少先例 , 但那很容易就成功了 。
how would we finance this ?	我們要如何資助這一點 ?
turns out singapore and hong kong are cities that made huge gains on the value of the land that they owned when they got started .	結果發現 , 新加坡和香港是種很大的城市 , 他們在一開始就有了土地的價值 。
you could use the gains on the value of the land to pay for things like the police , the courts , but the school system and the health care system too , which make this a more attractive place to live , makes this a place where people have higher incomes which , incidentally , makes the land more valuable .	你可以利用土地的價值 , 來支付像警察、法庭等東西 , 但學校和醫療保健體系也讓這個更吸引人的地方 , 讓人們有更高的收入 , 意外 , 讓土地變得更有價值 。
so the incentives for the people helping to construct this zone and build it , and set up the basic rules , go very much in the right direction .	所以 , 人們幫助建構這個區域的誘因 , 設立基礎規則 , 走對的方向 。
so there are many other details like this .	這裡還有很多其他細節 。
how could we have buildings that are low cost and affordable for people who work in a first job , assembling something like an iphone , but make those buildings energy efficient , and make sure that they are safe , so they don't fall down in an earthquake or a hurricane .	我們怎麼可能有建築物的成本很低 , 對第一份工作的人們來說 , 組裝像iphone這樣的東西 , 讓那些建築能有效率 , 確保它們是安全的 , 所以它們不會在地震或颶風中落下 。
many technical details to be worked out , but those of us who are already starting to pursue these things can already tell that there is no roadblock , there's no impediment , other than a failure of imagination , that will keep us from delivering on a truly global winwin solution .	許多技術上的細節都已經成功 , 但那些已經開始追求這些東西的人已經知道沒有道路 , 沒有任何阻礙 , 除了想像的失敗之外 , 會使我們無法實現真正全球的雙贏解決方案 。
let me conclude with this picture .	讓我用這張照片來做結論 。
the reason we can be so well off , even though there is so many people on earth , is because of the power of ideas .	我們之所以能如此順利 , 即使地球上有這麼多人 , 是因為想法的力量 。
we can share ideas with other people , and when they discover them , they share with us .	我們可以和他人分享想法 , 當他們發現他們時 , 他們會和我們分享 。
it's not like scarce objects , where sharing means we each get less .	不像缺乏物品 , 分享的意義就越少 。
when we share ideas we all get more .	當我們分享想法時 , 我們都會得到更多 。
when we think about ideas in that way , we usually think about technologies .	當我們用這種方式思考想法時 , 我們通常會想到科技 。
but there is another class of ideas: the rules that govern how we interact with each other ; rules like , let's have a tax system that supports a research university that gives away certain kinds of knowledge for free .	但還有另一類想法:我們如何與彼此互動的規則 ; 規則如 , 我們有一個稅制系統 , 支持一個研究大學 , 免費的知識 。
let's have a system where we have ownership of land that is registered in a government office , that people can pledge as collateral .	咱們來做一個系統 , 我們擁有一座政府辦公室的所有權 , 讓人們可以作為一座冰川 。
if we can keep innovating on our space of rules , and particularly innovate in the sense of coming up with rules for changing rules , so we don't get stuck with bad rules , then we can keep moving progress forward and truly make the world a better place , so that people like nelson and his friends don't have to study any longer under the streetlights . thank you .	如果我們能繼續創新我們的規則 , 尤其是創新 , 以改變規則的角度來看 , 我們就不會被困住 , 那麼我們就能繼續進步 , 真正讓世界變得更好 , 像nelson和他的朋友不再需要在街燈下學習 。 謝謝 。
genomics pioneer craig venter takes a break from his epic roundtheworld expedition to talk about the millions of genes his team has discovered so far in its quest to map the ocean’s biodiversity .	基因組學先驅克雷格•凡特從他的史詩圓頂探險中休息 , 談到他的團隊中數百萬個基因 , 到目前為止 , 發現了海洋生物多樣性 。
dna , biosphere , biotech , entrepreneur , genetics , invention , oceans , science , technology	dna , 生物圈、生物科技、企業家、基因、發明、海洋、科學、科技、科技、科技、科技 。
craig venter on dna and the sea	克雷格•凡特在dna和海上 。
at the break , i was asked by several people about my comments about the aging debate .	休息時 , 我被幾個人問到我對於老化辯論的評論 。
and this will be my only comment on it .	這將會是我唯一的留言 。
and that is , i understand that optimists greatly outlive pessimists .	那就是 , 我了解到樂觀主義者極度過時的悲觀主義者 。
what i'm going to tell you about in my 18 minutes is how we're about to switch from reading the genetic code to the first stages of beginning to write the code ourselves .	在我18分鐘內 , 我要告訴各位 , 我們將如何從基因編碼轉換到開始寫程式的第一階段 。
it's only 10 years ago this month when we published the first sequence of a freeliving organism , that of haemophilus influenzae .	只有10年前 , 當我們發表了第一序列的自由有機體時 , 海豚傳染了流感病毒的第一個序列 。
that took a genome project from 13 years down to four months .	這個計畫從13年到4個月 , 完成了基因組計畫 。
we can now do that same genome project in the order of two to eight hours .	我們現在可以在兩到八小時內完成同樣的基因組計劃 。
so in the last decade , a large number of genomes have been added: most human pathogens , a couple of plants , several insects and several mammals , including the human genome .	在過去的十年間 , 大量的基因組被加入了:大部分的人類病原體、幾種植物、幾種昆蟲和數種哺乳類 , 包括人類的基因組 。
genomics at this stage of the thinking from a little over 10 years ago was , by the end of this year , we might have between three and five genomes sequenced ; it's on the order of several hundred .	十多年前 , 基因組學的思考階段在今年年底 , 我們可能有三到五個基因組定序 , 數百個 。
we just got a grant from the gordon and betty moore foundation to sequence 130 genomes this year , as a side project from environmental organisms .	今年我們剛從戈登和貝蒂摩爾基金會取得了130個基因組 , 作為環保有機體的一方計畫 。
so the rate of reading the genetic code has changed .	所以 , 閱讀基因編碼的速度已經改變了 。
but as we look , what's out there , we've barely scratched the surface on what is available on this planet .	但當我們看到 , 外面的狀況 , 我們幾乎無法在這個星球上取得的表面上 。
most people don't realize it , because they're invisible , but microbes make up about a half of the earth's biomass , whereas all animals only make up about one onethousandth of all the biomass .	大部份人都不知道 , 因為它們是看不見的 , 但微生物佔了地球一半的生物量 , 而所有動物只佔所有生物量的一千分之一 。
and maybe it's something that people in oxford don't do very often , but if you ever make it to the sea , and you swallow a mouthful of seawater , keep in mind that each milliliter has about a million bacteria and on the order of 10 million viruses .	也許是牛津人常常會做的事 , 但如果你去海裡 , 吞下一口海水 , 請記住每一毫升的細菌和一千萬種病毒 。
less than 5 , 000 microbial species have been characterized as of two years ago , and so we decided to do something about it .	不到五千種微生物的物種 , 兩年前被特徵化 , 所以我們決定要做點什麼 。
and we started the sorcerer ii expedition , where we were , as with great oceanographic expeditions , trying to sample the ocean every 200 miles .	我們成立了srcer二次探險 , 在那裡 , 我們和偉大的海洋探險探險一樣 , 每兩百英哩都在海中進行樣本 。
we started in bermuda for our test project , then moved up to halifax , working down the u . s . east coast , the caribbean sea , the panama canal , through to the galapagos , then across the pacific , and we're in the process now of working our way across the indian ocean .	我們從bermuda開始進行測試 , 然後搬到哈利法克斯 , 沿著美國東岸 , 加勒比海 , 巴拿馬運河 , 到加拉帕戈斯 , 然後跨越太平洋 , 我們現在正在橫跨印度洋 。
it's very tough duty ; we're doing this on a sailing vessel , in part to help excite young people about going into science .	這是非常艱難的職責 ; 我們在船上做這件事 , 部分原因是協助年輕人進入科學領域 。
the experiments are incredibly simple .	實驗非常簡單 。
we just take seawater and we filter it , and we collect different size organisms on different filters , and then take their dna back to our lab in rockville , where we can sequence a hundred million letters of the genetic code every 24 hours .	我們只是把海水過濾 , 收集不同的大小生物 , 然後把它們的dna帶回我們在洛克維爾的實驗室 , 在那裡 , 我們每24小時就能定序一億個基因密碼 。
and with doing this , we've made some amazing discoveries .	透過這樣做 , 我們創造了一些驚人的發現 。
for example , it was thought that the visual pigments that are in our eyes there was only one or two organisms in the environment that had these same pigments .	舉例來說 , 人們認為我們的眼睛裡的視覺色素只有一到兩種有機體存在著相同的顏料
it turns out , almost every species in the upper parts of the ocean in warm parts of the world have these same photoreceptors , and use sunlight as the source of their energy and communication .	結果發現 , 幾乎全世界的所有物種都有相同的光接接收器 , 並用太陽光當它們的能量和溝通來源 。
from one site , from one barrel of seawater , we discovered 1 . 3 million new genes and as many as 50 , 000 new species .	從一個地點 , 從一個海水桶裡 , 我們發現了一百三十萬個新基因 , 大約五萬個新物種 。
we've extended this to the air now with a grant from the sloan foundation .	我們已經從sloan基金會把這個延伸到空氣中 。
we're measuring how many viruses and bacteria all of us are breathing in and out every day , particularly on airplanes or closed auditoriums .	我們在測量有多少病毒和細菌 , 我們每天都在呼吸 , 特別是在飛機或關閉的聽覺室 。
we filter through some simple apparatuses ; we collect on the order of a billion microbes from just a day filtering on top of a building in new york city .	我們過濾了一些簡單的外表 , 我們收集了十億微生物的數量 , 來自紐約市的一棟建築物 。
and we're in the process of sequencing all that at the present time .	而我們正處於當今的過程中 。
just on the data collection side , just where we are through the galapagos , we're finding that almost every 200 miles , we see tremendous diversity in the samples in the ocean .	只是在資料集的一面 , 我們在加拉帕戈斯的那一面 , 我們發現幾乎每200英里 , 我們看到海洋中的樣本有多樣性 。
some of these make logical sense , in terms of different temperature gradients .	有些是合乎邏輯的 , 在不同溫度的層面上 。
so this is a satellite photograph based on temperatures red being warm , blue being cold and we found there's a tremendous difference between the warm water samples and the cold water samples , in terms of abundant species .	這是一張衛星照片 , 以紅色為基礎的溫度為基礎 , 藍色是溫暖的 , 藍色是冷的 , 我們發現溫暖的水樣本和冷水樣本有很大的差別 。
the other thing that surprised us quite a bit is these photoreceptors detect different wavelengths of light , and we can predict that based on their amino acid sequence .	另一件令我們驚訝的事是這些光接收器偵測到不同波長的光 , 我們可以根據他們的胺基酸序列來預測 。
and these vary tremendously from region to region .	從區域到區域 , 這些差異很大 。
maybe not surprisingly , in the deep ocean , where it's mostly blue , the photoreceptors tend to see blue light .	也許不意外地 , 在深海中 , 大部分是藍色的 , 光接受器通常會看到藍光 。
when there's a lot of chlorophyll around , they see a lot of green light .	當有大量的染色體時 , 它們會看到大量的綠光 。
but they vary even more , possibly moving towards infrared and ultraviolet in the extremes .	但它們還會更大 , 可能在極端的情況下轉向紅外線和紫外線 。
just to try and get an assessment of what our gene repertoire was , we assembled all the data including all of ours thus far from the expedition , which represents more than half of all the gene data on the planet and it totaled around 29 million genes .	為了評估我們的基因複製 , 我們組裝了所有的資料 , 包括我們遠離探險的所有資料 , 代表了地球上所有基因資料的一半 , 總共有2千9百萬個基因 。
and we tried to put these into gene families to see what these discoveries are: are we just discovering new members of known families , or are we discovering new families ?	我們試著把這些基因改造給基因家庭 , 看看這些發現是什麼:我們只是發現已知家庭的新成員 , 還是我們發現了新的家人 ?
and it turns out we have about 50 , 000 major gene families , but every new sample we take in the environment adds in a linear fashion to these new families .	結果發現 , 我們有大約五萬個主要的基因家庭 , 但我們在環境中的每一種新樣本 , 都會在線性時期加入這些新家庭 。
so we're at the earliest stages of discovery about basic genes , components and life on this planet .	所以 , 我們正處於最早期的階段 , 發現這個星球上的基本基因、元素和生命 。
when we look at the socalled evolutionary tree , we're up on the upper righthand corner with the animals .	當我們觀察所謂的演化樹 , 我們就站在右上角和動物的角落 。
of those roughly 29 million genes , we only have around 24 , 000 in our genome .	其中大約有兩千九百萬個基因 , 我們的基因組中只有大約2萬4千個 。
and if you take all animals together , we probably share less than 30 , 000 and probably maybe a dozen or more thousand different gene families .	如果你把所有動物聚集在一起 , 我們可能有超過三萬個 , 也許是十萬個不同的基因家庭 。
i view that these genes are now not only the design components of evolution .	我認為這些基因現在不僅僅是演化的設計成分 。
and we think in a genecentric view maybe going back to richard dawkins' ideas than in a genomecentric view , which are different constructs of these gene components .	我們認為 , 在一個慷慨的觀點中 , 可能回到理查•達金斯的點子 , 和基因組成的不同結構 。
synthetic dna , the ability to synthesize dna , has changed at sort of the same pace that dna sequencing has over the last decade or two , and is getting very rapid and very cheap .	合成dna , 合成dna的能力 , 改變了過去十年間dna定序的速度 , 越來越低 。
our first thought about synthetic genomics came when we sequenced the second genome back in 1995 , and that from mycoplasma genitalium .	我們第一次想到合成基因組學 , 是在1995年 , 我們將第二個基因組定序 , 從菌絲體的生殖器 。
and we have really nice tshirts that say , you know , " i heart my genitalium . "	我們有很棒的t恤 , 上面寫著: 「 我很愛我的生殖器官 。 」
this is actually just a microorganism .	這其實只是個微生物 。
but it has roughly 500 genes .	但它有大約500個基因 。
haemophilus had 1 , 800 genes .	海底有一千八百個基因 。
and we simply asked the question , if one species needs 800 , another 500 , is there a smaller set of genes that might comprise a minimal operating system ?	我們只是問一個問題 , 如果一個物種需要800 , 另一個500 , 是否有一組較小的基因 , 可以組成一個最小的營運系統 ?
so we started doing transposon mutagenesis .	所以 , 我們開始進行轉移性突變 。
transposons are just small pieces of dna that randomly insert in the genetic code .	轉移只是基因編碼中的一小片dna , 隨機在基因編碼中插入 。
and if they insert in the middle of the gene , they disrupt its function .	如果他們在基因的中間插入 , 就會破壞它的功能 。
so we made a map of all the genes that could take transposon insertions and we called those " nonessential genes . "	所以我們做了一張基因的地圖 , 可以取代轉移的插入 , 我們稱之為 「 非正向基因 」 。
but it turns out the environment is very critical for this , and you can only define an essential or nonessential gene based on exactly what's in the environment .	但事實證明 , 環境對此非常重要 , 你只能根據環境中的環境來定義一個必要或正直的基因 。
we also tried to take a more directly intellectual approach with the genomes of 13 related organisms , and we tried to compare all of those , to see what they had in common .	我們也試著用更直接的智能方法來處理13個相關有機體的基因組 , 我們試著將這些基因組做比較 , 看看它們的共通點 。
and we got these overlapping circles . and we found only 173 genes common to all 13 organisms .	我們找到這些重疊的圓圈 。 我們發現 , 只有173個基因和13個有機體相同 。
the pool expanded a little bit if we ignored one intracellular parasite ; it expanded even more when we looked at core sets of genes of around 310 or so .	如果我們忽略了一個細胞寄生蟲的基因 , 它會擴展到310種核心基因組 , 以此類推 。
so we think that we can expand or contract genomes , depending on your point of view here , to maybe 300 to 400 genes from the minimal of 500 .	所以 , 我們認為我們可以擴張或收縮基因組 , 根據你的觀點來看 , 大約300到400個基因 。
the only way to prove these ideas was to construct an artificial chromosome with those genes in them , and we had to do this in a cassettebased fashion .	要證明這些想法的唯一方法就是建立一個人工染色體 , 裡面有這些基因 , 我們必須在以電腦為基礎的時尚中做這個 。
we found that synthesizing accurate dna in large pieces was extremely difficult .	我們發現 , 在大片片片段合成dna的合成是非常困難的 。
ham smith and clyde hutchison , my colleagues on this , developed an exciting new method that allowed us to synthesize a 5 , 000base pair virus in only a twoweek period that was 100 percent accurate , in terms of its sequence and its biology .	hmsmith和clydehutchison , 我的同事開發出了一種令人興奮的新方法 , 讓我們能在兩週內合成一種50000個鹼基對病毒 , 以它的序列和生物學來說 , 只有百分之百正確 。
it was a quite exciting experiment when we just took the synthetic piece of dna , injected it in the bacteria and all of a sudden , that dna started driving the production of the virus particles that turned around and then killed the bacteria .	這是個非常令人興奮的實驗 , 當我們把合成的dna注入細菌中 , 突然間 , dna開始驅動病毒粒子的生產 , 然後殺死細菌 。
this was not the first synthetic virus a polio virus had been made a year before but it was only one tenthousandth as active and it took three years to do .	這不是小兒麻痺病毒的第一個合成病毒一年才被製造出來的 , 但它只是活躍的一公分 , 花了三年的時間 。
this is a cartoon of the structure of phi x 174 .	這是phix-174的結構圖 。
this is a case where the software now builds its own hardware , and that's the notions that we have with biology .	這個案例是軟體現在建構自己的硬體 , 那就是我們對生物學的看法 。
people immediately jump to concerns about biological warfare , and i had recent testimony before a senate committee , and a special committee the u . s . government has set up to review this area .	人們馬上開始關心生物戰爭 , 我在參議院委員會之前有近期的證詞 , 以及美國政府設立了一項特殊委員會 , 來審視這個區域 。
and i think it's important to keep reality in mind , versus what happens with people's imaginations .	我認為 , 要讓現實保持在心中 , 和人們的想像有所不同 。
basically , any virus that's been sequenced today that genome can be made .	基本上 , 任何現今已經被定序的病毒 , 基因組可以被製造出來 。
and people immediately freak out about things about ebola or smallpox , but the dna from this organism is not infective .	人們馬上會想到伊波拉或天花 , 但這個有機體的dna不是感染的 。
so even if somebody made the smallpox genome , that dna itself would not cause infections .	所以即使有人做了天花基因組 , dna本身不會造成感染 。
the real concern that security departments have is designer viruses .	真正關注安全部的真正關心的是設計師病毒 。
and there's only two countries , the u . s . and the former soviet union , that had major efforts on trying to create biological warfare agents .	只有兩個國家 , 美國和前蘇聯有很大的努力 , 試圖創造生物武器 。
if that research is truly discontinued , there should be very little activity on the knowhow to make designer viruses in the future .	如果那份研究是真正不穩定的 , 那麼在未來 , 要讓設計師的病毒在未來就不應該有很大的活動 。
i think singlecell organisms are possible within two years .	我認為單細胞有機體在兩年內是有可能的 。
and possibly eukaryotic cells , those that we have , are possible within a decade .	可能在十年內 , 那些我們擁有的 , 可能是有可能的 。
so we're now making several dozen different constructs , because we can vary the cassettes and the genes that go into this artificial chromosome .	所以 , 我們現在在製造數十種不同的建構 , 因為我們可以改變種類和基因 , 進入這個人造染色體中 。
the key is , how do you put all of the others ?	關鍵在於 , 你要如何把所有其他人放在一起 ?
we start with these fragments , and then we have a homologous recombination system that reassembles those into a chromosome .	我們從這些碎片開始 , 再加上一個全面的重新組合系統 , 將它們組合成一個染色體 。
this is derived from an organism , deinococcus radiodurans , that can take three million rads of radiation and not be killed .	這是從一個有機體中衍生出來的 , 白血球菌 , 可以用三百萬種放射線來殺死 。
it reassembles its genome after this radiation burst in about 12 to 24 hours , after its chromosomes are literally blown apart .	它在這個放射線爆炸之後重新組合它的基因組大約12到24小時後它的染色體分開了
this organism is ubiquitous on the planet , and exists perhaps now in outer space due to all our travel there .	這個有機體在地球上無所不在 , 也許現在存在於外太空 , 由於我們的旅行 。
this is a glass beaker after about half a million rads of radiation .	這是一台玻璃洗衣機 , 大約有50萬個射線輻射 。
the glass started to burn and crack , while the microbes sitting in the bottom just got happier and happier .	玻璃開始燃燒和裂縫 , 而底部的微生物就變得更快樂和更快樂 。
here's an actual picture of what happens: the top of this shows the genome after 1 . 7 million rads of radiation .	這是一張真實的圖片:這個圖片的上方顯示了一百七十萬個輻射後的基因組 。
the chromosome is literally blown apart .	染色體其實是被拆散的 。
and here's that same dna automatically reassembled 24 hours later .	同樣的dna在24小時後自動重新組合 。
it's truly stunning that these organisms can do that , and we probably have thousands , if not tens of thousands , of different species on this planet that are capable of doing that .	令人驚訝的是這些生物可以做到這一點 , 我們可能有成千上萬的生物 , 如果沒有成千上萬的地球上不同的物種可以做到這一點 。
after these genomes are synthesized , the first step is just transplanting them into a cell without a genome .	在這些基因組合成之後 , 第一步就是將它們移植到一個沒有基因組的細胞中 。
so we think synthetic cells are going to have tremendous potential , not only for understanding the basis of biology but for hopefully environmental and society issues .	所以 , 我們認為合成細胞將會有巨大的潛力 , 不僅是為了了解生物學的基礎 , 還對環境和社會議題有希望 。
for example , from the third organism we sequenced , methanococcus jannaschii it lives in boiling water temperatures ; its energy source is hydrogen and all its carbon comes from co2 it captures back from the environment .	例如 , 第三種有機體 , 我們定序 , 甲烷佔據了它在沸水中的溫度 ; 它的能量來源是氫 , 所有的碳來自於環境中的二氧化碳 。
so we know lots of different pathways , thousands of different organisms now that live off of co2 , and can capture that back .	所以 , 我們知道很多不同的路徑 , 數以千計的有機體現在住在二氧化碳中 , 並且可以捕捉回來 。
so instead of using carbon from oil for synthetic processes , we have the chance of using carbon and capturing it back from the atmosphere , converting that into biopolymers or other products .	所以 , 不是用石油來做合成程序 , 我們有機會利用碳來捕捉它 , 從大氣中將它轉換成生物聚合物或其他產品 。
we have one organism that lives off of carbon monoxide , and we use as a reducing power to split water to produce hydrogen and oxygen .	我們有一個有機體 , 存在於二氧化碳 , 我們用它來降低水分 , 來產生氫和氧氣 。
also , there's numerous pathways that can be engineered metabolizing methane .	此外 , 有數條路徑可以被工程代謝甲烷 。
and dupont has a major program with statoil in norway to capture and convert the methane from the gas fields there into useful products .	杜邦有一個很大的計畫 , 用挪威的雕像來捕捉和將氣體的甲烷轉化為有用的產品 。
within a short while , i think there's going to be a new field called " combinatorial genomics , " because with these new synthesis capabilities , these vast gene array repertoires and the homologous recombination , we think we can design a robot to make maybe a million different chromosomes a day .	在短短的一段時間內 , 我認為有一個新領域叫做 「 組合基因組學 」 , 因為這些新的合成能力 , 這些巨大的基因庫和同性重組 , 我們認為我們可以設計一個機器人 , 來製造一個一天可能有百萬種不同的染色體 。
and therefore , as with all biology , you get selection through screening , whether you're screening for hydrogen production , or chemical production , or just viability .	因此 , 如同所有生物學一樣 , 你通過篩選 , 不論你是否在篩選氫產品 , 或化學生產 , 或只有可行性 。
to understand the role of these genes is going to be well within reach .	要了解這些基因的作用 , 將會很接近 。
we're trying to modify photosynthesis to produce hydrogen directly from sunlight .	我們試圖修改光合作用 , 直接從陽光中直接產生氫 。
photosynthesis is modulated by oxygen , and we have an oxygeninsensitive hydrogenase that we think will totally change this process .	光合作用是氧氣的調節 , 我們有一種氧氣敏感的氫氣 , 我們認為會完全改變這個過程 。
we're also combining cellulases , the enzymes that break down complex sugars into simple sugars and fermentation in the same cell for producing ethanol .	我們也在組合細胞 , 分解複雜糖的酵素 , 變成簡單的糖 , 在同一個細胞中產生乙醇 。
pharmaceutical production is already under way in major laboratories using microbes .	用微生物 , 製藥生產已經在大型實驗室中使用微生物 。
the chemistry from compounds in the environment is orders of magnitude more complex than our best chemists can produce .	環境中的化合物的化學成分比我們最好的化學家所產生的複雜性還要複雜 。
i think future engineered species could be the source of food , hopefully a source of energy , environmental remediation and perhaps replacing the petrochemical industry .	我認為未來的工程物種可以是食物的來源 , 希望是能源、環境的立場 , 或許可以取代石化工業 。
let me just close with ethical and policy studies .	讓我用倫理和政策研究做結尾 。
we delayed the start of our experiments in 1999 until we completed a yearandahalf bioethical review as to whether we should try and make an artificial species .	我們在1999年推行了我們的實驗 , 直到我們完成了一年半的生物倫理審查 , 來評估我們是否該嘗試並製造一個人造物種 。
every major religion participated in this .	每一個主要的宗教都參與其中 。
it was actually a very strange study , because the various religious leaders were using their scriptures as law books , and they couldn't find anything in them prohibiting making life , so it must be ok . the only ultimate concerns were biological warfare aspects of this , but gave us the go ahead to start these experiments for the reasons we were doing them .	這是個很奇怪的研究 , 因為各式各樣的宗教領袖使用他們的文字 , 他們找不到任何東西 , 禁止生存生命 , 所以這是唯一合理的 , 唯一的關注是生物戰爭方面的尊重 , 但給了我們前往這些實驗 , 為我們做這些實驗的理由 。
right now the sloan foundation has just funded a multiinstitutional study on this , to work out what the risk and benefits to society are , and the rules that scientific teams such as my own should be using in this area , and we're trying to set good examples as we go forward .	現在 , sloan基金會剛剛資助了一份多項制度的研究 , 來研究社會的風險和利益 , 以及科學團隊的規則 , 例如我自己應該要在這個領域中使用的這些規則 , 我們正嘗試在向前進行好的例子 。
these are complex issues .	這些都是複雜的議題 。
except for the threat of bioterrorism , they're very simple issues in terms of , can we design things to produce clean energy , perhaps revolutionizing what developing countries can do and provide through various simple processes .	除了生物恐怖主義的威脅 , 它們是非常簡單的議題 , 我們能設計出乾淨能源 , 或許革命化開發中國家可以做的事 , 通過各種簡單的過程 。
psychologist philip zimbardo says happiness and success are rooted in a trait most of us disregard: the way we orient toward the past , present and future . he suggests we calibrate our outlook on time as a first step to improving our lives .	心理學家菲利普•辛巴多說 「 快樂 」 和 「 成功 」 是根深蒂固的 , 我們大部分人都不知所措:我們如何朝向過去、現在和未來邁進 。 他建議我們在追求時間的第一步 , 來改善我們的生活 。
brain , business , happiness , mind , psychology , science	大腦、生意、快樂、心智、心理學、心理學、科學、科學 。
philip zimbardo prescribes a healthy take on time	philipzimbardo開了一段健康的日子 。
i want to share with you some ideas about the secret power of time , in a very short time .	我想和大家分享一些關於時間的秘密力量的一些想法 , 很短的時間內 。
video: all right , start the clock please . 30 seconds studio .	影片:好 , 開始時鐘 。 三十秒的工作室 。
keep it quiet please . settle down .	保持安靜 , 安靜下來 。
it's about time . end sequence . take one .	大約是時間 , 終結序列 。 拿一個 。
10 , nine , eight , seven , six , five , four , three , two . . .	十、九、八、七、五、四、三、二......
philip zimbardo: let's tune into the conversation of the principals in adam's temptation .	菲利普茲巴多:我們來談談亞當的誘惑中校長的誘惑 。
" come on adam , don't be so wishywashy . take a bite . " " i did . "	「 來吧亞當 , 不要那麼願望 。 多一點點 。 」 我真的這麼做了 。
" one bite , adam . don't abandon eve . "	「 一口 , 亞當 , 不要放棄 。 」
" i don't know , guys .	「 我不知道 , 各位 。
i don't want to get in trouble . "	我不想惹麻煩 。 」
" okay . one bite . what the hell ? "	「 好 , 一口 , 什麼 ? 」
life is temptation . it's all about yielding , resisting , yes , no , now , later , impulsive , reflective , present focus and future focus .	生命是暫時的 。 一切都在累積 , 抗拒 , 是的 , 不 , 後來 , 衝動 , 反思 , 現在和未來的焦點 。
promised virtues fall prey to the passions of the moment .	承諾美德會落入當下的熱情之中 。
of teenage girls who pledged sexual abstinence and virginity until marriage thank you george bush the majority , 60 percent , yielded to sexual temptations within one year .	青少年的女孩在婚前宣誓性墮胎和處女 , 直到婚前謝布希大部分人 , 60% , 在一年內就有性誘惑 。
and most of them did so without using birth control .	大部分的人都這麼做 , 不用用生育控制 。
so much for promises .	承諾太多了 。
now lets tempt fouryearolds , giving them a treat .	現在 , 讓我們暫時四歲的孩子 , 給予他們治療 。
they can have one marshmallow now . but if they wait until the experimenter comes back , they can have two .	他們現在可以有一顆棉花糖 。 但如果他們等到實驗員回來 , 他們就能有兩顆 。
of course it pays , if you like marshmallows , to wait .	當然 , 如果你喜歡棉花糖 , 等待它 。
what happens is twothirds of the kids give in to temptation .	孩子們有三分之二的誘惑 。
they cannot wait . the others , of course , wait .	他們無法等待 , 其他人當然 , 等等 。
they resist the temptation . they delay the now for later .	他們抗拒誘惑 , 現在他們延遲了 。
walter mischel , my colleague at stanford , went back 14 years later , to try to discover what was different about those kids .	華爾特•密克爾 , 我在史丹佛大學的同事 , 14年後回來 , 試圖找出那些孩子的差別 。
