there were enormous differences between kids who resisted and kids who yielded , in many ways .	孩子們有很大的差異 , 在許多方面 , 他們抗拒和孩子 。
the kids who resisted scored 250 points higher on the sat .	抗拒250分的孩子在土地上比較高的孩子 。
that's enormous . that's like a whole set of different iq points .	這很巨大 。 這就像是一整組不同的智商點 。
they didn't get in as much trouble . they were better students .	他們沒有那麼多麻煩 , 他們是比較好的學生 。
they were selfconfident and determined . and the key for me today , the key for you , is , they were futurefocused rather than presentfocused .	他們是自信和決心的 。 對我來說 , 對你來說 , 關鍵是 , 他們是未來發展的 , 而不是刻板印象 。
so what is time perspective ? that's what i'm going to talk about today .	所以 , 時間的觀點是什麼 ? 這就是我今天要談的 。
time perspective is the study of how individuals , all of us , divide the flow of your human experience into time zones or time categories .	時間觀點是研究個體 , 我們所有人 , 將人體經驗的分化成時間區或時間分類 。
and you do it automatically and nonconsciously .	你自動做得到 , 無意識地 。
they vary between cultures , between nations , between individuals , between social classes , between education levels .	他們在文化、國家、個人之間、社會階級之間、教育層面之間的差異 。
and the problem is that they can become biased , because you learn to overuse some of them and underuse the others .	問題是 , 它們會變得偏見 , 因為你學會克服其中的一些因素 , 不管是其他因素 。
what determines any decision you make ?	什麼決定你做出的決定 ?
you make a decision on which you're going to base an action .	你要做出一個決定 , 決定你要採取行動 。
for some people it's only about what is in the immediate situation , what other people are doing and what you're feeling .	對某些人來說 , 只有在當下的情況下 , 別人在做什麼 , 別人在做什麼 , 你的感受 。
and those people , when they make their decisions in that format we're going to call them " presentoriented , " because their focus is what is now .	而這些人 , 當他們在那種形式中做出決定時 , 我們稱他們為 「 簡報 」 , 因為他們的焦點是現在 。
for others , the present is irrelevant .	對其他人來說 , 現在是無關緊要的 。
it's always about " what is this situation like that i've experienced in the past ? "	總是在說: 「 我過去經歷過的這種狀況是什麼 ? 」
so that their decisions are based on past memories .	所以 , 他們的決定是根據過去的記憶 。
and we're going to call those people " pastoriented , " because they focus on what was .	我們將稱之為 「 牧師 」 , 因為他們專注於什麼 。
for others it's not the past , it's not the present , it's only about the future .	對他人來說 , 這不是過去 , 而是現在 , 只是關於未來 。
their focus is always about anticipated consequences .	他們的焦點在於預期後的後果 。
we're going to call them " futureoriented . " their focus is on what will be .	我們將稱之為 「 未來 」 , 他們的焦點是 「 未來 」 。
so , time paradox , i want to argue , the paradox of time perspective , is something that influences every decision you make , you're totally unaware of .	所以 , 時間悖論 , 我想爭論時間觀點的矛盾 , 是影響你所做的每一個決定 , 你完全不知道 。
namely , the extent to which you have one of these biased time perspectives .	換句話說 , 你有一個偏見的時光觀點
well there is actually six of them . there are two ways to be presentoriented .	其實有六個 。 有兩種方式可以呈現出來 。
there is two ways to be pastoriented , two ways to be future .	有兩種方式可以被主宰 , 兩種方式可以成為未來 。
you can focus on pastpositive , or pastnegative .	你可以把焦點放在貼紙上 , 或貼紙上 。
you can be presenthedonistic , namely you focus on the joys of life , or presentfatalist it doesn't matter , your life is controlled .	你也可以是具體的 , 你把焦點放在生命的喜悅 , 或現在的虛假主義者 , 不重要 , 你的生命被控制 。
you can be futureoriented , setting goals .	你可以是未來的、設定目標的目標 。
or you can be transcendental future: namely , life begins after death .	或者 , 你可以是超然的未來:生命從死亡開始 。
developing the mental flexibility to shift time perspectives fluidly depending on the demands of the situation , that's what you've got to learn to do .	發展出心理靈活性 , 來改變時間的觀點 , 取決於情境的需求 , 那就是你必須要學會做的事 。
so , very quickly , what is the optimal time profile ?	所以 , 很快地 , 最佳時機檔案是什麼 ?
high on pastpositive . moderately high on future .	積極的積極度 , 將來在高度上 。
and moderate on presenthedonism .	而現代主義 。
and always low on pastnegative and presentfatalism .	總是低於過去的負面和現代主義 。
so the optimal temporal mix is what you get from the past pastpositive gives you roots . you connect your family , identity and your self .	所以最佳的暫時性混合是你從過去的義肢中得到的 , 給你根源 。 連結你的家人、身分 , 以及你的自我 。
what you get from the future is wings to soar to new destinations , new challenges .	你從未來得到的 , 是翅膀 , 到新的目的 , 新的挑戰 。
what you get from the present hedonism is the energy , the energy to explore yourself , places , people , sensuality .	你從現在的 「 享樂主義 」 中得到的是能量 , 能探索你自己、地方、人、感官 。
any time perspective in excess has more negatives than positives .	任何時間的觀點都比正面更有負面 。
what do futures sacrifice for success ?	未來犧牲了什麼樣的成功 ?
they sacrifice family time . they sacrifice friend time .	他們犧牲家庭時光 , 犧牲了友誼的時間 。
they sacrifice fun time . they sacrifice personal indulgence .	他們犧牲了好玩的時間 , 犧牲了個人的侮辱 。
they sacrifice hobbies . and they sacrifice sleep . so it affects their health .	他們犧牲了嗜好 , 犧牲了睡眠 。 所以它會影響他們的健康 。
and they live for work , achievement and control .	他們為了工作、達成和掌控 。
i'm sure that resonates with some of the tedsters .	我相信 , 和一些ted的演說有所共鳴 。
and it resonated for me . i grew up as a poor kid in the south bronx ghetto , a sicilian family everyone lived in the past and present .	這對我有所共鳴 。 我在南布朗克斯•格赫托長大 , 一個西里亞的家庭 , 每個人都住在過去和現在 。
i'm here as a futureoriented person who went over the top , who did all these sacrifices because teachers intervened , and made me future oriented .	我來到這裡 , 身為一個將來的人 , 走過頂端的人 , 做了這些犧牲 , 因為老師介入了教學 , 讓我成為未來的靈感 。
told me don't eat that marshmallow , because if you wait you're going to get two of them , until i learned to balance out .	告訴我不要吃那顆棉花糖 , 因為如果你等著你拿到兩顆 , 直到我學會平衡 。
i've added presenthedonism , i've added a focus on the pastpositive , so , at 76 years old , i am more energetic than ever , more productive , and i'm happier than i have ever been .	我加入了現代主義 , 我在過去的76歲 , 我比以往更加活力 , 更有生產力 , 我比以前更快樂 。
i just want to say that we are applying this to many world problems: changing the dropout rates of school kids , combating addictions , enhancing teen health , curing vets' ptsd with time metaphors getting miracle cures promoting sustainability and conservation , reducing physical rehabilitation where there is a 50percent drop out rate , altering appeals to suicidal terrorists , and modifying family conflicts as timezone clashes .	我只是想說 , 我們把這個方法應用到許多世界問題上:改變學校的輟學率 , 將成癮率提高 , 增強青少年的健康 , 用時間比喻來治癒心智障礙 , 促進永續性和保育 , 減少身體復甦 , 在那裡有50%的退休率 , 改變了自殺恐怖份子 , 改變家庭的恐怖份子 。
so i want to end by saying: many of life's puzzles can be solved by understanding your time perspective and that of others .	最後我要說的是:許多生命的謎題都可以透過了解你的觀點和其他的觀點來解決 。
and the idea is so simple , so obvious , but i think the consequences are really profound .	這個想法很簡單 , 很顯而易見 , 但我認為 , 結果是很深刻的 。
how many of today's headlines will matter in 100 years ? 1000 ? kirk citron's " long news " project collects stories that not only matter today , but will resonate for decades even centuries to come . at ted2010 , he highlights recent headlines with the potential to shape our future .	現今的頭條有多少人在一百年會很重要 ? 一百年 ? 一百年 ? 克里斯•克特朗的《長新聞》收集故事 , 數十年來都不重要 , 甚至數百年來 , 他在ted2010年時 , 他的頭條有潛力可以塑造我們的未來 。
future , global issues , media , news , science	未來 , 全球議題、媒體、新聞、科學、科學 。
kirk citron: and now , the real news	kirkcitron:現在 , 真新聞報導了 。
we are drowning in news .	我們在新聞中淹沒 。
reuters alone puts out three and a half million news stories a year .	光是住家一年就發佈了三百五十萬則新聞 。
that's just one source .	這只是一個來源 。
my question is: how many of those stories are actually going to matter in the long run ?	我的問題是:長期來說 , 那些故事會很重要嗎 ?
that's the idea behind the long news .	這是長期新聞背後的想法 。
it's a project by the long now foundation , which was founded by tedsters including kevin kelly and stewart brand .	它是一個由tedsters所創立的計畫 , 包括凱文•凱利和史都華特的品牌 。
and what we're looking for is news stories that might still matter 50 or 100 or 10 , 000 years from now .	我們在尋找的新聞故事 , 可能還在50、100 , 000年後還會發生什麼事 。
and when you look at the news through that filter , a lot falls by the wayside .	當你透過那過濾的消息看新聞時 , 路面上的許多消息都落下了 。
to take the top stories from the a . p . this last year , is this going to matter in a decade ?	為了從a.p , 去年 , 這將會影響十年嗎 ?
is this going to matter in 50 or 100 years ?	在50或100年內 , 這會影響嗎 ?
okay , that was kind of cool .	好吧 , 這很酷 。
but the top story of this past year was the economy , and i'm just betting that , sooner or later , this particular recession is going to be old news .	但過去一年的頂尖故事是經濟 , 我打賭 , 不久後 , 這個衰退將會是古老的消息 。
so , what kind of stories might make a difference for the future ?	所以 , 什麼樣的故事會對未來有影響 ?
well , let's take science .	咱們來談談科學 。
someday , little robots will go through our bloodstreams fixing things .	有一天 , 小機器人會穿過我們的血流 , 來修復東西 。
that someday is already here if you're a mouse .	如果你是老鼠 , 某天就在這裡 。
some recent stories: nanobees zap tumors with real bee venom ; they're sending genes into the brain ; a robot they built that can crawl through the human body .	一些最近的故事:奈米生物會用真蜜蜂venom的腫瘤 ; 它們會把基因傳送到大腦 ; 一個可以在人體上爬行的機器人 。
what about resources ? how are we going to feed nine billion people ?	資源呢 ? 我們要如何餵養九十億人 ?
we're having trouble feeding six billion today .	現今我們有60億人口的營養問題 。
as we heard yesterday , there's over a billion people hungry .	如我們昨天聽到的 , 有超過十億人挨餓 。
britain will starve without genetically modified crops .	英國不會基因改造作物 , 英國會餓死 。
bill gates , fortunately , has bet a billion on [agricultural] research .	幸運的是 , 比爾•蓋茨有十億人在農業研究上 。
what about global politics ?	全球政治呢 ?
the world's going to be very different when and if china sets the agenda , and they may .	世界將會變得非常不一樣 , 如果中國設立了議程 , 他們可能會 。
they've overtaken the u . s . as the world's biggest car market , they've overtaken germany as the largest exporter , and they've started doing dna tests on kids to choose their careers .	他們已經超越了美國 , 成為世界上最大的汽車市場 , 他們已經超越了德國最大的出口國 , 他們開始在孩子們做dna測試 , 來選擇他們的職業 。
we're finding all kinds of ways to push back the limits of what we know .	我們發現各式各樣的方法 , 來推回我們所知的限制 。
some recent discoveries: there's an ant colony from argentina that has now spread to every continent but antarctica ; there's a selfdirected robot scientist that's made a discovery soon , science may no longer need us , and life may no longer need us either ; a microbe wakes up after 120 , 000 years .	一些近期的發現:阿根廷有一個蟻群 , 現在散播到每個大陸 , 但南極洲 , 有一個自主的機器人科學家 , 很快地 , 科學可能不再需要我們 , 生命可能不再需要我們 ; 超過120 , 000年 。
it seems that with or without us , life will go on .	看來 , 看似沒有我們 , 生命會持續下去 。
but my pick for the top long news story of this past year was this one: water found on the moon .	但過去一年 , 我為前長期新聞所做的選擇是:在月球上找到水 。
makes it a lot easier to put a colony up there .	讓它在上面放一個蟻群 , 更容易 。
and if nasa doesn't do it , china might , or somebody in this room might write a big check .	如果美國太空總署做不到 , 中國可能會 , 或在座的某個人可能會寫一份大支票 。
my point is this: in the long run , some news stories are more important than others .	我的重點是:長期來看 , 有些新聞故事比其他新聞更重要 。
planetary scientist carolyn porco shows images from the cassini voyage to saturn , focusing on its largest moon , titan , and on frozen enceladus , which seems to shoot jets of ice .	星球科學家carolynporco節目來自卡西尼航行到土星 , 專注在它最大的月球 , 土衛六和冰川上 , 這似乎是冰的噴射機 。
nasa , design , exploration , science , space , technology , universe , visualizations	美國太空總署、設計、探索、科學、科技、宇宙、視覺化 。
carolyn porco flies us to saturn	卡林•皮爾科把我們送到土星 。
in the next 18 minutes , i'm going to take you on a journey .	接下來的十八分鐘 , 我要帶你們踏上一段旅程 。
and it's a journey that you and i have been on for many years now , and it began some 50 years ago , when humans first stepped off our planet .	這是一段旅程 , 很多年來 , 我一直在旅行 , 50年前 , 人類第一次踏出地球 。
and in those 50 years , not only did we literally , physically set foot on the moon , but we have dispatched robotic spacecraft to all the planets all eight of them and we have landed on asteroids , we have rendezvoused with comets , and , at this point in time , we have a spacecraft on its way to pluto , the body formerly known as a planet .	在那50年裡 , 我們不僅僅是設定在月球上 , 我們還把機械太空船和其他八個行星分配到地球上 , 我們已經登陸了小行星 , 在這個時點 , 當時 , 我們有一艘太空船 , 飛到冥星上 , 人類被稱為行星 。
and all of these robotic missions are part of a bigger human journey: a voyage to understand something , to get a sense of our cosmic place , to understand something of our origins , and how earth , our planet , and we , living on it , came to be .	所有這些機械任務都是更大的人類旅程的一部分:一趟旅程 , 去了解宇宙的意義 , 去了解我們的起源 , 以及地球、地球、我們 , 都活在它上面 。
and of all the places in the solar system that we might go to and search for answers to questions like this , there's saturn . and we have been to saturn before we visited saturn in the early 1980s but our investigations of saturn have become far more indepth in detail since the cassini spacecraft , traveling across interplanetary space for seven years , glided into orbit around saturn in the summer of 2004 , and became at that point the farthest robotic outpost that humanity had ever established around the sun .	在太陽系中的所有地方 , 我們可能要去尋找像這樣的問題的答案 , 土星 。 我們去過土星 。 在1980年代早期 , 我們去過土星 , 但我們對土星的調查已經變得更加深刻 , 自從卡西太空船以來 , 跨越了星際空間 , 在2004年的夏天 , 在土星周圍繞著土星繞行 , 變成了最遙遠的飛行機器人 , 人類曾經在太陽周圍建立過太陽 。
now , the saturn system is a rich planetary system .	土星系統是個豐富的星球系統 。
it offers mystery , scientific insight and obviously splendor beyond compare , and the investigation of this system has enormous cosmic reach .	它提供了神秘、科學的洞見 , 明顯地 , 除了相較之外 , 這種系統的調查之外 , 已有巨大的宇宙觸及 。
in fact , just studying the rings alone , we stand to learn a lot about the discs of stars and gas that we call the spiral galaxies .	事實上 , 光是研究圈圈 , 我們就要學習很多關於恆星和氣體的距離 , 我們稱之為 「 螺旋星系 」 。
and here's a beautiful picture of the andromeda nebula , which is our closest , largest spiral galaxy to the milky way .	這是安德魯愛達•尼布拉的美麗照片 , 這是我們最接近的 , 最大的螺旋星系 , 到銀河系 。
and then , here's a beautiful composite of the whirlpool galaxy , taken by the hubble space telescope .	然後 , 這裡有個美麗的旋律銀河系 , 由哈伯太空望遠鏡拍攝 。
so the journey back to saturn is really part of and is also a metaphor for a much larger human voyage to understand the interconnectedness of everything around us , and also how humans fit into that picture .	所以 , 回到土星的旅程是真正的一部分 , 也是更大的人類航行的比喻 , 來了解我們周遭的所有事物的相互連結 , 以及人類如何符合這張照片 。
and it pains me that i can't tell you all that we have learned with cassini .	這讓我感到痛苦 , 我無法告訴各位 , 我們在卡西尼學到的所有東西 。
i can't show you all the beautiful pictures that we've taken in the last two and a half years , because i simply don't have the time .	我不能給你們看過去兩年半以來我們拍攝的美麗照片 , 因為我沒有時間 。
so i'm going to concentrate on two of the most exciting stories that have emerged out of this major exploratory expedition that we are conducting around saturn , and have been for the past two and a half years .	所以 , 我將專注在兩個最令人興奮的故事中 , 在這次重大的探險旅行中 , 我們在土星周圍進行了兩年半的探險 。
saturn is accompanied by a very large and diverse collection of moons .	土星是由非常大且多樣化的衛星組成的 。
they range in size from a few kilometers across to as big across as the u . s .	它們的大小和幾公里差不多 , 橫跨到美國 。
most of the beautiful pictures we've taken of saturn , in fact , show saturn in accompaniment with some of its moons . here's saturn with dione , and then , here's saturn showing the rings edgeon , showing you just how vertically thin they are , with the moon enceladus .	大部分我們拍攝土星的美麗照片 , 事實上 , 土星和一些月球相處 。 這是土星 , 土星和土星 , 這裡是土星 , 顯示土星邊緣是多麼微薄 , 和月土衛二 。
now , two of the 47 moons that saturn has are standouts .	現在 , 土星47顆月中有兩個是站立的 。
and those are titan and enceladus . titan is saturn's largest moon , and , until cassini had arrived there , was the largest single expanse of unexplored terrain that we had remaining in our solar system .	這些是土衛六和土衛二 。 土衛六是土星最大的月球 , 直到卡西尼到達那裡 , 是我們太陽系剩下最大一片未知的地形 。
and it is a body that has long intrigued people who've watched the planets .	它是一種身體 , 對於那些觀看行星的人 , 很有興趣 。
it has a very large , thick atmosphere , and in fact , its surface environment was believed to be more like the environment we have here on the earth , or at least had in the past , than any other body in the solar system .	它有一個非常大、厚的大氣層 , 事實上 , 它的表面環境被認為比較像我們在地球上所存在的環境 , 或至少在過去的任何一個太陽系中 。
its atmosphere is largely molecular nitrogen , like you are breathing here in this room , except that its atmosphere is suffused with simple organic materials like methane and propane and ethane .	它的大氣層大致上是分子氮 , 如你在這間房間裡呼吸 , 除了它的大氣層被簡單的有機物質所吸引 , 例如甲烷、丙烷和乙烷 。
and these molecules high up in the atmosphere of titan get broken down , and their products join together to make haze particles .	這些分子在土衛六大氣層中被破壞 , 它們的產品加入在一起 , 製造毛粒子 。
this haze is ubiquitous . it's completely global and enveloping titan .	這隻毛是無所不在的 , 完全是全球化的土衛六 。
and that's why you cannot see down to the surface with our eyes in the visible region of the spectrum .	這也是為什麼你看不到我們眼睛在光譜的可見區域看不見的原因 。
but these haze particles , it was surmised , before we got there with cassini , over billions and billions of years , gently drifted down to the surface and coated the surface in a thick organic sludge .	但這些黑色的粒子 , 被刺激了 , 在我們和卡西尼一起到那裡之前 , 數十億年來 , 溫柔地漂移到地面 , 覆蓋著厚的有機煙霧 。
so like the equivalent , the titan equivalent , of tar , or oil , or what we didn't know what .	就像泰坦一樣 , 泰坦和油 , 或我們不知道什麼 。
but this is what we suspected . and these molecules , especially methane and ethane , can be liquids at the surface temperatures of titan .	但這是我們懷疑的 。 這些分子 , 尤其是甲烷和乙烷 , 可能是泰坦的表面溫度 。
and so it turns out that methane is to titan what water is to the earth .	結果發現 , 甲烷就是土衛六的水 。
it's a condensable in the atmosphere , and so recognizing this circumstance brought to the fore a whole world of bizarre possibilities . you can have methane clouds , ok , and above those clouds , you have this hundreds of kilometers of haze , which prevent any sunlight from getting to the surface .	它在大氣層中是可以凝聚的 , 所以 , 辨識出這種情況 , 帶到整個奇異的可能性 。 你可以擁有甲烷雲 , 好 , 在雲層之上 , 你有上百公里的鐵路 , 可以防止任何陽光從水面到表面 。
the temperature at the surface is some 350 degrees below zero fahrenheit .	表面的溫度是零下350度 。
but despite that cold , you could have rain falling down on the surface of titan .	但 , 儘管如此寒冷 , 鐵達人的表面可能會下降 。
and doing on titan what rain does on the earth: it carves gullies ; it forms rivers and cataracts ; it can create canyons ; it can pool in large basins and craters .	土衛六在地球上所做的是:它會照顧衛星 , 形成河流和加沙 ; 它可以創造峽谷 ; 它能在大盆地和坑中池塘 。
it can wash the sludge off high mountain peaks and hills , down into the lowlands . so stop and think for a minute .	它可以在高山峰和山丘上沖水 , 沖下山丘 , 停下來 , 停下來想一想 。
try to imagine what the surface of titan might look like .	試著想像泰坦的表面會是什麼樣子 。
it's dark . high noon on titan is as dark as deep earth twilight on the earth .	它是黑暗的 。 土衛六的高點和地球的深處一樣黑暗 。
it's cold , it's eerie , it's misty , it might be raining , and you might be standing on the shores of lake michigan brimming with paint thinner .	很冷 , 很糟 , 很糟 , 可能會下雨 , 你可能站在密西根湖的岸上 , 用油漆薄薄 。
that is the view that we had of the surface of titan before we got there with cassini , and i can tell you that what we have found on titan , though it is not the same in detail , is every bit as fascinating as that story is .	這是我們在土衛六和土衛六一起到那裡之前的景象 , 我可以告訴你我們在土衛六上所發現的 , 不一樣細節 , 和那個故事都一樣令人著迷 。
and for us , it has been like the cassini people it has been like a jules verne adventure come true .	對我們來說 , 它就像是卡西尼號人 , 它是真的 。
as i said , it has a thick , extensive atmosphere .	如我所說 , 它有一個厚厚的大氣層 。
this is a picture of titan , backlit by the sun , with the rings as a beautiful backdrop .	這是泰坦的照片 , 太陽的背景 , 環圈是美麗的背景 。
and yet another moon there i don't even know which one it is . it's a very extensive atmosphere .	然而 , 另外一個月球 , 我甚至不知道它是哪一個 。 這是個非常廣泛的大氣層 。
we have instruments on cassini which can see down to the surface through this atmosphere , and my camera system is one of them .	我們在卡西尼號有樂器可以透過大氣層看到表面 , 我的攝影機系統是其中之一 。
and we have taken pictures like this .	我們拍了這樣的照片 。
and what you see is bright and dark regions , and that's about as far as it got for us .	而你看到的是明亮且黑暗的區域 , 正如它為我們帶來的那樣 。
it was so mystifying: we couldn't make out what we were seeing on titan .	這實在太神秘了:我們無法在泰坦上看到我們在泰坦身上看到的 。
when you look closer at this region , you start to see things like sinuous channels we didn't know . you see a few round things .	當你仔細觀察這個區域 , 你就會開始看到一些我們不知道的東西 。 你看到一些圓形的東西 。
this , we later found out , is , in fact , a crater , but there are very few craters on the surface of titan , meaning it's a very young surface .	後來我們發現 , 其實 , 其實 , 泰坦的表面有很少的螃蟹 , 意思是它是非常年輕的表面 。
and there are features that look tectonic .	有些特徵看起來是微生物 。
they look like they've been pulled apart .	他們看起來已經被拆散了 。
whenever you see anything linear on a planet , it means there's been a fracture , like a fault .	每當你在星球上看到任何線性 , 就意味著有一種裂痕 , 像是一個斷層 。
and so it's been tectonically altered .	所以它已經改變了 。
but we couldn't make sense of our images , until , six months after we got into orbit , an event occurred that many have regarded as the highlight of cassini's investigation of titan .	但我們無法理解我們的影像 , 直到我們進入軌道六個月後 , 一個事件發生了 , 許多人被視為是卡西尼號的調查 。
and that was the deployment of the huygens probe , the europeanbuilt huygens probe that cassini had carried for seven years across the solar system . we deployed it to the atmosphere of titan , it took two and a half hours to descend , and it landed on the surface .	那是土星探測器的部署 , 歐洲航空探測器在太陽系中載了七年 。 我們把它部署到土衛六的大氣層 , 花了兩個半小時才能下降 , 降到地表上 。
and i just want to emphasize how significant an event this is .	我只是想強調這個事件有多重要 。
this is a device of human making , and it landed in the outer solar system for the first time in human history .	這是人類製造的裝置 , 它是人類史上第一次登陸太陽系 。
it is so significant that , in my mind , this was an event that should have been celebrated with ticker tape parades in every city across the u . s . and europe , and sadly , that wasn't the case .	很顯著 , 在我腦海中 , 這場活動應該要在美國和歐洲和美國和歐洲的每個城市都在慶祝 , 很遺憾 , 這不是事實 。
it was significant for another reason . this is an international mission , and this event was celebrated in europe , in germany , and the celebratory presentations were given in english accents , and american accents , and german accents , and french and italian and dutch accents .	這是另外一個原因 。 這是國際化的使命 , 這個事件在歐洲 , 在德國慶祝 , 慶祝的簡報是英文口音、美國口音、德國口音、法國人、義大利人和荷蘭口口音 。
it was a moving demonstration of what the words " united nations " are supposed to mean: a true union of nations joined together in a colossal effort for good .	它是關於聯合國 「 聯合國 」 的動作 , 應該意味著:一個真正的國家團結 , 加入了對好事的努力 。
and , in this case , it was a massive undertaking to explore a planet , and to come to understand a planetary system that , for all of human history , had been unreachable , and now humans had actually touched it .	在這個例子中 , 它是一個巨大的探索一個星球 , 為了了解一個星球系統 , 人類歷史上所有人都不可思議 , 現在人類已經觸及了它 。
so it was i mean , i'm getting goose bumps just talking about it .	所以 , 我的意思是 , 我的意思是 , 我在談它 。
it was a tremendously emotional event , and it's something that i will personally never forget , and you shouldn't either .	那是個非常情緒化的事件 , 我個人永遠不會忘記 , 你也不該忘記 。
but anyway , the probe took measurements of the atmosphere on the way down , and it also took panoramic pictures .	總之 , 探測器在向下移動 , 測量了大氣層的測量 , 同時也拍攝了全景的照片 。
and i can't tell you what it was like to see the first pictures of titan's surface from the probe . and this is what we saw .	我無法告訴各位 , 第一次從探測器上看到泰坦的表面 。 這是我們看到的 。
and it was a shocker , because it was everything we wanted those other pictures taken from orbit to be .	那是個震撼人心的 , 因為我們希望其他照片從軌道拍攝到的一切 。
it was an unambiguous pattern , a geological pattern .	這是個不可知的模式 , 一個地質模式 。
it's a dendritic drainage pattern that can be formed only by the flow of liquids .	它是種垂直的乾燥模式 , 只靠液體流來形成 。
and you can follow these channels and you can see how they all converge .	你可以追蹤這些頻道 , 你可以看到它們如何轉換 。
and they converge into this channel here , which drains into this region .	他們把這條通道轉換成這個區域 。
you are looking at a shoreline .	你看到的是海岸線 。
was this a shoreline of fluids ? we didn't know .	這是流體的海岸線嗎 ? 我們不知道 。
but this is somewhat of a shoreline .	但這是一條海岸線的一些部分 。
this picture is taken at 16 kilometers .	這張照片是在16公里拍的 。
this is the picture taken at eight kilometers , ok ? again , the shoreline .	這張照片拍攝了8公里 , 好嗎 ? 再一次 , 海岸線 。
okay , now , 16 kilometers , eight kilometers this is roughly an airline altitude .	好 , 現在 , 16公里 , 8公里 , 大約是航空高度 。
if you were going to take an airplane trip across the u . s . , you would be flying at these altitudes .	如果你要穿越美國的飛機 , 你會在這些高度飛行 。
so , this is the picture you would have at the window of titanian airlines as you fly across the surface of titan .	這張照片是你在泰坦航空的窗戶 , 飛越泰坦的表面 。
and then finally , the probe came to rest on the surface , and i'm going to show you , ladies and gentlemen , the first picture ever taken from the surface of a moon in the outer solar system .	最後 , 探測器出現在表面上 , 各位先生女士們 , 第一個從外部太陽系的表面拍攝的照片 。
and here is the horizon , ok ?	這裡是地平線 , 好嗎 ?
these are probably water ice pebbles , yes ?	這些可能是水冰石 , 是嗎 ?
and obviously , it landed in one of these flat , dark regions and it didn't sink out of sight . so it wasn't fluid that we landed in .	很明顯地 , 它降落在一個平坦、黑暗的區域 , 它沒有被視覺淹沒 。 所以它不是我們登陸的液體 。
what the probe came down in was basically the titan equivalent of a mud flat .	探測器的成果基本上就是土衛六的平面 。
this is an unconsolidated ground that is suffused with liquid methane .	這是個不穩定的地面 , 上面有液態甲烷 。
and it's probably the case that this material has washed off the highlands of titan through these channels that we saw , and has drained over billions of years to fill in lowlying basins .	可能是這種物質在我們看到的這些通道上被沖下了泰坦的高地 , 經過了數十億年的水平 , 來填滿低水盆 。
and that is what the huygens probe landed in .	這就是huygens探測器登陸的目的 。
but still , there was no sign in our images , or even in the huygens' images , of any large , open bodies of fluids .	但 , 我們的影像中仍然沒有標誌 , 甚至在huygens的影像中 , 任何大型的液體 , 都有開放的液體 。
where were they ? it got even more puzzling when we found dunes .	牠們在哪裡 ? 當我們發現沙丘時 , 牠們變得更為令人困惑 。
ok , so this is our movie of the equatorial region of titan , showing these dunes . these are dunes that are 100 meters tall , separated by a few kilometers , and they go on for miles and miles and miles .	好 , 這是我們拍攝泰坦的赤道區域 , 展示這些沙丘 。 這些沙丘是一百公尺高 , 分離幾公里 , 幾公里 , 它們會持續幾英里 , 幾英里 。
there's hundreds , up to a 1 , 000 or 1 , 200 miles of dunes .	有數百、一千、二百英里的沙丘 。
this is the saharan desert of titan .	這是泰坦的撒哈拉沙漠
it's obviously a place which is very dry , or you wouldn't get dunes .	很顯然是一個非常乾燥的地方 , 或你不會得到沙丘 。
so again , it got puzzling that there were no bodies of fluid , until finally , we saw lakes in the polar regions .	再說一次 , 它有點困惑 , 沒有液體 , 直到最後 , 我們在北極地區看到湖泊 。
and there is a lake scene in the south polar region of titan .	在泰坦南極的南極地區有一個湖景 。
it's about the size of lake ontario .	大約是亞大略湖的大小 。
and then , only a week and a half ago , we flew over the north pole of titan and found , again , we found a feature here the size of the caspian sea .	然後 , 僅僅一個星期半前 , 我們飛越了泰坦北極 , 再次發現 , 我們找到了一大片的特色 , 加薩海的大小 。
so it seems that the liquids , for some reason we don't understand , or during at least this season , are apparently at the poles of titan .	所以看來 , 液體 , 是因為我們不了解的原因 , 或者至少這季 , 顯然是土衛六的兩極 。
and i think you would agree that we have found titan is a remarkable , mystical place . it's exotic , it's alien , but yet strangely earthlike , and having earthlike geological formations and a tremendous geographical diversity , and is a fascinating world whose only rival in the solar system for complexity and richness is the earth itself .	我想你會同意 , 我們發現泰坦是個不可思議、神秘的地方 。 它是外星人 , 它是外星人 , 但卻是奇怪的地質形成和一個巨大的地質多樣性 , 一個令人著迷的世界 , 為複雜和豐富度而生 。
and so now we go onto enceladus . enceladus is a small moon , it's about a tenth the size of titan . and you can see it here next to england , just to show you the size . this is not meant to be a threat .	所以現在我們來到土衛二 , 土衛二是小月球 , 大約是土衛六的尺寸 。 你可以在這裡看到它 , 向你展示大小 。 這不代表威脅 。
and enceladus is very white , it's very bright , and its surface is obviously wrecked with fractures .	土衛二是非常白的 , 它的表面很明亮 , 很明顯它的裂痕是被破碎的 。
it is a very geologically active body .	它是非常地活化的身體 。
but the mother lode of discoveries on enceladus was found at the south pole and we're looking at the south pole here where we found this system of fractures .	但土衛二的媽媽在南極發現了發現 , 我們在南極 , 發現了這個分裂的系統 。
and they're a different color because they're a different composition .	它們的顏色不同 , 因為它們是不同的組成 。
they are coated . these fractures are coated with organic materials .	它們是複製的 。 這些碎片是由有機物質組成的 。
moreover , this whole , entire region , the south polar region , has elevated temperatures . it's the hottest place on the planet , on the body .	此外 , 整個整個區域 , 南極區域 , 已經在高溫下升高 , 地球上最熱的地方 。
that's as bizarre as finding that the antarctic on the earth is hotter than the tropics .	這就像是發現地球上南極比熱帶熱得熱 。
and then , when we took additional pictures , we discovered that from these fractures are issuing jets of fine , icy particles extending hundreds of miles into space .	然後 , 當我們拿了額外的圖片 , 我們發現這些碎片是精緻的噴射機 , 冰粒會把數百英哩延伸到太空中 。
and when we colorcode this image , to bring out the faint light levels , we see that these jets feed a plume that , in fact , we see , in other images , goes thousands of miles into the space above enceladus .	當我們把這張影像編碼出來時 , 我們看到這些噴射機餵食的數量 , 事實上 , 在其它影像中 , 數千英哩進入了土衛二的太空船 。
my team and i have examined images like this , and like this one , and have thought about the other results from cassini .	我和我的團隊也檢視了像這樣的影像 , 就像這張 , 想了來自卡西尼號的其他結果 。
and we have arrived at the conclusion that these jets may be erupting from pockets of liquid water under the surface of enceladus .	而我們到了結論中 , 這些噴射可能是從土衛六表面的液態水中噴出來的 。
so we have , possibly , liquid water , organic materials and excess heat .	所以 , 我們可能有液態水、有機物質和多餘熱能 。
in other words , we have possibly stumbled upon the holy grail of modern day planetary exploration , or in other words , an environment that is potentially suitable for living organisms .	換句話說 , 我們可能已經發現了現代化日星探索的聖杯 , 或者 , 換句話說 , 一個適合生存有機體的環境 。
and i don't think i need to tell you that the discovery of life elsewhere in our solar system , whether it be on enceladus or elsewhere , would have enormous cultural and scientific implications .	我不認為我需要告訴你們 , 我們太陽系其他地方的生命發現 , 不論是在土衛二或其他地方 , 都會有巨大的文化和科學上的影響 。
because if we could demonstrate that genesis had occurred not once , but twice , independently , in our solar system , then that means , by inference , it has occurred a staggering number of times throughout the universe and its 13 . 7 billion year history .	因為如果我們能證明 , 基因有一次發生 , 不只一次 , 而是獨立的 , 在我們的太陽系中 , 那就意味著 , 由於它在宇宙中發生了很驚人的次數 , 並且它的137億年歷史 。
right now , earth is the only planet still that we know is teeming with life .	目前 , 地球是唯一的行星 , 我們仍然知道地球是充滿生命的 。
it is precious , it is unique , it is still , so far , the only home we've ever known .	它是很珍貴的 , 它是獨一無二的 , 到目前為止 , 我們所知唯一的家 。
and if any of you were alert and coherent during the 1960s and we'd forgive you , if you weren't , ok you would remember this very famous picture taken by the apollo 8 astronauts in 1968 .	如果你們之中有任何人在1960年代被警告 , 我們會原諒你們 , 如果你不在意 , 你還記得在1968年阿波羅8號太空人拍的這張很有名的照片 。
it was the first time that earth was imaged from space , and it had an enormous impact on our sense of place in the universe , and our sense of responsibility for the protection of our own planet .	那是第一次 , 地球是從太空而來的 , 它對我們在宇宙中的位置有著巨大的影響 , 以及我們對地球的保護的責任感 。
well , we on cassini have taken an equivalent first , a picture that no human eye has ever seen before .	嗯 , 我們在卡西尼號拍了一張相片 , 沒有人類眼睛見過的照片 。
it is a total eclipse of the sun , seen from the other side of saturn .	它是太陽的完整日蝕 , 從土星的另一側看到 。
and in this impossibly beautiful picture , you see the main rings backlit by the sun , you see the refracted image of the sun and you see this ring created , in fact , by the exhalations of enceladus .	在這個不可思議的圖片中 , 你可以看到太陽的主環背景 , 你可以看到太陽的轉折形象 , 你可以看到這個環 , 事實上 , 由土衛二延伸出來的延伸 。
but as if that weren't brilliant enough , we can spot , in this beautiful image , sight of our own planet , cradled in the arms of saturn's rings .	但就好像這樣 , 我們不夠聰明 , 可以在這個美麗的圖片中發現 , 我們自己的星球 , 在土星的圈中抓住它 。
now , there is something deeply moving about seeing ourselves from afar , and capturing the sight of our little , blueocean planet in the skies of other worlds .	現在 , 有件事深深地探究自己 , 從阿富汗 , 捕捉到我們小小、藍色的星球在其他世界的天空中 。
and that , and the perspective of ourselves that we gain from that , may be , in the end , the finest reward that we earn from this journey of discovery that started half a century ago .	而我們從中得到的觀點 , 可能是 , 最終 , 我們從這趟旅程中得到最好的獎賞 , 始於半個世紀前的發現 。
as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped . this slows the delivery of aid after a disaster and hides the economic potential of unused lands and unknown roads . in this short talk , google's lalitesh katragadda demos map maker , a group mapmaking tool that people around the globe are using to map their world .	至於2005年 , 世界上只有15%的人口被繪製了 。 這會減緩災難後的遞送方式 , 並隱藏無用的土地和未知的經濟潛力 。 在短短短的演說中 , 谷歌的卡達德達德達•德摩斯馬基 , 一群世界各地的人使用地圖來繪製他們的世界 。
collaboration , design , map , technology	合作、設計、地圖、技術、科技 。
lalitesh katragadda: making maps to fight disaster , build economies	萊特•卡特加達:製作地圖來對抗災難 , 建立經濟 。
in 2008 , cyclone nargis devastated myanmar .	2008年 , cyclonenagis摧毀了緬甸 。
millions of people were in severe need of help .	數百萬人受到嚴重的幫助 。
the u . n . wanted to rush people and supplies to the area .	聯合國想要壓迫人民 , 供應整個區域 。
but there were no maps , no maps of roads , no maps showing hospitals , no way for help to reach the cyclone victims .	但沒有地圖 , 沒有道路的地圖 , 沒有地圖顯示醫院 , 無法協助到達西哥受害者 。
when we look at a map of los angeles or london , it is hard to believe that as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped to a geocodable level of detail .	當我們觀察洛杉磯或倫敦的地圖時 , 很難相信在2005年時 , 世界上只有15%的地理位置是可編碼的細節 。
the u . n . ran headfirst into a problem that the majority of the world's populous faces: not having detailed maps .	聯合國執行總部陷入一個問題 , 世界上絕大部分的臉孔:沒有細節地圖 。
but help was coming .	但 , 協助要來了 。
at google , 40 volunteers used a new software to map 120 , 000 kilometers of roads , 3 , 000 hospitals , logistics and relief points .	在google , 40個志願者用一個新的軟體來繪製120萬公里的道路 , 三千間醫院、物流和救援點 。
and it took them four days .	他們花了四天的時間 。
the new software they used ? google mapmaker .	他們使用的新軟體 ? 谷歌地圖製作人 。
google mapmaker is a technology that empowers each of us to map what we know locally .	谷歌地圖製作者是一項技術 , 讓我們每人都能在地圖上繪製我們所知的事物 。
people have used this software to map everything from roads to rivers , from schools to local businesses , and video stores to the corner store .	人們用這個軟體來繪製所有東西 , 從公路到河流、學校、當地企業 , 到角落的商店 。
nobel prize nominee hernando de soto recognized that the key to economic liftoff for most developing countries is to tap the vast amounts of uncapitalized land .	諾貝爾獎諾貝爾獎•赫南多•德索托認定 , 大部分開發中國家的經濟訴訟的關鍵是要把大量未被統治的土地標記出來 。
for example , a trillion dollars of real estate remains uncapitalized in india alone .	舉例來說 , 僅僅在印度 , 一兆美元的房地產 , 還剩下無數次 。
in the last year alone , thousands of users in 170 countries have mapped millions of pieces of information , and created a map of a level of detail never thought viable .	光是去年 , 一百七十個國家就有數以百萬計的資訊 , 創造出了一系列細節 , 從來沒有想過的細節 。
and this was made possible by the power of passionate users everywhere .	由熱情使用者到處都是可以做到的 。
let's look at some of the maps being created by users right now .	現在讓我們來看看一些用戶製作的地圖 。
so , as we speak , people are mapping the world in these 170 countries .	如我們所說 , 在170個國家 , 人們在繪製世界 。
you can see bridget in africa who just mapped a road in senegal .	你可以看到非洲的橋樑 , 剛在塞內加爾畫了一條道路 。
and , closer to home , chalua , an n . g . road in bangalore .	離家更近 , 查盧亞 , 一個班加羅爾的ng道路 。
this is the result of computational geometry , gesture recognition , and machine learning .	這是計算幾何學的結果 , 手勢認可 , 機器學習 。
this is a victory of thousands of users , in hundreds of cities , one user , one edit at a time .	這是數以千計的使用者的勝利 , 在數百個城市 , 一個使用者 , 一個編輯 。
this is an invitation to the 70 percent of our unmapped planet .	這是我們70%未開發的地球的邀請 。
welcome to the new world .	歡迎來到新世界 。
in 2003 , the palestinian village of budrus mounted a 10monthlong nonviolent protest to stop a barrier being built across their olive groves . did you hear about it ? didn't think so . brazilian filmmaker julia bacha asks why we only pay attention to violence in the israelpalestine conflict and not to the nonviolent leaders who may one day bring peace .	2003年 , 佛教村落的巴勒斯坦村落在10個月的非暴力抗爭中 , 停止了一場屏障 。 你聽說過嗎 ? 不這麼想 。 巴西製片製作者朱利亞.巴哈問我們為何只關注以色列巴拉斯坦衝突 , 而非非暴力的領導者 , 可能有一天會帶來和平 。
arts , communication , compassion , entertainment , film , peace , violence , war	藝術、溝通、同情、娛樂、電影、和平、暴力、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭 。
julia bacha: pay attention to nonviolence	朱莉亞•巴哈:專注非暴力 。
for the last 8 years , i have dedicated my life to documenting the work of israelis and palestinians who are trying to end the conflict using peaceful means .	過去8年來 , 我致力於記錄以色列和巴勒斯坦人的作品 , 他們試圖用和平的方式結束衝突 。
when i travel with my work across europe and the united states , one question always comes up: where is the palestinian gandhi ?	當我在歐洲和美國旅行時 , 有一個問題總是浮現:巴勒斯坦甘地在哪裡 ?
why aren't palestinians using nonviolent resistance ?	為什麼巴勒斯坦人不使用非暴力抗爭 ?
the challenge i face when i hear this question is that often i have just returned from the middle east where i spent my time filming dozens of palestinians who are using nonviolence to defend their lands and water resources from israeli soldiers and settlers .	當我聽到這個問題時 , 我所面臨的挑戰是 , 我經常從中東回來 , 在那裡 , 我花了幾十位巴勒斯坦人使用非暴力來捍衛他們的土地和水資源 , 來自以色列士兵和居民 。
these leaders are trying to forge a massive national nonviolent movement to end the occupation and build peace in the region .	這些領導者正試著忘記一個龐大的國家非暴力運動 , 終結這個職業 , 並在這個地區建立和平 。
yet , most of you have probably never heard about them .	然而 , 大部分人可能從來沒有聽過他們 。
this divide between what's happening on the ground and perceptions abroad is one of the key reasons why we don't have yet a palestinian peaceful resistance movement that has been successful .	這種分裂在地面和國外的認知之間的差異 , 也是為什麼我們還沒有巴勒斯坦和平抗爭運動的關鍵原因之一 。
so i'm here today to talk about the power of attention , the power of your attention , and the emergence and development of nonviolent movements in the west bank , gaza and elsewhere but today , my case study is going to be palestine .	今天我來這裡是要談關注的力量、關注的力量 , 以及非暴力運動的興起和發展西岸的非暴力運動 , 加薩和其他地方 , 但是今天 , 我的案例研究將會是巴勒斯坦 。
i believe that what's mostly missing for nonviolence to grow is not for palestinians to start adopting nonviolence , but for us to start paying attention to those who already are .	我相信 , 成長中最少缺少的非暴力行為 , 不是為了巴勒斯坦人開始採用非暴力行為 , 而是為了我們開始關注那些已經有的人 。
allow me to illustrate this point by taking you to this village called budrus .	讓我來說明一下這個點 , 把你們帶到這個叫做布德魯斯的村莊 。
about seven years ago , they faced extinction , because israel announced it would build a separation barrier , and part of this barrier would be built on top of the village .	大約七年前 , 他們面臨絕種 , 因為以色列宣佈它會建立一個隔離障礙 , 而這個障礙的一部分則是建在村子的頂端 。
they would lose 40 percent of their land and be surrounded , so they would lose free access to the rest of the west bank .	他們會失去百分之四十的土地 , 圍繞著土地 , 所以他們會失去自由地取得西岸的其他銀行 。
through inspired local leadership , they launched a peaceful resistance campaign to stop that from happening .	透過啟發當地的領導力 , 他們發起了和平的抗爭活動 , 來阻止這種事發生 。
let me show you some brief clips , so you have a sense for what that actually looked like on the ground .	讓我給你們看一些簡短的片段 , 讓你們知道在地面上看起來是什麼樣子的 。
palestinian woman: we were told the wall would separate palestine from israel .	巴勒斯坦女人:我們被告知 , 牆會從以色列分離巴勒斯坦 。
here in budrus , we realized the wall would steal our land .	在布德魯斯 , 我們發現牆會偷走我們的土地 。
israeli man: the fence has , in fact , created a solution to terror .	以色列人: 「 柵欄 」 其實創造出了恐怖的解決方案 。
man: today you're invited to a peaceful march .	男子:今天你被邀請去和平遊行 。
you are joined by dozens of your israeli brothers and sisters .	你被數十個以色列兄弟和姐妹團結在一起 。
israeli activist: nothing scares the army more than nonviolent opposition .	以色列活躍主義者:軍隊沒有比非暴力的反對者還要害怕 。
woman: we saw the men trying to push the soldiers , but none of them could do that .	女人:我們看到男人試圖推動士兵 , 但他們沒有人能做到 。
but i think the girls could do it .	但我認為 , 女孩們可以做到 。
fatah party member: we must empty our minds of traditional thinking .	fatah黨員:我們必須把傳統思維的思維清醒 。
hamas party member: we were in complete harmony , and we wanted to spread it to all of palestine .	哈馬斯黨員:我們是完全和諧的 , 我們想要將它傳播給所有巴勒斯坦 。
chanting: one united nation .	查理:一國 。
fatah , hamas and the popular front !	fatah , 哈馬斯和流行的前面 !
news anchor: the clashes over the fence continue .	新聞主持人:這句話持續下去 。
reporter: israeli border police were sent to disperse the crowd .	記者:以色列邊界警察被送去散播群眾 。
they were allowed to use any force necessary .	他們被允許使用任何武力 。
man: these are live bullets .	男子:這是現場的預算 。
it's like fallujah . shooting everywhere .	這就像是夏洛伊賈 , 無所不在 。
israeli activist: i was sure we were all going to die .	以色列活躍主義者:我相信我們都會死 。
but there were others around me who weren't even cowering .	但在我身邊 , 有些人甚至還沒有更新 。
israeli soldier: a nonviolent protest is not going to stop the [unclear] .	以色列士兵:非暴力抗爭將無法阻止[不清楚]
protester: this is a peaceful march .	蛋白質:這是和平的遊行 。
there is no need to use violence .	沒有必要使用暴力 。
chanting: we can do it ! we can do it !	查理:我們能做到 ! 我們能做到 !
julia bacha: when i first heard about the story of budrus , i was surprised that the international media had failed to cover the extraordinary set of events that happened seven years ago , in 2003 .	朱莉亞•巴哈:當我第一次聽到布德魯斯的故事時 , 我很訝異國際媒體沒有報導七年前發生的非凡事件 , 在2003年 。
what was even more surprising was the fact that budrus was successful .	更令人驚訝的是 , 布德魯斯成功的事實 。
the residents , after 10 months of peaceful resistance , convinced the israeli government to move the route of the barrier off their lands and to the green line , which is the internationally recognized boundary between israel and the palestinian territories .	居民經過了10個月的和平抗爭 , 說服了以色列政府在他們的土地和綠色的路徑 , 以色列和巴勒斯坦的領土之間的界線 。
the resistance in budrus has since spread to villages across the west bank and to palestinian neighborhoods in jerusalem .	布德魯斯的抗爭自從散播到西岸的村莊 , 到巴勒斯坦的耶路撒冷社區 。
yet the media remains mostly silent on these stories .	然而 , 媒體仍保留在這些故事上 。
this silence carries profound consequences for the likelihood that nonviolence can grow , or even survive , in palestine .	這種沉默的後果對非暴力的可能性有很大的影響 , 甚至是巴勒斯坦的生存 。
violent resistance and nonviolent resistance share one very important thing in common ; they are both a form of theater seeking an audience to their cause .	暴力抗爭和非暴力抗爭分享了一件非常重要的共通事 ; 兩者都是劇場尋求他們的成因 。
if violent actors are the only ones constantly getting frontpage covers and attracting international attention to the palestinian issue , it becomes very hard for nonviolent leaders to make the case to their communities that civil disobedience is a viable option in addressing their plight .	如果暴力演員是唯一不斷地在前線報導 , 吸引國際關注巴勒斯坦議題 , 那對非暴力的領袖來說是非常困難的 , 讓他們的公民不服從的社區成為一個可行的選項 , 來解決他們的困境 。
the power of attention is probably going to come as no surprise to the parents in the room .	注意力的力量可能對房間裡的父母毫無意外 。
the surest way to make your child throw increasingly louder tantrums is by giving him attention the first time he throws a fit .	要讓孩子們更大聲地丟下幻肢的確是讓他第一次注意到他丟下一套裝置 。
the tantrum will become what childhood psychologists call a functional behavior , since the child has learned that he can get parental attention out of it .	突破會變成童年心理學家所謂的功能性行為 , 因為孩子學到他可以從中得到父母的注意力 。
parents can incentivize or disincentivize behavior simply by giving or withdrawing attention to their children .	父母能激勵或激勵行為 , 單單單是給予孩子的注意力或戒斷 。
but that's true for adults too .	但對成年人來說也是如此 。
in fact , the behavior of entire communities and countries can be influenced , depending on where the international community chooses to focus its attention .	事實上 , 整個社區和國家的行為可能會受到影響 , 取決於國際社會選擇集中其注意力的地方 。
i believe that at the core of ending the conflict in the middle east and bringing peace is for us to transform nonviolence into a functional behavior by giving a lot more attention to the nonviolent leaders on the ground today .	我相信 , 在結束中東衝突的核心 , 帶來和平的核心 , 是讓我們把非暴力轉化為一個功能的行為 , 讓非暴力領導者更加關注現今在地面上的非暴力領導者 。
in the course of taking my film to villages in the west bank , in gaza and in east jerusalem , i have seen the impact that even one documentary film can have in influencing the transformation .	在拍攝我在西岸的村莊、在加薩和東耶路撒冷的過程中 , 我看到了一部紀錄片的影響 , 甚至有一部紀錄片可以影響到轉變 。
in a village called wallajeh , which sits very close to jerusalem , the community was facing a very similar plight to budrus .	在一個叫做瓦拉吉的村莊 , 非常靠近耶路撒冷 , 社區正面臨著非常相似的困境 。
they were going to be surrounded , lose a lot of their lands and not have freedom of access , either to the west bank or jerusalem .	他們會被圍繞著 , 失去了許多土地 , 且沒有自由的權利 , 不論是西岸或耶路撒冷 。
they had been using nonviolence for about two years but had grown disenchanted since nobody was paying attention .	他們已經用了兩年的非暴力行為 , 但從沒有人注意到他們 。
so we organized a screening .	所以 , 我們組織了一支螢幕 。
a week later , they held the most wellattended and disciplined demonstration to date .	一週後 , 他們舉辦了最好且最精準的示範 , 到達日 。
the organizers say that the villagers , upon seeing the story of budrus documented in a film , felt that there were indeed people following what they were doing , that people cared .	組織者說 , 村民們 , 看到布德魯斯在電影中記錄下來的故事 , 感覺確實有人追蹤他們在做什麼 , 人們關心他們 。
so they kept on going .	所以他們繼續下去 。
on the israeli side , there is a new peace movement called solidariot , which means solidarity in hebrew .	在以色列 , 有一種新的和平運動 , 叫做索里達特 , 意思是希伯來語的團結 。
the leaders of this movement have been using budrus as one of their primary recruiting tools .	這種運動的領導者 , 用布德魯斯作為他們主要的招募工具之一 。
they report that israelis who had never been active before , upon seeing the film , understand the power of nonviolence and start joining their activities .	他們報導以色列以前從未活躍過 , 看到電影 , 了解非暴力的力量 , 開始加入他們的活動 。
the examples of wallajeh and the solidariot movement show that even a smallbudget independent film can play a role in transforming nonviolence into a functional behavior .	瓦拉雅和索里運動的例子顯示即使是一部小型的預算獨立電影也能扮演非暴力行為的角色 。
now imagine the power that big media players could have if they started covering the weekly nonviolent demonstrations happening in villages like bil'in , ni'lin , wallajeh , in jerusalem neighborhoods like sheikh jarrah and silwan the nonviolent leaders would become more visible , valued and effective in their work .	現在 , 想像一下 , 大型媒體玩家可以擁有的力量 , 如果他們開始在村落中 , 像布林、尼林、瓦拉賈、耶路撒冷社區 , 和西瓦納 , 非暴力的領導者 , 在他們的作品中 , 會變得更有價值、更有效 。
i believe that the most important thing is to understand that if we don't pay attention to these efforts , they are invisible , and it's as if they never happened .	我相信最重要的是要了解 , 如果我們不關心這些努力 , 它們是看不見的 , 就好像從來沒有發生過 。
but i have seen first hand that if we do , they will multiply .	但是我首先看過如果我們這麼做 , 它們會乘以倍數 。
if they multiply , their influence will grow in the overall israelipalestinian conflict .	如果他們乘以 , 他們的影響力會在以色列巴勒斯坦的衝突中成長 。
and theirs is the kind of influence that can finally unblock the situation .	而他們就是一種影響力 , 終於可以解開這個情境 。
these leaders have proven that nonviolence works in places like budrus .	這些領袖已經證明了非暴力在像布德魯斯這樣的地方工作 。
let's give them attention so they can prove it works everywhere .	讓我們給予他們注意力 , 讓他們可以證明它在哪裡運作 。
simon sinek has a simple but powerful model for inspirational leadership all starting with a golden circle and the question " why ? " his examples include apple , martin luther king , and the wright brothers . . .	simmonsinek有一個簡單又強大的鼓舞性領導模式 , 始於黃金圓和問題 「 為什麼 ? 」 他的例子包括蘋果、馬丁路德金和萊特兄弟......
bullseye , business , entrepreneur , leadership , sales , selling , success	布洛西、商業、企業家、領導力、銷售、成功、成功、成功 。
simon sinek: how great leaders inspire action	simonsinek:偉大的領導人有多大的啟發 。
how do you explain when things don't go as we assume ?	要怎麼解釋當事情不如我們所想的那樣時 , 你要怎麼解釋 ?
or better , how do you explain when others are able to achieve things that seem to defy all of the assumptions ?	或者 , 更好的是 , 你要如何解釋 , 當其他人能達到所有假設時 , 看似無解的事物 ?
for example: why is apple so innovative ?	例如:為什麼蘋果電腦如此創新 ?
year after year , after year , after year , they're more innovative than all their competition .	年復一年 , 年復一年 , 比起所有的競爭都來得更創新 。
and yet , they're just a computer company .	然而 , 他們只是一家電腦公司 。
they're just like everyone else .	他們和其他人一樣 。
they have the same access to the same talent , the same agencies , the same consultants , the same media .	他們有相同的才華、相同的機構、相同的顧問、相同的媒體 。
then why is it that they seem to have something different ?	爲什麽他們似乎有所不同 ?
why is it that martin luther king led the civil rights movement ?	為什麼馬丁路德•金恩領導民權運動 ?
he wasn't the only man who suffered in a precivil rights america , and he certainly wasn't the only great orator of the day .	他不是唯一在美國處於前驅權利的人 , 他肯定不是那天唯一的偉大管道 。
and why is it that the wright brothers were able to figure out controlled , powered man flight when there were certainly other teams who were better qualified , better funded . . .	為何萊特兄弟能夠想出掌控、發電飛行的力量 , 尤其是其他比較好的團隊 , 更好的資金......
and they didn't achieve powered man flight , and the wright brothers beat them to it .	他們沒有實現人飛行 , 萊特兄弟打敗了他們 。
there's something else at play here .	這裡還有其他東西 。
about three and a half years ago i made a discovery .	大約三年半前 , 我發現了一項發現 。
and this discovery profoundly changed my view on how i thought the world worked , and it even profoundly changed the way in which i operate in it .	這項發現深深地改變了我的看法 , 改變了我認為世界是如何運作的 , 甚至徹底改變了我在其中工作的方式 。
as it turns out , there's a pattern .	結果發現 , 有一個模式 。
as it turns out , all the great and inspiring leaders and organizations in the world whether it's apple or martin luther king or the wright brothers they all think , act and communicate the exact same way .	結果發現 , 世界上所有偉大、鼓舞人心的領導人和組織 , 無論是蘋果或馬丁•路德•金或他們所認為的萊特兄弟 , 採取行動 , 並以相同的方式溝通 。
and it's the complete opposite to everyone else .	與其他人完全相反 。
all i did was codify it , and it's probably the world's simplest idea .	我所做的就是編寫它 , 它可能是世界上最簡單的點子 。
i call it the golden circle .	我稱它為黃金圈 。
why ? how ? what ?	為什麼 ? 怎麼辦 ?
this little idea explains why some organizations and some leaders are able to inspire where others aren't .	這個小想法解釋了為什麼有些組織和一些領導人能夠鼓舞別人不在哪裡 。
let me define the terms really quickly .	讓我很快地定義這個詞 。
every single person , every single organization on the planet knows what they do , 100 percent .	地球上每一個組織都知道他們做什麼 , 百分之百 。
some know how they do it , whether you call it your differentiated value proposition or your proprietary process or your usp .	有些人知道他們是怎麼做到的 , 不管你稱之為你的不同價值觀提議 , 或你的特殊程序 。
but very , very few people or organizations know why they do what they do .	但很少人或組織知道他們為何要做這些事 。
and by " why " i don't mean " to make a profit . "	藉由 「 為什麼 」 我不是說 「 賺取利潤 」 。
that's a result . it's always a result .	結果是 , 結果總是如此 。
by " why , " i mean: what's your purpose ?	所謂 「 為什麼 」 我的意思是:你的目的是什麼 ?
what's your cause ? what's your belief ?	你的原因是什麼 ? 你的信念是什麼 ?
why does your organization exist ?	為什麼你的組織存在 ?
why do you get out of bed in the morning ?	為什麼你早上要離開床 ?
and why should anyone care ?	為什麼有人要關心呢 ?
well , as a result , the way we think , the way we act , the way we communicate is from the outside in .	結果是 , 我們思考的方式 , 我們的行為方式 , 我們的溝通方式來自外界 。
it's obvious . we go from the clearest thing to the fuzziest thing .	很明顯 , 我們從最清晰的物體到最炫的物體 。
but the inspired leaders and the inspired organizations regardless of their size , regardless of their industry all think , act and communicate from the inside out .	但激勵人心的領袖和激勵人心的組織 , 不管他們的大小 , 不管他們的產業都在想 , 行動和溝通 。
let me give you an example .	讓我舉個例子 。
i use apple because they're easy to understand and everybody gets it .	我用蘋果電腦是因為它們很容易理解 , 每個人都懂 。
if apple were like everyone else , a marketing message from them might sound like this: " we make great computers .	如果蘋果跟其他人一樣 , 行銷訊息可能會像這樣: 「 我們會製造出很棒的電腦 。
they're beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	他們設計得很漂亮 , 很簡單 , 很友善地使用 。
want to buy one ? " " meh . "	想要買一台嗎 ? " 梅 。 "
and that's how most of us communicate .	這就是我們大多數人溝通的方式 。
that's how most marketing is done , that's how most sales is done and that's how most of us communicate interpersonally .	這就是多數行銷的方式 , 多數銷售方式就是這樣運作的 , 這是我們大多數人之間的交流方式 。
we say what we do , we say how we're different or how we're better and we expect some sort of a behavior , a purchase , a vote , something like that .	我們會說我們怎麼做 , 我們說我們是不同的 , 或我們比較好 , 我們期待某種行為、購買、投票 , 等等 。
here's our new law firm: we have the best lawyers with the biggest clients , we always perform for our clients who do business with us .	這是我們的新法律公司:我們有最好的律師和最大的客戶 , 我們總是為我們的客戶做生意 。
here's our new car: it gets great gas mileage , it has leather seats , buy our car .	這是我們的新車:它有很大的氣體里程序 , 它有皮革座椅 , 買我們的車 。
here's how apple actually communicates .	蘋果是這樣溝通的 。
" everything we do , we believe in challenging the status quo .	「 我們所做的一切 , 我們相信挑戰現狀 。
we believe in thinking differently .	我們相信不同的思考方式 。
the way we challenge the status quo is by making our products beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	我們挑戰現狀的方式是把我們的產品設計得很漂亮 , 很簡單 , 很友善 。
we just happen to make great computers .	我們剛好創造了很棒的電腦 。
want to buy one ? "	想要買一台嗎 ? 」
totally different right ? you're ready to buy a computer from me .	完全不一樣吧 ? 你準備好要從我身上買一台電腦 。
all i did was reverse the order of the information .	我所做的就是反轉資訊的順序 。
what it proves to us is that people don't buy what you do ; people buy why you do it .	它向我們證明 , 人們不買你做什麼 ; 人們買你為什麼要買 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼要買 。
this explains why every single person in this room is perfectly comfortable buying a computer from apple .	這解釋了為什麼在座的每個人都很自在地買蘋果電腦 。
but we're also perfectly comfortable buying an mp3 player from apple , or a phone from apple , or a dvr from apple .	但我們也非常自在地買蘋果電腦的mp3播放器 , 或是蘋果電腦的手機 。
but , as i said before , apple's just a computer company .	但 , 就像我之前說的 , 蘋果只是一家電腦公司 。
there's nothing that distinguishes them structurally from any of their competitors .	沒有任何東西可以從任何競爭對手中分辨它們 。
their competitors are all equally qualified to make all of these products .	他們的競爭對手都同樣合格製造這些產品 。
in fact , they tried .	事實上 , 他們試過了 。
a few years ago , gateway came out with flat screen tvs .	幾年前 , 高速公路上有著平面的螢幕電視 。
they're eminently qualified to make flat screen tvs .	他們真的有資格製造平面螢幕電視 。
they've been making flat screen monitors for years .	他們數年來都在製造平面螢幕監視器 。
dell came out with mp3 players and pdas , and they make great quality products , and they can make perfectly welldesigned products and nobody bought one .	德拉爾帶著mp3個球員和pdas出去 , 他們做出了很棒的產品 , 可以做出完美的產品 , 沒有人買過 。
in fact , talking about it now , we can't even imagine buying an mp3 player from dell .	事實上 , 談到現在 , 我們甚至無法想像 , 買一台mp3的演員 。
why would you buy an mp3 player from a computer company ?	為什麼你會從電腦公司買一個mp3的玩家 ?
but we do it every day .	但我們每天都在做這件事 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼要買 。
the goal is not to do business with everybody who needs what you have .	目標不是和任何需要你所擁有的所有人做生意 。
the goal is to do business with people who believe what you believe .	目標是要和那些相信你所相信的人做生意 。
here's the best part: none of what i'm telling you is my opinion .	最好的部分是:沒有一個我告訴你們的是我的意見 。
it's all grounded in the tenets of biology .	這一切都在生物學的網絡裡 。
not psychology , biology .	不是心理學 , 生物學 。
if you look at a crosssection of the human brain , looking from the top down , what you see is the human brain is actually broken into three major components that correlate perfectly with the golden circle .	如果你看人腦的十字路口 , 從上看 , 向下看 , 你會發現 , 人類的大腦其實是分成三個主要的元件 , 與黃金循環完全相連 。
our newest brain , our homo sapien brain , our neocortex , corresponds with the " what " level .	我們最新的大腦 , 我們的人類大腦 , 我們的新皮質 , 和 「 什麼 」 的 「 什麼 」 有關 。
the neocortex is responsible for all of our rational and analytical thought and language .	新皮質負責我們所有的理性和分析思考和語言 。
the middle two sections make up our limbic brains , and our limbic brains are responsible for all of our feelings , like trust and loyalty .	中間兩個區塊構成我們的肢體大腦 , 我們的肢體大腦對我們所有的感受負責 , 比如信任和忠誠 。
it's also responsible for all human behavior , all decisionmaking , and it has no capacity for language .	對於所有人類的行為 , 所有決策 , 都有責任 , 也沒有語言的能力 。
in other words , when we communicate from the outside in , yes , people can understand vast amounts of complicated information like features and benefits and facts and figures .	換句話說 , 當我們從外面溝通時 , 是的 , 人們可以了解大量複雜的資訊 , 比如特徵、好處、事實和數字 。
it just doesn't drive behavior .	它不會驅動行為 。
when we can communicate from the inside out , we're talking directly to the part of the brain that controls behavior , and then we allow people to rationalize it with the tangible things we say and do .	當我們能從內部傳達出來 , 我們直接和控制行為的大腦對話 , 接著 , 我們允許人們將它與我們所說的具體事物作出關聯 。
this is where gut decisions come from .	這是腸道決策的來源 。
you know , sometimes you can give somebody all the facts and figures , and they say , " i know what all the facts and details say , but it just doesn't feel right . "	有時 , 你可以給別人所有事實和數字 , 他們會說: 「 我知道所有事實和細節是什麼 , 但感覺不對 。 」
why would we use that verb , it doesn't " feel " right ?	為什麼我們會用這個動詞 , 它不會 「 感覺 」 ?
because the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking doesn't control language .	因為大腦控制決策的部分無法控制語言 。
and the best we can muster up is , " i don't know . it just doesn't feel right . "	最好的一點是: 「 我不知道 , 感覺不對 。 」
or sometimes you say you're leading with your heart , or you're leading with your soul .	或者有時你會說你正帶著你的心 , 或者你正帶著你的靈魂 。
well , i hate to break it to you , those aren't other body parts controlling your behavior .	嗯 , 我討厭打破它 , 那些不是控制你的行為的其他身體部件 。
it's all happening here in your limbic brain , the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking and not language .	這一切都發生在你的邊緣大腦中 , 控制決策的大腦的一部分 , 而非語言 。
but if you don't know why you do what you do , and people respond to why you do what you do , then how will you ever get people to vote for you , or buy something from you , or , more importantly , be loyal and want to be a part of what it is that you do .	但如果你不知道你為什麼要做你做的事 , 人們會回應你為什麼要做的事 , 那麼你要如何讓人們投票給你 , 或是從你身上買東西 , 或者 , 更重要的是 , 忠誠 , 想要成為你所做的一部分 。
again , the goal is not just to sell to people who need what you have ; the goal is to sell to people who believe what you believe .	同樣的 , 目標不只是賣給需要你所擁有的人們 ; 目標是賣給那些相信你所相信的人們 。
the goal is not just to hire people who need a job ; it's to hire people who believe what you believe .	目標不只是要僱用需要工作的人 , 而是要僱用那些相信你所相信的人 。
i always say that , you know , if you hire people just because they can do a job , they'll work for your money , but if you hire people who believe what you believe , they'll work for you with blood and sweat and tears .	我總是說 , 如果你雇用人 , 只因為他們可以幫忙 , 他們會為你的錢工作 , 但如果你雇用那些相信你所相信的人 , 他們會幫你血汗和淚水工作 。
and nowhere else is there a better example of this than with the wright brothers .	除了萊特兄弟之外 , 還有一個更好的例子 。
most people don't know about samuel pierpont langley .	大部分的人都不知道samuelperpontlangley 。
and back in the early 20th century , the pursuit of powered man flight was like the dot com of the day .	回到二十世紀初期 , 電力飛行的追求 , 彷彿是一天的點 。
everybody was trying it .	每個人都在嘗試 。
and samuel pierpont langley had , what we assume , to be the recipe for success .	而samuelperpontlangley所說的 , 我們所假設的 , 是成功的秘方 。
i mean , even now , you ask people , " why did your product or why did your company fail ? "	我是說 , 即使現在 , 你問人們: 「 為什麼你的產品是不是你的公司會失敗 ? 」
and people always give you the same permutation of the same three things: undercapitalized , the wrong people , bad market conditions .	人們總是給你同樣的三樣東西的看法:在不好的人、不好的人、不好的市場狀況下 。
it's always the same three things , so let's explore that .	一直都是一樣的三樣東西 , 咱們來探究它 。
samuel pierpont langley was given 50 , 000 dollars by the war department to figure out this flying machine .	samuelpierpontlangley給了五萬美元 , 由戰爭部門來找出這台飛行機器 。
money was no problem .	錢不是問題 。
he held a seat at harvard and worked at the smithsonian and was extremely wellconnected ; he knew all the big minds of the day .	他在哈佛的一席工作 , 在史密森人工作 , 當時非常緊張 ; 他知道每天的大頭腦 。
he hired the best minds money could find and the market conditions were fantastic .	他雇用最好的心智 , 可以找到 , 而市場條件很棒 。
the new york times followed him around everywhere , and everyone was rooting for langley .	紐約時報隨後都跟著他 , 每個人都在為langley發聲 。
then how come we've never heard of samuel pierpont langley ?	那麼 , 我們從來沒有聽過samuelperpontlangley ?
a few hundred miles away in dayton ohio , orville and wilbur wright , they had none of what we consider to be the recipe for success .	在俄亥俄州的幾百英哩外 , 奧維爾和威爾布萊特 , 他們沒有我們認為是成功的食譜 。
they had no money ; they paid for their dream with the proceeds from their bicycle shop ; not a single person on the wright brothers' team had a college education , not even orville or wilbur ; and the new york times followed them around nowhere .	他們沒有錢 ; 他們付出了他們的夢想 , 付出他們自自行車店的成功 ; 不是一個在萊特兄弟的團隊裡的單人 , 沒有大學生 , 甚至是維爾或威爾布爾 ; 紐約時報隨後都跟著他們 。
the difference was , orville and wilbur were driven by a cause , by a purpose , by a belief .	不同之處在於 , 奧維爾和威爾布爾被一個原因所驅使 , 由一個信念所驅使 。
they believed that if they could figure out this flying machine , it'll change the course of the world .	他們相信如果他們能弄清楚這台飛行機器 , 就會改變世界的軌道 。
samuel pierpont langley was different .	samuelpierpontlangley不同 。
he wanted to be rich , and he wanted to be famous .	他想要富有 , 他想要有名 。
he was in pursuit of the result .	他在追求結果 。
he was in pursuit of the riches .	他在追求財富 。
and lo and behold , look what happened .	看看發生了什麼事 。
the people who believed in the wright brothers' dream worked with them with blood and sweat and tears .	那些相信萊特兄弟的夢想的人和他們一起工作 , 充滿血汗和淚水 。
the others just worked for the paycheck .	其他人只是為了付款而工作 。
and they tell stories of how every time the wright brothers went out , they would have to take five sets of parts , because that's how many times they would crash before they came in for supper .	他們會說故事 , 每當萊特兄弟出去時 , 他們就要採取五組零件 , 因為那是他們在供應商之前會碰到多少次 。
and , eventually , on december 17th , 1903 , the wright brothers took flight , and no one was there to even experience it .	最後 , 在1903年12月17日 , 萊特兄弟拿了飛機 , 沒有人會在那裡體驗它 。
we found out about it a few days later .	幾天後我們發現了它 。
and further proof that langley was motivated by the wrong thing: the day the wright brothers took flight , he quit .	更進一步證明 , 拉格利被錯誤的動機給激勵了:萊特兄弟拍飛機的那天 , 他辭掉了 。
he could have said , " that's an amazing discovery , guys , and i will improve upon your technology , " but he didn't .	他可以說: 「 這是個很棒的發現 , 各位 , 我會改善你的技術 。 」 但他沒有 。
he wasn't first , he didn't get rich , he didn't get famous so he quit .	他不是首先 , 他沒有變富有 , 他沒有變有名 , 所以他放棄 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼要買 。
and if you talk about what you believe , you will attract those who believe what you believe .	如果你談到你所相信的 , 你會吸引那些相信你所相信的人 。
but why is it important to attract those who believe what you believe ?	但為何要吸引那些相信你所相信的人呢 ?
something called the law of diffusion of innovation , and if you don't know the law , you definitely know the terminology .	一種叫做創新法則的擴散法則 , 如果你不知道法律 , 你絕對知道術語 。
the first two and a half percent of our population are our innovators .	前兩半的人口是我們的創新者 。
the next 13 and a half percent of our population are our early adopters .	接下來的13.5%的人口是我們早期的選民 。
the next 34 percent are your early majority , your late majority and your laggards .	接下來的34%是你早期的大多數人 , 你的後代和你們的大部份人 。
the only reason these people buy touch tone phones is because you can't buy rotary phones anymore .	只有這些人買到手機的唯一理由 , 是因為你再也買不到腐敗手機了 。
we all sit at various places at various times on this scale , but what the law of diffusion of innovation tells us is that if you want massmarket success or massmarket acceptance of an idea , you cannot have it until you achieve this tipping point between 15 and 18 percent market penetration , and then the system tips .	我們都坐在不同的時間點 , 但創新的擴散法則告訴我們 , 如果你想要大眾的成功或大眾的接受 , 你就無法做到直到你達到了15%到18%的市場損失 , 然後體制的秘訣 。
and i love asking businesses , " what's your conversion on new business ? "	我喜歡問企業: 「 你對新商業的看法是什麼 ? 」
and they love to tell you , " oh , it's about 10 percent , " proudly .	他們很樂意跟你說: 「 喔 , 大概是10% 。 」
well , you can trip over 10 percent of the customers .	嗯 , 你可以超過百分之十的客戶 。
we all have about 10 percent who just " get it . "	我們都有大約百分之十的 「 去做 」 。
that's how we describe them , right ?	我們就是這樣描述他們 , 對吧 ?
that's like that gut feeling , " oh , they just get it . "	那就像是那種感覺: 「 喔 , 他們就懂了 。 」
the problem is: how do you find the ones that get it before you're doing business with them versus the ones who don't get it ?	問題是:你要如何找到在你和他們做生意之前得到的那些人 , 而不是那些沒拿到的那些人 ?
so it's this here , this little gap that you have to close , as jeffrey moore calls it , " crossing the chasm " because , you see , the early majority will not try something until someone else has tried it first .	這裡是這個小小的鴻溝 , 正如jeffreymoore稱之為 「 跨越混亂 」 , 因為 , 早期的大多數人都不會嘗試直到別人先試過 。
and these guys , the innovators and the early adopters , they're comfortable making those gut decisions .	而這些人 , 創新者和早期採用者 , 他們很舒適地做出那些腸道決策 。
they're more comfortable making those intuitive decisions that are driven by what they believe about the world and not just what product is available .	他們比較自在地做出他們所相信的世界的直覺決定 , 而不是產品是可取得的 。
these are the people who stood in line for six hours to buy an iphone when they first came out , when you could have just walked into the store the next week and bought one off the shelf .	這些人站在線上六個小時買一台iphone , 剛剛出門時 , 才剛剛走進商店 , 再下週買下一台商品 。
these are the people who spent 40 , 000 dollars on flat screen tvs when they first came out , even though the technology was substandard .	這些人花了四萬美金在平面螢幕上第一次出櫃 , 即便科技是潛在的 。
and , by the way , they didn't do it because the technology was so great ; they did it for themselves .	順便一提 , 他們並沒有這麼做 , 因為這項技術很棒 , 他們為自己做這件事 。
it's because they wanted to be first .	是因為他們想要先做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it and what you do simply proves what you believe .	人們不買你做的事 , 他們買你做的事 , 只是證明你相信什麼 。
in fact , people will do the things that prove what they believe .	事實上 , 人們會做他們所相信的事 。
the reason that person bought the iphone in the first six hours , stood in line for six hours , was because of what they believed about the world , and how they wanted everybody to see them: they were first .	六個小時內 , 買了iphone的原因是六個小時 , 站在線上 , 是因為他們相信這個世界的信念 , 以及他們希望每個人看他們:他們是第一名 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼要買 。
so let me give you a famous example , a famous failure and a famous success of the law of diffusion of innovation .	讓我給你一個有名的例子 , 一個有名的失敗 , 以及一個有名的創新法則的成功 。
first , the famous failure .	首先 , 著名的失敗 。
it's a commercial example .	這是個商業例子 。
as we said before , a second ago , the recipe for success is money and the right people and the right market conditions , right ? you should have success then .	如我們先前所說 , 成功的食譜是金錢和對的人和對的市場條件 , 對吧 ? 你應該要成功 。
from the time tivo came out about eight or nine years ago to this current day , they are the single highestquality product on the market , hands down , there is no dispute .	八、九年前 , 蒂夫出櫃時 , 他們是市場上最高品質的產品 , 手下 , 沒有爭議 。
they were extremely wellfunded .	他們非常富裕 。
market conditions were fantastic .	市場條件很棒 。
i mean , we use tivo as verb .	我的意思是 , 我們用tivo作為動詞 。
i tivo stuff on my piece of junk time warner dvr all the time .	我一直都在垃圾時空的dvr上綁著東西 。
but tivo's a commercial failure .	但tivo是一個商業失敗 。
they've never made money .	他們從來沒有賺錢 。
and when they went ipo , their stock was at about 30 or 40 dollars and then plummeted , and it's never traded above 10 .	當他們來到ipo時 , 他們的股票大約有三到四十元 , 然後爆炸 , 從來沒有在十元以上交易 。
in fact , i don't think it's even traded above six , except for a couple of little spikes .	事實上 , 我不認為它在六歲以上交易 , 除非有幾個小煙霧 。
because you see , when tivo launched their product they told us all what they had .	因為你看 , 當tivo發佈他們的產品時 , 他們告訴我們他們所擁有的一切 。
they said , " we have a product that pauses live tv , skips commercials , rewinds live tv and memorizes your viewing habits without you even asking . "	他們說: 「 我們有一個產品 , 暫停電視、跳過商業廣告、改造現場的電視 , 不需要你問 。 」
and the cynical majority said , " we don't believe you .	而憤世嫉俗的大多數人說: 「 我們不相信你 。
we don't need it . we don't like it .	我們不需要它 。 我們不喜歡它 。
you're scaring us . "	你害怕我們 。 」
what if they had said , " if you're the kind of person who likes to have total control over every aspect of your life , boy , do we have a product for you .	如果他們說: 「 如果你是那種想要完全控制你人生的各個面向 , 男孩 , 我們是否能為你做一個產品 。
it pauses live tv , skips commercials , memorizes your viewing habits , etc . , etc . "	它會暫停現場電視、滑雪廣告、記憶你的觀點習慣等等 。 」
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it , and what you do simply serves as the proof of what you believe .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼要做 , 而你做的只是證明你相信什麼 。
now let me give you a successful example of the law of diffusion of innovation .	現在 , 讓我給你們一個成功的例子 , 關於創新的擴散法則 。
in the summer of 1963 , 250 , 000 people showed up on the mall in washington to hear dr . king speak .	在1963年夏天 , 有25萬人出現在華盛頓的商場上 , 聽見金恩博士演講 。
they sent out no invitations , and there was no website to check the date .	他們沒有邀請 , 沒有網站可以檢查日期 。
how do you do that ?	你要怎麼做呢 ?
well , dr . king wasn't the only man in america who was a great orator .	金恩博士不是美國唯一一個偉大的獨裁者 。
he wasn't the only man in america who suffered in a precivil rights america .	他不是美國唯一受過預防權的美國人 。
in fact , some of his ideas were bad .	事實上 , 他的一些想法很糟 。
but he had a gift .	但他有一個禮物 。
he didn't go around telling people what needed to change in america .	他沒有到處告訴人們 , 在美國 , 要改變什麼 。
he went around and told people what he believed .	他四處 , 告訴人們他所相信的 。
" i believe , i believe , i believe , " he told people .	「 我相信 , 我相信 , 我相信 , 」 他告訴別人 。
and people who believed what he believed took his cause , and they made it their own , and they told people .	那些相信他所相信的 , 取決於他的成因 , 他們創造了自己的成果 , 他們告訴別人 。
and some of those people created structures to get the word out to even more people .	其中一些人創造了結構 , 讓更多人發聲 。
and lo and behold , 250 , 000 people showed up on the right day at the right time to hear him speak .	沒錯 , 兩萬五萬人在正確的日子裡站起來 , 聽他說話 。
how many of them showed up for him ?	他們當中有多少人會為他出席 ?
they showed up for themselves .	他們為自己出席 。
it's what they believed about america that got them to travel in a bus for eight hours to stand in the sun in washington in the middle of august .	這是他們相信美國讓他們在八月中行進巴士的八個小時 , 站在太陽中央的華盛頓 。
it's what they believed , and it wasn't about black versus white: 25 percent of the audience was white .	這是他們所相信的 , 不是關於黑人和白人:25%的觀眾是白人 。
dr . king believed that there are two types of laws in this world: those that are made by a higher authority and those that are made by man .	金恩博士相信這世界上有兩種法則:那些被一個更高權威所制定的法律 , 那些是由男人所製造的 。
and not until all the laws that are made by man are consistent with the laws that are made by the higher authority will we live in a just world .	除非所有由人類所建立的法律 , 都是由高權威所制定的法律 , 我們會住在一個公義的世界 。
it just so happened that the civil rights movement was the perfect thing to help him bring his cause to life .	就這樣發生了 , 民權運動是最好的一件事 , 協助他把他的成因帶到人生中 。
we followed , not for him , but for ourselves .	我們追隨 , 不是為了他 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and , by the way , he gave the " i have a dream " speech , not the " i have a plan " speech .	順便一提 , 他給了 「 我有一個夢想 」 演講 , 不是 「 我有一個計畫 」 演講 。
listen to politicians now , with their comprehensive 12point plans .	現在傾聽政治人物 , 用他們全面的12點計畫 。
they're not inspiring anybody .	他們沒有鼓舞任何人 。
because there are leaders and there are those who lead .	因為有領導者和領導人 。
leaders hold a position of power or authority , but those who lead inspire us .	領導者持有權力或權威的位置 , 但領導者鼓舞我們 。
whether they're individuals or organizations , we follow those who lead , not because we have to , but because we want to .	不論是個人或組織 , 我們追隨那些領導的人 , 不是因為我們必須 , 而是我們想要 。
we follow those who lead , not for them , but for ourselves .	我們追隨那些領導的人 , 不是為了他們 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and it's those who start with " why " that have the ability to inspire those around them or find others who inspire them .	那些從 「 為什麼 」 開始的人 , 能鼓舞他們周圍的人 , 或找到啟發他們的人 。
how do you remember where you parked your car ? how do you know if you're moving in the right direction ? neuroscientist neil burgess studies the neural mechanisms that map the space around us , and how they link to memory and imagination .	你如何記得你在哪裡停車 ? 你怎麼知道你是否在正確的方向 ? 神經科學家neilges研究神經機制我們周遭的空間 , 以及它們如何連結記憶和想像力 。
brain , cognitive science , exploration , neuroscience , science	大腦、認知科學、探索、神經科學、科學、科學 。
neil burgess: how your brain tells you where you are	neilburges:你的大腦如何告訴你你身在何處 。
when we park in a big parking lot , how do we remember where we parked our car ?	當我們停在一個大停車場時 , 我們要如何記住車子的位置 ?
here's the problem facing homer .	問題來了荷馬 。
and we're going to try to understand what's happening in his brain .	我們要試著去了解他的大腦發生了什麼事 。
so we'll start with the hippocampus , shown in yellow , which is the organ of memory .	所以 , 我們先從海馬體開始 , 黃色是記憶的器官 。
if you have damage there , like in alzheimer's , you can't remember things including where you parked your car .	如果你有受損 , 例如阿茲海默症 , 你無法記得事物包括你停車位的位置 。
it's named after latin for " seahorse , " which it resembles .	它是以拉丁文為 「 海底 」 命名的 , 它是以 「 呼吸器 」 為名的 。
and like the rest of the brain , it's made of neurons .	和大腦其他部位一樣 , 它是由神經元組成 。
so the human brain has about a hundred billion neurons in it .	人類的大腦有大約一千億個神經元 。
and the neurons communicate with each other by sending little pulses or spikes of electricity via connections to each other .	神經元會互相溝通 , 透過發送小脈衝或發送電脈衝 , 互相傳遞訊息 。
the hippocampus is formed of two sheets of cells , which are very densely interconnected .	海馬體形成了兩塊細胞 , 密度很高 。
and scientists have begun to understand how spatial memory works by recording from individual neurons in rats or mice while they forage or explore an environment looking for food .	科學家已經開始了解 , 空間記憶如何在老鼠或老鼠身上記錄在老鼠身上的神經元 , 或探索環境尋找食物 。
so we're going to imagine we're recording from a single neuron in the hippocampus of this rat here .	所以 , 我們要想像我們是從這個老鼠的海馬體中記錄下來的 。
and when it fires a little spike of electricity , there's going to be a red dot and a click .	當它發出一點電力時 , 會有一個紅點和點擊 。
so what we see is that this neuron knows whenever the rat has gone into one particular place in its environment .	我們看到的是這個神經元每當老鼠進入一個特定的環境中 , 都知道這個神經元在其環境中 。
and it signals to the rest of the brain by sending a little electrical spike .	它會訊號到大腦其他部位 , 通過發送小小的電流 。
so we could show the firing rate of that neuron as a function of the animal's location .	所以 , 我們可以展現神經元的頻率 , 作為動物的位置 。
and if we record from lots of different neurons , we'll see that different neurons fire when the animal goes in different parts of its environment , like in this square box shown here .	如果我們從許多不同的神經元記錄下來 , 我們將會看到不同的神經元 , 當動物在其環境中的不同部位出現時 , 比如這個正方形的盒子 。
so together they form a map for the rest of the brain , telling the brain continually , " where am i now within my environment ? "	所以 , 他們在一起形成了大腦的地圖 , 不斷地告訴大腦: 「 我現在在我的環境中 ? 」
place cells are also being recorded in humans .	位置細胞也被記錄在人類身上 。
so epilepsy patients sometimes need the electrical activity in their brain monitoring .	所以 , 癲癇患者有時會需要他們的大腦監控電活動 。
and some of these patients played a video game where they drive around a small town .	有些病人玩了個電玩遊戲 , 他們在小鎮附近開車 。
and place cells in their hippocampi would fire , become active , start sending electrical impulses whenever they drove through a particular location in that town .	把細胞放在海馬體中會發射 , 活躍起來 , 每當他們開車穿過某個特定的小鎮時就會發送電脈衝 。
so how does a place cell know where the rat or person is within its environment ?	那麼 , 一個地點細胞如何知道老鼠在其環境中的哪個位置 ?
well these two cells here show us that the boundaries of the environment are particularly important .	這兩個細胞告訴我們 , 環境的界線特別重要 。
so the one on the top likes to fire sort of midway between the walls of the box that their rat's in .	所以最上方的那個 , 會發火 , 有點像是在盒子裡的牆壁之間 。
and when you expand the box , the firing location expands .	當你擴大盒子時 , 發出的位置就會擴大 。
the one below likes to fire whenever there's a wall close by to the south .	下面的一面是一面火 , 一面是一面牆接近南方 。
and if you put another wall inside the box , then the cell fires in both place wherever there's a wall to the south as the animal explores around in its box .	如果你把另一面牆放進盒子裡 , 細胞會在兩面牆上 , 不論在哪裡 , 都會有一面牆到南方的動物在盒子裡探索 。
so this predicts that sensing the distances and directions of boundaries around you extended buildings and so on is particularly important for the hippocampus .	所以 , 這種預測 , 讓你周圍的邊界和方向有限的建築物 , 尤其對海馬體來說是很重要的 。
and indeed , on the inputs to the hippocampus , cells are found which project into the hippocampus , which do respond exactly to detecting boundaries or edges at particular distances and directions from the rat or mouse as it's exploring around .	的確 , 針對海馬體的輸入 , 細胞會在海馬體中找到哪個項目 , 會反應出界限或特定距離的邊緣 , 從老鼠或老鼠四處探索 。
so the cell on the left , you can see , it fires whenever the animal gets near to a wall or a boundary to the east , whether it's the edge or the wall of a square box or the circular wall of the circular box or even the drop at the edge of a table , which the animals are running around .	左邊的細胞 , 你可以看到 , 每當動物接近一面牆或東邊的邊緣 , 不管是方形盒子的牆或圓形牆 , 或圓形牆 , 或甚至是桌子的邊緣 , 動物在周圍跑 。
and the cell on the right there fires whenever there's a boundary to the south , whether it's the drop at the edge of the table or a wall or even the gap between two tables that are pulled apart .	右邊的細胞每當南邊有一個界線 , 不管是桌子的邊緣 , 或是牆壁 , 甚至是兩張桌子之間的鴻溝 。
so that's one way in which we think place cells determine where the animal is as it's exploring around .	所以這就是我們認為 , 位置細胞決定了動物周圍的位置 。
we can also test where we think objects are , like this goal flag , in simple environments or indeed , where your car would be .	我們也能測試我們認為物品的位置 , 例如這個目標旗 , 在簡單的環境中 , 或確實 , 你的車會在哪裡 。
so we can have people explore an environment and see the location they have to remember .	所以我們可以讓人們去探索一個環境 , 看看他們必須記得的位置 。
and then , if we put them back in the environment , generally they're quite good at putting a marker down where they thought that flag or their car was .	然後 , 如果我們把它們放回環境中 , 一般來說 , 它們很擅長把標記放在他們認為旗幟或車子的位置 。
but on some trials , we could change the shape and size of the environment like we did with the place cell .	但在某些試驗中 , 我們可以改變環境的形狀和大小 , 例如我們和地點細胞一樣 。
in that case , we can see how where they think the flag had been changes as a function of how you change the shape and size of the environment .	在那個案例中 , 我們可以看到他們認為旗幟的位置是如何改變你如何改變環境的形狀和大小 。
and what you see , for example , if the flag was where that cross was in a small square environment , and then if you ask people where it was , but you've made the environment bigger , where they think the flag had been stretches out in exactly the same way that the place cell firing stretched out .	舉例來說 , 如果國旗在一個小方形的環境中 , 交叉的位置 , 然後如果你問人們在哪裡 , 但你讓環境變大 , 他們認為旗子的位置與位置接接觸的位置相同 。
it's as if you remember where the flag was by storing the pattern of firing across all of your place cells at that location , and then you can get back to that location by moving around so that you best match the current pattern of firing of your place cells with that stored pattern .	就好像你記住旗幟的位置 , 藉由儲存你位置的所有位置細胞的模式 , 然後你就可以回到那個位置 , 這樣你就可以最好符合你位置細胞的目前模式 , 來儲存這個位置的模式 。
that guides you back to the location that you want to remember .	那會引導你回到你想記住的地點 。
but we also know where we are through movement .	但是我們也知道我們在移動的位置 。
so if we take some outbound path perhaps we park and we wander off we know because our own movements , which we can integrate over this path roughly what the heading direction is to go back .	所以如果我們把一些外界的路徑 , 也許我們會停下來 , 我們就會知道 , 因為我們自己的運動 , 我們可以把這條路結合起來 , 大約是朝向的方向 。
and place cells also get this kind of path integration input from a kind of cell called a grid cell .	位置細胞也會從一個叫做網格細胞的細胞中取得這種通路 。
now grid cells are found , again , on the inputs to the hippocampus , and they're a bit like place cells .	網格細胞又被發現 , 輸入到海馬體 , 它們有點像位置細胞 。
but now as the rat explores around , each individual cell fires in a whole array of different locations which are laid out across the environment in an amazingly regular triangular grid .	但當老鼠在周圍探索時 , 每個細胞都在一系列不同的位置上發射出來 , 在一個奇妙的三角形網格中 。
and if you record from several grid cells shown here in different colors each one has a gridlike firing pattern across the environment , and each cell's gridlike firing pattern is shifted slightly relative to the other cells .	如果你從數個格子細胞記錄下來 , 每種顏色都不同 , 都有類似網格的連結模式 , 每個細胞的網格都在轉變 , 轉變為其他細胞 。
so the red one fires on this grid and the green one on this one and the blue on on this one .	這條紅色的線條上有綠色的線條 , 上面有藍色的線條 。
so together , it's as if the rat can put a virtual grid of firing locations across its environment a bit like the latitude and longitude lines that you'd find on a map , but using triangles .	所以 , 一起來 , 老鼠可以把虛擬的地點放到不同的環境中 , 有點像你在地圖上看到的緯度和長度線 , 但用三角形 。
and as it moves around , the electrical activity can pass from one of these cells to the next cell to keep track of where it is , so that it can use its own movements to know where it is in its environment .	隨著它四處移動 , 電子活動可以通過其中一個細胞傳到下一個細胞 , 來追蹤它的所在位置 , 讓它可以利用它自己的動作 , 來知道它在其環境中的位置 。
do people have grid cells ?	人們有網格細胞嗎 ?
well because all of the gridlike firing patterns have the same axes of symmetry , the same orientations of grid , shown in orange here , it means that the net activity of all of the grid cells in a particular part of the brain should change according to whether we're running along these six directions or running along one of the six directions in between .	因為所有像電網一樣的電線圖案有相同的對稱軸線 , 相同的電線 , 在這裡是橘色的 , 也就是說 , 大腦中所有電網的神經活動應該要根據我們在六個方向上跑 , 或在兩者之間跑六個方向 。
so we can put people in an mri scanner and have them do a little video game like the one i showed you and look for this signal .	我們可以把人放進磁共振掃描儀裡 , 讓他們做一個小小的電玩遊戲 , 像我剛剛給你們看的一樣 , 尋找這個信號 。
and indeed , you do see it in the human entorhinal cortex , which is the same part of the brain that you see grid cells in rats .	的確 , 你的確在人類的腦皮質中看到它 , 和你在老鼠身上看到的一樣 。
so back to homer .	回到家鄉 。
