he's probably remembering where his car was in terms of the distances and directions to extended buildings and boundaries around the location where he parked .	他可能還記得他的車位在距離和方向的位置 , 來延伸建築物和界線 , 在他停車的地方 。
and that would be represented by the firing of boundarydetecting cells .	那會是用限制偵測細胞的激發來呈現的 。
he's also remembering the path he took out of the car park , which would be represented in the firing of grid cells .	他還記得他從汽車公園走出來的路徑 , 代表著網格細胞 。
now both of these kinds of cells can make the place cells fire .	兩種細胞都可以讓位置細胞發火 。
and he can return to the location where he parked by moving so as to find where it is that best matches the firing pattern of the place cells in his brain currently with the stored pattern where he parked his car .	他可以回到他所在的位置 , 藉由移動的位置 , 找到最好符合他大腦中位置細胞的發揮模式 , 讓他停車位 。
and that guides him back to that location irrespective of visual cues like whether his car's actually there .	這引導他回到那個位置的虛擬暗示 , 像是他的車是否真的存在 。
maybe it's been towed .	或許它被壓倒了 。
but he knows where it was , so he knows to go and get it .	但他知道它在哪裡 , 所以他知道要去拿它 。
so beyond spatial memory , if we look for this gridlike firing pattern throughout the whole brain , we see it in a whole series of locations which are always active when we do all kinds of autobiographical memory tasks , like remembering the last time you went to a wedding , for example .	所以 , 除了空間記憶之外 , 如果我們在整個大腦中尋找像電網一樣的電線圖案 , 我們在一系列的位置中看到它總是活躍 , 當我們做各種自傳記憶任務時 , 比如記住你上次去婚禮 , 舉例來說 。
so it may be that the neural mechanisms for representing the space around us are also used for generating visual imagery so that we can recreate the spatial scene , at least , of the events that have happened to us when we want to imagine them .	所以 , 或許神經機制代表我們周遭的空間 , 也被用來產生視覺影像 , 這樣我們才能重建空間的場景 , 至少 , 當我們想要想像它們時 , 那些事件發生在我們身上 。
so if this was happening , your memories could start by place cells activating each other via these dense interconnections and then reactivating boundary cells to create the spatial structure of the scene around your viewpoint .	所以如果這發生了 , 你的記憶可以從細胞開始 , 以這些密度相互作用的密度來啟動彼此 , 然後重新啟動邊界細胞 , 來創造你觀點周圍的空間結構 。
and grid cells could move this viewpoint through that space .	網格細胞可以透過這個空間移動這個視角 。
another kind of cell , head direction cells , which i didn't mention yet , they fire like a compass according to which way you're facing .	另一種細胞 , 頭部導向細胞 , 我還沒提到 , 它們就像你面臨哪種面臨的方式一樣 。
they could define the viewing direction from which you want to generate an image for your visual imagery , so you can imagine what happened when you were at this wedding , for example .	他們可以定義你想要為你的視覺影像產生影像 , 所以你可以想像當你在這個婚禮上發生了什麼事 。
so this is just one example of a new era really in cognitive neuroscience where we're beginning to understand psychological processes like how you remember or imagine or even think in terms of the actions of the billions of individual neurons that make up our brains .	這只是一個新時代在認知神經科學中的一個例子 , 我們開始了解心理的過程 , 比如你如何記住或想像 , 甚至在數十億個神經元的行動中 , 產生我們的大腦 。
thank you very much .	非常謝謝 。
imagine a global security driven by collaboration among agencies , government , the private sector and the public . that's not just the distant hope of opensource fans , it's the vision of james stavridis , the supreme commander of nato , who shares vivid moments from recent military history to explain why security of the future should be built with bridges rather than walls .	想像一下 , 一個全球安全的驅動力 , 政府 , 私部門和公眾 。 這不僅僅是開放原始碼的期望 , 詹姆士斯•斯特里迪斯的最高謀殺手 , 來自最近的軍事歷史中 , 他分享了一些充滿活力的時刻 , 來解釋未來的安全性 , 而不是牆壁 。
collaboration , global issues , opensource , peace , politics , social media , violence , war	合作、全球議題、開放資源、和平、政治、社交媒體、暴力、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭 。
james stavridis: how nato's supreme commander thinks about global security	詹姆士斯•斯特里迪斯:南托的最高謀殺手如何看待全球安全 。
i'm gonna talk a little bit about opensource security , because we've got to get better at security in this 21st century .	我今天要談的是開放資源安全性 , 因為我們必須在21世紀得到更好的安全性 。
let me start by saying , let's look back to the 20th century , and kind of get a sense of how that style of security worked for us .	首先 , 讓我們回顧20世紀 , 來了解一下安全的風格如何為我們帶來的影響 。
this is verdun , a battlefield in france just north of the nato headquarters in belgium .	這位是verdun , 法國的一個戰場 , 位於北部的北部 , 位於比利時的北部 。
at verdun , in 1916 , over a 300day period , 700 , 000 people were killed , so about 2 , 000 a day .	1916年 , 在verdun , 超過300天 , 70萬人被殺 , 所以每天大約有2000人 。
if you roll it forward 20thcentury security into the second world war , you see the battle of stalingrad , 300 days , 2 million people killed .	如果你把它推向第二次世界大戰 , 你會看到史達林畢業的戰爭 , 三百天 , 有兩百萬人被殺 。
we go into the cold war , and we continue to try and build walls .	我們進入冷戰 , 繼續嘗試建造牆壁 。
we go from the trench warfare of the first world war to the maginot line of the second world war , and then we go into the cold war , the iron curtain , the berlin wall .	我們從第一次世界大戰的熱帶戰爭 , 到第二次世界大戰 , 然後我們進入冷戰、鐵幕、柏林牆 。
my thesis for us today is , instead of building walls to create security , we need to build bridges .	我的今天論點是 , 與其建立一個安全的牆壁 , 我們需要建造橋樑 。
this is a famous bridge in europe .	這是歐洲有名的橋樑 。
it's the bridge over the drina river , the subject of a novel by ivo andrić , and it talks about how , in that very troubled part of europe and the balkans , over time there's been enormous building of walls .	它是德文河的橋樑 , 一個小說的主題 , 內容是關於在歐洲和巴爾幹半島的地區 , 經過一段時間 , 充滿了巨大的牆壁 。
more recently , in the last decade , we begin to see these communities start , hesitatingly , to come together .	最近 , 在過去的十年 , 我們開始看到這些社區開始 , 猶豫地 , 團結在一起 。
i would argue , again , opensource security is about connecting the international , the interagency , the privatepublic , and lashing it together with strategic communication , largely in social networks .	我再次主張 , 開放資源安全是要聯繫國際、國際關係、私人共和國 , 並將它與策略溝通 , 大部份是社交網路 。
so let me talk a little bit about why we need to do that , because our global commons is under attack in a variety of ways , and none of the sources of threat to the global commons will be solved by building walls .	所以 , 讓我來談談為什麼我們需要這麼做 , 因為我們的全球公有物以各種方式攻擊 , 和全球公有物的來源都不會被建造牆所解決 。
now , i'm a sailor , obviously .	很顯然 , 我是個水手 。
this is a ship , a liner , clipping through the indian ocean .	這是一條船 , 一條線 , 穿過印度洋 。
what's wrong with this picture ?	這張照片有什麼問題 ?
it's got concertina wire along the sides of it .	它的側邊有音樂廳的電線 。
that's to prevent pirates from attacking it .	那就是防止海盜攻擊它 。
piracy is a very active threat today around the world . this is in the indian ocean .	陰謀是現今世界各地非常活躍的威脅 。 這是在印度洋 。
piracy is also very active in the strait of malacca .	盜版也非常活躍 。
it's active in the gulf of guinea .	它活躍於幾內亞灣 。
we see it in the caribbean .	我們在加勒比海看到它 。
it's a $10billionayear discontinuity in the global transport system .	在全球運輸系統中 , 它是10億美元的不穩定性 。
last year , at this time , there were 20 vessels , 500 mariners held hostage .	去年 , 當時有20艘船 , 500名遊客 , 住宿 。
this is an attack on the global commons .	這是全球公有物的攻擊 。
we need to think about how to address it .	我們需要思考如何處理它 。
let's shift to a different kind of sea , the cyber sea .	讓我們轉換到不同的海洋 , 網路海 。
here are photographs of two young men .	這是兩位年輕男子的照片 。
at the moment , they're incarcerated .	當時 , 他們被監禁了 。
they conducted a credit card fraud that netted them over 10 billion dollars .	他們做了一個信用卡詐欺 , 把他們網上超過一百億美金 。
this is part of cybercrime which is a $2trillionayear discontinuity in the global economy .	這是網路犯罪的一部分 , 是全球經濟的二百萬美元不穩定性 。
two trillion a year .	一年有兩兆人 。
that's just under the gdp of great britain .	這只是英國的gdp之下 。
so this cyber sea , which we know endlessly is the fundamental piece of radical openness , is very much under threat as well .	這種網路海洋 , 我們無止盡地知道 , 這種極端的開放 , 也是受到威脅的基礎 。
another thing i worry about in the global commons is the threat posed by trafficking , by the movement of narcotics , opium , here coming out of afghanistan through europe over to the united states .	我擔心全球公有物的另一件事 , 是被販賣的威脅 , 透過毒品、鴉片 , 來自阿富汗 , 歐洲到美國 。
we worry about cocaine coming from the andean ridge north .	我們擔心古柯鹼來自安地亞里奇北部 。
we worry about the movement of illegal weapons and trafficking . above all , perhaps , we worry about human trafficking , and the awful cost of it .	我們擔心非法武器和人口販運的運動 , 最重要的是 , 我們擔心人口販賣 , 以及它的成本 。
trafficking moves largely at sea but in other parts of the global commons .	人口販運大致上在海上移動 , 但在全球公有物的其他地方 。
this is a photograph , and i wish i could tell you that this is a very hightech piece of us navy gear that we're using to stop the trafficking .	這是一張照片 , 我希望我能告訴你們 , 這是一張非常高科技的美國海軍怪胎 , 用來阻止交通堵塞 。
the bad news is , this is a semisubmersible run by drug cartels .	壞消息是 , 這是個半數的毒品販經營 。
it was built in the jungles of south america .	它是在南美叢林裡建造出來的 。
we caught it with that lowtech raft — — and it was carrying six tons of cocaine .	我們用低科技的速率抓住它 , 它帶著六噸的可卡因 。
crew of four . sophisticated communications sweep .	四個 , 複雜的溝通方式 。
this kind of trafficking , in narcotics , in humans , in weapons , god forbid , in weapons of mass destruction , is part of the threat to the global commons .	這種販賣方式 , 不論是對人類、武器、上帝禁止大規模毀滅的武器 , 是對全球公有物的威脅 。
and let's pull it together in afghanistan today .	讓我們一起在阿富汗 。
this is a field of poppies in afghanistan .	這是阿富汗的貧窮場所 。
eighty to 90 percent of the world's poppy , opium and heroin , comes out of afghanistan .	世界上百分之八十到九十的貧窮、鴉片和海洛因 , 來自阿富汗 。
we also see there , of course , terrorism .	當然 , 我們也看到了恐怖主義 。
this is where al qaeda is staged from .	這是蓋達組織的所在地 ,
we also see a very strong insurgency embedded there .	我們也看到一個非常強大的衝動 , 嵌入在那裡 。
so this terrorism concern is also part of the global commons , and what we must address .	所以這場恐怖主義也是全球公有物的一部分 , 而我們必須解決的 。
so here we are , 21st century .	這裡是21世紀 。
we know our 20thcentury tools are not going to work .	我們知道我們的20世紀工具不會成功 。
what should we do ?	我們該怎麼做 ?
i would argue that we will not deliver security solely from the barrel of a gun .	我敢說 , 我們不會只靠槍枝的桶子來提供安全 。
we will not deliver security solely from the barrel of a gun .	我們不會只靠槍枝的桶子來提供安全 。
we will need the application of military force .	我們需要軍事力量的應用 。
when we do it , we must do it well , and competently .	當我們這麼做時 , 我們必須要做得很好 , 且要有競爭力 。
but my thesis is , opensource security is about international , interagency , privatepublic connection pulled together by this idea of strategic communication on the internet .	但我的論點是 , 開源安全是國際、國際間、私人的聯結 , 由於網路上有策略性的溝通 。
let me give you a couple of examples of how this works in a positive way .	讓我舉幾個例子說明這如何以正面的方式進行 。
this is afghanistan . these are afghan soldiers .	這是阿富汗 , 這是阿富汗的士兵 。
they are all holding books .	他們都拿著書 。
you should say , " that's odd . i thought i read that this demographic , young men and women in their 20s and 30s , is largely illiterate in afghanistan . "	你應該說: 「 這很奇怪 。 我覺得我讀到這個人口統計 , 年輕男女 , 二十到三十歲 , 大部分是阿富汗的象徵 。 」
you would be correct .	你是正確的 。
eightyfive percent cannot read when they enter the security forces of afghanistan .	當他們進入阿富汗的安全部隊時 , 百分之八十五無法閱讀八十五 。
why ? because the taliban withheld education during the period of time in which these men and women would have learned to read .	為什麼 ? 因為塔利班在時間的期間 , 這些男人和女人會學會閱讀 。
so the question is , so , why are they all standing there holding books ?	所以 , 問題是 , 為什麼他們都站在那裡拿著書 ?
the answer is , we are teaching them to read in literacy courses by nato in partnership with private sector entities , in partnership with development agencies .	答案是 , 我們在教導他們閱讀文學課程 , 由南托和私營機構合作 , 與發展機構合作 。
we've taught well over 200 , 000 afghan security forces to read and write at a basic level .	我們已經教導了超過二十萬個阿富汗安全部隊來閱讀和寫作基本的層面 。
when you can read and write in afghanistan , you will typically put a pen in your pocket .	當你閱讀和寫在阿富汗 , 你通常會把一支筆放在你的口袋裡 。
at the ceremonies , when these young men and women graduate , they take that pen with great pride , and put it in their pocket .	在這些年輕男性和女性畢業時 , 她們帶著那筆很驕傲 , 把它放在口袋裡 。
this is bringing together international — there are 50 nations involved in this mission — interagency — these development agencies — and privatepublic , to take on this kind of security .	這帶出國際公共事業有五十個國家參與這個使命-國際關係這些發展部門和私人的公共事務 , 來承擔這種安全 。
now , we are also teaching them combat skills , of course , but i would argue , opensource security means connecting in ways that create longer lasting security effect .	當然 , 我們也在教導他們戰鬥技巧 , 但我認為 , 開放資源安全意味著連結更長久的安全效應 。
this is a us navy warship .	這是美國海軍戰艦 。
it's called the comfort .	它叫做舒適 。
there's a sister ship called the mercy .	有一個姐妹船叫做 「 慈悲 」 。
they are hospital ships .	他們是醫院船隻 。
this one , the comfort , operates throughout the caribbean and the coast of south america conducting patient treatments .	這張 , 舒適 , 在加勒比海和南美海岸進行病人治療 。
on a typical cruise , they'll do 400 , 000 patient treatments .	在典型的危機上 , 他們會做四十萬個病人的治療 。
it is crewed not strictly by military but by a combination of humanitarian organizations: operation hope , project smile .	它並非由軍隊來統治 , 而是人道組織的組合:營運希望、計畫微笑 。
other organizations send volunteers .	其他組織發送志工 。
interagency physicians come out .	實習醫生出來了 。
they're all part of this .	這些都是其中的一部分 。
to give you one example of the impact this can have , this little boy , eight years old , walked with his mother two days to come to the eye clinic put on by the comfort .	給你一個例子 , 這個小男孩 , 8歲 , 和他的母親兩天走上眼科診所 , 讓他們感到舒適 。
when he was fitted , over his extremely myopic eyes , he suddenly looked up and said , " mama , veo el mundo . "	當他準備好時 , 在他極度的肉眼中 , 他突然抬頭說: 「 媽媽 , veoelmundo 。 」
" mom , i see the world . "	「 媽 , 我看到世界 。 」
multiply this by 400 , 000 patient treatments , this privatepublic collaboration with security forces , and you begin to see the power of creating security in a very different way .	把這個數目乘以四十萬個病人的治療 , 這種私人的公眾合作 , 以安全力量 , 你開始看到創造安全的力量 , 以非常不同的方式來創造安全 。
here you see baseball players .	這裡你可以看到棒球選手 。
can you pick out the two us army soldiers in this photograph ?	你能在這張照片中拿出兩位美國軍隊的士兵嗎 ?
they are the two young men on either side of these young boys . this is part of a series of baseball clinics , where we have explored collaboration between major league baseball , the department of state , who sets up the diplomatic piece of this , military baseball players , who are real soldiers with real skills but participate in this mission , and they put on clinics throughout latin america and the caribbean , in honduras , in nicaragua , in all of the central american and caribbean nations where baseball is so popular , and it creates security .	他們是這些年輕男孩的兩位年輕男生 。 這是一系列的棒球診所 , 在那裡 , 我們探討了大聯盟棒球 , 國家的部門 , 他們設立了外交棒球選手 , 他們是真正的軍事棒球選手 , 但參與了這個使命 , 他們在拉丁美洲和加勒比海和加勒比海 , 他們在南美洲和加勒比海 , 在那裡 , 在南北美和南加勒比海 , 創造了美國的熱帶 。
it shows role models to young men and women about fitness and about life that i would argue help create security for us .	它展現了年輕男人和女人的榜樣 , 關於健身和生活 , 我會爭論 , 幫助我們創造安全 。
another aspect of this partnership is in disaster relief .	這種合作關係的另一面是災難性的救濟 。
this is a us air force helicopter participating after the tsunami in 2004 which killed 250 , 000 people .	這是美國空軍直升機在2004年在海嘯後參加 , 殺害了25萬人 。
in each of these major disasters — the tsunami in 2004 , 250 , 000 dead , the kashmiri earthquake in pakistan , 2005 , 85 , 000 dead , the haitian earthquake , about 300 , 000 dead , more recently the awful earthquaketsunami combination which struck japan and its nuclear industry — in all of these instances , we see partnerships between international actors , interagency , privatepublic working with security forces to respond to this kind of natural disaster .	在這兩大災難中 , 2004年 , 25萬人死亡 , 2005年 , 巴基斯坦的卡米里地震 , 八萬五千人死於海地地地地震 , 大約有三十萬人死亡 , 最近發生了一場很糟的地震混合 , 發生了日本和核融合 , 在所有這些事件中 , 我們看到了國際演員、國際演員、私人協會之間的合作關係 , 和這種天然災害 。
so these are examples of this idea of opensource security .	所以 , 這些是關於開放資源安全的例子 。
we tie it together , increasingly , by doing things like this .	透過這樣的做法 , 我們將它結合在一起 , 越來越多 。
now , you're looking at this thinking , " ah , admiral , these must be sea lanes of communication , or these might be fiber optic cables . "	現在 , 你看到這個想法: 「 啊 , 道德 , 這些一定是溝通的海道 , 或這些可能是光纖電纜 。 」
no . this is a graphic of the world according to twitter .	不 , 這是世界的圖表 , 根據推特 。
purple are tweets . green are geolocation .	紫色是推特 , 綠色是地理分配 。
white is the synthesis .	白色是合成 。
it's a perfect evocation of that great population survey , the six largest nations in the world in descending order: china , india , facebook , the united states , twitter and indonesia .	對於人口調查的完美演化 , 世界上六大國家的下定律:中國、印度、facebook、美國、推特和印尼 。
why do we want to get in these nets ?	為什麼我們要進到這些蚊帳呢 ?
why do we want to be involved ?	為什麼我們要參與 ?
we talked earlier about the arab spring , and the power of all this .	我們先前談到阿拉伯之春 , 以及這一切的力量 。
i'll give you another example , and it's how you move this message .	我再舉一個例子 , 就是你如何移動這個訊息 。
i gave a talk like this in london a while back about this point . i said , as i say to all of you , i'm on facebook . friend me .	我在倫敦演講了一陣子 , 談到這一點 。 我跟你們說 , 我在臉書上 。 朋友 。
got a little laugh from the audience .	聽眾笑了 。
there was an article which was run by ap , on the wire .	有篇文章是由ap所經營的 , 在電線上 。
got picked up in two places in the world: finland and indonesia .	世界上有兩個地方 , 芬蘭和印尼 。
the headline was: nato admiral needs friends .	標題是:南圖阿密德需要朋友 。
and the story was a catalyst , and the next morning i had hundreds of facebook friend requests from indonesians and finns , mostly saying , " admiral , we heard you need a friend , and oh , by the way , what is nato ? "	這個故事是催化劑 , 隔天早上 , 我有數百個facebook朋友 , 來自印尼人和芬人 , 大部分都說: 「 安德森 , 我們聽說你需要一個朋友 , 喔 , 順便說一下 , 娜托是什麼 ? 」
yeah , we laugh , but this is how we move the message , and moving that message is how we connect international , interagency , privatepublic , and these social nets to help create security .	沒錯 , 我們笑了 , 但這就是我們如何移動這個訊息 , 讓這個訊息傳遞出去 , 就是我們如何連結國際、國際間、私人和這些社交網絡 , 來協助創造安全 。
now , let me hit a somber note .	現在 , 讓我按下一個音符 。
this is a photograph of a brave british soldier .	這是一張勇敢的英國士兵的照片 。
he's in the scots guards .	他在蘇格蘭警衛 。
he's standing the watch in helmand , in southern afghanistan .	他站在阿富汗南方阿富汗的手錶 。
i put him here to remind us , i would not want anyone to leave the room thinking that we do not need capable , competent militaries who can create real military effect .	我把他放在這裡提醒我們 , 我不希望任何人離開房間 , 認為我們不需要有能力、競爭的軍隊 , 能創造出真正的軍事效應 。
that is the core of who we are and what we do , and we do it to protect freedom , freedom of speech , all the things we treasure in our societies .	是我們的核心和我們所做的 , 我們要保護自由、言論自由 , 所有我們在社會中珍藏的事物 。
but , you know , life is not an onandoff switch .	但你知道 , 生命不是一個即興的開關 。
you don't have to have a military that is either in hard combat or is in the barracks .	你不需要有軍隊 , 不論是在艱難的戰鬥 , 或是在巴拉克斯 。
i would argue life is a rheostat .	我會主張人生是 「 戒律 」 。
you have to dial it in , and as i think about how we create security in this 21st century , there will be times when we will apply hard power in true war and crisis , but there will be many instances , as we've talked about today , where our militaries can be part of creating 21stcentury security , international , interagency , privatepublic , connected with competent communication .	你得把它放進去 , 如我所想的 , 我們在21世紀創造安全 , 未來有時候我們會用真正的戰爭和危機來解決困難的力量 , 但在今天 , 我們的軍隊可以創造出21世紀的安全、國際的、國際的、國際的、國際間的、私人的、私人的、私人的溝通 。
i would close by saying that we heard earlier today about wikipedia . i use wikipedia all the time to look up facts , and as all of you appreciate , wikipedia is not created by 12 brilliant people locked in a room writing articles .	最後 , 我會說 , 我們今天早期聽到維基百科 。 我常使用維基百科 , 來查看事實 , 你們都欣賞維基 , 維基百科並不是十二個聰明的人在房間寫文章 。
wikipedia , every day , is tens of thousands of people inputting information , and every day millions of people withdrawing that information .	維基百科 , 每天都有成千上萬的人輸入資訊 , 每一天 , 數百萬人將這些資訊拆解 。
it's a perfect image for the fundamental point that no one of us is as smart as all of us thinking together .	這是個完美的圖像 , 沒有人跟我們一起思考一樣聰明 。
no one person , no one alliance , no one nation , no one of us is as smart as all of us thinking together .	沒有一個人 , 沒有盟友 , 沒有一個國家 , 我們沒有一個人像我們所有人一樣聰明 。
the vision statement of wikipedia is very simple: a world in which every human being can freely share in the sum of all knowledge .	維基百科的遠景很簡單:一個人類能自由地分享的世界 , 在所有知識的總和中 。
my thesis for you is that by combining international , interagency , privatepublic , strategic communication , together , in this 21st century , we can create the sum of all security .	我的論點是 , 透過結合國際、介入、私人共通、策略溝通 , 在二十一世紀 , 我們就能創造出所有安全的總和 。
thank you very much . thank you . thank you .	非常謝謝各位 。 謝謝 。
